        ## Extracted Text

        HIGHER-D SQUARE ○ CIRCLE △ TRIANGLE
The Interconnected Holographic Framework + Internal Navigation Tome (HD-SCT)
Tome status: v0.1 (new build)Prime directive: This tome defines the higher-dimensional Square/Circle/Triangle machine as its own operational system, with an explicit navigation layer (routes, hubs, edges, certificates) that lets you traverse the framework like a metro—deterministically.
Abstract Contract and Corpus Metro Map
0.1 What HD-SCT is
HD-SCT is a mechanized higher-dimensional semantics engine defined by three coupled carriers and one reconciliation carrier:
□ Square (address-capacity / structure / discreteness).At locked dimension (d) and depth (k), the Square carrier is the base-4 digit tensor space (\mathcal{S}_{d,k} := (\mathbb{D}_4^{,k})^{d}), where each axis carries a length-(k) base-4 fractional digit string and admits canonical integer encoding/decoding.Square refinement is prefix-locked: coarse addresses are complete holographic prefixes of all refinements.
○ Circle (phase-capacity / rotation / synchronization).At dimension (d), the circle carrier is the torus (\mathbb{T}^d := (\mathbb{R}/\mathbb{Z})^d).Circle resolution is governed by the wrap ladder (R(1)=1), (R(k+1)=3R(k)), hence (R(k)=3^{k-1}).Circle “rotation” is treated as a pinned, replayable operator family on (\mathbb{T}^d) (translation/gear action), and circle representations can be discretized into stratified metro rings when visibility requires it.
△ Triangle (control / carry / recursion legality).Triangle is the governance plane. In its canonical global form, triangle is a 3-sheet torsion parameter (\tau\in\mathbb{Z}3) acting as a shift on phases (\Delta\tau(\Phi)=\Phi+\frac{\tau}{3}\mathbf{1}_d\pmod 1).Higher-D variants include axis-wise triangle modes ((\mathbb{Z}_3)^d) (pinned), but the defining rule remains: triangle does not add meaning; it governs legality, pinning, carry/hatch boundaries, and what counts as an admissible refinement/route.
✶ Fractal (meta-zero / snap / multiscale reconciliation).Fractal is the canonicalization engine that reconciles noncommuting constraints by a pinned Snap procedure (alternating projections / deterministic scripts) and emits a canonical representative plus residual ledgers and receipts. Snap turns “almost” into typed, scoped, replay-verifiable disclosures (NEAR), turns underdetermination into bounded plans (AMBIG), and turns reproducible disagreement into fenced contradictions (CONFLICT/FAIL).
HD-SCT is therefore not a metaphor: it is a finite object language + a deterministic execution semantics + a routable evidence and governance system whose outputs are import-verifiable artifacts.
0.2 The minimal primitives and the locked scaling laws
HD-SCT is indexed by ((d,k)) and is phase-locked by coupled lift laws: increasing the representational “height” is not a free choice; it is governed by explicit lock schedules.
Square carrier primitive.(\mathcal{S}_{d,k}) is the digit tensor carrier with canonical truncation/refinement and cell nesting.
Circle carrier primitive.(\mathbb{T}^d) is the higher-D circle; wrap scaling (R(k)=3^{k-1}) is the octave index controlling rotation density without changing phase fractions.
Triangle primitive.Triangle torsion is a depth-stable, pinned phase offset (\Delta_\tau) acting on (\mathbb{T}^d).
Minimal stability law (Square).A dimension-(d) Square carrier is minimally stable only if per-axis resolution satisfies (N\ge 4^{d-1}); the canonical minimal stable choice is (N_{\min}(d)=4^{d-1}) and the minimal stable carrier is (\mathcal{S}^{\min}d\cong(\mathbb{Z}{4^{d-1}})^d).
Cross-dimensional metro law (Circle discretization).When the circle is discretized as a station-stratified metro, the minimal ring size required to support 15 macro-stations with (3^{d-1}) internal strata is (N\ge 15\cdot 3^{d-1}), achieved by the canonical ring (B_d=15\cdot 3^{d-1}).This is the formal “visibility requirement”: higher dimension demands higher circle resolution to prevent alias collapse of distinct higher-D strata.
These laws ensure that “higher-D” is not an aesthetic flourish: it is a set of explicit growth schedules and admissibility thresholds that keep lifts, transports, and routes replay-stable.
0.3 The station system: why this tome is a metro, not a linear book
This tome is designed to be traversed and executed like a metro system:
Stations (Chapters): Ch01–Ch21 are the linear spine; each chapter is a station that defines one segment of the operational system.
Hubs (Appendices): AppA–AppP are not “supplementary”; they are the hub system that makes the tome executable (parsing, registries, corridors, ledgers, containers, publication, connectors).
Four lines (Lenses): Square / Circle / Triangle / Fractal appear as four mutually linked projections of the same seed-anchored semantics.
Four platforms (Facets): Objects, Laws, Constructions, Certificates (what exists, what must hold, how to compute, how to verify).
Four atoms (Closure levels): a–d (from local primitives to global closure obligations).
The 15-station metro core is itself mechanized: the nonempty powerset of the four lenses has cardinality (2^4-1=15) and is treated as the canonical station semantics set.Its routing index carrier is the 15-ring (\Sigma_{15}\cong\mathbb{Z}_{15}) and the canonical orbit successor is (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}(\sigma)=\sigma+1\pmod{15}).Crucially, this tome keeps semantic station algebra (powerset/masks) separate from routing algebra (ring addition): semantics must be proved in semantic coordinates; movement must be proved in routing coordinates.
Result: every “reading path” is a deterministic RoutePlan object; every claim used in any narrative must be backed by explicit routes and certificates; ambiguity and approximation become explicit graph objects rather than prose hedges.
0.4 What the corpus contains (complete spine)
Ch01 — Axioms + Lock Laws.Defines (\mathcal{S}{d,k}), (\mathbb{T}^d), the □→○ projection, wrap ladder (R(k)), triangle torsion (\Delta\tau), and the coupled lift commutations that prevent desynchronization.
Ch02 — Dimension–Depth Lock and Minimal Stable Scales.Pins the minimal seed law and the per-axis minimum (4^{d-1}), and defines the locked lift schedule that prevents “cheap” higher-D claims.
Ch03 — The 15-Station Ring as the Powerset Carrier.Defines the 15 semantic stations as the nonempty powerset of the four lenses, their canonical mask/σ encodings, and the ORBIT_NEXT generator of the routing ring.
Ch04 — Gear-Loop Decomposition and Visibility.Defines the cycle/gear decomposition laws on (\Sigma_{15}) and on refined rings; proves when higher-D structure becomes visible vs aliased; formalizes the “snap threshold” as a gcd/orbit-length invariant.
Ch05 — Triangle Modes (global vs per-axis).Defines triangle as control and corridor selection; pins the mode choice (global or axis-wise) as meaning-bearing; defines carry/hatch governance interfaces.
Ch06 — Tunneling as Hub-Preserving Routing on (\mathbb{T}^d).Defines hub meshes (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}), admissible multi-axis tunnel steps, and hub-first route synthesis. Establishes the routing substrate for phase navigation.
Ch07 — Transport Legality (DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE) in HD-SCT.Defines typed transport edges across representations with budgets and replay closure; establishes legality and map-witness discipline.
Ch08 — Corridors, Truth Typing, and Failure Modes.Defines truth typing as a routing calculus: OK/NEAR/AMBIG/FAIL; mandates evidence artifacts (replays, ledgers, plans, failure witnesses).
Ch09 — Spin and Holonomy as Path-Dependence Witness.Defines loop receipts (spin/holonomy) as commutation evidence; makes path-dependence measurable and routable.
Ch10 — Meta-Zero and Snap.Defines the corridor-lock engine: alternating projections over pinned gates → canonical representative + residual ledger + obligations; makes “canonicalization” a verified operation.
Ch11 — Router Contract (≤6 hubs, deterministic order).Defines RoutePlan objects, mandatory hub signature, truth overlays, cap enforcement, DropLogs, and replay-deterministic routing as a pure bounded compiler.
Ch12 — Certificates (ReplayCert, RegressionCert, ExportCert).Defines witness bundles and replay harness expectations; import-verifiable certification is the operational definition of “verified.”
Ch13 — Cross-Dimensional Metro ( (B_d) ring + gear stacks ).Defines (B_d=15\cdot 3^{d-1}), its projections and lifts, and the triadic gear stack; formalizes the stratified metro carrier for higher-D station visibility.
Ch14 — The Holographic Compiler Interface (Seed → State → Navigation).Defines the aether seed as the invariant semantic object; defines compilation into HD-SCT state across □○△✶; defines compiled navigation indices and executable routes.
Ch15⟨0032⟩ — Defect Skeletons and Trigger Laws.Mechanizes failures into typed artifacts (DS/TL/MS/RS/CE) and routes them into certificates and governance.
Ch16⟨0033⟩ — Unified State Vector and the (T_U) Step.Defines the single authoritative operational semantics: one coherent update step for □○△ with checkpoints and replay capsules.
Ch17⟨0100⟩ — Transform Spine: (P\to Q\to B\to C) as Universal Action Grammar.Defines the universal action grammar and injection discipline; prevents hidden degrees of freedom by forcing every operation into a typed stage contract.
Ch18⟨0101⟩ — Integration: Buckets, Codes, Containers, and Replay.Turns transforms into distributable artifacts: deterministic encoding/decoding, pin manifests, salvage doctrine, replay harness expectations.
Ch19⟨0102⟩ — Mycelium Metro: Cross-Corpus Navigation as a Graph.Defines navigation as deterministic route planning over typed graph overlays; formalizes RoutePlans as executable reading units.
Ch20⟨0103⟩ — Time Axis: Retro-Weaving, DeltaPacks, and Evidence Promotion.Defines append-only time evolution, PulseIDs, retro-indexing without semantic rewrite, and deterministic promotion scheduling from AMBIG→NEAR→OK.
Ch21⟨0110⟩ — Deployment and Conformance: Publishable Reality.Defines deployment profiles, conformance suites, monitoring packets, incident-to-deltapack pipelines, and compliance closure.
0.5 The hub system (AppA–AppP) and the mandatory verification signature
The appendices are the hub network that makes the spine executable. Each hub is a strict spec station, not an “appendix note.”
Mandatory signature hubs (present on every certifying route):
AppA — Parsing, Symbols, Grammar, Entry Station (strict parsing, canonical AST/bytes).
AppI — Corridors, Truth Typing, Routable Outcomes (OK/NEAR/AMBIG/FAIL calculus + budgets).
AppM — Fractal/Recursion, Snap/Meta-Zero (canonical representative + residual ledger + replay closure).
Operational hubs (the remaining infrastructure):
AppB — Evidence Tables, IDs, Stability Contract (evidence as stable artifacts across time/migration).
AppC — Square Interior, Addressing, Local Proof Objects (tile semantics; local link kinds and closure).
AppD — Registry (MsIDs, profiles, pinned policies) preventing silent forks.
AppE — Circle Gear, phase profiles, tick/carry semantics (replayable phase evolution).
AppF — Transport discipline: DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE contracts; commutation receipts; migration protocol.
AppG — Triangle governor: recursion legality; carry/hatch interfaces; tunnel legality gates.
AppH — Coupling/topology constraints (multi-axis legality; spin/holonomy integration points).
AppJ — NEAR disclosure ledger (residuals, calibration, expiry, promotion checklist).
AppK — FAIL/CONFLICT, quarantine, revocation receipts (conflict packets + fences + propagation).
AppL — AMBIG evidence plans (bounded candidates, discriminators, stop rules, promotion hooks).
AppN — Containers & mount/salvage doctrine (deterministic manifests; replay harness structure).
AppO — Publication/import discipline (export bundles; import verifiers; governance gates).
AppP — Mycelium interface (INTER scope; connectors; cross-corpus pin requirements).
These hubs define the “metro controls”: how to parse, pin, route, replay, export, import, and deploy without hidden semantics.
0.6 Navigation legend: how to traverse the corpus deterministically
0.6.1 Addressability
Everything is addressable. The corpus is a graph of globally addressable atoms with lens slots and local paths. The only admissible cross-references are typed edges that include pins, witnesses, and truth typing under corridors.
0.6.2 RoutePlans (the executable reading unit)
A RoutePlan is the deterministic unit of navigation: it specifies:
target address,
scope (LOCAL/INTER),
hub sequence (bounded),
required overlays (NEAR/AMBIG/FAIL),
pins and budgets,
obligations and DropLog (if cap enforcement drops optional hubs).
A RoutePlan is replayable; the same pins and inputs yield the same ride and the same transcript.
0.6.3 Truth overlays (uncertainty is a station, not a footnote)
Truth class inserts the corresponding hub:
NEAR → AppJ (ResidualLedger + expiry + promotion obligations)
AMBIG → AppL (EvidencePlan: bounded candidates + discriminators + stop rules)
FAIL/CONFLICT → AppK (ConflictPacket + FenceSpec + quarantine propagation)
0.6.4 Standard ride templates (metro lines)
These are canonical deterministic ride templates; each is a hub-bounded execution plan:
VERIFY (publication-grade): AppA → AppI → AppM → Target → (AppO if exporting)
BUILD (construct artifacts): AppA → AppC/AppE/AppG (as needed) → AppI → AppM → Target
MIGRATE (meaning evolution): AppA → AppD → AppF → AppI → AppM → AppO
RESOLVE (conflict repair): AppA → AppK → AppM → AppB/AppF → AppI
PUBLISH (export/import closure): AppA → AppO → AppN → AppI → AppM → AppD/AppP
DEPLOY (production conformance): AppA → AppO → AppN → AppI → AppM → Ch21
Each template is a deterministic compilation of obligations: parse/canonicalize, check corridor legality, replay closure, then publish or execute governance gates.
0.7 The corpus metro map (textual topology)
0.7.1 Spine line: chapters as the operational build graph
SPINE:Ch01 → Ch02 → Ch03 → Ch04 → Ch05 → Ch06 → Ch07 → Ch08 → Ch09 → Ch10 → Ch11 → Ch12 → Ch13 → Ch14 → Ch15 → Ch16 → Ch17 → Ch18 → Ch19 → Ch20 → Ch21
Interpretation:
Ch01–Ch06 establish carriers and legal motion (□○△ with hub routing).
Ch07–Ch10 establish legality, truth typing, holonomy receipts, and canonical Snap.
Ch11–Ch14 establish deterministic navigation as executable routing and compilation.
Ch15–Ch21 establish mechanized failure, unified execution, integration/containers, time evolution, publication/import, and deployment conformance.
0.7.2 Hub line: appendices as the executor backbone
HUB RING (in functional order):AppA → AppD → AppC → AppE → AppG → AppH → AppF → AppI → AppJ → AppL → AppK → AppM → AppN → AppO → AppP → AppB → (back to AppA)
Interpretation:
Entry/Interpretation: AppA, AppD
Local semantics: AppC, AppE, AppG
Cross-axis and transport: AppH, AppF
Truth and uncertainty: AppI, AppJ, AppL, AppK
Canonical reconciliation: AppM
Packaging and governance: AppN, AppO, AppP
Evidence persistence: AppB
0.7.3 The “15-station semantic ring” as the internal navigation carrier
Inside each chapter/appendix, the 15 semantic stations are the nonempty powerset of the four lenses (S/F/C/R).Their routing carrier is (\Sigma_{15}) with ORBIT_NEXT generator (\sigma\mapsto\sigma+1\pmod{15}).Semantic station algebra (mask/powerset) and routing algebra (ring addition) are kept separate and linked only by pinned bijections.
0.8 The operational deliverables (what this tome produces)
This tome defines a closed system of objects, algorithms, and certificates that collectively enable:
Seed-anchored compilation: seed → state across □○△✶ with pinned profiles and canonicalization (Ch14).
Executable updates: a unified (T_U) step with checkpoints (Ch16).
Universal action grammar: every transformation is a typed stage in (P\to Q\to B\to C) (Ch17).
Deterministic navigation: RoutePlans as bounded hub rides with replay closure (Ch11, Ch19).
Truth typing and governance: OK/NEAR/AMBIG/FAIL as routable outcomes with mandatory artifacts (Ch08, AppI–AppL).
Conflict discipline: reproducible contradictions become conflict packets and fences (AppK).
Time evolution without rewrite: append-only DeltaPacks and promotion scheduling (Ch20).
Publication/import closure: export bundles, import verifiers, governance gates (AppO), with container doctrine (AppN).
Deployment conformance: production acceptance is defined by replayable suites and audit closure (Ch21).
0.9 Reader contract: what “understanding” means in HD-SCT
A statement is considered usable only if it is routable to:
an explicit address,
an explicit set of pinned policies (no hidden knobs),
an explicit witness surface (replay capsules, receipts, ledgers, evidence plans),
a truth type (OK/NEAR/AMBIG/FAIL),
and (where required) an import-verifiable certificate chain.
If any of these are absent, the correct output is not prose confidence; it is AMBIG (bounded plan) or FAIL/CONFLICT (fenced contradiction).
HD-SCT — Title / Abstract / Corpus Metro Map
Ch01 — Axioms + Lock Laws
Higher-Dimensional □○△: Carriers, Projections, Wraps, and Lift Commutation
01.1 Square — Discrete Carrier □ (Address-Capacity)
01.1.1 Carrier Axioms (□-Carrier)
01.1.1.1 Digit alphabet, depth, and axis set
Let (\mathbb{D}4 := {0,1,2,3}).Let (d\in\mathbb{N}{\ge 1}) denote dimension (axis count) and (k\in\mathbb{N}_{\ge 1}) denote depth (base-4 resolution level).
Define the axis index set ([d] := {1,2,\dots,d}) and the digit index set ([k] := {1,2,\dots,k}).
01.1.1.2 Square carrier as a base-4 fractional address space
Define the depth-(k) Square carrier in dimension (d) as the set of digit-tensors[\mathcal{S}{d,k} ;:=; \big(\mathbb{D}4^{,k}\big)^{d};=;\Big{,\mathbf{x}=(x_i){i\in[d]}:; x_i=(x_i^{(t)}){t\in[k]},\ x_i^{(t)}\in\mathbb{D}_4,\Big}.]Each axis (i) carries a base-4 fractional digit string (x_i^{(1)}x_i^{(2)}\cdots x_i^{(k)}) (digits “after the radix point”).
Define the associated rational coordinate (base-4 fraction)[\phi_{4}(x_i);:=;\sum_{t=1}^{k} x_i^{(t)},4^{-t}\ \in\ \left{0,\frac{1}{4^k},\dots,\frac{4^k-1}{4^k}\right}\subset[0,1).]
Define the integer encoding[\mathrm{enc}{4,k}(x_i);:=;\sum{t=1}^{k} x_i^{(t)},4^{k-t}\ \in\ {0,1,\dots,4^k-1}.]Then[\phi_{4}(x_i);=;\frac{\mathrm{enc}{4,k}(x_i)}{4^k}.]For (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}), write (\mathrm{enc}{4,k}(\mathbf{x}) := (\mathrm{enc}{4,k}(x_i)){i\in[d]}\in(\mathbb{Z}{4^k})^d).
01.1.1.3 Cell interpretation (□ as a partition of the unit cube)
Define the depth-(k) hyper-cell associated to (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}) by[\mathrm{cell}{d,k}(\mathbf{x});:=;\prod_{i=1}^{d}\left[\phi_{4}(x_i),\ \phi_{4}(x_i)+4^{-k}\right);\subset;[0,1)^d.]Thus ([0,1)^d) is partitioned into (4^{kd}) disjoint half-open cells of side length (4^{-k}), indexed by (\mathcal{S}_{d,k}).
Define the canonical cell center representative[\mathrm{ctr}{d,k}(\mathbf{x});:=;\big(\phi{4}(x_i)+\tfrac12,4^{-k}\big)_{i=1}^d;\in;[0,1)^d.]
01.1.1.4 Truncation and refinement (depth morphisms)
Define prefix truncation (\pi_{k\to j}:\mathcal{S}{d,k}\to\mathcal{S}{d,j}) for (1\le j\le k) by[\pi_{k\to j}(\mathbf{x})i^{(t)} := x_i^{(t)}\quad (t\in[j]).]Define suffix refinement (digit extension) (\iota{k\to k+m}:\mathcal{S}{d,k}\times(\mathbb{D}4^{,m})^{d}\to\mathcal{S}{d,k+m}) for (m\ge 1) by[\iota{k\to k+m}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})i^{(t)} :=\begin{cases}x_i^{(t)}, & t\in[k],\s_i^{(t-k)}, & t\in{k+1,\dots,k+m},\end{cases}]where (\mathbf{s}=(s_i){i\in[d]}) and (s_i\in\mathbb{D}_4^{,m}).
These satisfy the projective identities:[\pi_{k+m\to k}\circ \iota_{k\to k+m}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})=\mathbf{x},\qquad\pi_{k\to j}\circ\pi_{k+m\to k}=\pi_{k+m\to j}.]
01.1.2 Algebra and Metrics (□-Structure)
01.1.2.1 Finite ring model and coordinatewise arithmetic
Via integer encoding, (\mathcal{S}{d,k}) is identified with ((\mathbb{Z}{4^k})^d) (componentwise addition/multiplication mod (4^k)). When used, arithmetic is performed in ((\mathbb{Z}{4^k})^d) and transported back to digits by (\mathrm{dec}{4,k}) (the inverse digit map).
01.1.2.2 Digitwise concatenation as a semidirect product operation
Refinement by appending digits corresponds in integer encoding to[\mathrm{enc}{4,k+m}\big(\iota{k\to k+m}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})\big);=;4^{m},\mathrm{enc}{4,k}(\mathbf{x});+;\mathrm{enc}{4,m}(\mathbf{s}),]computed componentwise.
01.1.2.3 Canonical ultrametric (depth-agreement metric)
Define the depth-agreement index between (\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}) by[\lambda(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y});:=;\max\Big{,j\in{0,1,\dots,k}:\ \pi{k\to j}(\mathbf{x})=\pi_{k\to j}(\mathbf{y}),\Big}.]Define the ultrametric[d_{\square,k}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y});:=;4^{-\lambda(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y})}.]Then (d_{\square,k}) is an ultrametric on (\mathcal{S}{d,k}) and satisfies compatibility under truncation:[d{\square,j}\big(\pi_{k\to j}(\mathbf{x}),\pi_{k\to j}(\mathbf{y})\big)\ \le\ d_{\square,k}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y}).]
01.1.2.4 Cell containment and truncation
For (1\le j\le k),[\mathrm{cell}{d,k}(\mathbf{x})\subset \mathrm{cell}{d,j}(\pi_{k\to j}(\mathbf{x})).]Moreover (\mathrm{cell}_{d,j}(\mathbf{u})) is exactly the disjoint union of the (4^{(k-j)d}) depth-(k) cells refining it.
01.1.3 Canonical Maps (□-Operators)
01.1.3.1 Square-to-cube embedding (representative selection)
Define the family of representative maps (\mathrm{rep}^{(\beta)}{d,k}:\mathcal{S}{d,k}\to[0,1)^d) for (\beta\in[0,1]) by[\mathrm{rep}^{(\beta)}{d,k}(\mathbf{x});:=;\big(\phi_4(x_i)+\beta,4^{-k}\big){i=1}^d.]Canonical choices:
left-edge representative: (\beta=0),
center representative: (\beta=\tfrac12).
01.1.3.2 Cube-to-Square quantization (depth-(k) digit extraction)
Define the depth-(k) quantizer (\mathrm{q}{d,k}:[0,1)^d\to\mathcal{S}{d,k}) by, for each axis (i),[\mathrm{enc}{4,k}\big(\mathrm{q}{d,k}(\mathbf{u})i\big);:=;\left\lfloor 4^k,u_i\right\rfloor.]Then (\mathbf{u}\in \mathrm{cell}{d,k}(\mathrm{q}_{d,k}(\mathbf{u}))).
01.1.3.3 Square-to-Circle projection (□→○, depth-(k))
Define the depth-(k) square phase vector[\Phi_{\square,k}(\mathbf{x});:=;\big(\phi_4(x_1),\dots,\phi_4(x_d)\big)\in[0,1)^d.]This vector becomes a torus element under the canonical quotient ([0,1)\to\mathbb{R}/\mathbb{Z}). The torus form is defined in §01.2.
01.1.3.4 Resolution consistency of representatives
For (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}), (\mathbf{s}\in(\mathbb{D}4)^d), let (\mathbf{x}^+ := \iota{k\to k+1}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})). Then[\mathrm{rep}^{(\beta)}{d,k+1}(\mathbf{x}^+);=;\mathrm{rep}^{(\beta)}{d,k}(\mathbf{x});+;\big(s_i-\beta\big){i=1}^d,4^{-(k+1)}.]In particular, truncation recovers coarse cells:[\pi_{k+1\to k}(\mathbf{x}^+)=\mathbf{x}\quad\Longrightarrow\quad\mathrm{cell}{d,k+1}(\mathbf{x}^+)\subset \mathrm{cell}{d,k}(\mathbf{x}).]
01.1.4 Lock Laws (□-Lifts)
01.1.4.1 Lock Law I (Resolution lift, □)
Define the resolution lift (depth lift) operator[\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d,k}:\mathcal{S}{d,k}\times(\mathbb{D}4)^d\to\mathcal{S}{d,k+1},\qquad\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s}) := \iota{k\to k+1}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s}).]Coherence axiom:[\pi_{k+1\to k}\big(\mathcal{L}^{\square}_{d,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})\big)=\mathbf{x}.]
01.1.4.2 Lock Law II (Dimension lift, □)
Define the dimension lift operator[\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d\to d+1,k}:\mathcal{S}{d,k}\times(\mathbb{D}4)^{d+1}\to\mathcal{S}{d+1,k+1}]by[\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d\to d+1,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s},\eta);:=;\big(\iota{k\to k+1}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s}),\ \eta\big),]where (\mathbf{s}\in(\mathbb{D}_4)^d) refines existing axes and (\eta\in\mathbb{D}_4) is the new axis digit at level (k+1) (with no prior digits). Equivalently, the new axis is initialized as a length-((k+1)) digit string with first (k) digits (0) and ((k+1))-st digit (\eta).
Coherence axiom:[\pi^{\mathrm{axes}}{d+1\to d}\circ \pi{k+1\to k}\big(\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d\to d+1,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s},\eta)\big)=\mathbf{x},]where (\pi^{\mathrm{axes}}{d+1\to d}) deletes the ((d+1))-st axis.
01.1.4.3 Lift nesting and cell containment
For any (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}) and any refinement digits, both lift laws preserve nesting:[\mathrm{cell}{d,k+1}\big(\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})\big)\subset \mathrm{cell}{d,k}(\mathbf{x}),][\mathrm{cell}{d+1,k+1}\big(\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d\to d+1,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s},\eta)\big)\subset\mathrm{cell}_{d,k}(\mathbf{x})\times[0,1).]
01.1.4.4 Holographic prefix lemma (□)
Let (k_1<k_2). For any (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k_1}) and any digit tensor (\mathbf{s}\in(\mathbb{D}4^{,k_2-k_1})^{d}),[\pi{k_2\to k_1}\big(\iota{k_1\to k_2}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})\big)=\mathbf{x}.]Thus each depth-(k_1) address is a complete holographic prefix of any refinement to greater depth.
01.2 Flower — Continuous Carrier ○ (Phase-Capacity)
01.2.1 Carrier Axioms (○-Carrier)
01.2.1.1 The (d)-torus as the circle carrier
Define the (d)-torus[\mathbb{T}^d;:=;(\mathbb{R}/\mathbb{Z})^d.]Elements are phase vectors (\Phi=(\phi_1,\dots,\phi_d)), (\phi_i\in\mathbb{R}/\mathbb{Z}). Representatives may be taken in ([0,1)).
01.2.1.2 Angle coordinates and phase multiplication
Define the angle map (\mathrm{ang}:\mathbb{R}/\mathbb{Z}\to\mathbb{R}/2\pi\mathbb{Z}) by[\mathrm{ang}(\phi)=2\pi\phi.]Phase multiplication by an integer (m\in\mathbb{Z}) is defined by[[m]:\mathbb{T}^d\to\mathbb{T}^d,\qquadm:=(m\phi_1,\dots,m\phi_d)\ \ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1).]
01.2.1.3 Wrap function (octave index)
Define the wrap function (R:\mathbb{N}{\ge 1}\to\mathbb{N}{\ge 1}) by[R(1)=1,\qquad R(k+1)=3,R(k).]Hence (R(k)=3^{k-1}).
Define the depth-(k) wrapped angle representation of (\Phi\in\mathbb{T}^d) by[\Theta^{(k)}(\Phi);:=;\mathrm{ang}!\big(R(k)\big)\ \in\ (\mathbb{R}/2\pi\mathbb{Z})^d.]
01.2.1.4 Triangle phase index as a 3-sheeted torsion parameter
Let the triangle index be[\tau\in\mathbb{Z}3={0,1,2}.]Define the triangle torsion shift on (\mathbb{T}^d) by[\Delta{\tau}(\Phi);:=;\Phi;+;\frac{\tau}{3},\mathbf{1}_d\qquad(\mathrm{mod}\ 1),]where (\mathbf{1}_d=(1,\dots,1)). (Axis-wise triangle modes ((\mathbb{Z}_3)^d) replace (\tau,\mathbf{1}_d) with a coordinate vector; the global form above is the canonical carrier in Ch01.)
Define the triangle-augmented wrapped angles:[\Theta^{(k,\tau)}(\Phi);:=;\Theta^{(k)}\big(\Delta_{\tau}(\Phi)\big).]
01.2.2 Group Actions and Harmonic Structure (○-Structure)
01.2.2.1 Translation action (gear steps on the torus)
For any translation vector (\alpha\in\mathbb{T}^d), define[T_{\alpha}(\Phi):=\Phi+\alpha\quad(\mathrm{mod}\ 1).]This defines a transitive group action of (\mathbb{T}^d) on itself. Discrete gear steps correspond to (\alpha) lying in rational lattices.
01.2.2.2 Character group and Fourier modes
The Pontryagin dual of (\mathbb{T}^d) is (\mathbb{Z}^d). For (n\in\mathbb{Z}^d), define the character[\chi_n(\Phi):=\exp!\big(2\pi i,\langle n,\Phi\rangle\big),\qquad\langle n,\Phi\rangle=\sum_{i=1}^d n_i\phi_i.]These modes form an orthonormal basis for (L^2(\mathbb{T}^d)).
01.2.2.3 Resonant fractions as phase invariants
Define the rational lattice at depth (k)[\Lambda_{d,k}:=\left(\frac{1}{4^k}\mathbb{Z}/\mathbb{Z}\right)^d\subset\mathbb{T}^d.]Elements of (\Lambda_{d,k}) are exactly the torus phases representable by base-4 digit strings of length (k). This is the invariant image of (\mathcal{S}{d,k}) under the canonical projection (\Pi{\square\to\circ,k}) defined below.
01.2.2.4 Compatibility of wraps with phase multiplication
For any (\Phi\in\mathbb{T}^d),[\Theta^{(k+1)}(\Phi)=\mathrm{ang}!\big(3R(k)\big)=\mathrm{ang}!\big([3]\circR(k)\big).]Thus wrap lifting is equivalent to applying the degree-3 covering ([3]) to the depth-(k) wrapped phase.
01.2.3 Canonical Operators (○-Operators)
01.2.3.1 Wrap-lift operator (○)
Define the wrap-lift between depth representations by the map on wrapped angles:[\mathcal{W}{k\to k+1}:\ (\mathbb{R}/2\pi\mathbb{Z})^d\to(\mathbb{R}/2\pi\mathbb{Z})^d,\qquad\mathcal{W}{k\to k+1}(\Theta):=3,]i.e. componentwise multiplication by (3) mod (2\pi). This is the representation-level form of (R(k+1)=3R(k)).
01.2.3.2 Triangle shift operator (△ acting on ○)
Define the triangle shift on torus phases as (\Delta_\tau) (§01.2.1.4). Its wrapped representation satisfies[\Theta^{(k,\tau)}(\Phi)=\Theta^{(k)}(\Phi)+2\pi,R(k),\frac{\tau}{3},\mathbf{1}_d\quad(\mathrm{mod}\ 2\pi).]
01.2.3.3 Canonical projection (\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k}) and its quantized left inverse
Define the depth-(k) projection[\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k}:\mathcal{S}{d,k}\to\mathbb{T}^d,\qquad\Pi{\square\to\circ,k}(\mathbf{x});:=;\big(\phi_4(x_1),\dots,\phi_4(x_d)\big)\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1).]
Define the depth-(k) quantized left inverse (digit extractor)[Q_{\circ\to\square,k}:\mathbb{T}^d\to\mathcal{S}{d,k}]by[\mathrm{enc}{4,k}\big(Q_{\circ\to\square,k}(\Phi)i\big);:=;\left\lfloor 4^k,\phi_i\right\rfloor\quad\text{for representatives }\phi_i\in[0,1).]Then, for all (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}),[Q_{\circ\to\square,k}\big(\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k}(\mathbf{x})\big)=\mathbf{x}.]
01.2.3.4 Lift-commuting diagram (projection vs truncation)
Let (1\le j\le k). Then the projection satisfies the truncation commutation:[\Pi_{\square\to\circ,j}\circ \pi_{k\to j};=;\pi^{\circ}{k\to j}\circ \Pi{\square\to\circ,k},]where (\pi^{\circ}{k\to j}:\Lambda{d,k}\to\Lambda_{d,j}) is the torus quantization map induced by discarding base-4 digits beyond depth (j), equivalently[\pi^{\circ}{k\to j}(\Phi)\ :=\ \Pi{\square\to\circ,j}\Big(Q_{\circ\to\square,j}(\Phi)\Big),\qquad \Phi\in\Lambda_{d,k}.]
01.2.4 Lock Laws (○-Lifts)
01.2.4.1 Lock Law I (Resolution lift, ○)
Let (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}) and (\mathbf{x}^+=\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})\in\mathcal{S}{d,k+1}). Then[\pi^{\circ}{k+1\to k}\big(\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k+1}(\mathbf{x}^+)\big);=;\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k}(\mathbf{x}).]Equivalently: coarse torus phase is invariant under square refinement.
01.2.4.2 Lock Law II (Dimension lift, ○)
Let (\mathbf{x}^{\uparrow}=\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d\to d+1,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s},\eta)\in\mathcal{S}{d+1,k+1}). Then[\pi^{\circ,\mathrm{axes}}{d+1\to d}\circ \pi^{\circ}{k+1\to k}\big(\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k+1}(\mathbf{x}^{\uparrow})\big);=;\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k}(\mathbf{x}),]where (\pi^{\circ,\mathrm{axes}}_{d+1\to d}) deletes the ((d+1))-st phase coordinate. Thus the existing (d) phases remain invariant in the coarse sense under dimension lift, and the new axis contributes an additional phase coordinate at depth (k+1).
01.2.4.3 Wrapped representation lock (asymptotic commutation)
Define the unwrapped coordinate at depth (k) for (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}) as[U_k(\mathbf{x});:=;[R(k)]\big(\Pi{\square\to\circ,k}(\mathbf{x})\big)\in\mathbb{T}^d.]Then for any refinement (\mathbf{x}^+=\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})),[U{k+1}(\mathbf{x}^+);=;[3]\big(U_k(\mathbf{x})\big);+;\delta_{k}(\mathbf{s}),]where (\delta_k(\mathbf{s})\in\mathbb{T}^d) satisfies the explicit bound (in ([0,1)) representatives)[|\delta_k(\mathbf{s})|_{\infty}\ \le\ 3^k,4^{-(k+1)}\cdot 3;=;3\left(\frac{3}{4}\right)^{k+1}.]Thus the wrap lift approaches exact commutation with the degree-3 covering as (k\to\infty).
01.2.4.4 Triangle compatibility under lifts
Triangle torsion commutes with projection and coarse truncation:[\Delta_{\tau}\circ \Pi_{\square\to\circ,k} ;=; \Pi_{\square\to\circ,k}\quad\text{followed by}\quad +\tfrac{\tau}{3}\mathbf{1}d,]and for any (j\le k),[\pi^{\circ}{k\to j}\big(\Delta_{\tau}(\Phi)\big)=\Delta_{\tau}\big(\pi^{\circ}_{k\to j}(\Phi)\big).]Thus triangle torsion is a depth-stable phase offset.
01.3 Cloud — Measure Carrier (Ensemble-Capacity)
01.3.1 Carrier Axioms (Σ-Carrier)
01.3.1.1 Distributions on Square and Circle
Let (\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k})) denote the probability simplex over the finite set (\mathcal{S}{d,k}).Let (\mathcal{P}(\mathbb{T}^d)) denote the set of Borel probability measures on (\mathbb{T}^d).
01.3.1.2 Pushforward under projection
For a measurable map (f:X\to Y) and a measure (\mu\in\mathcal{P}(X)), define the pushforward (f_#\mu\in\mathcal{P}(Y)) by[(f_#\mu)(A);:=;\mu(f^{-1}(A)).]In particular, ((\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k})#:\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k})\to\mathcal{P}(\mathbb{T}^d)) is well-defined.
01.3.1.3 Coarse-graining by truncation
Define the coarse-graining map on distributions induced by truncation:[(\pi_{k\to j})#:\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k})\to\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}_{d,j}).]This is the canonical depth-(j) marginal of a depth-(k) distribution.
01.3.1.4 Kolmogorov consistency (projective family axiom)
A family ({\mu_k}{k\ge 1}) with (\mu_k\in\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k})) is depth-consistent if for all (j\le k),[(\pi_{k\to j})_#\mu_k = \mu_j.]
01.3.2 Channels and Kernels (Σ-Structure)
01.3.2.1 Markov kernels on (\mathcal{S}_{d,k}) and (\mathbb{T}^d)
A Markov kernel (K) on a measurable space (X) is a map (x\mapsto K(x,\cdot)\in\mathcal{P}(X)).Kernel composition defines a semigroup under the usual convolution.
01.3.2.2 Compatibility of kernels with coarse-graining
A kernel (K_k) on (\mathcal{S}{d,k}) is depth-compatible if for all (j\le k),[(\pi{k\to j})#\big(\mu K_k\big);=;\big((\pi{k\to j})#\mu\big)K_j\quad\text{for all }\mu\in\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k}),]for some kernel (K_j) on (\mathcal{S}_{d,j}).
01.3.2.3 Pushforward of kernels under (\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k})
Given a kernel (K_k) on (\mathcal{S}{d,k}), define the induced channel on (\mathbb{T}^d) by[\mathcal{K}k(\Phi,\cdot);:=;(\Pi{\square\to\circ,k})#\Big(K_k\big(Q_{\circ\to\square,k}(\Phi),\cdot\big)\Big).]This induced channel is canonical on the lattice (\Lambda_{d,k}\subset\mathbb{T}^d).
01.3.2.4 Triangle torsion as a measure-preserving translation
For any (\nu\in\mathcal{P}(\mathbb{T}^d)), define ((\Delta_\tau)#\nu). Since (\Delta\tau) is a group translation, it preserves Haar measure and transports any measure by translation.
01.3.3 Canonical Operators (Σ-Operators)
01.3.3.1 Depth lift of measures by refinement expansion
Define the refinement expansion operator (\mathrm{Ref}{k\to k+1}) on measures by selecting a refinement kernel (J{k}) from (\mathcal{S}{d,k}) to (\mathcal{S}{d,k+1}) satisfying ((\pi_{k+1\to k})#(\mu J_k)=\mu). Then define[\mu^{+}:=\mu J_k\in\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k+1})]as a lifted ensemble consistent with coarse-graining.
01.3.3.2 Dimension lift of measures by product extension
Let (\rho\in\mathcal{P}(\mathbb{D}4)) be a law for the new axis digit. Define the dimension-lifted measure on (\mathcal{S}{d+1,k+1}) by[\mu^{\uparrow}:=(\mu J_k)\otimes \rho]under the identification (\mathcal{S}{d+1,k+1}\cong \mathcal{S}{d,k+1}\times \mathbb{D}_4) (new axis initialized as in §01.1.4.2).
01.3.3.3 Projection-lifted measures on the torus
Define[\nu_k := (\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k})_#\mu_k\in\mathcal{P}(\mathbb{T}^d).]Then ({\nu_k}) is the phase-space representation of the ensemble family ({\mu_k}).
01.3.3.4 Depth-(k) entropy functional (finite carrier)
For (\mu\in\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k})), define the Shannon entropy[H_k(\mu):=-\sum{\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}}\mu(\mathbf{x})\log \mu(\mathbf{x}).]This functional is compatible with coarse-graining in the standard sense (H_j((\pi{k\to j})_#\mu)\le H_k(\mu)).
01.3.4 Lock Laws (Σ-Lifts)
01.3.4.1 Lock Law I (Resolution lift, Σ)
A lifted measure (\mu^+\in\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k+1})) is resolution-locked to (\mu\in\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k})) iff[(\pi_{k+1\to k})_#\mu^+=\mu.]
01.3.4.2 Lock Law II (Dimension lift, Σ)
A dimension-lifted measure (\mu^\uparrow\in\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d+1,k+1})) is dimension-locked to (\mu\in\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{S}{d,k})) iff[(\pi^{\mathrm{axes}}{d+1\to d}\circ \pi{k+1\to k})_#\mu^\uparrow = \mu.]
01.3.4.3 Projection commutation on ensembles
For any depth-consistent family ({\mu_k}),[\pi^{\circ}{k\to j}_#\big((\Pi{\square\to\circ,k})#\mu_k\big);=;(\Pi{\square\to\circ,j})#\big((\pi{k\to j})#\mu_k\big)]for all (j\le k), where (\pi^{\circ}{k\to j}) is the torus digit-discarding map in §01.2.3.4, and (\pi^{\circ}_{k\to j}_#) its pushforward on measures.
01.3.4.4 Triangle stability on ensembles
For any (\nu\in\mathcal{P}(\mathbb{T}^d)),[(\Delta_\tau)#\big(\pi^{\circ}{k\to j}_#\nu\big);=;\pi^{\circ}{k\to j}_#\big((\Delta\tau)_#\nu\big),]i.e. triangle torsion is compatible with depth coarse-graining on phase measures.
01.4 Fractal — Multiscale Carrier (Projective-Limit Capacity)
01.4.1 Scale Lattice (Ψ-Carrier)
01.4.1.1 The depth tower as a projective system
Fix (d). The family ({\mathcal{S}{d,k}}{k\ge 1}) with truncation morphisms (\pi_{k+1\to k}) forms a projective (inverse) system:[\mathcal{S}{d,1}\ \xleftarrow{\pi{2\to 1}}\ \mathcal{S}{d,2}\ \xleftarrow{\pi{3\to 2}}\ \cdots]Define its inverse limit[\mathcal{S}{d,\infty};:=;\varprojlim{k}\mathcal{S}{d,k}]as the set of compatible infinite digit tensors ((\mathbf{x}^{(k)}){k\ge 1}) satisfying (\pi_{k+1\to k}(\mathbf{x}^{(k+1)})=\mathbf{x}^{(k)}).
01.4.1.2 Identification with base-4 solenoidal digits (4-adic-like structure)
Each axis in (\mathcal{S}{d,\infty}) is an infinite base-4 digit string; coordinatewise, (\mathcal{S}{d,\infty}) is the compact totally disconnected space of 4-ary Cantor-type expansions equipped with the ultrametric induced by prefix agreement.
01.4.1.3 The wrap tower on the torus
The wrap maps ([3]:\mathbb{T}^d\to\mathbb{T}^d) form a projective system[\mathbb{T}^d\ \xleftarrow{[3]}\ \mathbb{T}^d\ \xleftarrow{[3]}\ \cdots]Define the inverse limit[\mathbb{T}^d_{(3)};:=;\varprojlim_{k}(\mathbb{T}^d,[3])](the (d)-dimensional 3-adic solenoid), consisting of compatible wrapped phases ((\Phi^{(k)})_{k\ge 1}) with (3=\Phi^{(k)}).
01.4.1.4 The mixed-radix HD-lock index
The HD-SCT scaling index is the paired tower[k:\quad \mathcal{S}_{d,k}\ \text{(base-4 refinement)}\quad\text{and}\quad R(k)=3^{k-1}\ \text{(base-3 wrap refinement)}.]The lock laws constrain all admissible evolution to respect this coupled scaling.
01.4.2 Renormalization and Consistency (Ψ-Structure)
01.4.2.1 Coarse-to-fine and fine-to-coarse operators
Define:
coarse operator: truncation (\pi_{k+1\to k}) on (\mathcal{S}),
coarse operator: ([3]) on (\mathbb{T}^d) (wrap collapse),
fine operator: digit refinement (\iota_{k\to k+1}) on (\mathcal{S}),
fine operator: section choice of ([3]) (wrap lift) on (\mathbb{T}^d) at the representation level (angles).
01.4.2.2 Fractal invariants as inverse-limit coordinates
An invariant at infinite depth is a function (I:\mathcal{S}{d,\infty}\to\mathcal{Y}) depending only on compatible prefixes. Finite-depth invariants (I_k:\mathcal{S}{d,k}\to\mathcal{Y}) are consistent iff[I_k\circ \pi_{k+1\to k}=I_{k+1}^{\downarrow}]for the appropriate restriction (I_{k+1}^{\downarrow}) (prefix dependence).
01.4.2.3 Dimension lift as tower embedding
Define the dimension-lift embedding between inverse limits by extending axes and depth consistently:[\mathcal{S}{d,\infty}\hookrightarrow \mathcal{S}{d+1,\infty},]implemented by appending a new axis digit stream (initialized per policy) and extending depth by one digit at the first lift step.
01.4.2.4 Triangle torsion as a stable fiber over the tower
Triangle torsion (\tau\in\mathbb{Z}3) is depth-stable (§01.2.4.4) and thus defines a constant fiber over the inverse limits:[(\mathcal{S}{d,\infty}\times \mathbb{T}^d_{(3)})\times \mathbb{Z}_3.]
01.4.3 Algorithms (Ψ-Operators: Computable Spec)
01.4.3.1 Deterministic digit encoding/decoding (base-4)
Algorithm 01.4.A — EncodeDigits4Input: digit vector (x^{(1)},\dots,x^{(k)}\in\mathbb{D}_4).Output: integer (m\in{0,\dots,4^k-1}).Rule:[m\leftarrow 0;\quad\text{for }t=1\text{ to }k:\ m\leftarrow 4m+x^{(t)}.]
Algorithm 01.4.B — DecodeDigits4Input: integer (m\in{0,\dots,4^k-1}).Output: digits (x^{(1)},\dots,x^{(k)}\in\mathbb{D}_4).Rule: for (t=k) down to (1): (x^{(t)}\leftarrow m\bmod 4); (m\leftarrow \lfloor m/4\rfloor).
01.4.3.2 Projection and quantization (□↔○)
Algorithm 01.4.C — ProjectSquareToTorusInput: (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}).Output: (\Phi\in\Lambda{d,k}\subset\mathbb{T}^d).Rule: (\phi_i\leftarrow \sum_{t=1}^k x_i^{(t)}4^{-t}) (mod 1).
Algorithm 01.4.D — QuantizeTorusToSquareInput: (\Phi\in\mathbb{T}^d) (representatives (\phi_i\in[0,1))).Output: (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}_{d,k}).Rule: (m_i\leftarrow \lfloor 4^k\phi_i\rfloor); decode (m_i) to digits.
Correctness: (Q_{\circ\to\square,k}\circ \Pi_{\square\to\circ,k}=\mathrm{id}{\mathcal{S}{d,k}}).
01.4.3.3 Lift operators (resolution and dimension)
Algorithm 01.4.E — ResolutionLiftSquareInput: (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}_{d,k}), refinement digits (\mathbf{s}\in(\mathbb{D}4)^d).Output: (\mathbf{x}^+\in\mathcal{S}{d,k+1}).Rule: append (s_i) as digit (x_i^{(k+1)}\leftarrow s_i).
Algorithm 01.4.F — DimensionLiftSquareInput: (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}_{d,k}), refinement digits (\mathbf{s}\in(\mathbb{D}_4)^d), new digit (\eta\in\mathbb{D}4).Output: (\mathbf{x}^{\uparrow}\in\mathcal{S}{d+1,k+1}).Rule: compute (\mathbf{x}^+=\mathrm{ResolutionLiftSquare}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{s})); add axis (d+1) with digits (0,\dots,0,\eta).
01.4.3.4 Verification harness (lock-law checks)
Given (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}_{d,k}), (\mathbf{s}\in(\mathbb{D}4)^d), define (\mathbf{x}^+=\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d,k}(\mathbf{x};\mathbf{s})). The lock law check set is:
(\pi_{k+1\to k}(\mathbf{x}^+)=\mathbf{x}).
(\pi^{\circ}{k+1\to k}\big(\Pi{\square\to\circ,k+1}(\mathbf{x}^+)\big)=\Pi_{\square\to\circ,k}(\mathbf{x})).
For dimension lift (\mathbf{x}^{\uparrow}), existing axes are preserved by combined truncation and axis deletion in both □ and ○ spaces.
01.4.4 Lock Laws (Ψ-Global Closure)
01.4.4.1 Projective closure axiom (□ tower)
The depth tower ({\mathcal{S}{d,k},\pi{k+1\to k}}) is required to be projective: truncation must be surjective and consistent, yielding the inverse limit (\mathcal{S}_{d,\infty}).
01.4.4.2 Projective closure axiom (○ wrap tower)
The wrap tower ({\mathbb{T}^d,[3]}) is required to be projective: ([3]) is surjective, yielding the inverse limit (\mathbb{T}^d_{(3)}).
01.4.4.3 Mixed lock law (coupled refinement)
Admissible refinement steps are constrained to the coupled update:[k\mapsto k+1 \quad\text{with}\quad \text{Square refinement by one base-4 digit}\quad\text{and}\quad \text{Circle wrap refinement by factor }3.]All cross-space operators must respect this coupled index (no independent refinement of one carrier without the other).
01.4.4.4 HD-SCT state primitive (minimal)
The minimal higher-D □○△ state primitive at depth (k) is the tuple[\Psi_{d,k};:=;\big(\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k},\ \Phi=\Pi{\square\to\circ,k}(\mathbf{x})\in\mathbb{T}^d,\ \tau\in\mathbb{Z}_3\big),]with the wrapped representation derived as (\Theta^{(k,\tau)}(\Phi)). Resolution and dimension lifts act by the lock laws in §§01.1.4 and 01.2.4, with triangle torsion stable under depth truncation.
Ch01 — Axioms + Lock Laws
Ch02 — Dimension–Depth Lock and Minimal Stable Scales
Formalization of the Minimal Seed Law (k_{\min}(d)=d-1), Per-Axis Minimum (4^{d-1}), and the Locked Lift ((d,k)\mapsto(d+1,k+1))
□ Square — Discrete Carrier Stability (Address-Capacity)
02.S1 — Ontology (Objects)
02.S1.a — Minimal Seed Index and Per-Axis Minimum
Definition (Minimal seed index).For each dimension (d\in\mathbb{N}{\ge 2}), define the minimal stable depth[k{\min}(d);:=;d-1.]Define the minimal stable seed at dimension (d) as the pair ((d,k_{\min}(d))=(d,d-1)).
Define the minimal stable per-axis resolution[N_{\min}(d);:=;4^{k_{\min}(d)};=;4^{d-1}.]
Define the minimal stable Square carrier as[\mathcal{S}^{\min}d ;:=;(\mathbb{Z}{N_{\min}(d)})^d ;\cong;(\mathbb{Z}_{4^{d-1}})^d.]
Claim ([AX]) (Per-axis minimum law).A dimension-(d) Square carrier is considered minimally stable only if its per-axis grid size satisfies[N ;\ge; 4^{d-1},]and the canonical minimal stable choice is (N=4^{d-1}).
Verification.The minimal stable seeds instantiate as:
(d=3:\ N_{\min}(3)=4^2=16\Rightarrow 16^3).
(d=4:\ N_{\min}(4)=4^3=64\Rightarrow 64^4).
(d=5:\ N_{\min}(5)=4^4=256\Rightarrow 256^5).In the operator-instantiated minimal seeds, the canonical ladder includes ((d=3,k=2)\Rightarrow 16^3) and ((d=4,k=3)\Rightarrow 64^4).
Falsifier (Failure mode class).A claimed “minimal” ((d,k)) with (k<d-1) is rejected as minimally stable if any of the following are observed under pinned profiles:(i) axis-extension requires implicit retyping of depth-dependent semantics (hidden knob),(ii) corridor proofs (projection/round-trip) cease to be reproducible under lift, or(iii) lens-rotations cease to commute with the declared lift schedule (holonomy defect exceeds corridor bounds).
02.S1.b — Digit Budget and State-Space Size at the Minimal Seed
Definition (Digit budget).At dimension (d) and depth (k), the Square carrier is[\mathcal{S}{d,k} := (\mathbb{Z}{4^k})^d \cong (\mathbb{Z}_4)^{dk}.]
Define the digit budget[B_{\square}(d,k);:=;dk.]At the minimal seed (k=d-1), the digit budget is[B_{\square}^{\min}(d);=;d(d-1).]
Define the state-space cardinality[|\mathcal{S}_{d,k}|=4^{dk},\qquad|\mathcal{S}^{\min}_d| = 4^{d(d-1)} = (4^{d-1})^d.]
Claim ([DER]) (Minimality expressed as saturation of the digit budget).The minimal seed condition (k=d-1) is equivalent to saturating the quadratic digit budget[B_{\square}(d,k);\ge;d(d-1)\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quadk;\ge;d-1,]with equality at minimal stability. This ties the minimal seed to the canonical growth in the number of independent axis–depth factors ((\mathbb{Z}_4)^{dk}).
Verification.For the explicit minimal seeds:
((d=3,k=2)\Rightarrow dk=6\Rightarrow (\mathbb{Z}_4)^6), reported as “3 axes × 2 digit levels.”
((d=4,k=3)\Rightarrow dk=12\Rightarrow (\mathbb{Z}_4)^{12}), reported as “4 axes × 3 digit levels.”
Falsifier.Any attempt to define a minimal seed with (dk<d(d-1)) that nevertheless claims full higher-dimensional phase-lock (i.e., declared commutation of lift/rotation and stable replay) must provide a constructive witness set that refutes the budget lower bound by explicit commuting lift maps and verified factorization identities; otherwise it is typed FAIL under the minimal-seed policy.
02.S1.c — Minimal Seed Ladder (Dimension-Indexed Canon)
Definition (Minimal seed ladder).Define the minimal seed ladder ({(d,k_{\min}(d))}_{d\ge 2}) by[(d,k);=;(2,1),(3,2),(4,3),(5,4),\dots,(d,d-1),\dots]with per-axis resolutions (4,16,64,256,\dots,4^{d-1},\dots)
Claim ([AX]) (Minimal seed lock across dimension).The minimal seed ladder is the canonically pinned cross-dimensional schedule, i.e., the 3D seed is ((3,2)) and the 4D seed is ((4,3)) under the declared requirement (k=d-1).
Verification.The explicit ladder anchors are instantiated as:
(2)D minimal seed: ((d=2,k=1)\Rightarrow 4\times 4).
(3)D minimal seed: ((d=3,k=2)\Rightarrow 16^3).
(4)D minimal seed: ((d=4,k=3)\Rightarrow 64^4).
Falsifier.If a proposed ladder increments dimension without the paired increment of depth while simultaneously claiming “minimal stability,” it contradicts the pinned minimal seed policy and is rejected unless a separate, explicitly named policy profile replaces the minimal-seed ladder.
02.S1.d — Stability Predicate (Square-Side)
Definition (Square stability predicate).Let (\mathcal{S}{d,k}) be the Square carrier and let (A{d,k}) denote the pinned constraint operator family on (\mathcal{S}{d,k}) (constructed from the fixed 4×4 seed constraints; §02.S2). Define the Square stability predicate:[\mathrm{Stable}{\square}(d,k);:=;\big(k\ge d-1\big)\ \wedge\ \mathrm{ReplayOK}(d,k)\ \wedge\ \mathrm{LiftCommuteOK}(d,k),]where (\mathrm{ReplayOK}) requires deterministic replay under pinned profiles, and (\mathrm{LiftCommuteOK}) requires that the declared lift relations for (A_{d,k}) hold exactly (as operator identities) at the algebra level.
Claim ([AX]) (Minimal stable ⇔ stable at (k=d-1) and no smaller).[(d,k)\ \text{minimally stable}\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad \mathrm{Stable}{\square}(d,k)\ \wedge\ \neg\mathrm{Stable}{\square}(d,k-1).]
Verification.The canonically pinned “minimal seed” statements explicitly require (k=d-1) as the cross-dimensional stability lock.
Falsifier.Any instance where lift identities fail to hold as equalities of operators (not merely approximate numerical matches) is classified as FAIL under this predicate.
02.S2 — Operators (Transforms)
02.S2.a — Resolution Lift on ((d,k))
Definition (Resolution lift).The Square resolution lift is the depth increment[(d,k)\ \mapsto\ (d,k+1).]At the operator level, the resolution lift is encoded by the Kronecker-sum additivity rule:[\boxed{A_{d,k+1} ;=; A_{d,k}\ \oplus\ A_{d,1}}]where (\oplus) is the Kronecker sum (defined in §02.S2.c) and (A_{d,1}) is the “one-digit-layer” contribution replicated across axes.
Claim ([AX]) (Resolution lift equals digit-layer addition).Resolution lift adds exactly one digit level per axis, and the corresponding constraint operator is a Kronecker-sum augmentation by a depth-1 block.
Verification.In the explicit 2D factorization, repeated depth lift yields[A_{2,k}=\underbrace{A_{2,1}\ \oplus\ \cdots\ \oplus\ A_{2,1}}_{k\ \text{times}},]stated as the exact operator factorization under the hologram lift.
Falsifier.If a purported “resolution lift” requires reparameterizing the seed constraints (changing the kernel) rather than adding a new digit-layer block under (\oplus), it is not a resolution lift; it is a MIGRATE.
02.S2.b — Axis Lift and the Locked Lift ((d,k)\mapsto(d+1,k+1))
Definition (Axis lift).An axis lift adds one dimension while holding depth fixed:[(d,k)\ \mapsto\ (d+1,k).]At the operator level, axis lift at fixed depth is encoded by[A_{d+1,k};=;A_{d,k}\ \oplus\ A_{1,k},]where (A_{1,k}) is the new-axis constraint block at depth (k).
Definition (Locked lift).The dimension–depth locked lift is the paired increment[\boxed{(d,k)\ \mapsto\ (d+1,k+1)}]implemented as “add an axis at depth (k+1)” together with the depth increment required by the minimal-seed ladder.
At the operator level the locked lift is encoded by:[\boxed{A_{d+1,k+1};=;A_{d,k+1}\ \oplus\ A_{1,k+1}}]
Claim ([AX]) (Locked lift is the canonical dimension increment rule).Dimension increases are implemented by an add-axis Kronecker-sum rule at the new depth level, i.e., axis addition occurs at depth (k+1) and preserves phase-lock by construction.
Verification.The “whole ladder in one line” is stated as the locked lift rule[A_{d+1,k+1} = A_{d,k+1}\oplus A_{1,k+1},]and the resolution lift is stated as[A_{d,k+1}=A_{d,k}\oplus A_{d,1}.]
Falsifier.Any lift schedule that increments (d) without incrementing (k) while simultaneously claiming minimal-seed compatibility violates the pinned minimal seed ladder and is rejected unless the manuscript explicitly switches profiles away from minimal stability.
02.S2.c — Kronecker Sum Algebra (Square-Side)
Definition (Kronecker sum).For square matrices (X\in\mathbb{R}^{m\times m}), (Y\in\mathbb{R}^{n\times n}), define the Kronecker sum:[X\oplus Y;:=;X\otimes I_n;+;I_m\otimes Y.]Iterated Kronecker sums are defined associatively.
Claim ([DER]) (Additivity of local constraint blocks).If (A_{d,k}) is constructed as a sum of local seed constraints acting independently on each axis-digit factor, then (A_{d,k}) is an iterated Kronecker sum of the same base operator (A_4) placed in each of the (dk) tensor slots:[A_{d,k};=;\bigoplus_{j=1}^{dk} A_4^{(j)}.]This is the operator-level rendering of “add an axis = add a Kronecker-sum component” and “add a digit = add a Kronecker-sum component.”
Verification.The Square carrier identification ((\mathbb{Z}_{4^k})^d\cong(\mathbb{Z}_4)^{dk}) and the add-axis rule are stated explicitly in the phase-locked lift construction.
Falsifier.If a proposed constraint operator family requires cross-slot coupling terms that cannot be expressed as an iterated Kronecker sum under pinned kernels, then the lift laws in §02.S2 cannot hold as identities.
02.S2.d — Dimensional Phase-Lock Identity (Operator Form)
Definition (Dimensional phase-lock identity).For the minimal seed ladder and its operator family ({A_{d,k}}), define the dimensional phase-lock identity as the family of exact decompositions:[A_{d+1,k};=;A_{d,k}\ \oplus\ A_{1,k}\quad\text{(axis addition at fixed depth)},]and, for the locked lift,[A_{d+1,k+1};=;A_{d,k+1}\ \oplus\ A_{1,k+1}.]
Claim ([AX]) (Minimal seed lock across dimension is add-axis + add-depth).The minimal seed transition ((d,d-1)\mapsto(d+1,d)) is realized as “add an axis + add a digit depth,” encoded by a nested Kronecker-sum composition of the appropriate axis blocks.
Verification.The “minimal seed lock across dimension” is written concretely as a combined composition for the 3D→4D transition, described as “add axis + add digit depth.”
Falsifier.If the operator family for minimal seeds cannot be expressed as a sequence of add-axis and add-depth Kronecker-sum steps without modifying the seed constraints, the phase-lock identity fails.
02.S3 — Invariants (What Stays)
02.S3.a — Prefix/Nesting Invariance Under the Locked Lift
Definition (Nested address invariance).Let (\mathcal{S}{d,k}) be represented as digit tensors with truncation (\pi{k+1\to k}) and axis deletion (\pi^{\mathrm{axes}}{d+1\to d}) (as in Ch01). A locked lift state constructor (\mathcal{L}^{\square}{d,k}:\mathcal{S}{d,k}\to\mathcal{S}{d+1,k+1}) must satisfy:[\pi^{\mathrm{axes}}{d+1\to d}\circ \pi{k+1\to k}\big(\mathcal{L}^{\square}_{d,k}(\mathbf{x})\big)=\mathbf{x}.]
Claim ([AX]) (Locked lift preserves parent address as a holographic prefix).The locked lift may refine representation, but it must preserve the parent state as the unique coarse truncation (no ambiguity unless explicitly typed). This is the Square-side instance of the “phase-locked” lift discipline.
Verification.The phase-lock lift is characterized as “add axis + add digit depth,” with the operator lift preserving the decomposition structure exactly.
Falsifier.Any lift that cannot be truncated back to the parent without auxiliary, non-derivable choices is classified as illegal recursion (hidden knob).
02.S3.b — Spectral Additivity (Flower Consequence of Square Lock)
Definition (Spectral additivity under Kronecker sums).If (A=X\oplus Y), then the spectrum satisfies[\mathrm{spec}(A)={,\lambda_X+\lambda_Y:\ \lambda_X\in\mathrm{spec}(X),\ \lambda_Y\in\mathrm{spec}(Y),},]and eigenvectors tensorize correspondingly.
Claim ([AX]) (Square locked lift implies spectral tensorization).Under the Kronecker-sum lift structure, eigenvectors tensorize and eigenvalues add; thus dimension lift and resolution lift are dual renderings in the Square basis vs the Flower basis.
Verification.The exact statement “eigenvectors tensorize, eigenvalues add” is given as the Flower consequence of Kronecker sums, supporting the phase-lock equivalence across bases.
Falsifier.If cross-slot coupling terms break Kronecker-sum form, eigenvector tensorization fails, and the diagonalization basis can no longer be constructed as a tensor product.
02.S3.c — Semigroup Factorization (Cloud Consequence of Square Lock)
Definition (Semigroup factorization).Let (A) be a constraint operator generating a continuous-time Markov semigroup (P(t)=e^{-tA}). If (A=X\oplus Y), then[e^{-tA}=e^{-tX}\otimes e^{-tY}.]
Claim ([AX]) (Minimal seed operator factorization implies probabilistic factorization).At the minimal seeds, the semigroup factorizes exactly as a tensor product of seed semigroups, yielding a phase-locked Cloud evolution that is compatible with dimension and depth lifts.
Verification.For the 2D minimal seed, the Cloud consequence is explicitly recorded:[e^{-tA_{2,1}} = e^{-tA_4}\otimes e^{-tA_4}.]
Falsifier.If a proposed operator includes non-separable couplings, (P(t)) will not factorize and Cloud evolution cannot remain phase-locked under the declared lift identities.
02.S3.d — Minimality as an Exact Operator Decomposition Property
Definition (Exact decomposition witness).Define the minimality witness for ((d,k)=(d,d-1)) as the existence of exact identities:[A_{d,d-1};=;\bigoplus_{\alpha=1}^{d}\bigoplus_{t=1}^{d-1} A_4^{(\alpha,t)}.]For explicit minimal seeds, this is presented as a sum over axis (\alpha) and digit-level (t).
Claim ([AX]) (Minimal seed = minimal factor count with stable decomposition).The minimal seed is the smallest ((d,k)) for which the canonical decomposition as a sum (or iterated Kronecker sum) of seed blocks is admitted under the pinned lift schedule.
Verification.The minimal seeds are explicitly written as:[A_{3,2}=\sum_{\alpha=1}^3\sum_{t=1}^2 A_4^{(\alpha,t)},\qquadA_{4,3}=\sum_{\alpha=1}^4\sum_{t=1}^3 A_4^{(\alpha,t)}.]
Falsifier.If a smaller ((d,k)) purportedly achieves the same exact decomposition and replay stability, it must provide the explicit decomposition, lift commutation proofs, and pinned-profile regression receipts; otherwise the minimal seed law stands.
02.S4 — Protocols (How to Compute / Verify)
02.S4.a — MinimalSeed Constructor
Definition (Constructor).Given (d\ge 2), define:[k\leftarrow d-1,\quad N\leftarrow 4^k,\quad \mathcal{S}^{\min}_d\leftarrow(\mathbb{Z}_N)^d.]
Claim ([REP]) (Deterministic output).The constructor outputs the canonical minimal seed ((d,d-1)) and its per-axis resolution (4^{d-1}).
Verification (Deterministic checks).Check:[N=4^{d-1},\qquad |\mathcal{S}^{\min}_d| = (4^{d-1})^d.]
Falsifier.Any alternative constructor that outputs ((d,k)) with (k<d-1) is not a minimal-seed constructor; it is a different profile.
02.S4.b — LockedLift Constructor (State-Level)
Definition (Locked state lift).Let (\mathbf{x}\in\mathcal{S}{d,k}) be represented as axis-digit tensors. Define (\mathbf{x}^{\uparrow}\in\mathcal{S}{d+1,k+1}) by:
append one new digit to each existing axis (depth refinement),
introduce a new axis initialized with (k) zero digits and one terminal digit at depth (k+1).This realizes ((d,k)\mapsto(d+1,k+1)) as a single constructor.
Claim ([AX]) (Truncation recovers parent).The constructor must satisfy:[\pi^{\mathrm{axes}}{d+1\to d}\circ\pi{k+1\to k}(\mathbf{x}^{\uparrow})=\mathbf{x}.]
Verification.Run truncation and axis deletion; verify equality in the discrete carrier.
Falsifier.If recovery requires any additional parameters not present in the parent state and the pinned lift policy, the constructor is illegal.
02.S4.c — LockedLift Constructor (Operator-Level)
Definition (Operator lift scripts).Given seed block (A_4), define:
(A_{d,1}:=\bigoplus_{\alpha=1}^d A_4^{(\alpha,1)}) (one digit layer across (d) axes),
(A_{d,k+1}:=A_{d,k}\oplus A_{d,1}) (resolution lift),
(A_{d+1,k+1}:=A_{d,k+1}\oplus A_{1,k+1}) (locked dimension lift).
Claim ([AX]) (Script correctness).The scripts reproduce the canonical dimension-depth lock identities exactly.
Verification.Verification obligations:
Shape check: operator dimensions match ((4^{k+1})^{d+1}\times(4^{k+1})^{d+1}).
Algebra check: equality holds symbolically under Kronecker-sum expansions.
Regression check: for (d=2,k=1), confirm the stated factorization patterns (e.g., semigroup tensor product).
Falsifier.Any operator family not reproducible by the scripts without modifying (A_4) is outside the locked-lift class.
02.S4.d — Minimal Stability Test Suite (Square)
Definition (Test suite).A minimal stability test suite for ((d,k)) includes:
Seed compliance: verify (k=d-1) for minimal stability claims.
Lift identity tests: verify the two boxed identities for resolution and locked dimension lift.
Spectral tests (Flower projection): verify eigenvalue additivity / eigenvector tensorization.
Semigroup tests (Cloud projection): verify tensor product factorization of (e^{-tA}) in minimal seeds.
Claim ([REP]) (Pass/fail criterion).A dimension-depth configuration passes minimal stability only if all tests pass under pinned profiles.
Verification.For the canonical minimal seeds ((2,1)), ((3,2)), ((4,3)), run the test suite with the corresponding constructions explicitly listed in the minimal seed instantiations.
Falsifier.Any configuration that fails operator lift identities, or breaks spectral/semigroup factorization where claimed, is rejected as minimally stable.
❀ Flower — Spectral/Resonance Stability (Phase-Capacity Shadow of the Square Lock)
02.F1 — Ontology (Objects)
02.F1.a — Spectral Objects Induced by (A_{d,k})
Definition.Given a Square constraint operator (A_{d,k}), define the Flower spectral triple:[\mathsf{Spec}{d,k}:=(U{d,k},\Lambda_{d,k},\widehat{\psi}{d,k}),\quadA{d,k}=U_{d,k}\Lambda_{d,k}U_{d,k}^{-1},\quad\widehat{\psi}{d,k}=U{d,k}^{-1}\psi_{d,k}.]
Claim ([AX]) (Flower objects exist canonically under pinned diagonalization policy).When (A_{d,k}) is in the Kronecker-sum class, the diagonalization is compatible with lift by tensorization.
Verification.Diagonalize seed blocks and verify tensor structure of eigenvectors under (\oplus).
Falsifier.Non-separable coupling terms break tensor diagonalization, invalidating the Flower lift compatibility.
02.F1.b — Minimal Stable Spectral Resolution (Dimension-Coupled)
Definition.Define the minimal stable spectral regime at dimension (d) as the spectral object generated by the minimal seed ((d,d-1)):[\mathsf{Spec}^{\min}d := \mathsf{Spec}{d,d-1}.]
Claim ([REP]) (Spectral minimal seed aligns with Square minimal seed).The Flower minimal stable scale is induced by the Square minimal stable seed, not chosen independently.
Verification.Compute (\mathsf{Spec}_{d,k}) at ((d,d-1)) and confirm that lift to ((d+1,d)) follows the tensor rule.
Falsifier.Any procedure that chooses Flower spectral scale independently from Square’s minimal seed violates phase-lock (unsynchronized lift schedule) unless explicitly reprofiled.
02.F1.c — Dimension–Depth Lock as Spectral Additivity
Definition.
Under the locked lift, the operator identity
[
A_{d+1,k+1}=A_{d,k+1}\oplus A_{1,k+1}
]
implies the spectral additivity law:
[
\mathrm{spec}(A_{d+1,k+1})
\mathrm{spec}(A_{d,k+1})+\mathrm{spec}(A_{1,k+1})](Minkowski sum).
Claim ([AX]).Dimension–depth lock is equivalent to spectral additivity in the Flower basis.
Verification.Compute eigenvalues for small (d,k) and confirm additivity.
Falsifier.Observed non-additive spectral shifts under locked lift contradict Kronecker-sum structure.
02.F1.d — Minimal Seed Ladder as a Spectral Growth Schedule
Definition.Define the spectral ladder:[\mathsf{Spec}^{\min}_2 \to \mathsf{Spec}^{\min}_3 \to \cdots \to \mathsf{Spec}^{\min}_d \to \cdots]induced by ((d,d-1)\mapsto(d+1,d)).
Claim ([AX]).The spectral ladder is the Flower-side manifestation of the minimal seed ladder.
Verification.Confirm spectral additivity at each ladder step.
Falsifier.If ladder steps require renormalizing the seed kernel to maintain diagonalization, the ladder is not minimally stable.
02.F2 — Operators
02.F2.a — Diagonal Lift Operators
Definition.Define the diagonal lift maps induced by Kronecker sum:[U_{X\oplus Y}=U_X\otimes U_Y,\qquad\Lambda_{X\oplus Y}=\Lambda_X\oplus \Lambda_Y.]
Claim ([AX]).Eigenvectors tensorize and eigenvalues add under the Kronecker-sum lift.
Verification.Direct computation at minimal seeds (2D/3D/4D) confirms the tensor structure.
Falsifier.Failure of tensorization signals non-Kronecker coupling.
02.F2.b — Locked Lift in the Flower Basis
Definition.The Flower-basis locked lift is the mapping:[(U_{d,k+1},\Lambda_{d,k+1})\ \mapsto\ (U_{d+1,k+1},\Lambda_{d+1,k+1})]with[U_{d+1,k+1}=U_{d,k+1}\otimes U_{1,k+1}.]
Claim ([AX]).The Flower locked lift is the diagonalization-equivalent of the Square locked lift.
Verification.Compute and compare.
Falsifier.If the Flower lift cannot be expressed by tensor extension, Square lift is not phase-locked.
02.F2.c — Minimal Stable Spectral Band (Carrier-Dependent)
Definition.Let (\Lambda_{d,k}) be ordered by magnitude. Define a minimal stable Flower band as the low-spectrum window pinned by profile:[\Lambda_{d,k}^{(\le \Lambda_\star)} := {\lambda\in\mathrm{spec}(A_{d,k}) : |\lambda|\le \Lambda_\star}.]
Claim ([REP]).In minimal stability mode, (\Lambda_\star) is chosen as a function of ((d,d-1)) and inherited under lift (no silent retuning).
Verification.Confirm inherited band selection under lift.
Falsifier.Retuning (\Lambda_\star) without explicit profile change is a hidden knob.
02.F2.d — Spectral Certificate for Lift Correctness
Definition.A Flower lift certificate consists of:
eigenvalue-additivity check: (\Lambda_{d+1,k+1} \approx \Lambda_{d,k+1}\oplus \Lambda_{1,k+1}) (exact in the algebraic model),
eigenvector tensor structure check: (U_{d+1,k+1}=U_{d,k+1}\otimes U_{1,k+1}).
Claim ([REP]).These certificates are sufficient to verify lift correctness in the Flower basis under Kronecker-sum structure.
Verification.Execute certificate checks at minimal seeds.
Falsifier.Any mismatch indicates a lift law violation.
02.F3 — Invariants
02.F3.a — Spectral Invariants Under Minimal Seed Ladder
Definition.Define the spectral invariants as those preserved by Kronecker-sum lift (additivity/tensorization).
Claim ([AX]).The minimal seed ladder preserves the spectral composition rule exactly.
Verification.Check at each ladder step.
Falsifier.Non-additive deviations violate the lock.

Definition.Flower stability is separability of the diagonal basis with bounded holonomy across lift and lens-switch.
Claim ([DER]).Separability is equivalent to Kronecker-sum structure in the Square basis.
Verification.Confirm diagonal lift maps exist.
Falsifier.Observed spectral entanglement beyond tensor products.
02.F3.c — Dimension–Depth Lock Preserves Mode-Indexing Semantics
Definition.Mode indexing is stable if mode labels at ((d,k)) embed deterministically into mode labels at ((d+1,k+1)).
Claim ([REP]).Tensorization induces deterministic mode embedding.
Verification.Construct embedding map on indices.
Falsifier.Non-deterministic mode relabeling.
02.F3.d — Minimality as the First Spectrally Complete Dimension
Definition.Define “spectrally complete at dimension (d)” as the first (k) for which the spectral ladder admits the locked lift without retyping.
Claim ([AX]).This occurs at (k=d-1) under the pinned minimal seed policy.
Verification.Directly follow the minimal seed ladder.
Falsifier.Any smaller depth satisfying the same criteria must provide full lift certificates.

✶ Fractal — Multiscale/Recursion Stability (Schedule-Capacity)
02.R1 — Ontology (Objects)
02.R1.a — Dimension–Depth Schedule Object
Definition.Define the dimension–depth schedule as a sequence ({(d_n,k_n)}_{n\ge 0}). The minimal-seed schedule is:[d_n = d_0+n,\qquad k_n = k_0+n,\qquad k_0=d_0-1,]so that (k_n=d_n-1) for all (n).
Claim ([AX]).The minimal seed lock across dimension is precisely the rule (k=d-1).
Verification.Check invariance (k_n=d_n-1).
Falsifier.Any step violating (k=d-1) without explicit profile override.
02.R1.b — Lifted Operator Tower ({A_{d_n,k_n}})
Definition.Define the operator tower under locked lift:[A_{d_{n+1},k_{n+1}} = A_{d_n,k_{n+1}}\oplus A_{1,k_{n+1}}.]
Claim ([AX]).The tower is phase-locked by structured Kronecker-sum composition at each step.
Verification.Check tower identities inductively.
Falsifier.Any step requiring kernel mutation.
02.R1.c — Minimal Seed as the First Admissible Recursion Frame
Definition.Define the first recursion frame at dimension (d) as the first depth at which the locked-lift identities can be satisfied without retyping: (k=d-1).
Claim ([AX]).This is the canonically pinned meaning of “minimal seed” for higher dimension.
Verification.Use the minimal ladder instances.
Falsifier.A smaller frame would need full lift certificates.
02.R1.d — Recursion Meaning: Lift = Add Axis + Add Depth
Definition.Define the Fractal meaning of the locked lift as the compound action “add axis + add digit depth,” with the operator-level realization of the same.
Claim ([AX]).The locked lift is the minimal recursion move consistent with the dimensional phase-lock identity.
Verification.Check the explicit combined form described for the 3D→4D minimal seed transition.
Falsifier.If recursion changes meaning without explicit encoding, it is illegal under the general recursion discipline.
02.R2 — Operators
02.R2.a — Locked Lift as the Canonical Fractal Move
Definition.Fractal lift operator:[\mathcal{L}{\mathrm{Fr}}:(A{d,k})\mapsto (A_{d+1,k+1})]implemented by the boxed operator identity.
Claim ([AX]).Fractal lift is an exact algebraic operator move (not heuristic).
Verification.Symbolic identity check.
Falsifier.Any approximation-only lift is not the locked lift.
02.R2.b — Resolution Lift as the Canonical Depth Move
Definition.Depth lift:[A_{d,k+1}=A_{d,k}\oplus A_{d,1}.]
Claim ([AX]).Depth is implemented as a Kronecker-sum digit-layer addition.
Verification.Check the (A_{2,k}) identity.
Falsifier.Kernel mutation under depth lift.
02.R2.c — Minimal Seed Lift Composition
Definition.Minimal seed lift step:[(d,d-1)\mapsto(d+1,d)]is realized as:[A_{d+1,d}=\big(A_{d,d-1}\oplus A_{d,1}\big)\oplus A_{1,d}.](“add digit depth, then add axis at the new depth” as a structured composition).
Claim ([AX]).This is the minimal-seed ladder move.
Verification.Compare to the described combined lift logic.
Falsifier.Non-associative or non-reproducible lift outcomes.
02.R2.d — Tower Factorization Lemma
Definition.Let (A_{d,k}=\bigoplus_{j=1}^{dk}A_4^{(j)}). Then each lift step appends additional (A_4) blocks in a strictly typed manner.
Claim ([DER]).The tower is a strictly monotone factor extension in the Kronecker-sum sense.
Verification.Count factors: (dk\mapsto(d+1)(k+1)=dk+d+k+1).
Falsifier.Missing factors or extra hidden factors.
02.R3 — Invariants
02.R3.a — Schedule Invariant (k=d-1)
Definition.In the minimal seed schedule, maintain (k_n=d_n-1).
Claim ([AX]).This is the phase-lock identity for minimal stability.
Verification.Check at each step.
Falsifier.Violation without profile override.
02.R3.b — Lift Commutation Invariant
Definition.Lift commutation invariant requires that lift identities hold exactly as equalities of operators.
Claim ([AX]).The boxed identities define the commutation invariants.
Verification.Symbolic checks.
Falsifier.Any identity failure.
02.R3.c — Minimality Invariant (No Smaller Stable Seed)
Definition.Minimality invariant asserts that (k=d-1) is the smallest depth satisfying the locked lift schedule.
Claim ([AX]).Minimal seed lock explicitly enforces (k=d-1).
Verification.Attempt (k=d-2) and observe lift/certificate failure under pinned policies.
Falsifier.A full certificate set at (k=d-2).
02.R3.d — Lens-Agreement Invariant Under Locked Lift
Definition.Lens agreement means Square (operator identity), Flower (spectral tensorization), Cloud (semigroup factorization) remain simultaneously true under lift.
Claim ([AX]).This joint agreement is enforced by the shared Kronecker-sum structure.
Verification.Run Square/Flower/Cloud tests in §02.S4.d.
Falsifier.Any cross-lens mismatch.
02.R4 — Protocols
02.R4.a — Minimal Seed Ladder Builder
Definition.Algorithm:[(d_0,k_0)=(2,1);\quad \text{for }n\ge 0:\ (d_{n+1},k_{n+1})=(d_n+1,k_n+1).]
Claim ([REP]).Builds ((d,k)=(d,d-1)) for all (d\ge 2).
Verification.Direct.
Falsifier.Deviation.
02.R4.b — Lift Certificate Emitter
Definition.Emit certificates:
Square: verify boxed lift identities,
Flower: verify tensorization/additivity,
Cloud: verify semigroup factorization.
Claim ([REP]).Sufficient for dimension–depth lock certification.
Verification.Run on minimal seeds.
Falsifier.Any failed certificate.
02.R4.c — Counterexample Search Protocol
Definition.Search for counterexamples by:
selecting (k<d-1),
attempting to construct lift-consistent (A_{d,k}) without kernel mutation,
checking lift identities and cross-lens factorization.
Claim ([REP]).This protocol generates falsifiers when minimality is violated.
Verification.Run for (d=3,k=1) against minimal policy.
Falsifier.No falsifier found implies either policy has been overridden or tests are incomplete.
02.R4.d — Replay-Deterministic Schedule Audit
Definition.Audit requires that the schedule and its operator tower are replay-deterministic under pinned profiles: same inputs yield identical (A_{d,k}) and certificates.
Claim ([REP]).Determinism is guaranteed by fixed seed (A_4) and Kronecker-sum construction.
Verification.Hash operator constructions and compare.
Falsifier.Non-reproducible outputs under identical pins.
Ch02 — Dimension–Depth Lock and Minimal Stable Scales
Ch03 — The 15-Station Ring as the Powerset Carrier
Station Encoding, (\sigma) Indexing, and (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT})
□ Square — Combinatorial Carrier (Station Semantics and Bit Encoding)
03.S1 — Ontology (Objects)
03.S1.a — Lens basis set and nonempty powerset
Let the lens basis be the ordered 4-tuple[\mathbb{L}_4 := (\square,\flower,\cloud,\fractal),]and its underlying set (by abuse of notation) ({\square,\flower,\cloud,\fractal}).
Define the nonempty powerset carrier (the station semantics set)[\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}_4) ;:=; \mathcal{P}({\square,\flower,\cloud,\fractal}) \setminus {\varnothing}.]Then[\big|\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}_4)\big| = 2^4-1 = 15.]Elements (U\in\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}_4)) are called stations (semantic stations).
03.S1.b — Bitmask model of stations
Define the bit index map aligned to (\mathbb{L}_4):[\mathrm{bit}(\square)=0,\quad \mathrm{bit}(\flower)=1,\quad \mathrm{bit}(\cloud)=2,\quad \mathrm{bit}(\fractal)=3.]For any station (U\in\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)), define its indicator bits (b_j(U)\in{0,1}) by[b_j(U) := \mathbf{1}{,\ell\in U:\ \mathrm{bit}(\ell)=j,}.]Define the mask encoding (semantic code)[m(U) ;:=; \sum{j=0}^{3} b_j(U),2^j \ \in\ {1,2,\dots,15}.]Thus, semantic stations are represented uniquely by nonzero 4-bit masks.
03.S1.c — Ring index set and canonical (\sigma) coordinates
Define the 15-ring index set[\Sigma_{15} ;:=; \mathbb{Z}_{15} ;\cong; {0,1,\dots,14},]with addition modulo (15).
Define the ring coordinate (\sigma) associated to a station (U) by[\sigma(U);:=;m(U)-1\ \in\ \Sigma_{15}.]Conversely, for (\sigma\in\Sigma_{15}) define (m(\sigma):=\sigma+1\in{1,\dots,15}).
03.S1.d — Canonical bijections (\mathrm{ENC}) and (\mathrm{DEC})
Define the canonical encodings:[\mathrm{ENC}{\mathrm{mask}}:\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)\to{1,\dots,15},\quad \mathrm{ENC}{\mathrm{mask}}(U)=m(U),][\mathrm{ENC}{\sigma}:\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)\to\Sigma{15},\quad \mathrm{ENC}_{\sigma}(U)=\sigma(U).]
Define the canonical decodings:[\mathrm{DEC}{\mathrm{mask}}:{1,\dots,15}\to\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4),]where for (m\in{1,\dots,15}), letting (b_j=\big\lfloor m/2^j\big\rfloor\bmod 2),[\mathrm{DEC}{\mathrm{mask}}(m);:=;{\ \ell\in\mathbb{L}4:\ b{\mathrm{bit}(\ell)}=1\ }.]Then[\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}:\Sigma_{15}\to\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4),\quad \mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}(\sigma):=\mathrm{DEC}_{\mathrm{mask}}(\sigma+1).]
Correctness (bijection laws):[\mathrm{DEC}{\mathrm{mask}}\circ \mathrm{ENC}{\mathrm{mask}}=\mathrm{id}{\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)},\quad\mathrm{ENC}{\mathrm{mask}}\circ \mathrm{DEC}{\mathrm{mask}}=\mathrm{id}{{1,\dots,15}},][\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}\circ \mathrm{ENC}{\sigma}=\mathrm{id}{\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)},\quad\mathrm{ENC}{\sigma}\circ \mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}=\mathrm{id}{\Sigma_{15}}.]
03.S2 — Operators (Transforms)
03.S2.a — Semantic set-operators on stations (mask realization)
For stations (U,V\in\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}_4)), define:[U\cup V,\quad U\cap V,\quad U\setminus V,\quad U\triangle V\ (\text{symmetric difference}).]Let (\vee,\wedge,\oplus) denote bitwise OR/AND/XOR on masks. Then[m(U\cup V)=m(U)\vee m(V),\qquad m(U\cap V)=m(U)\wedge m(V),][m(U\triangle V)=m(U)\oplus m(V),]and (U\cup V\neq\varnothing) always; while (U\cap V) may be empty and thus is outside (\mathcal{P}^\star) unless explicitly retyped. When a set-operator yields (\varnothing), the operation is considered undefined in the station carrier unless a dedicated null station policy is introduced.
Define the station weight (lens-count)[w(U):=|U|=\sum_{j=0}^{3} b_j(U);=;\mathrm{popcount}(m(U)).]
03.S2.b — Canonical station labeling and normal forms
Define the canonical label of a station (U) as the 4-bit string[\mathrm{bits}(U):=b_3(U)b_2(U)b_1(U)b_0(U)\in{0,1}^4\setminus{0000},]with the leftmost bit corresponding to (\fractal) and the rightmost to (\square).
Define the canonical label of (\sigma\in\Sigma_{15}) as (\mathrm{bits}(\sigma):=\mathrm{bits}(\mathrm{DEC}_{\sigma}(\sigma))).
These labels are canonical under the pinned bit ordering ((\square,\flower,\cloud,\fractal)).
03.S2.c — (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) on the 15-ring ((\sigma)-space)
Define the next-orbit operator on the ring as the endomorphism[\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}:\Sigma_{15}\to\Sigma_{15},\qquad\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}(\sigma):=\sigma+1\pmod{15}.]Define the (n)-step orbit advance for (n\in\mathbb{Z}) as[\mathrm{ORBIT_ADVANCE}(\sigma;n):=\sigma+n\pmod{15}.]Define orbit iteration:[\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^{,t}(\sigma)=\sigma+t\pmod{15},\qquad t\in\mathbb{N}.]
03.S2.d — (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) transported to station semantics (powerset space)
Transport (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) to (\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)) via (\mathrm{ENC}{\sigma}) and (\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}):[\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^\star:=\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}\circ \mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}\circ \mathrm{ENC}_{\sigma}:\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}_4)\to\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4).]Equivalently, in mask coordinates (m\in{1,\dots,15}),[\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^\star(U)=\mathrm{DEC}{\mathrm{mask}}!\left((m(U)\bmod 15)+1\right).]
Define the directed edge set of the orbit graph:[E_{\mathrm{next}}:={,(\sigma,\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}(\sigma)):\ \sigma\in\Sigma_{15},}.]This is a single directed 15-cycle.
03.S3 — Invariants (What Stays)
03.S3.a — Encoding/decoding correctness invariants
For all (U\in\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)),[\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}(\mathrm{ENC}{\sigma}(U))=U,\qquad\mathrm{DEC}{\mathrm{mask}}(\mathrm{ENC}{\mathrm{mask}}(U))=U.]For all (\sigma\in\Sigma{15}),[\mathrm{ENC}{\sigma}(\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}(\sigma))=\sigma,\qquad\mathrm{ENC}{\mathrm{mask}}(\mathrm{DEC}{\mathrm{mask}}(\sigma+1))=\sigma+1.]
03.S3.b — Cyclic group invariants of the orbit operator
The operator (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) is a generator of the cyclic group action of (\Sigma_{15}) on itself:[\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^{,15}=\mathrm{id}{\Sigma{15}},\qquad\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^{,t}\neq \mathrm{id}\ \text{for}\ 1\le t<15.]Hence the orbit graph ((\Sigma_{15},E_{\mathrm{next}})) is strongly connected and has period (15).
03.S3.c — Station-weight partition and cardinality invariants
Define weight classes[\mathcal{W}_r:={,U\in\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}_4):\ w(U)=r,},\qquad r\in{1,2,3,4}.]Then[|\mathcal{W}_1|=\binom{4}{1}=4,\quad|\mathcal{W}_2|=\binom{4}{2}=6,\quad|\mathcal{W}_3|=\binom{4}{3}=4,\quad|\mathcal{W}_4|=\binom{4}{4}=1,]and[\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)=\bigsqcup{r=1}^{4}\mathcal{W}_r.]The orbit operator is a permutation of stations and therefore preserves this partition as a multiset (it permutes elements across classes but preserves the global counts).
03.S3.d — Separation of semantics vs routing invariants
There are two independent algebraic structures:
Semantic algebra on stations (U) given by set operations (equivalently bitwise operations on masks).
Routing algebra on indices (\sigma) given by addition modulo (15).
No identification of these algebras is assumed; station semantics are transported along routing only through the pinned bijection (\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}\circ\mathrm{ENC}{\sigma}). Any proof obligation involving semantics must be stated in semantic coordinates (powerset/mask), and any proof obligation involving orbit movement must be stated in routing coordinates ((\Sigma_{15})).
03.S4 — Protocols (How to Compute / Verify)

Let the bit order be ((\fractal,\cloud,\flower,\square)) for display (MSB→LSB). Let (m=\sigma+1). The station mapping is:

03.S4.b — Reference algorithms: (\mathrm{ENC}) and (\mathrm{DEC})
# Lens basis order (LSB -> MSB): Square, Flower, Cloud, Fractal
LENS = ["SQUARE", "FLOWER", "CLOUD", "FRACTAL"] # indices 0..3
def enc_mask(station: set[str]) -> int:
"""
Input: station ⊆ {SQUARE,FLOWER,CLOUD,FRACTAL}, station ≠ ∅
Output: m ∈ {1..15}
"""
m = 0
for j, name in enumerate(LENS):
if name in station:
m |= (1 << j)
assert 1 <= m <= 15
return m
def dec_mask(m: int) -> set[str]:
"""
Input: m ∈ {1..15}
Output: station ⊆ {SQUARE,FLOWER,CLOUD,FRACTAL}, station ≠ ∅
"""
assert 1 <= m <= 15
station = set()
for j, name in enumerate(LENS):
if (m >> j) & 1:
station.add(name)
return station
def enc_sigma(station: set[str]) -> int:
"""
