Output: σ ∈ Z_15 represented as {0..14}
"""
return enc_mask(station) - 1
def dec_sigma(sigma: int) -> set[str]:
"""
Input: σ ∈ {0..14}
"""
assert 0 <= sigma <= 14
return dec_mask(sigma + 1)
03.S4.c — Reference algorithms: (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) and orbit utilities
MOD = 15
def orbit_next(sigma: int) -> int:
"""
σ ↦ σ+1 mod 15
"""
return (sigma + 1) % MOD
def orbit_advance(sigma: int, n: int) -> int:
"""
σ ↦ σ+n mod 15, n may be negative
"""
return (sigma + (n % MOD)) % MOD
def orbit_next_station(station: set[str]) -> set[str]:
"""
Transport ORBIT_NEXT to station semantics.
"""
return dec_sigma(orbit_next(enc_sigma(station)))
def orbit_distance_forward(a: int, b: int) -> int:
"""
Forward steps from a to reach b under ORBIT_NEXT.
"""
return (b - a) % MOD
def orbit_distance_min(a: int, b: int) -> int:
"""
Minimal cyclic distance on the 15-ring.
"""
fwd = orbit_distance_forward(a, b)
return min(fwd, MOD - fwd)
03.S4.d — Verification harness (axioms as executable checks)
def verify_bijections():
# ENC/DEC correctness on all σ
for sigma in range(15):
st = dec_sigma(sigma)
assert enc_sigma(st) == sigma
# ORBIT cycle length
for sigma0 in range(15):
sigma = sigma0
for _ in range(15):
sigma = orbit_next(sigma)
assert sigma == sigma0
def verify_mask_ops_consistency():
# Semantic union/intersection via masks
for a in range(1, 16):
for b in range(1, 16):
Ua = dec_mask(a)
Ub = dec_mask(b)
assert enc_mask(Ua | Ub) == (a | b)
inter = Ua & Ub
if inter:
assert enc_mask(inter) == (a & b)
❀ Flower — Cyclic Harmonic Carrier (Ring as Phase Orbit)
03.F1 — Ontology (Objects)
03.F1.a — Ring as a finite cyclic group
Identify (\Sigma_{15}) with the cyclic group (G_{15}:=(\mathbb{Z}{15},+)). A ring coordinate (\sigma\in\Sigma{15}) is a group element.
Define the orbit action of (G_{15}) on itself:[T_n(\sigma):=\sigma+n\pmod{15},\qquad n\in\mathbb{Z}_{15}.]Then (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}=T_1).
03.F1.b — Canonical embedding into the circle (\mathbb{T}^1)
Define the phase embedding[\iota:\Sigma_{15}\to\mathbb{T}^1,\qquad \iota(\sigma):=\frac{\sigma}{15}\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1).]Under (\iota), (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) corresponds to circle rotation by (1/15):[\iota(\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}(\sigma))=\iota(\sigma)+\frac{1}{15}\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1).]
03.F1.c — Function space and regular representation
Let (\mathbb{C}^{15}\cong{f:\Sigma_{15}\to\mathbb{C}}). Define the shift operator (left translation)[(\mathsf{T}f)(\sigma):=f(\sigma-1\pmod{15}).]Then (\mathsf{T}) is the linear operator representing (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) on functions by pullback.
03.F1.d — Characters (Fourier modes) on the ring
For (n\in\Sigma_{15}), define the character[\chi_n(\sigma):=\exp!\left(2\pi i,\frac{n\sigma}{15}\right).]The set ({\chi_n}{n=0}^{14}) is an orthogonal basis of (\mathbb{C}^{15}) under the standard inner product[\langle f,g\rangle:=\sum{\sigma\in\Sigma_{15}} f(\sigma),\overline{g(\sigma)}.]
03.F2 — Operators (Transforms)
03.F2.a — Orbit translation operator on phases
Under the phase embedding (\iota), translation by (n) acts as[\iota(T_n(\sigma))=\iota(\sigma)+\frac{n}{15}\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1).]Thus the ring action is a discrete subgroup of circle rotations.
03.F2.b — Diagonalization of (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) via characters
The shift operator (\mathsf{T}) satisfies[\mathsf{T}\chi_n = \exp!\left(2\pi i,\frac{n}{15}\right)\chi_n,]so the Fourier basis diagonalizes (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) (as a unitary permutation on (\mathbb{C}^{15})).
03.F2.c — Discrete Fourier transform (DFT(_{15}))
Define the DFT and inverse DFT:[\widehat{f}(n):=\sum_{\sigma=0}^{14} f(\sigma),\exp!\left(-2\pi i,\frac{n\sigma}{15}\right),\qquadf(\sigma)=\frac{1}{15}\sum_{n=0}^{14}\widehat{f}(n),\exp!\left(2\pi i,\frac{n\sigma}{15}\right).]
03.F2.d — Orbit power spectrum and shift invariants
Define the power spectrum (P_f(n):=|\widehat{f}(n)|^2). Under orbit shift (T_a), the Fourier coefficients rotate by phases:[\widehat{(f\circ T_a)}(n)=\exp!\left(-2\pi i,\frac{na}{15}\right)\widehat{f}(n),]so (P_f(n)) is invariant under orbit translation.
03.F3 — Invariants (What Stays)
03.F3.a — Order and periodicity
[\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^{,15}=\mathrm{id},\qquad\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^{,t}\neq\mathrm{id}\ \ (1\le t<15).]Equivalently, the rotation angle (2\pi/15) has exact order (15) in (\mathbb{T}^1).
03.F3.b — Spectral invariants of the shift operator
The eigenvalues of (\mathsf{T}) are precisely[\lambda_n=\exp!\left(2\pi i,\frac{n}{15}\right),\qquad n=0,\dots,14,]each with multiplicity (1).
03.F3.c — Translation invariance of the power spectrum
For any (f), the power spectrum (P_f) is invariant under orbit translations. This provides a canonical orbit-invariant signature for station-indexed observables.
03.F3.d — Compatibility of phase embedding with orbit arithmetic
For all (\sigma\in\Sigma_{15}) and (n\in\mathbb{Z}),[\iota(\mathrm{ORBIT_ADVANCE}(\sigma;n))=\iota(\sigma)+\frac{n}{15}\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1).]Hence orbit arithmetic in (\Sigma_{15}) and phase arithmetic in (\mathbb{T}^1) are strictly compatible via (\iota).
03.F4 — Protocols (How to Compute / Verify)
03.F4.a — Fourier diagonal check for (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT})
Compute the permutation matrix (P) of (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) on (\mathbb{C}^{15}). Compute the DFT matrix (F). Verify[F^{-1}PF=\mathrm{diag}(\lambda_0,\dots,\lambda_{14}).]
03.F4.b — Phase embedding regression check
Verify numerically (or symbolically) for all (\sigma):[\iota(\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}(\sigma))-\iota(\sigma)=\frac{1}{15}\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1).]
03.F4.c — Orbit-invariant signature protocol
Given any station observable (f:\Sigma_{15}\to\mathbb{R}), compute (\widehat{f}) and output (P_f(n)=|\widehat{f}(n)|^2) as the orbit-invariant signature.
03.F4.d — Character orthogonality check
Verify:[\sum_{\sigma=0}^{14}\chi_n(\sigma)\overline{\chi_m(\sigma)}=15,\delta_{nm}.]
☁ Cloud — Probabilistic Carrier (Distributions over Stations)
03.C1 — Ontology (Objects)
03.C1.a — Probability simplex over stations
Let[\Delta_{15}:=\Big{,p\in\mathbb{R}^{15}:\ p_\sigma\ge 0,\ \sum_{\sigma=0}^{14}p_\sigma=1,\Big}]be the simplex of probability distributions over (\Sigma_{15}).
03.C1.b — Station-measure interpretation in semantics space
Equivalently, a distribution over semantic stations is a measure (\mu) on (\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)). The bijection (\mathrm{ENC}{\sigma}) induces an identification[\mathcal{P}(\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4))\ \cong\ \Delta{15}]by pushforward/pullback.
03.C1.c — Deterministic orbit kernel
Define the Markov kernel (K_{\mathrm{next}}) on (\Sigma_{15}) by[K_{\mathrm{next}}(\sigma,\sigma'):=\mathbf{1}{\sigma'=\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}(\sigma)}.]Then (K_{\mathrm{next}}) is a permutation kernel (deterministic transition).
03.C1.d — Pushforward of distributions under orbit maps
For any measurable (T:\Sigma_{15}\to\Sigma_{15}), define the pushforward of (p\in\Delta_{15}) by[(T_#p){\sigma'}:=\sum{\sigma:\ T(\sigma)=\sigma'} p_\sigma.]For (T=\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}), this equals a cyclic shift.
03.C2 — Operators (Transforms)
03.C2.a — Distribution update under (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT})
Let (p\in\Delta_{15}). Then
[
(\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}#p){\sigma}
p_{\sigma-1\pmod{15}}.]
03.C2.b — Permutation matrix representation
Define (P\in{0,1}^{15\times 15}) by[P_{\sigma',\sigma}=K_{\mathrm{next}}(\sigma,\sigma')=\mathbf{1}{\sigma'=\sigma+1\pmod{15}}.]Then (p' = Pp) is the distribution update.
03.C2.c — Composition of orbit kernels
For (t\in\mathbb{N}), define (K_{\mathrm{next}}^{(t)}) by convolution (kernel composition). Then[K_{\mathrm{next}}^{(t)}(\sigma,\sigma')=\mathbf{1}{\sigma'=\sigma+t\pmod{15}},\qquadP^t\ \text{represents}\ K_{\mathrm{next}}^{(t)}.]
03.C2.d — Semantic-station distribution update
Transport the update to semantic station space:
[
(\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^\star)_#\mu
\big(\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}\big)#\big(\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}#(\mathrm{ENC}{\sigma})#\mu\big).]All probabilistic updates over stations are therefore representable as updates in (\Delta{15}) composed with the fixed enc/dec bijections.
03.C3 — Invariants (What Stays)
03.C3.a — Mass conservation
For all (p\in\Delta_{15}),[\sum_{\sigma=0}^{14} (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}#p)\sigma=\sum_{\sigma=0}^{14}p_\sigma=1.]
03.C3.b — Stationarity and periodicity
The uniform distribution (u_\sigma:=1/15) satisfies (Pu=u).However, the chain is periodic with period (15); for any (p), the sequence (p_t=P^t p) is exactly periodic:[p_{t+15}=p_t.]
03.C3.c — Entropy invariance under permutation dynamics
For Shannon entropy (H(p):=-\sum_\sigma p_\sigma\log p_\sigma),[H(Pp)=H(p),]since (P) is a permutation.
03.C3.d — Fourier-space transport of distributions
Identifying (p) as a function on (\Sigma_{15}), the DFT satisfies[\widehat{(Pp)}(n)=\exp!\left(2\pi i,\frac{n}{15}\right)\widehat{p}(n),]so (|\widehat{p}(n)|) is invariant under orbit evolution.
03.C4 — Protocols (How to Compute / Verify)
03.C4.a — Kernel construction and validation
Construct (K_{\mathrm{next}}) or (P). Verify:[\sum_{\sigma'}K_{\mathrm{next}}(\sigma,\sigma')=1\ \ (\forall\sigma),\qquad P\mathbf{1}=\mathbf{1}.]
03.C4.b — Simulation protocol
Given initial (p_0\in\Delta_{15}), compute (p_t=P^t p_0). Verify periodicity by checking (p_{15}=p_0).
03.C4.c — Orbit-invariant statistics protocol
Compute entropy (H(p_t)) and verify (H(p_t)) constant in (t). Compute (|\widehat{p_t}(n)|) and verify invariance in (t).
03.C4.d — Semantic distribution alignment protocol
Given a distribution (\mu) over semantic stations, push forward to (p=(\mathrm{ENC}{\sigma})#\mu), evolve (p) via (P), then pull back via (\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}). Verify equivalence to directly evolving via ((\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^\star)#).
✶ Fractal — Recursive Carrier (Orbit Iteration, Route Logs, and Coarse-Graining)
03.R1 — Ontology (Objects)
03.R1.a — Orbit words and route logs
Define the orbit word monoid ((\mathbb{Z},+)) acting on (\Sigma_{15}) by (\mathrm{ORBIT_ADVANCE}(\cdot;n)).A route log is a pair ((\sigma_0,n)) representing the map (\sigma\mapsto \sigma+n) applied at (\sigma_0), or a word (n_1n_2\cdots n_T) representing successive advances.
03.R1.b — Canonical compression of route logs
Any finite word (n_1,\dots,n_T\in\mathbb{Z}) composes to a single advance
[
n_{\mathrm{tot}}:=\sum_{t=1}^T n_t,
\qquad
\mathrm{ORBIT_ADVANCE}(\sigma_0;n_1)\circ\cdots\circ\mathrm{ORBIT_ADVANCE}(\sigma_0;n_T)
\mathrm{ORBIT_ADVANCE}(\sigma_0;n_{\mathrm{tot}}).]Thus a route log canonically compresses to ((\sigma_0, n_{\mathrm{tot}}\bmod 15)).
03.R1.c — Coarse observables on the station carrier
Define coarse observables on semantic stations, e.g. the weight map[w:\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}4)\to{1,2,3,4},\quad w(U)=|U|.]Transported to (\Sigma{15}) via (\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}), define (w(\sigma):=w(\mathrm{DEC}{\sigma}(\sigma))).
03.R1.d — Induced action on observables
For any observable (f:\Sigma_{15}\to X), define its orbit-shifted version by[(\mathsf{T}f)(\sigma):=f(\sigma-1\pmod{15}),]and iterates (\mathsf{T}^t f(\sigma)=f(\sigma-t\pmod{15})). This defines the recursion/iteration layer for station-indexed structures.
03.R2 — Operators (Transforms)
03.R2.a — Route concatenation
Concatenation corresponds to modular addition of advances:[(\sigma_0,n_1)\star(\sigma_0,n_2)=(\sigma_0,n_1+n_2),]with canonical reduction (n\mapsto n\bmod 15).
03.R2.b — Canonical normal form of a route
Define the canonical normal form:[\mathrm{NF}(\sigma_0,n):=(\sigma_0,\ n\bmod 15)\in \Sigma_{15}\times\Sigma_{15}.]Two routes are equivalent iff they share the same normal form.
03.R2.c — Coarse-graining operators on station observables
Given a coarse map (c:\Sigma_{15}\to Y), define the pushforward of a distribution (p\in\Delta_{15}) to (Y) by[(c_#p)(y):=\sum_{\sigma:\ c(\sigma)=y} p_\sigma.]For (c=w), this yields the induced distribution over lens-counts ({1,2,3,4}).
03.R2.d — Orbit-equivalence classes of observables
Define the orbit equivalence relation on observables (f:\Sigma_{15}\to X):[f\sim g \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad \exists t\in\Sigma_{15}:\ g=\mathsf{T}^t f.]The orbit-invariant signature of (f) is any complete invariant under this relation; e.g., the power spectrum (|\widehat{f}(n)|^2).
03.R3 — Invariants (What Stays)
03.R3.a — Route equivalence invariant
For all (\sigma_0) and all integers (n),[\mathrm{ORBIT_ADVANCE}(\sigma_0;n)=\mathrm{ORBIT_ADVANCE}(\sigma_0;n+15q)\quad(\forall q\in\mathbb{Z}),]hence route meaning depends only on (n\bmod 15).
03.R3.b — Canonical compression invariant
Any finite route word compresses to a single residue class in (\Sigma_{15}). This establishes a strict “holographic” compression property for orbit logs: route histories collapse to a residue without loss of net effect.
03.R3.c — Coarse-map invariants under orbit permutations
For any coarse map (c), the multiset ({c(\sigma):\sigma\in\Sigma_{15}}) is invariant under orbit permutations. In particular, the global counts of weights ((4,6,4,1)) remain invariant.
03.R3.d — Minimal generator invariant
(\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}) generates the full action of (\Sigma_{15}) on itself. Any orbit step is expressible as (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}^t) for a unique (t\in\Sigma_{15}).
03.R4 — Protocols (How to Compute / Verify)
03.R4.a — Canonical route compression protocol
Given a route word (n_1,\dots,n_T), compute (n_{\mathrm{tot}}=\sum n_t), reduce (n_{\mathrm{tot}}\bmod 15), output (\mathrm{NF}(\sigma_0,n_{\mathrm{tot}})).
03.R4.b — Orbit-equivalence audit for observables
Given (f,g:\Sigma_{15}\to\mathbb{R}), compute (|\widehat{f}(n)|^2) and (|\widehat{g}(n)|^2). If spectra differ, then (f\not\sim g). If spectra agree, optionally verify by direct shift search (t\in\Sigma_{15}) such that (g=\mathsf{T}^t f).
03.R4.c — Coarse distribution protocol (weight map)
Given (p\in\Delta_{15}), compute (p^{(w)}:=w_#p) on ({1,2,3,4}) by summing masses over stations of equal weight.
03.R4.d — Deterministic reproducibility audit
Audit requires that all mappings (\mathrm{ENC}), (\mathrm{DEC}), (\mathrm{ORBIT_NEXT}), and derived operators are uniquely determined by the pinned lens order ((\square,\flower,\cloud,\fractal)) and the choice (\Sigma_{15}=\mathbb{Z}_{15}). Reproducibility is certified by passing the verification harness in §03.S4.d.
Ch03 — The 15-Station Ring as the Powerset Carrier
Ch04 — Gear-Loop Decomposition and “Visibility”
Cycle Decomposition on (N=15) and (N=B_d); Resolution Requirements for Higher-Dimensional Tunnel Observability
□ Square — Discrete Gear Actions on Finite Rings (Cycle Structure as an Algebraic Invariant)
04.S1 — Ontology (Objects)
04.S1.a — Gear ring and step map
Let (N\in\mathbb{N}{\ge 2}). Define the gear ring[\Sigma_N:=\mathbb{Z}N={0,1,\dots,N-1}]with addition modulo (N).For a step (s\in\Sigma_N), define the gear translation[T{N,s}:\Sigma_N\to\Sigma_N,\qquad T{N,s}(u):=u+s\pmod N.]
04.S1.b — Orbit, cycle, and cycle decomposition
For (u\in\Sigma_N), define the orbit[\mathcal{O}{N,s}(u):={T{N,s}^{,t}(u):t\in\mathbb{N}}.]A cycle is a finite orbit. The cycle decomposition of (T_{N,s}) is the partition of (\Sigma_N) into disjoint cycles under the action of the subgroup (\langle s\rangle\subseteq\Sigma_N).
04.S1.c — Cycle invariants: period and multiplicity
Define the orbit period (cycle length) at (u) as[\mathrm{per}{N,s}(u):=\min{,t\in\mathbb{N}{\ge 1}:\ T_{N,s}^{,t}(u)=u,}.]Define the cycle count[\mathrm{cyc}{N,s}:=#{\text{cycles in the decomposition of }T{N,s}}.]
04.S1.d — Visibility carrier (projection to the 15-station semantics)
Fix a dimension parameter (d\in\mathbb{N}_{\ge 1}). Define the dimension-indexed circle resolution[\boxed{B_d:=15\cdot 3^{d-1}}]as the canonical fine ring size required to represent the 15-station metro with (3^{d-1}) internal phase strata.
Define the station projection[\pi_d:\Sigma_{B_d}\to\Sigma_{15},\qquad\pi_d(u):=\left\lfloor \frac{u}{3^{d-1}}\right\rfloor,]so each station block has size (3^{d-1}). Define the internal stratum coordinate[q_d(u):=u-3^{d-1}\pi_d(u)\in{0,\dots,3^{d-1}-1}.]Thus each (u\in\Sigma_{B_d}) has a unique decomposition[u = 3^{d-1}\sigma + q,\qquad \sigma=\pi_d(u)\in\Sigma_{15},\quad q=q_d(u)\in{0,\dots,3^{d-1}-1}.]
04.S2 — Operators (Transforms)
04.S2.a — Cycle decomposition theorem (gcd law)
Let (N\in\mathbb{N}{\ge 2}), (s\in\Sigma_N). Let (g:=\gcd(N,s)). Then:[\boxed{\mathrm{cyc}{N,s}=g,\qquad \mathrm{per}{N,s}(u)=\frac{N}{g}\ \ \forall u\in\Sigma_N.}]Moreover, the cycles are the cosets of the subgroup (\langle s\rangle) and are precisely the residue classes modulo (g):[\boxed{\mathcal{O}{N,s}(u)={,u+t s\pmod N:\ t=0,1,\dots,\tfrac{N}{g}-1,}={,v\in\Sigma_N:\ v\equiv u\ (\mathrm{mod}\ g),}.}]
04.S2.b — The (N=15) gear and the (R)-step specialization
On the 15-ring, the canonical step values of interest are (s=R\pmod{15}), for gear parameter (R\in\mathbb{Z}). The resulting translation is[T_{15,R}(\sigma)=\sigma+R\pmod{15}.]The step (R=9) is a central case: the ring decomposes into three disjoint 5-cycles.
04.S2.c — Explicit 15-ring cycle families at step (R=9)
Let (N=15) and (s=9). Then (g=\gcd(15,9)=3), so there are (3) cycles of length (5). Concretely, the decomposition is by residue class modulo (3):
Cycle family A ((\sigma\equiv 0\pmod 3)):[(0\to 9\to 3\to 12\to 6\to 0).]
Cycle family B ((\sigma\equiv 1\pmod 3)):[(1\to 10\to 4\to 13\to 7\to 1).]
Cycle family C ((\sigma\equiv 2\pmod 3)):[(2\to 11\to 5\to 14\to 8\to 2).]These are the same three 5-cycles reported as the “gear loops” induced by the (R=9) circle gear.
04.S2.d — Transport of 15-ring cycles into station semantics (S/F/C/R subsets)
Using the station decoding (\mathrm{DEC}\sigma:\Sigma{15}\to\mathcal{P}^\star(\mathbb{L}_4)) from Ch03, the three 5-cycles become three semantic loop families on the 15 nonempty lens subsets. For (R=9), the explicit station membership lists are:
Family A: (\sigma={0,3,6,9,12}) with stations ({S,\ FC,\ R,\ SFCR,\ FCR}).
Family B: (\sigma={1,4,7,10,13}) with stations ({SF,\ C,\ SR,\ SFC,\ SC}).
Family C: (\sigma={2,5,8,11,14}) with stations ({F,\ CR,\ SFR,\ SCR,\ FR}).
These families constitute the structural partition revealed “purely by the circle gear.”
04.S3 — Invariants (What Stays)
04.S3.a — Orbit length and cycle count are gcd invariants
For a fixed (N), all orbits under (T_{N,s}) have identical length (N/\gcd(N,s)), and the number of cycles is (\gcd(N,s)). These are complete invariants of the translation’s cycle decomposition.
04.S3.b — Residue-class invariance (coset partition)
The partition of (\Sigma_N) induced by (T_{N,s}) equals the partition into congruence classes modulo (\gcd(N,s)). In particular, the 15-ring (R=9) decomposition is exactly the partition into (\sigma\bmod 3) classes.
04.S3.c — Semantic cycle membership invariance under encoding choice
Once the lens basis order and the station encoding (\sigma\leftrightarrow) (nonempty subsets of ({\square,\flower,\cloud,\fractal})) are pinned (Ch03), the induced semantic loop families are uniquely determined by the arithmetic of (T_{15,R}). The family membership sets ({0,3,6,9,12}), ({1,4,7,10,13}), ({2,5,8,11,14}) are fixed under that pinning.
04.S3.d — Tunnel signature at (N=15) (5-cycle criterion)
Define a 15-metro tunnel as a 5-cycle in (\Sigma_{15}) whose station set equals one of the residue-class cycles modulo (3). Under this definition, the tunnel signature is purely algebraic: it is the existence of a step (s) with (\gcd(15,s)=3), which yields exactly three disjoint 5-cycles. The “hidden corridors” are therefore equivalently characterized as 5-cycles in the 15-ring regime.
04.S4 — Protocols (How to Compute / Verify)
04.S4.a — Cycle decomposition algorithm (general (N,s))
def cycle_decomposition(N: int, s: int):
"""
Return disjoint cycles of translation u -> u+s mod N.
"""
s %= N
seen = [False]*N
cycles = []
for u0 in range(N):
if seen[u0]:
continue
cyc = []
u = u0
while not seen[u]:
seen[u] = True
cyc.append(u)
u = (u + s) % N
cycles.append(cyc)
return cycles
04.S4.b — gcd-based closed form checker
import math
def gcd_cycle_stats(N: int, s: int):
s %= N
g = math.gcd(N, s)
return {"gcd": g, "num_cycles": g, "cycle_length": N // g}
04.S4.c — (N=15,R=9) verification harness
cycles = cycle_decomposition(15, 9)
stats = gcd_cycle_stats(15, 9)
assert stats["gcd"] == 3 and stats["cycle_length"] == 5 and stats["num_cycles"] == 3
assert sorted([sorted(c) for c in cycles]) == [[0,3,6,9,12],[1,4,7,10,13],[2,5,8,11,14]]
This matches the reported three-family gear-loop partition at (R=9).
04.S4.d — Station-semantic loop extraction (15-ring)
# assumes enc/dec tables from Ch03 are available
def cycles_in_semantics(step_R: int):
cycles = cycle_decomposition(15, step_R)
return [[dec_sigma(sig) for sig in cyc] for cyc in cycles]
❀ Flower — Circle Gear as a Phase Router (From 15-Ring to (B_d)-Ring)
04.F1 — Ontology (Objects)
04.F1.a — Gear-locked phase increment (15-metro lock)
Fix the 15-station metro. The canonical gear-lock chooses (\alpha=\tfrac{1}{15}) and defines[\boxed{\Delta(R)=\frac{R}{15}\pmod 1.}]Under spin step (S_+(R)), (\psi\mapsto \psi+\Delta(R)) and the induced station step is[\boxed{\sigma \xrightarrow{S_+(R)} (\sigma+R)\bmod 15, \qquad\sigma \xrightarrow{S_-(R)} (\sigma-R)\bmod 15.}]
04.F1.b — Dimension-indexed refinement and the (B_d) circle resolution
In higher dimension, the circle must be refined to resolve internal phase strata associated to the triangle-per-axis structure; the canonical fine circle grid is[\boxed{B_d = 15\cdot 3^{d-1}.}]The key requirement is that increasing (d) requires increasing circle phase resolution; otherwise aliasing collapses distinct higher-dimensional tunnel classes into the same observed shadows.
04.F1.c — (B_d)-phase coordinate and station projection
Let (\psi\in\mathbb{T}^1) and define the (B_d)-phase integer coordinate[u:=u_{d}(\psi):=\lfloor B_d,\psi\rfloor\in\Sigma_{B_d}.]Define the station projection (\pi_d:\Sigma_{B_d}\to\Sigma_{15}) and internal coordinate (q_d) as in §04.S1.d:[u = 3^{d-1}\sigma + q,\qquad \sigma=\pi_d(u),\ q=q_d(u).]
04.F1.d — (B_d)-gear step for radial ladder (R=3^n)
Fix the radial ladder (R=3^n), (n\in\mathbb{Z}). On the (B_d)-grid, the canonical integer step for (n\ge 0) is[\boxed{S_+(n):\ u\mapsto u+3^n\pmod{B_d}.}]When micro-scales (n<0) must be treated as integer steps on a single grid, refine by (3^5) so that (R=3^{-5}=1/243) becomes a unit step:[\boxed{M_d:=B_d\cdot 3^{5}=15\cdot 3^{d+4}.}]
04.F2 — Operators (Transforms)
04.F2.a — Orbit length on (B_d) under macro step (3^n)
Let (B_d=15\cdot 3^{d-1}=5\cdot 3^d). For (n\ge 0), set (s=3^n). Then
[
\gcd(B_d,3^n)=3^{\min(d,n)},
]
and the orbit length is
[
\boxed{
L_{B}(d,n) := \frac{B_d}{\gcd(B_d,3^n)}
\begin{cases}5\cdot 3^{d-n}, & n\le d,\[4pt]5, & n\ge d.\end{cases}}]This is the (B_d)-analog of the master orbit-length law reported on the refined grid.
04.F2.b — Induced station dynamics and the crawl regime
Write (u=3^{d-1}\sigma+q). For step (u\mapsto u+3^n), the internal coordinate updates as[q\mapsto q+3^n\pmod{3^{d-1}},]and the station coordinate increments by the carry[\sigma\mapsto \sigma+\kappa(q;n)\pmod{15},\qquad\kappa(q;n):=\left\lfloor\frac{q+3^n}{3^{d-1}}\right\rfloor\in{0,1,2,\dots}.]For (n<d-1), (3^n<3^{d-1}) so (\kappa(q;n)\in{0,1}), yielding a deterministic crawl: (\sigma) advances by (1) once every (3^{d-1-n}) microsteps (on average) as (q) crosses the station boundary. This formalizes the “slow in high (d)” phenomenon.
04.F2.c — The snap regime and tunnel collapse ((n=d))
At (n=d) (i.e., (R=3^d)), the orbit length collapses to (5):[L_B(d,d)=5.]Equivalently, (u) advances by (3^d), which is (3\cdot 3^{d-1}), so the induced station step is (\sigma\mapsto \sigma+3\pmod{15}), forcing (\sigma) onto one of the three 5-cycles (residue classes modulo (3)). This is the precise “tunnel reveal” threshold and matches the snap-octave statement that at (R=3^d) the orbit is exactly a 5-cycle.
04.F2.d — Unified macro/micro integer stepping on (M_d) (±243 coverage)
On the refined grid (M_d=15\cdot 3^{d+4}), define the integer spin-step at radial exponent (n\in\mathbb{Z}) by[\boxed{S_+(n):\ u\mapsto u+3^{n+5}\pmod{M_d},}]so that (n=-5) yields step size (1).The orbit length is[\boxed{L(d,n)=\frac{M_d}{\gcd(M_d,3^{n+5})}}]with closed form[\boxed{L(d,n)=\begin{cases}5\cdot 3^{d-n}, & n\le d,\[4pt]5, & n\ge d.\end{cases}}]
04.F3 — Invariants (What Stays)
04.F3.a — Orbit length as the visibility invariant
For fixed ((d,n)), the orbit length (L_B(d,n)) (macro on (B_d)) or (L(d,n)) (macro/micro on (M_d)) is invariant under choice of starting (u_0); it is the primary algebraic invariant determining whether the observed station projection can collapse to a 5-cycle.
04.F3.b — Tunnel criterion on the station projection
Define the 15-metro tunnel families (in station index space) as the three 5-cycles:[\mathcal{T}_0={0,3,6,9,12},\quad\mathcal{T}_1={1,4,7,10,13},\quad\mathcal{T}_2={2,5,8,11,14}.]These are exactly the gear-loop families revealed at (R=9) (equivalently, step (s\equiv 0\pmod 3) but (s\not\equiv 0\pmod{15})).
A dimension-(d) orbit is tunnel-visible at exponent (n) if its station projection (\pi_d(\mathcal{O}_{B_d,3^n}(u_0))) is contained in a single (\mathcal{T}_r) and has period (5). The snap regime (n\ge d) is sufficient for tunnel visibility.
04.F3.c — Dimension delays the reveal (threshold law)
Higher dimension increases the internal 3-power strata (the (3^{d-1}) factor in (B_d)), which delays when the radial step (3^n) overwhelms internal strata and collapses to a 5-cycle regime.Formally, the threshold is[\boxed{n\ge d\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad L_B(d,n)=5\quad(\text{tunnel regime}).}]
04.F3.d — Resolution necessity as an aliasing invariant
If the circle is sampled at insufficient resolution relative to (d), distinct internal strata (q) collapse under projection (\pi_d), producing an aliasing/leakage defect: many-to-one mapping from true phase states to observed station states. This is a Nyquist-corridor failure mode in the general holographic transition grammar (fold/unfold is many-to-one outside corridor).
04.F4 — Protocols (How to Compute / Verify)
04.F4.a — (B_d) builder and station projection
def B_d(d: int) -> int:
return 15 * (3 ** (d - 1))
def proj_sigma(u: int, d: int) -> int:
return u // (3 ** (d - 1)) # in {0..14} when 0 <= u < B_d(d)
def proj_q(u: int, d: int) -> int:
return u % (3 ** (d - 1))
04.F4.b — Orbit-length closed form (macro)
import math
def orbit_length_B(d: int, n: int) -> int:
N = B_d(d)
s = 3 ** n
return N // math.gcd(N, s)
04.F4.c — Visibility threshold solver
def snap_exponent(d: int) -> int:
# minimal n such that orbit length collapses to 5 (tunnel regime)
return d
def snap_radius(d: int) -> int:
return 3 ** d
04.F4.d — Station-trace generator (crawl vs tunnel)
def station_trace(d: int, n: int, steps: int, u0: int = 0):
N = B_d(d)
s = 3 ** n
u = u0 % N
out = []
for _ in range(steps):
out.append(proj_sigma(u, d))
u = (u + s) % N
return out
☁ Cloud — Visibility as an Observation Channel (Aliasing, Coarse-Graining, and Information Loss)
04.C1 — Ontology (Objects)
04.C1.a — Deterministic gear walk as a Markov kernel
For (N) and step (s), define the deterministic Markov kernel on (\Sigma_N):[K_{N,s}(u,v):=\mathbf{1}{v=T_{N,s}(u)}.]This induces a permutation evolution on distributions (p\in\Delta_N):[p_{t+1}=K_{N,s#}p_t,\qquad (K_{N,s#}p)v=\sum_u p_u K{N,s}(u,v).]
04.C1.b — Observation channel: station projection (\pi_d)
Define the observation map (\pi_d:\Sigma_{B_d}\to\Sigma_{15}) (block projection).For a distribution (p\in\Delta_{B_d}), define the observed distribution[\bar p := (\pi_d)# p\in\Delta{15},\qquad\bar p_\sigma=\sum_{u:\ \pi_d(u)=\sigma} p_u.]
04.C1.c — Visibility as an identifiability property
A gear regime is observable at station level if the induced process on (\Sigma_{15}) is Markov and its state-transition structure is identifiable from (\bar p_t) without requiring access to the hidden variable (q).
04.C1.d — Aliasing defect as many-to-one collapse
The map (\pi_d) is many-to-one with fiber size (3^{d-1}). When the gear step is too small relative to the fiber size (crawl regime), the observed evolution (\bar p_t) loses information about the true orbit in (u)-space and can exhibit apparent stasis. This is the observation-channel analogue of spectral fold aliasing outside corridor.
04.C2 — Operators (Transforms)
04.C2.a — Coarse-grained evolution operator
Define the coarse-grained evolution operator on observed distributions by:[\bar p_{t}:=(\pi_d)# p_t,\qquad p{t+1}=K_{B_d,3^n#}p_t.]In general,[\bar p_{t+1} \neq \bar K_# \bar p_t]for any kernel (\bar K) on (\Sigma_{15}) unless the hidden coordinate (q) decouples (i.e., unless step size is a multiple of (3^{d-1}) and carries vanish). This separation of visible and hidden dynamics is the formal statement of “tunnels invisible at low projection.”
04.C2.b — Tunnel regime decoupling ((n\ge d))
When (n\ge d), the orbit collapses to a 5-cycle at the (u)-level, and the induced station dynamics becomes a strict 5-cycle within one tunnel family:[\sigma\mapsto \sigma+3\pmod{15},]hence the observed process is deterministic and Markov on its support.
04.C2.c — Crawl regime dwell-time scaling ((n<d-1))
For (n<d-1), (\sigma) advances by carry only. The expected dwell time per station scale is[\boxed{\tau_{\mathrm{dwell}}(d,n)\asymp 3^{d-1-n},}]reflecting that (q) must accumulate (3^{d-1}) units in increments (3^n) to advance (\sigma) once.
04.C2.d — Macro/micro unified channel on (M_d)
On the refined grid (M_d), the observation map (\pi_d^{(M)}:\Sigma_{M_d}\to\Sigma_{15}) is defined by block size (3^{d+4}):[\pi_d^{(M)}(u):=\left\lfloor \frac{u}{3^{d+4}}\right\rfloor.]The same crawl/tunnel dichotomy is governed by the orbit length (L(d,n)).
04.C3 — Invariants (What Stays)
04.C3.a — Period invariance and non-mixing
Since (K_{N,s}) is a permutation kernel, the evolution is periodic with period (N/\gcd(N,s)) and does not mix. All entropy functionals invariant under permutations remain constant.
04.C3.b — Information-loss invariant under coarse-graining
The channel ((\pi_d)_#) strictly decreases information unless the distribution is constant on fibers. This is a structural (not stochastic) uncertainty inflation: distinct (u)-states map to the same observed (\sigma)-state.
04.C3.c — Visibility invariant = station-level support collapse
A sufficient visibility invariant is:[|\mathrm{supp}(\pi_d(\mathcal{O}_{B_d,3^n}(u_0)))|\in{5,15}.]The tunnel regime yields size (5); the pre-tunnel regimes yield size (15) or slow coverage of (15) depending on (n) relative to (d).
04.C3.d — Corridor interpretation (Nyquist analogy)
The station projection is a sampling map. Insufficient circle resolution produces aliasing in the observation channel, matching the general defect family “aliasing/leakage” where fold is many-to-one outside the Nyquist corridor.
04.C4 — Protocols (How to Compute / Verify)
04.C4.a — Observed support size and dwell-time diagnostics
def observed_support_size(d: int, n: int, steps: int, u0: int = 0):
trace = station_trace(d, n, steps, u0=u0)
return len(set(trace))
def dwell_times(trace):
out = []
cur = trace[0]
run = 1
for x in trace[1:]:
if x == cur:
run += 1
else:
out.append((cur, run))
cur = x
run = 1
out.append((cur, run))
return out
04.C4.b — Tunnel visibility test (station-level)
T0 = {0,3,6,9,12}
T1 = {1,4,7,10,13}
T2 = {2,5,8,11,14}
def is_tunnel_visible_station_level(d: int, n: int, steps: int = 10_000, u0: int = 0):
tr = station_trace(d, n, steps, u0=u0)
supp = set(tr)
return (supp <= T0) or (supp <= T1) or (supp <= T2)
04.C4.c — Alias audit (fiber variability)
def fiber_size(d: int) -> int:
return 3 ** (d - 1)
def fiber_members(d: int, sigma: int):
# all u mapping to a given station sigma
b = 3 ** (d - 1)
start = sigma * b
return list(range(start, start + b))
04.C4.d — Cross-check with orbit-length law
def expected_tunnel(d: int, n: int) -> bool:
return n >= d # equivalent to orbit length 5 in the macro B_d model
✶ Fractal — Visibility Thresholds Across Dimension (Snap Octaves and Delayed Reveals)
04.R1 — Ontology (Objects)
04.R1.a — Dimension-indexed orbit length and snap exponent
Define the macro orbit length on (B_d):[L_B(d,n)=\frac{B_d}{\gcd(B_d,3^n)}.]Define the snap exponent (n_\star(d)) as the smallest (n\ge 0) such that (L_B(d,n)=5).
04.R1.b — Tunnel definition (intrinsic)
A tunnel is defined as a 5-cycle regime in the station projection, equivalently the regime in which the underlying gear action collapses to 5-cycle orbits and the observed station orbit lies entirely in one of the three tunnel families (\mathcal{T}_0,\mathcal{T}_1,\mathcal{T}_2).
04.R1.c — Dimension-dependent delay mechanism
Higher dimension increases the internal (3)-power strata ((3^{d-1}) blocks), which delays when a radial step (3^n) reaches the snap regime.
04.R1.d — Empirical visibility claims as schedule constraints
The dimension-by-d visibility outcomes at fixed macro radius (e.g., (R=243)) and varying (d) are governed by the snap inequality (n\ge d). The reported thresholds (“(d=5) first reveal at (R=243)”; “(d=7) needs (R\ge 2187)”) instantiate this law.
04.R2 — Operators (Transforms)
04.R2.a — Visibility theorem (macro (B_d))
Theorem (Visibility threshold on (B_d)).Let (B_d=15\cdot 3^{d-1}=5\cdot 3^d). Consider the macro gear step (u\mapsto u+3^n\pmod{B_d}) with (n\ge 0). Then:[L_B(d,n)=\begin{cases}5\cdot 3^{d-n}, & n\le d,\[4pt]5, & n\ge d.\end{cases}]In particular,[\boxed{n_\star(d)=d,\qquad R_\star(d)=3^d.}]At and beyond the snap exponent (n\ge d), every orbit in (u)-space is a 5-cycle and the station projection is confined to one tunnel family.
Proof.(\gcd(B_d,3^n)=\gcd(5\cdot 3^d,3^n)=3^{\min(d,n)}). Substitute into (L_B(d,n)=B_d/\gcd(B_d,3^n)).
04.R2.b — Refined visibility theorem (macro/micro (M_d))
On the refined grid (M_d=15\cdot 3^{d+4}=5\cdot 3^{d+5}), with step (u\mapsto u+3^{n+5}), the orbit length is exactly[L(d,n)=\begin{cases}5\cdot 3^{d-n}, & n\le d,\[4pt]5, & n\ge d,\end{cases}]matching the reported master law.
04.R2.c — Corollary (dimension-by-d snap points)
From (R_\star(d)=3^d), the snap radii are:[d=3\Rightarrow R_\star=27,\quadd=4\Rightarrow R_\star=81,\quadd=5\Rightarrow R_\star=243,\quadd=6\Rightarrow R_\star=729,\quadd=7\Rightarrow R_\star=2187.]These values align with the reported dimension-by-d outcomes (“(d=3) see at (R\ge 27)”; “(d=5) first reveal at (R=243)”; “(d=7) needs (R\ge 2187)”).
04.R2.d — Projection consequence (why “magic” appears)
For fixed (d), as (n) increases through (d), the orbit length drops discretely from (15) (at (n=d-1)) to (5) (at (n=d)). At the station level this appears as a sudden transition from full-station traversal to confinement on a tunnel 5-cycle, which constitutes the precise mechanism of “sudden teleports” at higher dimension when the threshold is crossed.
04.R3 — Invariants (What Stays)
04.R3.a — Snap invariance under starting state
For fixed ((d,n)), all orbits have identical length (L_B(d,n)) (or (L(d,n)) on (M_d)); thus the snap threshold depends only on ((d,n)), not on initial conditions.
04.R3.b — Dimension monotonicity of the reveal
The snap exponent (n_\star(d)=d) is strictly increasing with (d). Therefore, higher dimension strictly delays the first tunnel-visible octave.
04.R3.c — Tunnel structure invariance (three families)
When tunnel-visible, the station projection is confined to one of three invariant 5-cycles (the residue-class cycles modulo (3)) whose membership is independent of (d); only the internal strata (q) changes with (d).
04.R3.d — Alias invariance as a defect-class marker
Pre-snap regimes ((n<d)) necessarily involve nontrivial internal-stratum evolution and therefore nontrivial information loss under station projection. This is a structural aliasing defect, not numerical error, and is classified under the general “aliasing/leakage” defect family.
04.R4 — Protocols (How to Compute / Verify)
04.R4.a — Snap point computation (macro)
def snap_radius_macro(d: int) -> int:
return 3 ** d
def snap_exponent_macro(d: int) -> int:
return d
04.R4.b — Orbit-length table generator (macro)
def orbit_length_table(d_max: int, n_max: int):
out = {}
for d in range(1, d_max+1):
out[d] = {}
for n in range(0, n_max+1):
out[d][n] = orbit_length_B(d, n)
return out
04.R4.c — Visibility verification against reported thresholds
For a fixed macro radius (R=243=3^5) (i.e., (n=5)), the theorem predicts:
tunnel-visible iff (5\ge d),
pre-tunnel iff (d>5),matching the reported classification ((d=5) critical; (d=7) still invisible).
04.R4.d — Explicit tunnel-family extractor (15-ring)
def tunnel_families_15():
return [sorted([r + 3*k for k in range(5)]) for r in [0,1,2]]
This returns (\mathcal{T}_0,\mathcal{T}_1,\mathcal{T}_2) as the canonical 5-cycle families.
Ch04 — Gear-Loop Decomposition and “Visibility”
Ch05 — Triangle Modes (global vs per-axis)
Option A vs Option B as a Pinned Corridor Policy
□ Square — Discrete Control Carriers (Policy Objects, State Types, and Serialization)
05.S1 — Objects
05.S1.a — Triangle phase alphabets and index sets
Let (\mathbb{Z}3:={0,1,2}) with addition modulo (3).Let (d\in\mathbb{N}{\ge 1}) and let ([d]:={1,\dots,d}).
Define the two admissible Triangle phase carriers:
Option A (per-axis Triangle):[\mathcal{T}^{A}_d := (\mathbb{Z}_3)^d,\qquad\tau^{A}=(\tau_1,\dots,\tau_d)\in\mathcal{T}^{A}_d .]This is the higher-dimensional “triangle per axis” semantics.
Option B (global Triangle):[\mathcal{T}^{B} := \mathbb{Z}_3,\qquad\tau^{B}\in\mathcal{T}^{B}.]This is the “one shared governor” semantics.
05.S1.b — Control-state triple (recursion governor)
Define the Triangle control state (governor state) as the canonical trit triple[G:=(t_0,t_1,t_2)\in \mathbb{Z}_3^3,]with pinned interpretation under a control profile digest.
Define the serialization-only scalar encoding[\mathrm{val}(G):=t_0+3t_1+9t_2\in\mathbb{Z}_{27},]used strictly for indexing/serialization (control logic operates on components).
Triangle is a governor: recursion/control events (carry/hatch) are the only legal mechanism to increase depth; Triangle cannot introduce new content, only controls legal refinement and nesting.
05.S1.c — Corridor policy object pinning Triangle mode
Define a TriangleModePolicy as a pinned policy object[\Pi_\triangle := (\mathrm{Mode},\ \mathrm{QuantizerID},\ \mathrm{MixID},\ \mathrm{AggID},\ \mathrm{Pins}),]where:
(\mathrm{Mode}\in{\mathrm{AXIS},\mathrm{GLOBAL}}) selects Option A vs B.
(\mathrm{QuantizerID}) pins the trit-extraction rule (including whether fractional-part reduction is used and how wrap scaling enters).
(\mathrm{MixID}) pins the global mix operator (required iff (\mathrm{Mode}=\mathrm{GLOBAL})).
(\mathrm{AggID}) pins the aggregation map from ((\mathbb{Z}_3)^d\to\mathbb{Z}_3) if the control-plane requires scalar gating but the observation plane is per-axis (optional; must be explicit if used).
(\mathrm{Pins}) contains digests required by “no hidden knobs” discipline (any variability affecting meaning must be pinned or deterministically derived).
Changing (\Pi_\triangle) is semantic (must be represented as an explicit evolution edge under the corpus’ transport discipline).
05.S1.d — Typed Triangle state objects (A vs B)
Let (\delta) be the depth budget and (\varepsilon) be pinned trigger thresholds (corridor-controlled). TriangleState is always accompanied by such budgets and pins.
Define the Triangle subsystem state as:
Option A state:[\mathsf{TriState}^{A}(d):=(\tau^{A}\in(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d,\ G\in\mathbb{Z}3^3,\ \delta,\ \varepsilon,\ \Pi\triangle).]
Option B state:[\mathsf{TriState}^{B}:=(\tau^{B}\in\mathbb{Z}_3,\ G\in\mathbb{Z}3^3,\ \delta,\ \varepsilon,\ \Pi\triangle).]
Determinism requirement: all updates to (G) and to the triangle phase(s) are deterministic given inputs and pinned profiles.
05.S2 — Operators
05.S2.a — Core trit quantizer (discrete rule)
Define the trit quantizer on a unit phase coordinate (u\in\mathbb{T}^1=\mathbb{R}/\mathbb{Z}) by[Q_3(u):=\big\lfloor 3u\big\rfloor\in\mathbb{Z}_3,]where (u) is represented as a canonical fractional representative in ([0,1)).
Define the wrapped quantizer at wrap factor (R\in\mathbb{N}):[Q_3^{(R)}(\phi):=Q_3\big(\operatorname{frac}(R\phi)\big)\in\mathbb{Z}_3,\qquad \operatorname{frac}(x):=x-\lfloor x\rfloor.]This makes “triangle is a 3-phase operator on the circle coordinate” literal.
05.S2.b — Option A operator: per-axis Triangle extraction
Given a torus phase (\Phi=(\phi_1,\dots,\phi_d)\in\mathbb{T}^d) and wrap (R), define[\boxed{\mathsf{Tri}^{A}_{R}(\Phi):=\big(Q_3^{(R)}(\phi_1),\dots,Q_3^{(R)}(\phi_d)\big)\in(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d.}]This is the componentwise triangle described for higher-D: “you have a triangle per axis unless intentionally collapsed.”
The induced discrete product structure is the clean generalization of (12=4\times 3):[(\mathbb{Z}_4\times\mathbb{Z}_3)^d \cong (4\times 3)^d = 12^d.]
05.S2.c — Option B operator: global Triangle extraction via pinned mix
Option B requires a pinned combiner (\mathrm{mix}:\mathbb{T}^d\to\mathbb{T}^1) that is stable under the system’s holographic truncation discipline.
A canonical lossless mix is induced by digit interleaving of the square address (a chart change that preserves the hologram):interleave base-4 digits into a single base-4 integer (J) with (kd) digits, and define[\phi_{\mathrm{global}}:=\frac{J}{4^{kd}}.]This yields a bijection[(\mathbb{Z}{4^k})^d \longleftrightarrow \mathbb{Z}{4^{kd}}.]
Given such a pinned (\phi_{\mathrm{global}}), define[\boxed{\mathsf{Tri}^{B}{R}(\Phi):=Q_3^{(R)}!\big(\phi{\mathrm{global}}(\Phi)\big)\in\mathbb{Z}_3.}]This is the “one global Triangle phase (shared governor)” semantics.
05.S2.d — Mode policy gates and legal transitions
Define the policy gate:[(\mathrm{Mode}=\mathrm{AXIS}) \Rightarrow \tau\in(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d,\qquad(\mathrm{Mode}=\mathrm{GLOBAL}) \Rightarrow \tau\in\mathbb{Z}_3.]
A mode switch is a semantic change to the typed state space and therefore must be explicit under the corpus’ evolution discipline (“no silent forks; no hidden knobs”).
If a conversion (F:(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d\to\mathbb{Z}3) is used (aggregation), then (F) is part of (\Pi\triangle) and must be pinned; otherwise the conversion is illegal.
05.S3 — Invariants
05.S3.a — Consistency: both modes are phase-locked admissible choices
Both Option A and Option B are consistent higher-dimensional choices and are phase-locked when defined via pinned quantizers/mixers.
Formally, for any pinned (R), the image sets are:[\mathsf{Tri}^A_R:\mathbb{T}^d\to(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d,\qquad\mathsf{Tri}^B_R:\mathbb{T}^d\to\mathbb{Z}_3,]and both commute with the canonical action of integer translation in wrap space up to modular equivalence on (\mathbb{Z}_3) (since the codomain is discrete).
05.S3.b — Determinism and “no hidden knobs” invariants
All Triangle updates are deterministic given inputs and pinned profile identity; any adaptive behavior must be encoded or deterministically derived.
Any variability affecting decode/meaning must be pinned (digest) or deterministically derived from pinned tables and encoded artifacts.
05.S3.c — Information relations between Option A and Option B
Option A carries (d) trits per evaluation; Option B carries one trit per evaluation. Consequently:
There exists a surjective aggregation map (F:(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d\to\mathbb{Z}_3) (many choices), but (F) is not canonical without a pinned policy.
There is no injective map (\mathbb{Z}_3\to(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d) consistent with semantics without adding extra information.
Thus, Option B is a quotient of Option A at the level of (\tau)-representation (even when (\phi_{\mathrm{global}}) is lossless).
05.S3.d — Governor invariants (Triangle cannot create content; only gates refinement)
Triangle is the recursion/control plane; it governs initiation/mixing/stabilization selection and the legality of depth change, while not introducing new content.
Any depth increase must be represented by a certified hatch event and must pass trigger legality, depth budget, inheritance pin equality, checkpoint creation, and replay verification; implicit recursion is illegal.
05.S4 — Protocols
05.S4.a — Canonical digit-interleaving mix (lossless global phase)
Given (d,k) and square coordinates (x_i\in{0,\dots,4^k-1}), write base-4 digits[x_i=\sum_{t=0}^{k-1} x_{i,t}4^{t},\qquad x_{i,t}\in{0,1,2,3}.]Define the interleaved integer[J:=\sum_{t=0}^{k-1}\sum_{i=1}^{d} 4^{dt+(i-1)},x_{i,t},\qquad\phi_{\mathrm{global}}:=\frac{J}{4^{kd}}.]This realizes the bijection ((\mathbb{Z}{4^k})^d\leftrightarrow \mathbb{Z}{4^{kd}}).
05.S4.b — Reference implementation (Triangle phases A/B)
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Callable, List, Literal, Tuple
Mode = Literal["AXIS", "GLOBAL"]
def frac(x: float) -> float:
# Canonical fractional part in [0,1)
return x - int(x // 1)
def q3(u01: float) -> int:
# u01 in [0,1)
t = int(3 * u01)
return t if t < 3 else 2 # guard against u01=1.0 by float error
def q3_wrapped(phi: float, R: int) -> int:
return q3(frac(R * phi))
def interleave_base4_digits(x: List[int], d: int, k: int) -> int:
"""
x: list length d with 0 <= x[i] < 4^k
returns interleaved J in [0, 4^(k*d)-1]
"""
assert len(x) == d
J = 0
for t in range(k):
for i in range(d):
digit = (x[i] >> (2 * t)) & 0b11 # base-4 digit at level t
J |= (digit << (2 * (d * t + i)))
return J
def phi_global_from_square(x: List[int], d: int, k: int) -> float:
J = interleave_base4_digits(x, d, k)
return J / float(4 ** (k * d))
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class TriangleModePolicy:
mode: Mode
quantizer_id: str
mix_id: str | None # required for GLOBAL
agg_id: str | None # optional
pins: Tuple[Tuple[str, str], ...] # (key,digest) pairs
def tri_A_from_phi(phi_vec: List[float], R: int) -> Tuple[int, ...]:
return tuple(q3_wrapped(phi, R) for phi in phi_vec)
def tri_B_from_phi(phi_global: float, R: int) -> int:
return q3_wrapped(phi_global, R)
05.S4.c — Policy validation harness
def validate_policy(policy: TriangleModePolicy):
assert policy.mode in ("AXIS", "GLOBAL")
if policy.mode == "GLOBAL":
assert policy.mix_id is not None
# pins must be deterministic and ordered
assert all(isinstance(k, str) and isinstance(v, str) for k, v in policy.pins)
def verify_interleave_bijection(d: int, k: int, samples: List[List[int]]):
# Empirical collision check on provided samples
seen = {}
for x in samples:
J = interleave_base4_digits(x, d, k)
if J in seen and seen[J] != x:
raise AssertionError("Collision detected (violates bijection on sample).")
seen[J] = x
05.S4.d — Conformance obligations for mode selection
A TriangleModePolicy instance (\Pi_\triangle) is publishable as OK only if:
(\mathrm{Mode}) is pinned and referenced by digest in the registry/policy manifest (no hidden knobs).
If (\mathrm{Mode}=\mathrm{GLOBAL}), (\mathrm{MixID}) pins a stable mixing operator; if interleaving is used, its correctness is witnessed by the bijection law.
Any aggregation (F) used to feed scalar control gates from per-axis phases is pinned ((\mathrm{AggID})) and replay-verifiable.
Any policy change is represented explicitly under corpus evolution (no silent forks).
❀ Flower — Continuous Triangle Semantics on (\mathbb{T}^d) (Phase, Wraps, and Quantization)
05.F1 — Objects
05.F1.a — Torus phase and revolution scaling
Let[\mathbb{T}^d := (\mathbb{R}/\mathbb{Z})^d,\qquad \Phi=(\phi_1,\dots,\phi_d)\in\mathbb{T}^d.]Higher-D “circle” is a torus.
Define revolution scaling componentwise:[\Phi_R := {R\Phi} = ({R\phi_1},\dots,{R\phi_d}).]
05.F1.b — Triangle extraction as a 3-partition of wrapped phase
Define per-axis triangle as:[\tau_i(R):=\big\lfloor 3,{R\phi_i}\big\rfloor\in\mathbb{Z}_3.]This formalizes “Triangle (3-phase) becomes componentwise.”
05.F1.c — Global collapse (chart change) enabling global Triangle
A lossless collapse torus (\to) one global circle is realized by a bijection between ((\mathbb{Z}{4^k})^d) and (\mathbb{Z}{4^{kd}}) via digit interleaving into (J), inducing (\phi_{\mathrm{global}}=J/4^{kd}).
This yields a canonical (pinned) (\mathrm{mix}) operator:[\mathrm{mix}{d,k}(\Phi):=\phi{\mathrm{global}}(\Phi)\in\mathbb{T}^1.]
05.F1.d — Two correct higher-D Triangle choices (semantic statement)
In higher dimension, triangle is per axis unless intentionally collapsed to a global one.Both choices are consistent and phase-locked:[\text{Option A: }\ \tau_i=\lfloor 3\phi_i\rfloor\in\mathbb{Z}_3,\qquad\text{Option B: }\ \tau=\lfloor 3,\mathrm{mix}(\Phi)\rfloor\in\mathbb{Z}_3.]
05.F2 — Operators
05.F2.a — Option A: torus-to-trit vector operator
Define[\mathsf{Tri}^{A}:\mathbb{T}^d\times\mathbb{N}\to(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d,\qquad\mathsf{Tri}^{A}(\Phi;R):=(\tau_1(R),\dots,\tau_d(R)).]
05.F2.b — Option B: torus-to-trit scalar operator via mix
Define[\mathsf{Tri}^{B}:\mathbb{T}^d\times\mathbb{N}\to\mathbb{Z}_3,\qquad\mathsf{Tri}^{B}(\Phi;R):=\left\lfloor 3,{R,\mathrm{mix}(\Phi)}\right\rfloor.]If (\mathrm{mix}) is implemented via digit interleaving, it is a chart change, not a loss of information at the phase level.
05.F2.c — Phase-advance operator (mode rotation)
Define the mode rotation on (\mathbb{Z}_3):[\mathrm{Rot}_3(\tau):=\tau+1\pmod 3.]For Option A, define (\mathrm{Rot}_3) componentwise on ((\mathbb{Z}_3)^d).
05.F2.d — Compatibility operator: scalarization of vector Triangle (pinned)
If a scalar gate is required while observing per-axis phases, define a pinned map[F:(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d\to\mathbb{Z}3](e.g., majority, parity, weighted sum mod 3, or a digest-pinned lookup). No such map is implied; it is admissible only if pinned in (\Pi\triangle).
05.F3 — Invariants
05.F3.a — Range invariants
For any (\Phi) and (R),[\tau_i(R)\in{0,1,2},\qquad \mathsf{Tri}^{A}(\Phi;R)\in(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d,\qquad \mathsf{Tri}^{B}(\Phi;R)\in\mathbb{Z}_3.]
05.F3.b — Wrap-scaling invariance class
Triangle depends only on the wrapped phase ({R\phi}). Therefore, for any integer (m),[{R\phi}={(R+m)\phi}]holds iff (m\phi\in\mathbb{Z}) (i.e., the additional wraps land on an integer boundary). This characterizes when wrap increments are triangle-invisible.
05.F3.c — Phase-lock compatibility with higher-D circle definition
The system treats higher-D circle coordinates as (\Phi=(x_1/4^k,\dots,x_d/4^k)) under the canonical projection.Triangle extraction operates on these fractions via the quantizer; thus Triangle is a discrete shadow of the same hologram state, not an independent degree of freedom.
05.F3.d — Structural interpretation invariant (axis vs global)
Option A treats Triangle as an axis-factorized 3-phase traversal, yielding a product structure.Option B treats Triangle as a shared governor participating in a single meta-cycle.The chosen interpretation is part of the meaning-bearing policy and must be pinned.
05.F4 — Protocols
05.F4.a — Exact evaluation protocol at rational hubs
For (\phi_i=p_i/q_i) with (q_i\mid R), ({R\phi_i}=0) and (\tau_i(R)=0).Thus hub fractions aligned with wrap scaling become exact Triangle reset points (a deterministic trigger surface candidate).
05.F4.b — Cross-check protocol: global mode with lossless mix
When (\mathrm{mix}) is implemented by digit interleaving (lossless), verify:[\Phi \leftrightarrow \phi_{\mathrm{global}}]is bijective at the Square address level ((\mathbb{Z}{4^k})^d \leftrightarrow \mathbb{Z}{4^{kd}}).Then Triangle scalar extraction is a deterministic function of the same underlying state.
05.F4.c — Mode conformance test suite (analytic)
A Triangle implementation passes conformance if:
Option A returns a (d)-vector of trits and is componentwise consistent with (\tau_i(R)=\lfloor 3{R\phi_i}\rfloor).
Option B returns a scalar trit and uses a pinned (\mathrm{mix}).
Any use of a global Triangle when starting from per-axis phases is documented as either (i) lossless chart-change at the phase carrier level, or (ii) an intentional quotient at the trit shadow level (policy pinned).
05.F4.d — Phase-to-control signal protocol (bridge contract)
Define a pinned mapping from triangle phase(s) to control signals used by (G) (stress/defect/depth gate counters). The mapping is deterministic and referenced by the control profile digest.
☁ Cloud — Distributions over Triangle Modes (Uncertainty, Identifiability, and Coarse-Graining)
05.C1 — Objects
05.C1.a — Distribution spaces for Triangle observations
Define the simplices:[\Delta(\mathbb{Z}_3):={p\in\mathbb{R}^3:\ p_i\ge 0,\ \sum_i p_i=1},\qquad\Delta((\mathbb{Z}_3)^d):={p\in\mathbb{R}^{3^d}:\ p\ge 0,\ |p|_1=1}.]These represent uncertainty over global vs per-axis Triangle phase readouts.
05.C1.b — Pushforward under quantization (observation channel)
Let (\Phi) be a random variable on (\mathbb{T}^d) with law (\mu).Define the induced Triangle laws by pushforward:[p^{A} := (\mathsf{Tri}^{A}{R})# \mu \in \Delta((\mathbb{Z}3)^d),\qquadp^{B} := (\mathsf{Tri}^{B}{R})_# \mu \in \Delta(\mathbb{Z}_3).]
05.C1.c — Policy-conditioning (mode is not inferential)
Triangle mode selection is not inferred from data; it is pinned by (\Pi_\triangle) (a corridor/policy object).Therefore, probabilistic statements about (\tau) are always conditioned on the pinned mode.
05.C1.d — Control context as a random variable under noise models
If phase measurements are noisy, treat (\Phi) as an uncertain latent and (G) as a deterministic state updated from pinned signals; then the induced uncertainty in Triangle observations is entirely via the observation channel (\Phi\mapsto \tau) and never via unpinned update rules.
05.C2 — Operators
05.C2.a — Marginalization from Option A to Option B (pinned aggregator)
Given (p^{A}\in\Delta((\mathbb{Z}3)^d)) and a pinned aggregator (F:(\mathbb{Z}3)^d\to\mathbb{Z}3), define[p^{B}{F} := F# p^{A}\in\Delta(\mathbb{Z}3),\qquadp^{B}{F}(t)=\sum{\mathbf{u}:F(\mathbf{u})=t} p^{A}(\mathbf{u}).]No default (F) exists without policy pins.
05.C2.b — Fiber uniformity tests (lossless mix vs lossy aggregation)
If Option B uses lossless (\mathrm{mix}) at the phase level, then (\Phi\leftrightarrow \phi_{\mathrm{global}}) is bijective (address-level).Any additional reduction to a scalar trit is a lossy coarse-graining; characterize its fibers as:[\mathsf{Tri}^{B}_{R}{}^{-1}(t)\subseteq \mathbb{T}^d.]
05.C2.c — Entropy invariants under deterministic time evolution
When the Triangle update on (\tau) is a deterministic permutation (e.g., (\tau\mapsto\tau+1) mod 3, componentwise), the induced distribution evolves by permutation, hence Shannon entropy is invariant:[H(p_{t+1}) = H(p_t).]
05.C2.d — Identifiability criterion for per-axis vs global observation
Given only scalar (\tau^B), the per-axis (\tau^A) is generally non-identifiable (multiple latent (\tau^A) map to the same observed (\tau^B)) unless additional observations or pinned constraints are provided. This is a structural uncertainty (many-to-one observation channel), not sampling noise.
05.C3 — Invariants
05.C3.a — Policy invariance of admissibility
Mode (\mathrm{AXIS}) and (\mathrm{GLOBAL}) are both admissible choices; admissibility is determined by the corridor/policy, not by posterior probability.
05.C3.b — Conservation of probability mass under Triangle permutations
Triangle phase updates that are group actions preserve (\ell^1) mass and simplex constraints by construction.
05.C3.c — No-hidden-knobs invariant for probabilistic statements
Any statistical pipeline that outputs a claim about Triangle must include (\Pi_\triangle) pins in its digestable provenance; otherwise claims are invalid (policy not declared).
05.C3.d — Governor constraint invariant (depth increases are not probabilistic accidents)
Depth increases occur only via certified hatch events, not via stochastic drift; uncertainty may exist in trigger evidence, but the act of recursion is a typed event requiring verification.
05.C4 — Protocols
05.C4.a — Empirical estimator protocol for (p^A) and (p^B)
Given samples (\Phi^{(n)}), estimate:[\widehat{p}^{A}(u)=\frac{1}{N}\sum_{n=1}^N \mathbf{1}{\mathsf{Tri}^{A}R(\Phi^{(n)})=u},\quad\widehat{p}^{B}(t)=\frac{1}{N}\sum{n=1}^N \mathbf{1}{\mathsf{Tri}^{B}R(\Phi^{(n)})=t}.]Attach the pinned (\Pi\triangle) digest to the estimator output.
05.C4.b — Drift audit protocol
If observed empirical frequencies shift across runs, the replay kernel must detect whether the shift is attributable to (i) changed pins, (ii) changed input digests, or (iii) nondeterminism; unpinned variability is a typed failure.
05.C4.c — Aggregator conformance protocol (if used)
If an aggregator (F) is used, produce a conformance witness containing:
definition of (F) (table or formula),
proof that (F) is deterministic,
regression tests verifying identical output under replay.
05.C4.d — Evidence-plan protocol for mode ambiguity claims
If any pipeline claims uncertainty about whether Option A or Option B is “correct,” such a claim must be typed AMBIG and must return an evidence plan; however, within this framework the mode is a pinned policy choice, so “mode ambiguity” is treated as a policy conflict, not a data inference.
✶ Fractal — Triangle as the Legal Recursion Plane (Carry, Hatch, and Replay Discipline)
05.R1 — Objects
05.R1.a — Tria Prima operator basis (control action families)
Define the triadic operator basis[\mathsf{OT}:=(\mathsf{Su},\mathsf{Me},\mathsf{Sa}),]each a typed control interface producing a new control context and obligations.
Interpretation: Su emphasizes initiation/partition, Me emphasizes mixing/transport, Sa emphasizes stabilization/sealing; behavior is pinned.
05.R1.b — Carry hyperplanes and trigger predicates
Define the carry hyperplane set (\mathrm{CH}) as the certified boundary locus where carry-free and carry-propagating laws diverge, detected by pinned deterministic detectors.
Trigger predicates reference (\mathrm{CH}) and additional pinned signals (residual drift, lock proximity), all replayable.
05.R1.c — HatchEvent object (the only legal recursion mechanism)
Define HatchEvent as the only legal recursion mechanism:[\mathsf{HE}:=(\mathrm{HatchID},\mathrm{ParentSnapshot},\mathrm{TriggerEvidence},\mathrm{InheritanceSpec},\mathrm{ChildInitOffsets},\mathrm{Checkpoint},\mathrm{Obligations},\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{PulseID}),]with mandatory checkpoint and replay pointer.
05.R1.d — ControlContext object
A control context (\mathsf{CC}) includes (G) and profile pins (and optional depth stack/offsets when recursion is enabled).
05.R2 — Operators
05.R2.a — Carry operator and hatch emission
Define a deterministic carry operator[\mathrm{Carry}_\triangle:\mathsf{CC}\times\mathsf{Signals}\to(\mathsf{CC}',\ \mathsf{HE}\ \text{or}\ \emptyset),]consistent with the master operator-family schema.
05.R2.b — Recursion legality operator (hatch verifier)
Define (\mathrm{VerifyHatch}(\mathsf{HE})) which returns a truth type under corridor evaluation and requires replay verification for OK. Any implicit recursion is illegal.
05.R2.c — Mode-consistent signal extraction for control updates
Define a pinned mapping from (\tau^{A}) or (\tau^{B}) into control signals driving (G). The mapping is part of (\Pi_\triangle) and must be deterministic; it may depend on axis index only through declared tables (no implicit coupling).
05.R2.d — Serialization and replay capsules for Triangle events
All Triangle events (carry/hatch updates) must be replayable under pinned environment and pins; replay determinism is the criterion for OK closure.
05.R3 — Invariants
05.R3.a — Legal recursion invariant
Any depth increase must be represented by a HatchEvent that passes trigger legality, depth budget, inheritance pin equality, checkpoint creation, and replay verification.
05.R3.b — Triangle mediation invariant (admissibility gate)
Triangle mediation is an admissibility gate constraining which Circle/Square couplings are legal; coupling affecting meaning requires declared bridges and pinned profile identity with witnesses/replays.
05.R3.c — Control cannot introduce new content
Triangle cannot introduce new content; it only governs legal refinement and nesting.
05.R3.d — Mode pinning invariant across recursion boundaries
Hatch inheritance must specify which profiles are inherited and which overrides (if any) are permitted; Triangle mode ((\Pi_\triangle)) is an inherited pin unless explicitly overridden under an inheritance spec that is itself pinned and verified.
05.R4 — Protocols
05.R4.a — Deterministic hatch construction protocol
A HatchEvent must include:
parent snapshot including (\circ!\square!\triangle) state and pins,
trigger evidence binding (\mathrm{CH}) evaluation,
deterministic child init offsets,
checkpoint creation,
obligations list,
replay pointer and pins.
05.R4.b — Minimal replay capsule for Triangle legality
A minimal replay capsule for hatch legality includes: pinned corridor profile, pinned TriangleModePolicy (\Pi_\triangle), trigger inputs, expected legality outcome, and canonical digests to compare.
05.R4.c — Reference implementation (Triangle control-state skeleton)
@dataclass
class TriangleState:
# Governor trits
t0: int # in {0,1,2}
t1: int
t2: int
# Budgets / thresholds (opaque but pinned)
depth_budget: int
pins: Tuple[Tuple[str, str], ...]
def val_G(ts: TriangleState) -> int:
return (ts.t0 + 3*ts.t1 + 9*ts.t2) % 27
def carry_triangle_step(ts: TriangleState, signals: dict) -> TriangleState:
"""
Deterministic update rule placeholder.
The concrete rule is pinned by ControlProfileDigest; any variation must be encoded.
"""
# Example deterministic skeleton:
t0 = (ts.t0 + int(signals.get("drive_inc", 0))) % 3
t1 = (ts.t1 + int(signals.get("defect_inc", 0))) % 3
t2 = (ts.t2 + int(signals.get("depth_gate_inc", 0))) % 3
return TriangleState(t0=t0, t1=t1, t2=t2, depth_budget=ts.depth_budget, pins=ts.pins)
05.R4.d — Audit protocol for mode integrity
At every recursion boundary (hatch), verify:
(\Pi_\triangle) digest equality under inheritance (or explicit override with pinned justification),
deterministic reproduction of (\tau) extraction given the same (\Phi) (or (\mathbf{x})) and wrap rule,
deterministic reproduction of (G) updates under pinned control profile.
Any mismatch under identical pins is a typed integrity failure requiring quarantine/fence propagation.
Ch05 — Triangle Modes (global vs per-axis)
Ch06 — Tunneling as Hub-Preserving Routing on (\mathbb{T}^d)
Hub meshes (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}), multi-axis tunnel steps, and deterministic hub-first route synthesis
□ Square — Hub Keys, Hub Classes, and Address-Compatible Routing
06.S1 — Objects
06.S1.a — The 1D hub set (\mathcal{H}) (nexus fractions)
Let the hub denominator set be[\mathcal{D}:={2,3,4,6,12,36}.]Define the 1D hub set (modulo (1)) by[\boxed{\mathcal{H}:=\left{\frac{k}{d}\ \bmod 1:\ d\in\mathcal{D},\ k\in\mathbb{Z}\right}\subset \mathbb{T}^1.}]This (\mathcal{H}) is the explicit “tunneling skeleton” of stable nexus fractions.
06.S1.b — The (d)-dimensional hub mesh (\mathcal{H}^{(d)})
Define the hub mesh in (\mathbb{T}^d) as the Cartesian power[\boxed{\mathcal{H}^{(d)} := \mathcal{H}^d\subset \mathbb{T}^d.}]Equivalently, (\mathbf{h}\in\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) iff each coordinate (h_i\in\mathcal{H}).
06.S1.c — Circle distance and nearest-hub selector (pinned)
Define the circular distance on (\mathbb{T}^1) by[\mathrm{dist}{\mathbb{T}^1}(u,v):=\min{m\in\mathbb{Z}}\big| (u-v)-m\big|\in\left[0,\tfrac12\right].]On (\mathbb{T}^d), fix a pinned product metric (\mathrm{Dist}{\mathbb{T}^d}) by policy; the default metric is[\mathrm{Dist}{\infty}(\Phi,\Psi):=\max_{1\le i\le d}\mathrm{dist}{\mathbb{T}^1}(\phi_i,\psi_i).]Define the nearest-hub selector on (\mathbb{T}^1) by[\boxed{\mathrm{Hub}(\phi):=\operatorname*{argmin}{q\in\mathcal{H}}\ \mathrm{dist}_{\mathbb{T}^1}(\phi,q),}]with a deterministic tie-break rule pinned in the corridor profile (e.g., minimal denominator then minimal residue class). The canonical hub selection rule is required to be stable under truncation: prefix truncation must not change the coarse hub class.
Extend coordinatewise to (\mathbb{T}^d):[\boxed{\mathrm{Hub}^{(d)}(\Phi):=\big(\mathrm{Hub}(\phi_1),\dots,\mathrm{Hub}(\phi_d)\big)\in \mathcal{H}^{(d)}.}]
06.S1.d — The hub-preserving key (\psi_\star) and coarse hub class
Define the hub-preserving key for (\phi\in\mathbb{T}^1) at octave/depth index (n\in\mathbb{N}{\ge 1}) as[\boxed{\psi\star(\phi;n):=(h,r,n),\qquadh=\mathrm{Hub}(\phi),\quad r=\phi-h\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1)\in[-\tfrac12,\tfrac12).}]This key stores the nearest hub, signed residual, and octave level as the canonical holographic descriptor.
In (d) dimensions, define[\boxed{\psi_\star^{(d)}(\Phi;n):=\big(\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r},n\big),\qquad\mathbf{h}=\mathrm{Hub}^{(d)}(\Phi),\quad\mathbf{r}=\Phi-\mathbf{h}\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1)\in[-\tfrac12,\tfrac12)^d.}]Define the coarse hub class of (\Phi) as (\mathbf{h}\in\mathcal{H}^{(d)}). The primary requirement is that prefix truncation must not change this coarse hub class.
06.S2 — Operators
06.S2.a — Hub snap and residual extraction
Define the hub snap (nearest-hub projection) on (\mathbb{T}^d) by[\boxed{\mathrm{Snap}(\Phi):=\mathrm{Hub}^{(d)}(\Phi)=\mathbf{h}.}]Define the residual extraction[\boxed{\mathrm{Res}(\Phi):=\Phi-\mathrm{Snap}(\Phi)\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1),\quad \mathrm{Res}(\Phi)\in[-\tfrac12,\tfrac12)^d.}]These are the deterministic maps producing the hub-key ((\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r},n)).
06.S2.b — Allowed 1D tunnel steps and the multi-axis step set
Define the allowed 1D tunnel step set (hub group steps) by[\boxed{\Delta\mathcal{H}:=\left{\pm\frac{1}{6},\ \pm\frac{1}{12},\ \pm\frac{1}{4},\ \pm\frac{1}{3},\ \pm\frac{1}{36}\right}\subset\mathbb{T}^1.}]A “good tunnel” step on an axis is a translation by a value in (\Delta\mathcal{H}).
Define the multi-axis tunnel step set on (\mathbb{T}^d) by[\boxed{\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)}:=\left{\delta\in\mathbb{T}^d:\ \delta_i\in\Delta\mathcal{H}\cup{0}\ \ \forall i\right}.}]A multi-axis tunnel step is permitted to change any subset of axes; every changed axis must use an allowed step.
06.S2.c — Hub-preserving legality predicate (mesh corridor)
Define the hub corridor around the mesh (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) at radius (\rho\in(0,\tfrac12]) by[\mathrm{Corr}\rho(\mathcal{H}^{(d)}):=\bigcup{\mathbf{h}\in\mathcal{H}^{(d)}}\left{\Phi\in\mathbb{T}^d:\ \mathrm{Dist}{\infty}(\Phi,\mathbf{h})\le \rho\right}.]A route is hub-preserving if it remains inside (\mathrm{Corr}\rho(\mathcal{H}^{(d)})) for a pinned (\rho) and does not change coarse hub class under allowed truncations. The stability statement “good tunneling becomes a corridor mesh” is formalized by this definition.
06.S2.d — Hub-first tunneling operator (route synthesis schema)
Given start and target phases (\Phi_A,\Phi_B\in\mathbb{T}^d), define the canonical hub-first schema:
Snap in: move (\Phi_A\to \mathbf{h}_A=\mathrm{Snap}(\Phi_A));
Hub route: move (\mathbf{h}_A\to \mathbf{h}_B=\mathrm{Snap}(\Phi_B)) by a finite sequence of steps in (\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)});
Snap out: move (\mathbf{h}_B\to \Phi_B).
This is the explicit “Hub-first” routing strategy: snap to a nearest hub using small allowed steps, perform typed moves at hubs, then snap out to the target.
The hub route is required to be deterministic under pinned policies (tie-break rules; axis ordering; step preference ordering), producing a replayable route artifact.
06.S3 — Invariants
06.S3.a — Coarse hub class invariance under truncation
The hub-preserving requirement is: prefix truncation must not change the coarse hub class. Formally, for any admissible truncation operator (\pi) on the Square carrier inducing a coarse phase map on (\mathbb{T}^d), the induced hub class must satisfy[\mathrm{Snap}\big(\Pi(\pi(\mathbf{x}))\big)=\mathrm{Snap}\big(\Pi(\mathbf{x})\big)]whenever (\pi) is declared “coarse-preserving” in the corridor profile. The core requirement is explicitly stated: prefix truncation must not change the coarse hub class.
06.S3.b — Mesh stability under allowed steps (hub-grid closure intent)
A “good tunnel” step keeps the route on, or returns it to, the hub grids in each coordinate: moves are good if they keep you on (or land you on) the hub grid (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}).The admissibility predicate is therefore a mesh predicate: a step is legal if it maps hub neighborhoods to hub neighborhoods within corridor budget.
06.S3.c — Hub key sufficiency and storage invariance
The state key ((\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r},n)) is sufficient to reconstruct:
hub identity (\mathbf{h}) (coarse class),
residual (\mathbf{r}) (local offset),
octave level (n) (resolution tag).
Storing hubs/residual/octave is the explicit canonical strategy.
06.S3.d — Deterministic bounded hub rides (route artifact invariant)
A tunnel route is represented as a finite hub ride that is deterministic and replayable under pinned profiles (route plans include pins and are not allowed to vary by optimization that changes semantics).This chapter instantiates hub rides in (\mathbb{T}^d) using the hub mesh (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) as the routing substrate.
06.S4 — Protocols
06.S4.a — Nearest-hub computation (1D and (d)D)
from math import floor
D = [2, 3, 4, 6, 12, 36]
def dist_T1(a: float, b: float) -> float:
"""a,b in [0,1). Circular distance on T^1."""
x = (a - b) % 1.0
return min(x, 1.0 - x)
def hubs_1d():
"""Enumerate canonical hubs in [0,1) with denominators in D."""
H = set()
for den in D:
for k in range(den):
H.add(k / den)
return sorted(H)
H1 = hubs_1d()
def nearest_hub_1d(phi: float) -> float:
"""Deterministic nearest hub in H1 (ties broken by smaller denominator then smaller value)."""
phi %= 1.0
best = None
best_d = 1.0
for q in H1:
d = dist_T1(phi, q)
if d < best_d - 1e-15:
best, best_d = q, d
elif abs(d - best_d) <= 1e-15:
# tie-break: prefer smaller denominator representation; then smaller q
# implement by comparing minimal den in D that represents q exactly
def den_rank(x):
for den in D:
if abs(x * den - round(x * den)) <= 1e-15:
return den
return 10**9
if (den_rank(q), q) < (den_rank(best), best):
best, best_d = q, d
return best
def snap(phi_vec):
return [nearest_hub_1d(phi) for phi in phi_vec]
def residual(phi_vec, hub_vec):
out = []
for phi, h in zip(phi_vec, hub_vec):
r = (phi - h) % 1.0
if r >= 0.5:
r -= 1.0
out.append(r)
return out
06.S4.b — Multi-axis tunnel steps and legality test
STEP = [ 1/6, -1/6, 1/12, -1/12, 1/4, -1/4, 1/3, -1/3, 1/36, -1/36, 0.0 ]
def in_step_set(x: float) -> bool:
return any(abs((x - s) % 1.0) <= 1e-15 for s in STEP)
def legal_step(delta_vec) -> bool:
return all(in_step_set(d) for d in delta_vec)
def apply_step(phi_vec, delta_vec):
return [ (phi + d) % 1.0 for phi, d in zip(phi_vec, delta_vec) ]
06.S4.c — Hub-first route synthesis (coordinatewise canonical plan)
def hub_first_route(phiA, phiB):
"""
Returns a route artifact:
- hA, rA, hB, rB
- hub_steps: a list of delta vectors (each coordinate in STEP)
The hub path is constructed coordinatewise by reducing hub differences mod 1
into a short word over {±1/36, ±1/12, ±1/6, ±1/4, ±1/3}.
"""
hA = snap(phiA)
hB = snap(phiB)
rA = residual(phiA, hA)
rB = residual(phiB, hB)
# Route on hubs: move hA -> hB in each coordinate using 1/36 granularity
# (since all denominators divide 36).
hub_steps = []
cur = hA[:]
# deterministic axis order: 1..d
d = len(cur)
for i in range(d):
# represent difference on i-th coordinate in [-1/2,1/2)
diff = (hB[i] - cur[i]) % 1.0
if diff >= 0.5:
diff -= 1.0
# exact rational step count in units of 1/36
m = round(diff * 36)
# apply |m| steps of ±1/36 on axis i
step = 1/36 if m > 0 else -1/36
for _ in range(abs(m)):
delta = [0.0]*d
delta[i] = step
hub_steps.append(delta)
cur = apply_step(cur, delta)
return {
"phiA": phiA, "hA": hA, "rA": rA,
"phiB": phiB, "hB": hB, "rB": rB,
"hub_steps": hub_steps
}
This protocol implements the “Hub-first” schema: snap to nearest hubs, route along a hub-step generating set, then snap out.
06.S4.d — Hub-preserving hash output (storage key)
def hub_key(phi_vec, octave_n: int):
h = snap(phi_vec)
r = residual(phi_vec, h)
return {"h": h, "r": r, "n": octave_n}
This is the explicit storage form ((\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r},n)) of the hologram key.
❀ Flower — Hub Mesh Geometry on (\mathbb{T}^d) and Multi-Axis Tunnels
06.F1 — Objects
06.F1.a — Hub grids as rational sublattices of (\mathbb{T}^d)
The mesh (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}=\mathcal{H}^d) is a finite union of rational grids in (\mathbb{T}^d), induced by denominators (\mathcal{D}).A hub vector (\mathbf{h}\in\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) is a multi-axis nexus point; “good tunneling becomes a lattice in (\mathbb{T}^d).”
06.F1.b — Step geometry: the hub step set as a discrete subgroup
Let[\Gamma := \left\langle \Delta\mathcal{H} \right\rangle \le \mathbb{T}^1]be the subgroup generated by the allowed steps. Since all step denominators divide (36), (\Gamma\subseteq \tfrac{1}{36}\mathbb{Z}/\mathbb{Z}) and thus (\Gamma) is a finite cyclic subgroup of order dividing (36).
Define the multi-axis subgroup[\Gamma^{(d)}:=\Gamma^d\le \mathbb{T}^d.]Then every multi-axis tunnel step sequence is a word in (\Gamma^{(d)}).
06.F1.c — Good tunnels as hub-grid preserving translations
A good tunnel move is any translation that keeps you on (or lands you on) the hub grid in each coordinate, i.e., for each axis you are changing, the step size lies in the allowed list.Formally, a step (\delta\in\mathbb{T}^d) is admissible if (\delta\in\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)}), and a path is admissible if all of its steps are admissible.
06.F1.d — The sextile spine as a universal router (pinned)
Within the allowed step family, the sextile (\tfrac{1}{6}) is treated as a universal routing spine: it is explicitly used as a bridge among finer hubs and the primary quarter/third structure by composing small hub steps.
06.F2 — Operators
06.F2.a — Multi-axis tunnel step operator
Define the multi-axis tunnel step operator:[\mathrm{Step}\delta:\mathbb{T}^d\to\mathbb{T}^d,\qquad\mathrm{Step}\delta(\Phi):=\Phi+\delta\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 1),]with admissibility constraint (\delta\in\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)}).
06.F2.b — Hub-preserving route operator (geometric form)
A hub-preserving route from (\Phi_A) to (\Phi_B) is a finite composition
[
\Phi_B
\mathrm{Step}{\delta_T}\circ\cdots\circ \mathrm{Step}{\delta_1}(\Phi_A)]such that (i) each (\delta_t\in\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)}), and (ii) the path stays within a pinned corridor radius (\rho) of (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}). This is the torus-geometric rendering of the corridor mesh.
06.F2.c — Hub-first routing (geometric contract)
The hub-first routing contract is:[\Phi_A \xrightarrow{\text{snap}} \mathbf{h}_A\xrightarrow{\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)}} \mathbf{h}_B\xrightarrow{\text{snap}} \Phi_B,]where the hub middle segment is executed on the discrete mesh and the snap segments use bounded residual motion (within corridor budget). This contract is explicitly stated as the canonical routing strategy.
06.F2.d — Hub-preserving hash as a chart-independent descriptor
Define the chart-independent descriptor of (\Phi) by ((\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r},n)). The LensSwitch/interpretation maps are functions of this key rather than raw angles.
06.F3 — Invariants
06.F3.a — Mesh invariance under octave lift
Octave lift preserves phase fractions: (\Phi) remains unchanged while the octave index increments and resolution changes.Therefore, (\mathbf{h}=\mathrm{Hub}^{(d)}(\Phi)) is invariant under octave lift (for fixed hub policy), and tunneling semantics are stable under higher-resolution renderings.
06.F3.b — Axis-separability invariant for hub membership
(\Phi\in\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) iff each (\phi_i\in\mathcal{H}). Thus, hub membership is axis-separable.
06.F3.c — Admissible step invariance is coordinatewise
A multi-axis step is admissible iff each changed axis uses an allowed step. This is the higher-D “phase-locked corridor” condition as a mesh.
06.F3.d — Hub class invariance as the routing anchor
The hub-preserving requirement “prefix truncation must not change the coarse hub class” is the anchor invariant; it guarantees that coarse routing decisions remain consistent under truncation and refinement.
06.F4 — Protocols
06.F4.a — Hub mesh builder in (\mathbb{T}^d) (finite enumeration at bounded denominator)
To enumerate a finite working hub mesh, choose a denominator cap (default (36)) and form the rational grid
[
\mathcal{H}_{\le 36}
\bigcup_{d\in\mathcal{D}}\left{\frac{k}{d}:k=0,\dots,d-1\right}.]Then (\mathcal{H}_{\le 36}^{(d)}) is the Cartesian product grid used by the router.
06.F4.b — Deterministic axis ordering and step preference
Pin:
axis order ((1,2,\dots,d));
step preference ordering (default: (\pm\tfrac{1}{36}\prec\pm\tfrac{1}{12}\prec\pm\tfrac{1}{6}\prec\pm\tfrac{1}{4}\prec\pm\tfrac{1}{3}));
tie-break policy for nearest hubs.
These pins are part of the corridor policy; changing them is a semantic change and must be explicit.
06.F4.c — Hub-to-hub shortest path on the mesh (BFS)
Construct a graph whose nodes are (\mathcal{H}_{\le 36}) and whose edges connect hubs differing by an element of (\Delta\mathcal{H}); run BFS from (h_A) to (h_B). Execute coordinatewise for (d) dimensions or in joint product space under a pinned cost model.
06.F4.d — Route artifact structure (geometric)
A route artifact records:
(\psi_\star^{(d)}(\Phi_A;n)) and (\psi_\star^{(d)}(\Phi_B;n));
hub sequence (intermediate (\mathbf{h}) waypoints) and step vectors;
pinned policies (tie-break, cost, step preference, admissibility);
replay hash and obligations.
This “hub ride” form is a direct specialization of the general route-plan discipline (finite hub rides with pinned profiles).
☁ Cloud — Residual-Based Uncertainty, Confidence, and Hub-Preserving Belief Transport
06.C1 — Objects
06.C1.a — Residual magnitude as uncertainty thickness
For the hub-key ((\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r},n)), define residual magnitude (default (L^\infty)):[|\mathbf{r}|_\infty := \max_i |r_i|.]Residual size encodes “fog thickness”; smaller residual yields sharper certainty.
06.C1.b — Hub posterior and confidence weight
Given (\Phi\in\mathbb{T}^d), define the induced hub posterior over (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) under a pinned noise model (\mathcal{N}) by[\mathbb{P}(\mathbf{h}\mid \Phi)\ \propto\ \exp!\left(-\frac{\mathrm{Dist}_{\infty}(\Phi,\mathbf{h})^2}{2\sigma^2}\right),]with (\sigma) pinned or derived as a monotone function of (|\mathbf{r}|). The minimal model ties (\sigma) to (|r|): smaller residual implies sharper certainty.
06.C1.c — Hub-corridor belief state
Define a belief state as a measure (\mu) on (\mathbb{T}^d) whose mass is concentrated in (\mathrm{Corr}_\rho(\mathcal{H}^{(d)})). The belief is hub-preserving if its pushforward under truncation preserves the same coarse hub class distribution (within typed tolerance).
06.C1.d — Observation model: hub class and residual are sufficient statistics (pinned)
Under the pinned model, the pair ((\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r})) is the sufficient descriptor for routing-relevant uncertainty: (\mathbf{h}) selects the macro basin; (\mathbf{r}) measures closeness and thus confidence.
06.C2 — Operators
06.C2.a — Belief transport under tunnel steps
For an admissible step (\delta\in\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)}), define the transport of a measure (\mu) by pushforward:[(\mathrm{Step}\delta)#\mu(A):=\mu(A-\delta).]This is the exact measure transport induced by the deterministic tunnel move.
06.C2.b — Belief snap and corridor projection
Define the corridor projection operator (\Pi_{\mathrm{corr}}) that maps a general (\mu) to a corridor-supported (\tilde\mu) by snapping mass to nearby hub neighborhoods under a pinned rule (e.g., maximum a posteriori hub per sample). This is the probabilistic analog of the deterministic snap operator.
06.C2.c — Confidence update rule under residual reduction
If a snap operation reduces residual magnitude, update confidence monotonically. The minimal model implements confidence as an inverse function of (|\mathbf{r}|), consistent with “hub closeness = confidence; residual size = uncertainty thickness.”
06.C2.d — Hub-first belief routing
Execute belief routing by:
concentrate mass near (\mathbf{h}_A) (snap-in),
transport the concentrated belief along a mesh route (hub steps),
expand to match target residual constraints (snap-out),all while maintaining corridor support and pinned policies.
06.C3 — Invariants
06.C3.a — Corridor mass invariant under admissible steps
If (\mu) is supported in (\mathrm{Corr}\rho(\mathcal{H}^{(d)})) and (\delta) is a hub-step that maps hub neighborhoods to hub neighborhoods within the same (\rho), then ((\mathrm{Step}\delta)_#\mu) remains corridor-supported.
