06.C3.b — Deterministic hub class of a point is stable under truncation (policy)
The deterministic hub class (\mathbf{h}=\mathrm{Snap}(\Phi)) is the routing anchor, and stability under prefix truncation is an explicit requirement.
06.C3.c — Residual monotonicity under snap (when pinned to nearest hub)
Under nearest-hub snap, (|\mathbf{r}|) is minimal among all candidate hub centers under the pinned metric. This enforces local optimality of snap.
06.C3.d — Policy-pinned tie-break invariance
All probabilistic claims involving (\mathrm{Hub}) must use the same pinned tie-break and metric; otherwise the induced posterior over hubs is not comparable across runs.
06.C4 — Protocols
06.C4.a — Posterior over hubs (finite mesh approximation)
Approximate (\mathcal{H}) by (\mathcal{H}{\le 36}) and compute unnormalized weights[w(\mathbf{h})=\exp!\left(-\frac{\mathrm{Dist}{\infty}(\Phi,\mathbf{h})^2}{2\sigma^2}\right),]then normalize over the finite set.
06.C4.b — Corridor-support audit
Audit a belief state by estimating (\mathbb{P}[\Phi\in\mathrm{Corr}_\rho(\mathcal{H}^{(d)})]) under (\mu). If it falls below a pinned threshold, the state is outside the corridor.
06.C4.c — Route-confidence transcript
Emit a transcript recording, at each hop:
hub waypoint,
residual statistics,
confidence measures,
corridor support status,
pinned policy digest.
06.C4.d — Evidence plan when hub posterior is ambiguous
If multiple hubs are tied or near-tied under the pinned metric and tie-break is insufficient (rare under exact rational states), the output is typed AMBIG and the plan requires additional constraints or higher resolution.
✶ Fractal — Multi-Scale Tunneling: Octave Lifts, Fixed-Corridor Convergence, and Hub Stability
06.R1 — Objects
06.R1.a — Octave index and stability under lifting
The hub key ((\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r},n)) carries octave index (n). Octave lift advances (n) while preserving phase fractions, and thus preserves hub fractions.
06.R1.b — Fixed corridor and convergence descriptor
Define the fixed corridor as (\mathrm{Corr}_\rho(\mathcal{H}^{(d)})) for pinned (\rho). The Fractal shadow of a state reads:
stability of the hub under octave lifting,
whether residual shrinks under lift+snap rules, i.e., convergence to the corridor fixed set.
06.R1.c — Multi-scale hub mesh (two-tier refinement)
A multi-tier hub system refines coarse policy hubs by inserting finer hubs inside basins without replacing the macro backbone. This produces a two-tier routing rule: macro spine selection followed by micro hub snapping within the chosen basin.
06.R1.d — Tunnel as a transport operator with certificate obligations
Tunneling is a transport operator: it must be explicit, replayable, and corridor-gated; it must obey truth typing and certificate obligations (never bypass corridor validation).
06.R2 — Operators
06.R2.a — Lift–Snap operator (one recursion step)
Define the Lift–Snap operator on keys:[\mathsf{LS}:\ (\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r},n)\ \mapsto\ (\mathbf{h}',\mathbf{r}',n+1),]where (n\mapsto n+1) (octave lift), then ((\mathbf{h}',\mathbf{r}')) is recomputed by applying (\mathrm{Snap}) and (\mathrm{Res}) at the refined resolution under the pinned policy. Hub stability under lifting is a primary output.
06.R2.b — Fixed-corridor contraction test
Define the contraction test:[|\mathbf{r}'| \le \kappa |\mathbf{r}|]for pinned (\kappa\in(0,1]). If (\kappa<1) holds repeatedly, the route converges to the hub mesh under lift–snap recursion.
06.R2.c — Two-tier snap operator (macro then micro)
Under a two-tier hub policy, define:
select dominant macro denominator (d^\star\in{2,3,4,6}) by pinned basin rule;
within that basin, snap to the nearest micro hub (k/12).This operator refines placement while preserving the macro routing backbone.
06.R2.d — RoutePlan and replay closure for tunnels
A tunnel RoutePlan is a finite hub ride plus obligations and pins; it is replay-verified, and any mismatch produces a conflict packet under fork-guard rules.
06.R3 — Invariants
06.R3.a — Hub stability under octave lift
Since phase fractions are unchanged by octave lift, hub fractions are stable under lift when the hub selector is pinned.
06.R3.b — Residual-to-corridor distance is the fixed-point distance
The residual magnitude (|\mathbf{r}|) is the distance-to-mesh proxy. Fractal outputs “distance to fixed corridor” and “convergence under recursion” by tracking (|r|) under lift+snap.
06.R3.c — Hub-first routes preserve coherence by returning to nexus lattice
The hub-first routing strategy formalizes the coherence principle: stability comes from returning to the hub lattice before performing typed moves and before leaving to targets.
06.R3.d — Forbidden implicit tunneling invariant
Any tunneling not explicitly declared and pinned is forbidden; any cross-scope jump must be pinned and auditable.
06.R4 — Protocols
06.R4.a — Multi-scale tunnel execution protocol
Protocol for a hub-preserving tunnel with recursion:
compute ((\mathbf{h},\mathbf{r},n));
route on (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) using admissible steps;
after each major hub waypoint, optionally apply Lift–Snap;
verify corridor support and residual bounds;
emit RoutePlan with pins and replay capsule.
06.R4.b — Convergence audit under repeated Lift–Snap
Run (m) iterations of Lift–Snap and record (|\mathbf{r}^{(t)}|). Output OK if the sequence decreases under pinned contraction criteria; otherwise output NEAR/AMBIG with obligations.
06.R4.c — Two-tier hub refinement audit
Verify that adding micro hubs refines inside macro basins without changing the macro hub sequence of a route (macro backbone preserved).
06.R4.d — Replay capsule schema for tunnels
A tunnel replay capsule includes:
(\Phi_A,\Phi_B) digests (or their hub keys),
hub mesh version and denominator set,
admissible step set,
distance metric and tie-break pins,
corridor radius (\rho),
route artifact (hub sequence, step vectors),
verification outcomes and obligations.
Tunneling is treated as a transport operator and must obey the same replay/certificate constraints as all transports.
Ch06 — Tunneling as Hub-Preserving Routing on (\mathbb{T}^d)
Ch07 — Transport Legality (DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE) in HD-SCT
Certified transport schema, corridor budgets, and replay-bound legality across Higher-Dimensional Square–Circle–Triangle representations
□ Square — Transport Objects and Typed Schemas
07.S1 — Objects
07.S1.a — Lens set and HD-SCT representation families
Let the lens alphabet be[\mathcal{L}:={S,F,C,R},]where (S) denotes the Square lens, (F) the Flower lens, (C) the Cloud lens, and (R) the Fractal lens.
An HD-SCT representation family is a pinned family of typed spaces[\mathcal{R}{L}^{(d,k)} \quad (L\in\mathcal{L},\ d\in\mathbb{N}{\ge1},\ k\in\mathbb{N}_{\ge0}),]whose elements encode the same semantic atom at a given ((d,k)) under lens (L), subject to pinned corridor profiles, pinned normal-form profiles, and pinned decoding/encoding rules.
07.S1.b — GlobalAddr endpoints and lens slots
Fix a station identifier (X) and a facet/atom identifier ((f,t)). The lens slots for that atom are[X.L.f.t \quad\text{for}\quad L\in\mathcal{L},]and transport edges always connect explicit slots (X.L.f.t\to X.L'.f.t) (or their cross-manuscript analogs) rather than implicit “same thing” claims.
A GlobalAddr is a canonical endpoint record that uniquely specifies the atom and representation context:[\boxed{\mathsf{GA}:=(X,\ f,t,\ d,k,\ L,\ \pi_{\mathrm{NF}},\pi_{\mathrm{bytes}},\pi_{\mathrm{metric}},\pi_{\mathrm{corr}},\ \mathrm{SchemaVer}),}]where each (\pi_\star) is a pinned profile digest (or a registry key resolving to one).
All transport transcripts and witnesses must cite endpoints as GlobalAddr (including intermediate nodes of any chain).
07.S1.c — Corridor profile and the canonical budget vector
A corridor is a typed policy object that pins allowed transport kinds, obligation rules, promotion/downgrade rules, and a budget vector.
The canonical budget vector is[\boxed{\mathbf{b}:=(\kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi),}]with semantics:
(\kappa): commutation residual budget (allowed non-commutation);
(\beta): drift/approximation budget (allowed deviation from exact invariants);
(\delta): depth budget (caps recursion/hatches relevant to transports that require nested verification);
(\chi): cost budget (caps computational effort and replay work).
Budgets are pinned per corridor; changing budget semantics or values is a meaning evolution and requires MIGRATE.
07.S1.d — Fingerprints bind transport claims
Let (\pi) denote the complete pinned profile tuple sufficient to interpret canonicalization and equivalence.
Let (\mathrm{NF}\pi) be the pinned normal-form operator and (\mathrm{CanonBytes}\pi) the pinned canonical serialization. Define[\boxed{\mathrm{fp}\pi(x):=\mathrm{SHA256}!\big(\mathrm{CanonBytes}\pi(\mathrm{NF}_\pi(x))\big).}]Fingerprints bind equivalence claims, transport correctness, migrations, and publish/import integrity. Any fingerprint claim without (\pi) is AMBIG by definition.
07.S1.e — Transport kind vs truth class
A transport edge has:
a kind (\in{\mathrm{DUAL},\mathrm{EQUIV},\mathrm{MIGRATE}}), and
a truth class (\tau \in \mathbb{T}:={\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL},\mathrm{CONFLICT}}),
with truth typing governed by corridor rules and evidence closure.
The kind classification rule (structural) is:
DUAL: an adjacent-lens swap under a pinned adjacency profile (\mathsf{AP}), preserving declared invariants under replay (or yielding NEAR with bounded residual).
EQUIV: a semantic equivalence bridge with explicit forward/backward maps and invariants, with commutation evidence under budgets.
MIGRATE: a meaning evolution edge required when semantic fingerprints change or declared invariants are not preserved; requires compatibility matrix, regression witnesses, and rollback plan.
07.S1.f — AdjacencyProfile (\mathsf{AP}) (legality graph for DUAL)
An AdjacencyProfile is the pinned legality graph for lens swaps:[\boxed{\mathsf{AP}:=(\mathcal{L},E_{\mathrm{adj}},\mathrm{TieBreak},\mathrm{Pins}),\qquad\mathcal{L}={S,F,C,R}.}]Here (E_{\mathrm{adj}}\subseteq\mathcal{L}\times\mathcal{L}) is the set of legal adjacent swaps, and (\mathrm{TieBreak}) is a pinned comparator required for deterministic planning.
Define the legality predicate:[\boxed{\mathrm{LegalDUAL}(L\to L') \iff (L,L')\in E_{\mathrm{adj}}\ \text{under pinned }\mathsf{AP}.}]DUAL is legal iff adjacency holds; otherwise a direct swap is forbidden and only an explicit adjacent chain is legal.
07.S1.g — DUAL payload schema (single swap contract)
A DUAL payload is the minimal proof-carrying object for a single adjacent swap:[\boxed{\mathsf{DUALPayload}:=(\mathrm{APDigest},\mathrm{Src},\mathrm{Dst},\mathrm{SrcLens},\mathrm{DstLens},\mathrm{MapFwd},\mathrm{MapBwd?},\mathcal{I},\mathbf{b},\mathrm{DomainSpec},\mathrm{WitnessPtr},\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{SchemaVer}).}]Requirements include:
(\mathrm{APDigest}) pins adjacency legality,
(\mathrm{MapFwd}) explicit; (\mathrm{MapBwd}) mandatory where invertibility is claimed,
invariant set (\mathcal{I}) explicit,
budgets (\mathbf{b}=(\kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi)) explicit,
(\mathrm{DomainSpec}) declares where maps are defined,
(\mathrm{WitnessPtr}) and (\mathrm{ReplayPtr}) mandatory for OK/NEAR.
DUAL is an edge kind with corridor truth typing and is not automatically OK.
07.S1.h — EQUIV claim schema (bidirectional equivalence contract)
An EQUIV claim is a proof-carrying object asserting “same meaning” between two endpoints under pinned profiles and budgets:[\boxed{\mathsf{Eq}_\pi(u,v):=(\mathrm{Src},\mathrm{Dst},\mathrm{Kind},\mathrm{MapFwd},\mathrm{MapBwd},\mathcal{I},\mathbf{b},\mathrm{ResidualLedger?},\mathrm{WitnessPtr},\mathrm{ReplayPtr}).}]Here (\mathrm{Kind}\in{\mathrm{EQUIV},\mathrm{DUAL}}) (with DUAL required to obey (\mathsf{AP})), and (\mathrm{ResidualLedger}) is mandatory whenever the truth class is NEAR.
Minimum EQUIV requirements: explicit forward and backward maps on declared domains, declared invariants, commutation checks where required, and replay capsules reproducing checks; absent any requirement, the claim is AMBIG or FAIL, never OK.
07.S1.i — MIGRATE payload schema (meaning evolution contract)
A MIGRATE edge is required when fingerprints change or invariants are not preserved but an evolution is intended; the witness suite includes:
fingerprint delta report (scoped by GlobalAddr),
compatibility matrix,
regression set and witnesses,
rollback plan,
replay capsules and pinned profiles.
Formally define:[\boxed{\mathsf{MIGRATEPayload}:=(\mathrm{SrcProfile},\mathrm{DstProfile},\mathrm{DeltaReport},\mathrm{CompatMatrix},\mathrm{RegressSet},\mathrm{RollbackPlan},\mathrm{ReplayPtrs},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{SchemaVer}).}]
07.S1.j — TransportPath schema (swap chain / composite transport)
A TransportPath is a compositional transport object:[\boxed{\mathsf{Path}:=(e_1,e_2,\dots,e_m;\ \mathrm{Pins};\ \mathrm{BudgetLedger};\ \mathrm{CompositeMap?};\ \mathrm{Outcome})}]where each (e_i) is a LinkEdge (DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE/…). The path includes pins for all profiles used, a budget ledger recording (\kappa/\beta) spending and (\delta/\chi) enforcement, an optional composite map (if steps compose on compatible domains), and an outcome (\tau\in\mathbb{T}).
Non-adjacent swaps require decomposition into an explicit AP-adjacent chain; all intermediate nodes and edges are first-class and must be routable. Failure to find a legal chain is FAIL; multiple plausible chains without pinned discriminators is AMBIG.
07.S1.k — ConjugacyWitness schema (NF + metric + replay binding)
A ConjugacyWitness (CW) is the evidence object that binds “same meaning under transport” to pinned normal forms and pinned metrics:[\boxed{\mathsf{CW}:=(\mathrm{NFProfileDigest},\mathrm{MetricDigest},\mathrm{DomainSpec},\mathcal{I},\kappa,\beta,\mathrm{ResidualLedger?},\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{Outcome}).}]Outcome typing:
OK if invariants hold and NF equality is proved under replay,
NEAR if residual is bounded (requires residual ledger),
AMBIG if underdetermined (multiple NFs or domain ambiguity),
FAIL/CONFLICT if violated or disagreement reproducible.
CW is required for EQUIV claims induced by transport and for any DUAL that asserts semantic invariance.
07.S1.l — ResidualLedger, EvidencePlan, and ConflictPacket objects
A ResidualLedger is mandatory for NEAR:
metric definition,
bound value,
scope (exact addresses impacted),
validity window/expiry,
obligations for promotion to OK,
replay recipe reproducing the measurement.
An EvidencePlan is mandatory for AMBIG:
bounded candidate set with ranks,
discriminators (concrete tests/proofs/measurements),
routes to generate required evidence,
expected failure modes and classifications,
promotion rules.
A ConflictPacket is mandatory for reproducible disagreements between admissible paths:[\boxed{\mathsf{Payload}_{\mathrm{CONFLICT}}:=(\mathrm{Src},\mathrm{Dst},\mathsf{Path}_A,\mathsf{Path}_B,\mathrm{MinWitnessSet},\mathrm{ReproRecipe},\mathrm{FenceSpec},\mathrm{ProposedResolutions}).}]The minimal witness set must be computed deterministically (bounded search under (\chi)).
07.S2 — Operators
07.S2.a — Canonical fingerprint operator
Given pinned profile (\pi), define:[\mathrm{fp}\pi(x)=\mathrm{SHA256}(\mathrm{CanonBytes}\pi(\mathrm{NF}_\pi(x))).]This operator is used by:
EQUIV/DUAL semantic invariance checks (via equality of normal forms and/or fingerprints),
MIGRATE detection (via fingerprint deltas),
conflict detection (via reproducible divergence under identical pins).
07.S2.b — DUAL legality and lift-chain planning
Given (\mathsf{AP}) and lenses (L_s,L_d), define:[\mathrm{LegalDUAL}(L_s\to L_d)\iff (L_s,L_d)\in E_{\mathrm{adj}}.]If illegal, define the LiftPath operator that returns a shortest AP-legal chain:[\boxed{\mathrm{LiftPath}{\mathsf{AP}}(L_s,L_d):=(L_s=L{i_0}\to L_{i_1}\to\cdots\to L_{i_m}=L_d),}]computed by BFS on the adjacency graph with pinned (\mathrm{TieBreak}) for determinism.
07.S2.c — Map composition and composite transport
Given transport maps (T_i:\mathcal{R}{A_i}\rightharpoonup\mathcal{R}{B_i}) for the edges (e_i) of a path, define the composite partial map[T:=T_m\circ\cdots\circ T_1]when domains/codomains compose under explicit DomainSpec intersections; otherwise (\mathrm{CompositeMap?}=\emptyset) and the path cannot claim a composite equivalence map.
Composite transport must preserve declared invariants or explicitly declare MIGRATE; silent invariant drift is forbidden.
07.S2.d — Transport classification operator (kind + truth)
Given a candidate edge with maps and pins, define the classifier:
Determine Kind (\in{\mathrm{DUAL},\mathrm{EQUIV},\mathrm{MIGRATE}}):
if adjacent under (\mathsf{AP}) and the edge is a lens swap contract (\Rightarrow) DUAL candidate;
else if explicit fwd/bwd maps exist with declared invariants (\Rightarrow) EQUIV candidate;
else if semantic fingerprint changes (or invariants not preserved but evolution intended) (\Rightarrow) MIGRATE required.
Determine Truth Class (\tau\in\mathbb{T}) by corridor evaluation:
OK: all schema obligations satisfied; replay closes; invariants proved;
NEAR: residuals bounded by (\beta) or commutation residuals bounded by (\kappa), with a residual ledger and disclosures;
AMBIG: underdetermined (missing pins, ambiguous domain, multiple plausible paths) with bounded candidate set and evidence plan;
FAIL: illegality, missing mandatory artifacts where required, budget violation beyond policy;
CONFLICT: reproducible disagreement under identical pins.
07.S3 — Invariants
07.S3.a — Adjacency restriction invariant
If (L_1) and (L_2) are not adjacent under (\mathsf{AP}), a direct DUAL is illegal. Any legal transport must be decomposed into an explicit adjacent chain whose intermediate nodes/edges are first-class, witnessed, and replayable.
07.S3.b — Explicit maps and pinned profiles invariant
For DUAL and EQUIV:
MapFwd must be explicit;
MapBwd is mandatory where invertibility is claimed;
invariants (\mathcal{I}) and budgets (\mathbf{b}) must be explicit;
DomainSpec must declare where maps apply.
Missing pins for decode-relevant transport is a quarantine trigger.
07.S3.c — Commutation discipline invariant
Composite transport is legal only if commutation residuals among interacting transforms stay within (\kappa). Violation yields FAIL (deterministic violation) or CONFLICT (reproducible verifier disagreement).
07.S3.d — Replay determinism binds legality
Transport legality is a property of replay: if two verifiers under identical pins disagree, the correct output is CONFLICT, not averaging or preference selection.
Map changes that alter meaning-bearing behavior change fingerprints of maps/witnesses and therefore require MIGRATE (or a new EQUIV claim with new witnesses).
07.S4 — Protocols
07.S4.a — Certified DUAL protocol (single swap)
To construct a certified DUAL edge (X.L.f.t \to X.L'.f.t):
Validate adjacency: ((L,L')\in E_{\mathrm{adj}}) under pinned (\mathrm{APDigest}).
Construct explicit (\mathrm{MapFwd}) (and (\mathrm{MapBwd}) if invertibility is claimed).
Declare invariants (\mathcal{I}) and budgets (\mathbf{b}).
Produce (\mathsf{CW}) if the DUAL asserts semantic invariance (NF invariance).
Run replay closure; attach (\mathrm{WitnessPtr}) and (\mathrm{ReplayPtr}); output truth class by corridor evaluation.
Illegal adjacency or missing mandatory artifacts yields FAIL (or AMBIG only if corridor explicitly permits missing information with an evidence plan).
07.S4.b — Certified EQUIV protocol (bridge)
To construct a certified EQUIV edge between representations (\mathcal{R}_A^{(d,k)}) and (\mathcal{R}_B^{(d,k)}):
Provide explicit (\mathrm{MapFwd}) and (\mathrm{MapBwd}) on declared domains.
Declare invariants (\mathcal{I}) including NF invariance and decode invariance where codec-relevant.
Produce (\mathsf{CW}) (NFProfileDigest, MetricDigest, DomainSpec, residuals/ledger, replay).
Run required commutation checks for interacting transforms; charge (\kappa).
Output OK if invariants are proved and replay closes; NEAR only if bounded residual with residual ledger; otherwise AMBIG/FAIL/CONFLICT by corridor rules.
07.S4.c — Certified MIGRATE protocol (meaning evolution)
To construct a certified MIGRATE edge from old profile bundle (\pi_{\mathrm{old}}) to new profile bundle (\pi_{\mathrm{new}}):
Compute fingerprint delta report listing impacted GlobalAddr.
Build a compatibility matrix over declared features (NF rules, canonical bytes rules, metric selection, budget semantics, transport legality).
Select and execute regression set; attach witnesses and replay capsules.
Produce a rollback plan.
Publish (\mathsf{MIGRATEPayload}) with pins and replay closure.
07.S4.d — Reference implementation skeleton (schemas + planner + evaluator)
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Callable, Dict, Iterable, List, Literal, Optional, Sequence, Tuple
Lens = Literal["S","F","C","R"]
Truth = Literal["OK","NEAR","AMBIG","FAIL","CONFLICT"]
Kind = Literal["DUAL","EQUIV","MIGRATE"]
Digest = str
Ptr = str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Budget:
kappa: float # commutation residual budget
beta: float # drift / approximation budget
delta: int # depth budget
chi: int # cost budget
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class GlobalAddr:
station: str
facet: str
atom: str
d: int
k: int
lens: Lens
nf_digest: Digest
bytes_digest: Digest
metric_digest: Digest
corridor_digest: Digest
schema_ver: str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class DomainSpec:
# Declarative description of the domain (addresses, constraints).
spec: str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class AdjacencyProfile:
lenses: Tuple[Lens, ...]
adj: Dict[Tuple[Lens,Lens], bool]
tiebreak_digest: Digest
pins: Tuple[Tuple[str,str], ...]
ap_digest: Digest
def legal_dual(self, a: Lens, b: Lens) -> bool:
return bool(self.adj.get((a,b), False))
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class ResidualLedger:
metric_id: str
bound: float
scope: Tuple[str, ...] # impacted GlobalAddr ids or ranges
expiry: Optional[str]
obligations: Tuple[str, ...]
replay_ptr: Ptr
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class EvidencePlan:
candidates: Tuple[str, ...] # bounded candidate set ids
discriminators: Tuple[str, ...]
routes: Tuple[str, ...]
promotion_rules: Tuple[str, ...]
replay_ptrs: Tuple[Ptr, ...]
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class ConjugacyWitness:
nf_profile_digest: Digest
metric_digest: Digest
domain: DomainSpec
invariants: Tuple[str, ...]
kappa: float
beta: float
residual_ledger: Optional[ResidualLedger]
replay_ptr: Ptr
outcome: Truth
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class DualPayload:
ap_digest: Digest
src: GlobalAddr
dst: GlobalAddr
src_lens: Lens
dst_lens: Lens
map_fwd_id: str
map_bwd_id: Optional[str]
invariants: Tuple[str, ...]
budget: Budget
domain: DomainSpec
witness_ptr: Ptr
replay_ptr: Ptr
schema_ver: str
truth: Truth
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class EquivPayload:
src: GlobalAddr
dst: GlobalAddr
map_fwd_id: str
map_bwd_id: str
invariants: Tuple[str, ...]
budget: Budget
domain: DomainSpec
cw: ConjugacyWitness
witness_ptr: Ptr
replay_ptr: Ptr
schema_ver: str
truth: Truth
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class MigratePayload:
old_profile: Digest
new_profile: Digest
delta_report_ptr: Ptr
compat_matrix_ptr: Ptr
regress_set_ptr: Ptr
rollback_plan_ptr: Ptr
replay_ptrs: Tuple[Ptr, ...]
pins: Tuple[Tuple[str,str], ...]
schema_ver: str
truth: Truth
LinkEdge = Tuple[Kind, object] # payload object depends on kind
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class TransportPath:
edges: Tuple[LinkEdge, ...]
pins: Tuple[Tuple[str,str], ...]
budget_ledger_ptr: Ptr
composite_map_id: Optional[str]
outcome: Truth
def bfs_lift_path(AP: AdjacencyProfile, src: Lens, dst: Lens) -> List[Lens]:
# Deterministic BFS over the adjacency graph; neighbors enumerated in pinned lens order.
from collections import deque
q = deque([src])
prev: Dict[Lens, Optional[Lens]] = {src: None}
order = list(AP.lenses)
def neighbors(L: Lens) -> List[Lens]:
return [L2 for L2 in order if AP.legal_dual(L, L2)]
while q:
x = q.popleft()
if x == dst:
break
for y in neighbors(x):
if y not in prev:
prev[y] = x
q.append(y)
if dst not in prev:
return []
# reconstruct
path: List[Lens] = []
cur: Optional[Lens] = dst
while cur is not None:
path.append(cur)
cur = prev[cur]
return list(reversed(path))
def classify_commutation(residual: float, kappa: float, replay_agrees: bool) -> Truth:
if not replay_agrees:
return "CONFLICT"
if residual == 0.0:
return "OK"
if 0.0 < residual <= kappa:
return "NEAR"
return "FAIL"
❀ Flower — Laws of Transport Under Pinned Normal Forms
07.F1 — Objects
07.F1.a — Transport operator as typed partial function
A transport operator is a typed partial function[T:\mathcal{R}_A^{(d,k)}\rightharpoonup \mathcal{R}_B^{(d,k)}]equipped with:
declared domain (\mathrm{Dom}(T)),
declared invariants (\mathcal{I}(T)),
declared budgets ((\kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi)),
declared classification target (DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE).
07.F1.b — Commutator and commutation residual
For operators (T_1,T_2) on a common domain with inverses (or declared partial inverses), define the commutator:[\boxed{\mathrm{Comm}(T_1,T_2):=T_1\circ T_2\circ T_1^{-1}\circ T_2^{-1}.}]Let (d_\pi) be a pinned metric; define residual:[\boxed{r_\kappa:=d_\pi(\mathrm{Comm}(T_1,T_2),\mathrm{Id}).}]Typing:
OK if (r_\kappa=0) under replay,
NEAR if (0<r_\kappa\le\kappa) with residual ledger,
FAIL if (r_\kappa>\kappa),
CONFLICT if replays disagree under identical pins.
07.F2 — Laws
07.F2.a — Conjugacy law (transport under pinned normal forms)
Representation change is legal only as transport under pinned normal forms:
DUAL swaps must be adjacent under adjacency profile,
EQUIV requires explicit forward/backward maps and invariants,
MIGRATE is required when semantics change,and all transport claims are replay-verifiable; transport without replay closure cannot be OK.
07.F2.b — Composite transport preserves invariants or declares MIGRATE
Composite transport must preserve declared invariants:
if invariants preserved (\Rightarrow) EQUIV may be asserted with witnesses/replay,
if invariants not preserved but evolution intended (\Rightarrow) MIGRATE required,
if invariants violated unexpectedly (\Rightarrow) FAIL/CONFLICT with quarantine.
07.F2.c — Multiple legal paths disagreeing imply CONFLICT
If two admissible transport paths from the same source to the same destination yield different replay-verified fingerprints under identical pins, the correct outcome is CONFLICT and affected regions are quarantined until resolved by replay-verifiable repair or explicit migration.
07.F2.d — Map changes imply MIGRATE
If MapFwd/MapBwd changes in a meaning-bearing way, fingerprint changes and the prior EQUIV claim is no longer the same claim; MIGRATE is required (or a new EQUIV with new witnesses).
07.F3 — Constructions
07.F3.a — Conjugacy witness test construction
Given (T) and pinned normal forms (\mathrm{NF}_A,\mathrm{NF}_B), define discrepancy:[\Delta(x):=d!\left(\mathrm{NF}_B(T(x)),\mathrm{NF}_A(x)\right).]If (\sup_x\Delta(x)=0) under replay: OK; if (\sup_x\Delta(x)\le\beta): NEAR with residual ledger; otherwise FAIL/CONFLICT depending on reproducibility.
07.F3.b — Deterministic planner construction (AP BFS)
Given (L_s,L_d), compute shortest adjacency path via BFS; determinism requires pinned tie-break and pinned neighbor ordering; tie-break ambiguity yields AMBIG unless pinned.
07.F3.c — Map-invariant checker library
Construct a deterministic invariant checker library including:
NF invariance checks,
bijection checks (finite domains),
checksum/structure invariants,
schedule legality invariants,
corridor adherence invariants (pins, budgets).
07.F3.d — Budgeted commutator ledger construction
Ledger entries bind commutation checks to pins, domains, metrics, and replay recipes; they are used for NEAR disclosures, promotion obligations, and conflict reproduction.
07.F4 — Certificates
Certified transport requires certificate-bearing artifacts, including:
DUALLegalityCert (APDigest pinned, adjacency satisfied, payload includes maps and invariants, replay verifies),
ConjugacyCert (NF preserved exactly or within (\beta) with residual ledger; commutation checks performed; replay reproduces),
PathAgreementCert (two independent admissible paths agree under pinned profiles),
ConflictPacketCert (minimal witness set, deterministic reproduction recipe, quarantine fences, resolution candidates),
MigrationCert (compat matrices, regressions, rollback, pins, replay).
☁ Cloud — Corridor Truth Typing, AMBIG/NEAR Discipline, and Publishing Risk Envelopes
07.C1 — Objects
07.C1.a — Transport corridor profile
Define a transport corridor profile (\mathfrak{C}_{\mathrm{transport}}) that pins:
allowed kinds (DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE/CONFLICT),
(\kappa) and (\beta) budgets,
required replay closure for OK,
mandatory quarantine behavior for conflicts.
07.C1.b — Risk envelope for publishing
Publishing forbids unresolved AMBIG on critical paths, allows NEAR only with disclosed residual bounds and warnings, and forbids traversal of quarantined regions.
07.C1.c — Evidence plans and residual ledgers as first-class outputs
AMBIG outputs must include bounded candidate set, evidence plan id, routes to generate evidence, and explicit classification of what is missing (pins, witnesses, or definitions).
NEAR outputs must include a residual ledger (bounds, scope, metric, expiry), promotion obligations, and replay recipe; NEAR disclosures must travel with claims into narratives, seals, and publication bundles.
07.C2 — Laws
07.C2.a — AMBIG when multiple plausible transports exist
If multiple plausible transports exist and deterministic tie-break is not pinned, output AMBIG with bounded candidates and an evidence plan.
07.C2.b — FAIL when no legal lift path exists
If AP yields no legal chain between lenses or maps cannot compose under declared domains, output FAIL and quarantine any route depending on the impossible transport.
07.C2.c — CONFLICT when disagreement is reproducible
If two lawful paths disagree under replay and identical pins, output CONFLICT, build a conflict packet, and quarantine. Any resolution must be replay-verifiable and must preserve fingerprints or record diffs explicitly.
07.C2.d — Budget violations cannot be ignored
Budget violations cannot be ignored; corridor rules may permit downgrade OK→NEAR with disclosures, otherwise FAIL.
07.C3 — Constructions
07.C3.a — Evidence plan generator for transport ambiguity
Generate evidence plans by enumerating bounded candidate paths, selecting discriminators (commutation tests, invariant checks, replay comparisons), routing to hubs that can generate required artifacts, and defining promotion rules that uniquely select a path upon sufficient evidence.
07.C3.b — Quarantine fence propagation
Fence propagation excludes conflicting edges, any dependent edges requiring them, and any route plan traversing fenced regions for OK/publish; propagation is deterministic and replayable.
07.C3.c — Repair plan generator (EQUIV strengthening vs MIGRATE)
Generate repair candidates by either strengthening EQUIV proofs (new witnesses, tighter NF/metrics, expanded regression sets) or introducing MIGRATE with compat and regressions; revoke incorrect artifacts when necessary.
07.C3.d — Conflict reproduction recipe
Construct reproduction recipes containing minimal witness inputs, exact pinned profiles, exact replay steps, and expected divergent digests.
07.C4 — Certificates
Cloud-side certificates bind uncertainty handling to determinism:
EvidencePlanCert (bounded candidates, concrete discriminators, routable obligations),
ResidualBoundCert (metric pinned, bound (\beta), scope correct, replayable),
FenceCert (deterministic fence generation/propagation),
RepairCert (repair obligations and routes are minimal and replay-verifiable),
QuarantineTriggerCert (deterministic triggers and correct fences/packets).
✶ Fractal — Replay Closure, Transcripts, Regression, and Migration Governance
07.R1 — Objects
07.R1.a — Transport transcripts (append-only)
A transport transcript records:
endpoints (GlobalAddr),
selected path and DropLog,
maps used and fingerprints,
residual metrics and bounds,
corridor/profile pins,
replay capsule ids,
truth classification,and is address-indexed and append-only.
07.R1.b — Replay capsules and deterministic verification
Replay capsules reconstruct planner choice, map composition, commutation checks, endpoint comparisons, and classification; replay must reproduce outcomes under identical pins.
07.R1.c — Regression suites for transport packs
Regression fixtures cover adjacent swaps, composite lift chains, near-commutation cases, conflict reproduction cases, and AP migration cases; regression failures trigger quarantine.
07.R1.d — Transport atlas index
Construct an atlas that maps each pair ((\mathcal{R}_A,\mathcal{R}_B)) to known transport paths and their truth status, records best-known EQUIV/DUAL/MIGRATE options, records conflicts and fences, and is replay-verifiable; atlas entries are certified graph objects, not recommendations.
07.R2 — Laws
07.R2.a — Replay determinism binds legality
Transport legality is defined by replay determinism: reproducible verifier disagreement under identical pins is CONFLICT.
07.R2.b — Map changes require MIGRATE mediation
Meaning-bearing changes in maps/witnesses invalidate prior EQUIV claims; resolution is MIGRATE or issuance of a new EQUIV claim with new witnesses and pins.
07.R2.c — Registry collisions resolved by manifest change
Any collision of ids/digests is resolved only by changing manifest inputs and producing explicit MIGRATE edges; never by silent overwrite.
07.R2.d — Conflicts remain quarantined until resolved
Quarantines cannot be lifted by time or preference; resolution requires replay-verifiable repair/migration or permanent quarantine with revocation receipts.
07.R3 — Constructions
07.R3.a — Reusable transport harness
Construct a deterministic transport harness that:
computes lift paths,
constructs maps,
runs conjugacy checks and commutation tests,
emits transcripts, residual ledgers, and conflict packets,
packages replay capsules.
07.R3.b — Exporter/importer for transport bundles
Define a bundle format containing maps, invariants, residual ledgers, transcripts, replay capsules, and all required pinned profiles; the importer replays and validates before admitting claims into OK routes.
07.R3.c — AP migration plan template
When (\mathsf{AP}) changes, compute impacted lift paths, build compat matrix old-vs-new AP features, rerun critical transport replays, emit MIGRATE edges for AP profile, quarantine routes relying on now-illegal swaps.
07.R3.d — Audit reports for transport usage
Audit reports list transport paths used, commutation residuals and NEAR disclosures, open obligations and quarantines, and migration histories; audits must be deterministic and suitable for governance.
07.R4 — Protocols
07.R4.a — Replay closure protocol for OK transport
A transport claim is OK only if replay reproduces planner outputs, residual computations, endpoint comparisons, and final truth classification under pinned profiles.
07.R4.b — Conflict packet protocol
On reproducible mismatch:
compute minimal witness set (bounded under (\chi)),
include deterministic reproduction recipe,
generate quarantine fences and propagate,
propose resolution candidates (repair or migration).
07.R4.c — Migration acceptance protocol
A MIGRATE edge is accepted only if:
compat matrices are complete over declared scope,
regressions succeed under replay,
rollback plan exists,
importer validates pins and replays before admission.
07.R4.d — HD-SCT specialization: transport endpoints are ((d,k))-typed
In HD-SCT, all transport endpoints and domain specs must explicitly bind ((d,k)) and any meaning-bearing policy digests (NF profile, canonical bytes profile, metric profile, corridor profile). Any attempt to transport across ((d,k)) without an explicit map and explicit invariants is invalid and must be typed AMBIG/FAIL by corridor rules; any attempt to change profiles without MIGRATE is invalid by governance law.
Ch07 — Transport Legality (DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE) in HD-SCT
Ch08 — Corridors, Truth Typing, and Failure Modes
(\mathrm{OK}/\mathrm{NEAR}/\mathrm{AMBIG}/\mathrm{FAIL}) as Routable Outcomes
□ Square — Corridors as Typed Constraints on Transforms and Routes
08.S1 — Corridor Objects
08.S1.a — Corridor profile as a first-class policy object
A corridor is a pinned policy object that constrains which transforms are legal, how transforms are verified, and how outcomes are typed. A corridor is not a heuristic; it is a contract.
Define a CorridorProfile as the tuple[\boxed{\mathfrak{C}:=\big(\mathrm{CorrID},\ \mathrm{Scope},\ \mathrm{Pins},\ \mathbf{b},\ \mathrm{Rules},\ \mathrm{Promote},\ \mathrm{RoutePolicy},\ \mathrm{SchemaVer}\big)}]with components:
(\mathrm{CorrID}): unique identifier (digest) of the corridor profile.
(\mathrm{Scope}): typed scope of applicability (address ranges; lens pairs; ((d,k))-ranges; operator families).
(\mathrm{Pins}): complete pinset required to interpret legality (normal-form profile, metric profile, serialization profile, adjacency profile, triangle mode policy, hub policy, etc.).
(\mathbf{b}): budget vector[\boxed{\mathbf{b}:=(\kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi)}]where (\kappa) bounds commutation residuals, (\beta) bounds approximation drift, (\delta) bounds recursion depth/verification depth, and (\chi) bounds computational work (step count, search expansion, replay cost).
(\mathrm{Rules}): outcome typing rules and mandatory artifacts.
(\mathrm{Promote}): promotion obligations and procedures (e.g., (\mathrm{NEAR}\to\mathrm{OK})).
(\mathrm{RoutePolicy}): routability constraints for planning (allowed truth thresholds, tie-break ordering, and publication gating).
(\mathrm{SchemaVer}): schema version.
Any claim that depends on unpinned corridor content is invalid under the corridor and is typed (\mathrm{AMBIG}) or (\mathrm{FAIL}) per rules below.
08.S1.b — Certified claim object and endpoint typing
Let (\mathcal{R}) denote the union of all representation types used by HD‑SCT across lenses and resolutions. A claim is a typed transform assertion between endpoints:[\boxed{\mathsf{Claim}:=(\mathrm{Src},\mathrm{Dst},\mathrm{Kind},T,\mathcal{I},\mathrm{Domain},\mathfrak{C})}]where:
(\mathrm{Src},\mathrm{Dst}) are typed endpoints (must pin lens (L\in{S,F,C,R}), dimension (d), scale (k), and all decode-relevant policy digests).
(\mathrm{Kind}) is the transport kind (e.g., DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE), when the corridor requires kinded transport.
(T) is an explicit forward map (partial function) (T:\mathcal{R}{\mathrm{Src}}\rightharpoonup\mathcal{R}{\mathrm{Dst}}).
(\mathcal{I}) is the invariant set declared by the claim (NF invariance, decode invariance, schedule invariance, commutation constraints, etc.).
(\mathrm{Domain}) is a DomainSpec (where (T) is defined; where verification is valid).
(\mathfrak{C}) is the corridor profile governing evaluation.
A claim without explicit endpoints and explicit domain is not eligible for (\mathrm{OK}).
08.S1.c — Evidence artifacts as mandatory outputs
Corridor evaluation produces an Outcome accompanied by structured evidence artifacts.
Define the evidence artifact types:
ReplayCapsule (\mathsf{RC}): deterministic procedure and inputs sufficient to reproduce evaluation, including all pins and digests.
Witness (\mathsf{W}): concrete check results (hash matches, invariant checks, commutation checks, decode checks).
ResidualLedger (\mathsf{RL}): a bounded residual disclosure required for (\mathrm{NEAR}).
EvidencePlan (\mathsf{EP}): a bounded candidate set and discriminators required for (\mathrm{AMBIG}).
FailureWitness (\mathsf{FW}): minimal counterexample or deterministic failure certificate required for (\mathrm{FAIL}) (including a reproduction recipe).
Evidence objects are routable: they may be traversed and composed along paths and are required to be address-indexed.
08.S1.d — Outcome object and truth typing
Define the truth type set[\boxed{\mathbb{T}_4:={\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL}}.}]
Define the Outcome object:[\boxed{\mathsf{Out}:=(\tau,\ \mathsf{RC},\ \mathsf{W},\ \mathsf{RL?},\ \mathsf{EP?},\ \mathsf{FW?},\ \mathrm{BudgetUse},\ \mathrm{Obligations})}]with:
(\tau\in\mathbb{T}_4) the truth label.
(\mathsf{RC}) a replay capsule pointer (mandatory for (\mathrm{OK}) and (\mathrm{NEAR}); optional but recommended for (\mathrm{AMBIG}); mandatory for (\mathrm{FAIL}) when reproducible).
(\mathsf{W}) the witness pointer set.
(\mathsf{RL}) present iff (\tau=\mathrm{NEAR}).
(\mathsf{EP}) present iff (\tau=\mathrm{AMBIG}).
(\mathsf{FW}) present iff (\tau=\mathrm{FAIL}) (unless corridor permits “unknown failure” classification; such corridors are non-publication corridors).
(\mathrm{BudgetUse}) records charged ((\kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi)) usage.
(\mathrm{Obligations}) is a list of promotion/repair obligations.
Outcome objects are first-class vertices in the routing layer: they are not annotations; they determine which routes exist.
08.S2 — Truth Algebra for Routing
08.S2.a — Truth order and meet/join semantics
Define a total preorder on (\mathbb{T}_4) by quality:[\boxed{\mathrm{FAIL}\prec \mathrm{AMBIG}\prec \mathrm{NEAR}\prec \mathrm{OK}.}]Define meet (\wedge) and join (\vee) as:[\tau_1\wedge\tau_2:=\min(\tau_1,\tau_2)\quad(\text{worst-link composition}),\qquad\tau_1\vee\tau_2:=\max(\tau_1,\tau_2)\quad(\text{best alternative}).]
08.S2.b — Sequential composition of outcomes (path typing)
Given a path (P=(e_1,\dots,e_m)) with per-edge outcomes (\mathsf{Out}i), define the composite truth:[\boxed{\tau(P):=\bigwedge{i=1}^m \tau(e_i).}]Define budget accumulation with pinned aggregation operators, defaulting to:[\kappa(P):=\sum_i \kappa_i,\quad\beta(P):=\sum_i \beta_i,\quad\delta(P):=\max_i \delta_i,\quad\chi(P):=\sum_i \chi_i,]and corridor acceptance requires:[\kappa(P)\le \kappa_{\max},\\beta(P)\le \beta_{\max},\delta(P)\le \delta_{\max},\chi(P)\le \chi_{\max}.]Corridors may replace (\sum) with (\max) for (\kappa,\beta) if the semantics are “peak residual” rather than “spent residual,” but the choice must be pinned in (\mathfrak{C}).
Composite evidence is the union of pointers; composite obligations are concatenated and deduplicated.
08.S2.c — Routability predicate
A corridor declares a route admissibility threshold (\tau_{\min}\in\mathbb{T}4). A path is routable under corridor (\mathfrak{C}) iff:[\boxed{\tau(P)\succeq \tau{\min}\quad\text{and}\quad\mathrm{BudgetUse}(P)\le \mathbf{b}\quad\text{and}\quad\mathrm{AllMandatoryArtifactsPresent}(P).}]Common thresholds:
Operational corridor: (\tau_{\min}=\mathrm{NEAR}) permitted with mandatory residual ledger disclosures.
Publication corridor: (\tau_{\min}=\mathrm{OK}) only.
Exploration corridor: (\tau_{\min}=\mathrm{AMBIG}) permitted, but must return evidence plans.
Threshold selection is itself pinned in (\mathfrak{C}).
08.S2.d — Promotion operator and closure
Define a promotion relation (\leadsto) between outcomes:[\boxed{\mathsf{Out}_{\mathrm{NEAR}} \leadsto \mathsf{Out}_{\mathrm{OK}}}]when all obligations in (\mathrm{Obligations}) are discharged and replay verifies the strengthened witness set under the same pins (or an explicit MIGRATE to new pins).
Promotion is not a rewrite: the promoted outcome is a new outcome with a new digest, new witness pointers, and a replay capsule reproducing the new checks.
08.S3 — Corridor Evaluation: Deterministic Typing Rules
08.S3.a — Minimal conditions for each truth type
Let (\mathsf{Claim}) be evaluated under corridor (\mathfrak{C}). Define deterministic outcome rules:
(1) (\mathrm{OK}) iff all conditions hold:
All required pins are present and match corridor scope.
DomainSpec is well-typed and non-empty.
Mandatory artifacts are present (maps, reverse maps where required, invariants).
Replay capsule reproduces the evaluation exactly.
All declared invariants (\mathcal{I}) are proved under pinned metrics and pinned NF/codec policies.
All residuals are exactly zero where the corridor requires exactness (e.g., NF equality), and commutation residuals satisfy (r_\kappa=0) when exact commutation is required.
(2) (\mathrm{NEAR}) iff:
All required pins are present and match corridor scope.
Replay reproduces evaluation deterministically.
Invariants hold within bounded residuals, with residual bounds (\le \beta) and commutation residuals (\le \kappa).
A ResidualLedger exists and includes metric id, bound, scope, obligations, and replay pointer.
(3) (\mathrm{AMBIG}) iff:
The claim cannot be made (\mathrm{OK}) or (\mathrm{NEAR}) because of underdetermination, but the corridor can bound the ambiguity into a finite candidate set; and
An EvidencePlan exists describing candidates, discriminators, routes, and promotion rules.
Typical AMBIG causes:
missing pins but corridor can propose required pinset;
multiple legal routes without pinned tie-break;
multiple normal forms under incomplete canonicalization;
domain ambiguity (uncertain applicability).
(4) (\mathrm{FAIL}) otherwise, including:
illegality under corridor (forbidden transform, forbidden swap, forbidden domain);
budget violation beyond corridor downgrade rules;
invariant violation beyond (\beta) or commutation residual beyond (\kappa);
nondeterminism or replay failure;
unbounded ambiguity (no finite candidate set within (\chi));
contradiction (two replayed witnesses disagree under identical pins for the same claim).
FAIL must include a FailureWitness with a reproduction recipe unless the corridor explicitly permits “non-reproducible fail” classification (not permitted for publication corridors).
08.S3.b — Corridors as recognizers of legality languages
Let (\mathcal{E}) be the set of all candidate edges (primitive transforms) and (\mathcal{P}) the set of all finite paths over (\mathcal{E}). A corridor defines a recognized language[\mathcal{L}_{\mathfrak{C}} \subseteq \mathcal{P}]of legal routable paths under its thresholds and budgets. Truth typing is the mechanism that assigns each word (P\in\mathcal{P}) to (\mathbb{T}4) and therefore determines membership in (\mathcal{L}{\mathfrak{C}}).
08.S3.c — Deterministic evaluation function
Define the corridor evaluation function[\boxed{\mathrm{Eval}_{\mathfrak{C}}:\mathsf{Claim}\to\mathsf{Out}}]as a deterministic function of:
claim payload,
pinned corridor profile,
declared invariants and metrics,
bounded computational budget (\chi).
Determinism requirement: given identical claim digests and identical corridor pins, (\mathrm{Eval}_{\mathfrak{C}}) must return identical outcome digests and identical truth types.
08.S3.d — Route planning as a certified optimization problem
Define a transport/transform graph (G=(V,E)) whose edges are claims (or families of claims) and whose edge evaluation is (\mathrm{Eval}_{\mathfrak{C}}). A route planner must produce:
the selected path,
the per-edge outcomes,
a composite outcome,
a replay capsule reproducing planning choices (tie-breaks and search ordering must be pinned).
The objective function is corridor-defined. A canonical objective is lexicographic:[\text{maximize }\tau(P),\ \text{then minimize }\chi(P),\ \text{then minimize }\beta(P),\ \text{then minimize }\kappa(P),]subject to admissibility constraints.
08.S4 — Reference Algorithms and Data Structures
08.S4.a — Truth and outcome composition
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import List, Optional, Tuple, Literal
Truth = Literal["OK","NEAR","AMBIG","FAIL"]
TRUTH_RANK = {"FAIL":0, "AMBIG":1, "NEAR":2, "OK":3}
def truth_meet(a: Truth, b: Truth) -> Truth:
return a if TRUTH_RANK[a] <= TRUTH_RANK[b] else b
def truth_join(a: Truth, b: Truth) -> Truth:
return a if TRUTH_RANK[a] >= TRUTH_RANK[b] else b
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Budget:
kappa: float
beta: float
delta: int
chi: int
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class ResidualLedger:
metric_id: str
bound: float
scope: Tuple[str, ...]
obligations: Tuple[str, ...]
replay_ptr: str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class EvidencePlan:
candidates: Tuple[str, ...]
discriminators: Tuple[str, ...]
routes: Tuple[str, ...]
promotion_rules: Tuple[str, ...]
replay_ptrs: Tuple[str, ...]
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class FailureWitness:
reason: str
repro_recipe_ptr: str
minimal_counterexample_ptr: Optional[str]
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Outcome:
truth: Truth
replay_ptr: Optional[str]
witness_ptrs: Tuple[str, ...]
residual_ledger: Optional[ResidualLedger]
evidence_plan: Optional[EvidencePlan]
failure_witness: Optional[FailureWitness]
budget_use: Budget
obligations: Tuple[str, ...]
def compose_outcomes(outs: List[Outcome], budget_cap: Budget) -> Outcome:
truth: Truth = "OK"
kappa = 0.0
beta = 0.0
delta = 0
chi = 0
witnesses = []
obligations = []
replay_ptrs = []
for o in outs:
truth = truth_meet(truth, o.truth)
kappa += o.budget_use.kappa
beta += o.budget_use.beta
delta = max(delta, o.budget_use.delta)
chi += o.budget_use.chi
witnesses.extend(o.witness_ptrs)
obligations.extend(o.obligations)
if o.replay_ptr is not None:
replay_ptrs.append(o.replay_ptr)
# budget enforcement
if kappa > budget_cap.kappa or beta > budget_cap.beta or delta > budget_cap.delta or chi > budget_cap.chi:
truth = "FAIL"
# composite artifacts: NEAR requires at least one residual ledger; AMBIG requires at least one evidence plan.
rl = next((o.residual_ledger for o in outs if o.residual_ledger is not None), None)
ep = next((o.evidence_plan for o in outs if o.evidence_plan is not None), None)
fw = next((o.failure_witness for o in outs if o.failure_witness is not None), None)
if truth == "NEAR" and rl is None:
truth = "FAIL"
if truth == "AMBIG" and ep is None:
truth = "FAIL"
if truth == "FAIL" and fw is None:
fw = FailureWitness(reason="Composite failure (budget/edge failure)", repro_recipe_ptr="REPRO_TODO", minimal_counterexample_ptr=None)
return Outcome(
truth=truth,
replay_ptr=replay_ptrs[-1] if replay_ptrs else None,
witness_ptrs=tuple(witnesses),
residual_ledger=rl,
evidence_plan=ep,
failure_witness=fw,
budget_use=Budget(kappa=kappa, beta=beta, delta=delta, chi=chi),
obligations=tuple(dict.fromkeys(obligations)),
)
08.S4.b — Deterministic edge evaluation skeleton
from typing import Callable, Dict, Any
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class CorridorProfile:
corr_id: str
pins: Tuple[Tuple[str,str], ...]
budget_cap: Budget
truth_threshold: Truth
schema_ver: str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Claim:
claim_id: str
src: str
dst: str
kind: str
domain_spec: str
invariants: Tuple[str, ...]
map_fwd_id: str
map_bwd_id: Optional[str]
pins: Tuple[Tuple[str,str], ...] # claim pins (must cover corridor pins)
# pointers to optional artifacts
witness_ptr: Optional[str]
replay_ptr: Optional[str]
def eval_claim(claim: Claim, C: CorridorProfile, verifier: Callable[[Claim, CorridorProfile], Dict[str, Any]]) -> Outcome:
"""
verifier returns a dict including:
- replay_ok: bool
- pins_ok: bool
- domain_ok: bool
- invariants_ok: bool
- residual_beta: float
- residual_kappa: float
- chi_cost: int
- witness_ptrs: list[str]
- obligations: list[str]
- evidence_plan: EvidencePlan|None
- failure_witness: FailureWitness|None
"""
r = verifier(claim, C)
# hard gating
if not r.get("pins_ok", False) or not r.get("domain_ok", False):
return Outcome("FAIL", claim.replay_ptr, tuple(r.get("witness_ptrs", [])),
None, None, r.get("failure_witness", FailureWitness("Pins/domain illegal", "REPRO_TODO", None)),
Budget(r.get("residual_kappa",0.0), r.get("residual_beta",0.0), 0, r.get("chi_cost",0)),
tuple(r.get("obligations", [])))
if not r.get("replay_ok", False) and C.truth_threshold in ("NEAR","OK"):
return Outcome("FAIL", claim.replay_ptr, tuple(r.get("witness_ptrs", [])),
None, None, r.get("failure_witness", FailureWitness("Replay failed", "REPRO_TODO", None)),
Budget(r.get("residual_kappa",0.0), r.get("residual_beta",0.0), 0, r.get("chi_cost",0)),
tuple(r.get("obligations", [])))
inv_ok = bool(r.get("invariants_ok", False))
beta = float(r.get("residual_beta", 0.0))
kappa = float(r.get("residual_kappa", 0.0))
chi = int(r.get("chi_cost", 0))
# typing
if inv_ok and beta == 0.0 and kappa == 0.0 and claim.replay_ptr is not None:
truth: Truth = "OK"
rl = None
ep = None
fw = None
elif inv_ok and beta <= C.budget_cap.beta and kappa <= C.budget_cap.kappa and claim.replay_ptr is not None:
truth = "NEAR"
rl = ResidualLedger(metric_id="METRIC_PINNED", bound=max(beta,kappa), scope=(claim.claim_id,), obligations=tuple(r.get("obligations", ())), replay_ptr=claim.replay_ptr)
ep = None
fw = None
else:
# if bounded candidates exist, allow AMBIG with evidence plan; otherwise FAIL
ep = r.get("evidence_plan", None)
if ep is not None:
truth = "AMBIG"
rl = None
fw = None
else:
truth = "FAIL"
rl = None
fw = r.get("failure_witness", FailureWitness("Invariant violation or unbounded ambiguity", "REPRO_TODO", None))
out = Outcome(
truth=truth,
replay_ptr=claim.replay_ptr,
witness_ptrs=tuple(r.get("witness_ptrs", [])),
residual_ledger=rl,
evidence_plan=ep,
failure_witness=fw,
budget_use=Budget(kappa=kappa, beta=beta, delta=0, chi=chi),
obligations=tuple(r.get("obligations", [])),
)
# corridor budget enforcement
if out.budget_use.chi > C.budget_cap.chi:
return Outcome("FAIL", out.replay_ptr, out.witness_ptrs, None, None,
FailureWitness("Cost budget exceeded", "REPRO_TODO", None),
Budget(out.budget_use.kappa, out.budget_use.beta, out.budget_use.delta, out.budget_use.chi),
out.obligations)
return out
08.S4.c — Route search with truth threshold and budgets
import heapq
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Optional
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Edge:
claim: Claim
to_node: str
def route_search(graph: Dict[str, List[Edge]], src: str, dst: str, C: CorridorProfile,
verifier: Callable[[Claim, CorridorProfile], Dict[str, Any]]) -> Optional[Tuple[List[Outcome], Outcome]]:
"""
Lexicographic best-first search:
maximize truth, then minimize chi, then minimize beta, then minimize kappa.
Only returns routes whose composite truth >= corridor threshold and budgets satisfied.
"""
# priority: (-truth_rank, chi, beta, kappa)
pq = []
init_outs: List[Outcome] = []
init_comp = Outcome("OK", None, tuple(), None, None, None, Budget(0.0,0.0,0,0), tuple())
heapq.heappush(pq, (-TRUTH_RANK[init_comp.truth], 0, 0.0, 0.0, src, init_outs, init_comp))
best = {}
while pq:
neg_tr, chi, beta, kappa, node, outs, comp = heapq.heappop(pq)
key = (node, comp.truth, chi)
if key in best:
continue
best[key] = True
if node == dst:
# enforce threshold
if TRUTH_RANK[comp.truth] >= TRUTH_RANK[C.truth_threshold]:
return outs, comp
continue
for e in graph.get(node, []):
o = eval_claim(e.claim, C, verifier)
outs2 = outs + [o]
comp2 = compose_outcomes(outs2, C.budget_cap)
# prune below threshold early if desired
if TRUTH_RANK[comp2.truth] < TRUTH_RANK[C.truth_threshold]:
continue
heapq.heappush(pq, (-TRUTH_RANK[comp2.truth],
comp2.budget_use.chi, comp2.budget_use.beta, comp2.budget_use.kappa,
e.to_node, outs2, comp2))
return None
08.S4.d — Routable outcome registry (edges as publishable graph items)
A certified system must maintain an outcome registry in which every evaluated edge is stored as a graph item:
edge id (\to) outcome digest,
truth type and mandatory artifacts,
corridor id and pinset digest,
expiry window for residual ledgers (optional),
promotion status.
Routes are computed over this registry, not over raw transforms.
❀ Flower — Corridors as Geometric Neighborhoods and Corridor-Nyquist Constraints
08.F1 — Corridors as subsets of state space
A corridor induces a set of admissible states and transitions. Let (\mathcal{X}) be a state manifold/carrier (e.g., (\mathbb{T}^d), a station ring (\Sigma_{B_d}), or a Square address lattice). A corridor specifies:
a pinned metric (d_\pi) on (\mathcal{X}),
a pinned admissible subset (\mathrm{Corr}\subseteq\mathcal{X}) defined by inequalities (hub-corridors, carry corridors, lock corridors),
and a pinned set of admissible transitions (\mathcal{U}) (e.g., allowed tunnel steps, allowed wraps, allowed lifts).
A claim is (\mathrm{OK}) only if it maps corridor states to corridor states and preserves pinned invariants; it is (\mathrm{NEAR}) if it maps corridor states into a bounded neighborhood of corridor with bounded residual.
08.F2 — Commutation corridors and noncommutative residuals
For transforms (T_1,T_2) on a shared corridor subset, the commutator residual[r_\kappa := d_\pi!\left(T_1\circ T_2,\ T_2\circ T_1\right)]is typed against (\kappa). This is the geometric form of “corridor commutation”: corridors constrain which operator reorderings are legal, and bound how far from exact commutation the system may drift.
08.F3 — Resolution corridors and aliasing failure
Corridors must include resolution constraints: if a projection reduces resolution (e.g., from (B_d) to (15)), the corridor must declare whether the projection is inside a Nyquist-like corridor where fold/unfold is invertible enough for the intended use. If not, the projection is many-to-one and must be typed (\mathrm{AMBIG}) (bounded ambiguity) or (\mathrm{FAIL}) (unbounded ambiguity), depending on whether the fiber can be bounded under (\chi).
08.F4 — Corridor intersections and routing feasibility
Corridor composition corresponds to intersection of admissible sets and conjunction of constraints. A route spanning multiple corridors is feasible only if there exists a nonempty intersection corridor on which all transforms and verifications are well-defined. Empty intersection implies route (\mathrm{FAIL}).
☁ Cloud — Truth Typing as Uncertainty Management with Bounded Evidence
08.C1 — (\mathrm{NEAR}) as bounded uncertainty with explicit disclosure
(\mathrm{NEAR}) is not “almost OK.” It is a different truth class requiring an explicit residual ledger that bounds the deviation under a pinned metric and declares scope and obligations. Any route that traverses (\mathrm{NEAR}) edges must carry these disclosures as part of the route artifact, and publication corridors typically forbid (\mathrm{NEAR}).
08.C2 — (\mathrm{AMBIG}) as bounded non-identifiability with a finite candidate set
(\mathrm{AMBIG}) is legal only when the system can bound the ambiguity into a finite, explicitly enumerated set of candidates under budget (\chi), and when an evidence plan specifies discriminators that would collapse ambiguity (promotion). If ambiguity is unbounded or cannot be enumerated within (\chi), the correct type is (\mathrm{FAIL}), not (\mathrm{AMBIG}).
08.C3 — Route-level uncertainty aggregation
Given a path outcome (\tau(P)), the route-level semantics are:
(\mathrm{OK}): route is fully certified under corridor.
(\mathrm{NEAR}): route is admissible only if the corridor allows NEAR; disclosures are mandatory and are inherited by any downstream reasoning.
(\mathrm{AMBIG}): route can be used only to generate an evidence plan; it cannot be used as a meaning-preserving rewrite.
(\mathrm{FAIL}): route cannot be used; downstream routes depending on it are invalid.
Thus truth typing is a routing calculus, not a narrative.
08.C4 — Publishing envelopes
A corridor defines a publishing envelope by specifying:
forbidden truth types for publication (usually (\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL})),
allowed disclosures (if any),
required closure checks (replay closure, invariant suite closure),
and quarantine behavior for failures.
✶ Fractal — Failure Modes as Typed Defect Classes and Repair Loops
08.R1 — Failure mode taxonomy (typed)
Define the failure mode classes (non-exhaustive but closed under corridor extension), each mapped to a default truth type and mandatory artifact:
PIN‑MISSING: unpinned meaning-bearing parameter (hidden knob).
default: (\mathrm{FAIL}) for publication corridors; (\mathrm{AMBIG}) allowed only if a finite pin completion set exists with an evidence plan.
DOMAIN‑ILLEGAL: transform applied outside declared domain; missing domain spec.
default: (\mathrm{FAIL}) with minimal counterexample.
INVAR‑VIOLATION: declared invariant fails beyond (\beta).
default: (\mathrm{FAIL}) with failing witness.
COMM‑VIOLATION: commutation residual exceeds (\kappa).
default: (\mathrm{FAIL}) unless corridor permits downgrade to (\mathrm{NEAR}) with residual ledger (rare; must be explicit).
ALIAS‑LEAK: many-to-one projection outside corridor, producing non-identifiability.
default: (\mathrm{AMBIG}) if fibers are bounded and enumerated; otherwise (\mathrm{FAIL}).
NONDET‑REPLAY: replay does not reproduce results under identical pins.
default: (\mathrm{FAIL}) with reproduction recipe.
BUDGET‑OVERFLOW: (\chi) overflow (search explosion), (\delta) overflow (verification depth), or residual overflow ((\beta,\kappa)).
default: (\mathrm{FAIL}), or (\mathrm{AMBIG}) only if a bounded alternative plan exists.
PATH‑DIVERGENCE: two admissible routes yield incompatible certified results under identical pins.
default: (\mathrm{FAIL}) with deterministic minimal witness set; corridors may refine into a dedicated conflict class, but within (\mathbb{T}_4) it is treated as (\mathrm{FAIL}) with quarantine.
08.R2 — Quarantine and fence propagation (routability closure)
A corridor must define quarantine rules:
An edge with outcome (\mathrm{FAIL}) is non-routable.
Any path that requires a failed edge is non-routable.
A fence is a deterministic exclusion set of edges and derived routes impacted by a failure witness.
Fence propagation is computed by traversing dependency graphs of route artifacts and endpoint scopes.
Quarantine is lifted only by:
promotion (NEAR→OK) under identical pins and verified obligations, or
explicit migration to new pins with certified compatibility and regression witnesses.
08.R3 — Repair loops as corridor-governed recursion
Repair is a typed recursion controlled by corridor rules:
Repair from NEAR: discharge obligations (tighten bounds, add witnesses, improve resolution, refine domain specs), then re-evaluate under same pins; if residual becomes zero, promote to OK.
Repair from AMBIG: execute evidence plan discriminators to collapse candidate set; if a unique candidate remains, re-evaluate and issue OK/NEAR; otherwise remain AMBIG.
Repair from FAIL: produce either (i) new evidence that changes evaluation legitimately under same pins (rare; typically a missing artifact), or (ii) a MIGRATE to new pins with a compatibility matrix and regression suite.
Repair outputs are new routable artifacts; repairs do not overwrite old artifacts.
08.R4 — Certification closure for corridor correctness
A corridor profile (\mathfrak{C}) is itself subject to certification:
determinism of evaluation and planning,
completeness of pinset requirements,
explicit thresholds and budget semantics,
mandatory artifact rules for each truth type,
and regression suites proving that common failure modes are correctly typed and fenced.
A corridor that cannot be replay-verified is non-admissible for any route claimed as (\mathrm{OK}).
Ch08 — Corridors, Truth Typing, and Failure Modes
Ch09 — Spin and Holonomy as Path-Dependence Witness
Spin loops as commutation receipts in HD‑SCT
□ Square — Discrete Holonomy in the Certified Transport Graph
09.S1 — Objects
09.S1.a — Typed endpoints and admissible morphisms
Fix a dimension/scale pair ((d,k)) and a pinned corridor profile (\mathfrak{C}) with budget vector[\mathbf{b}=(\kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi).]Let (\mathcal{O}) be the set of typed endpoints (addresses) in HD‑SCT, where each endpoint includes:
representation lens (L\in{S,F,C,R}),
dimension (d) and scale (k),
pinned normal-form profile digest,
pinned metric profile digest,
pinned codec/serialization profile digest,
pinned corridor/profile digests required for decode and legality.
A certified morphism (edge) is a proof-carrying transport/transform object[e:\ A \rightharpoonup B]equipped with:
an explicit forward map (T_e),
an explicit domain specification (\mathrm{Dom}(e)\subseteq \mathcal{R}_A),
optional backward map (T_e^{-1}) when the claim asserts invertibility,
declared invariant set (\mathcal{I}(e)),
evaluation outcome (\tau(e)\in{\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL}}) under corridor (\mathfrak{C}),
replay capsule pointer and witness pointers.
In this chapter, holonomy and spin are defined only for morphisms whose replay closure exists and whose domains are explicitly declared; holonomy is never asserted on implicit transport.
09.S1.b — Paths, composite maps, and partiality
A path (P) from (A) to (B) is a finite sequence of morphisms[P=(e_1,\dots,e_m),\qquad e_i:\ V_{i-1}\rightharpoonup V_i,\quad V_0=A,\ V_m=B.]The composite map of (P) is the partial map[T_P:=T_{e_m}\circ \cdots\circ T_{e_1},]with domain[\mathrm{Dom}(P):=\left{x\in\mathrm{Dom}(e_1):\ T_{e_1}(x)\in\mathrm{Dom}(e_2),\dots,\ T_{e_{m-1}}\circ\cdots\circ T_{e_1}(x)\in\mathrm{Dom}(e_m)\right}.]A path is evaluable at (x\in\mathcal{R}_A) iff (x\in\mathrm{Dom}(P)).
09.S1.c — Loops and loop holonomy as endomorphism content
A loop at endpoint (A) is a path (L) with identical endpoints:[L:\ A\rightharpoonup A.]The holonomy map of a loop (L) is the induced partial endomorphism (T_L:\mathcal{R}_A\rightharpoonup\mathcal{R}_A) with domain (\mathrm{Dom}(L)).
A loop is identity-holonomic on a test set (U\subseteq\mathrm{Dom}(L)) if (T_L(x)=x) for all (x\in U) in the corridor’s exact-equality sense (typically equality of pinned normal forms and/or pinned fingerprints). Otherwise it has nontrivial holonomy.
09.S1.d — Path-difference loop (holonomy witness for two routes)
Let (P,Q) be two evaluable paths from (A) to (B). If (Q) admits a certified inverse path (Q^{-1}) on a declared codomain subset containing (T_P(U)), define the path-difference loop at (A) by[\boxed{\mathrm{Loop}(P,Q):=Q^{-1}\circ P:\ A\rightharpoonup A.}]When this loop is evaluable on (U\subseteq \mathrm{Dom}(P)\cap \mathrm{Dom}(Q)), it is the canonical witness of path dependence:[T_{\mathrm{Loop}(P,Q)}(x)=x \ \ \forall x\in U\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quadT_P(x)=T_Q(x)\ \ \forall x\in U.]
This converts “two routes disagree” into a single loop endomorphism that can be measured, budgeted, replayed, and routed around.
09.S1.e — Spin loop (commutator loop)
Let (A) be a fixed endpoint and let (a,b:\ A\rightharpoonup A) be two certified endomorphisms (often composites of primitive steps). Suppose both admit certified partial inverses on a declared common corridor domain.
Define the spin loop (group commutator path) by[\boxed{\mathrm{Spin}(a,b):=a\circ b\circ a^{-1}\circ b^{-1}:\ A\rightharpoonup A.}]Spin is a loop-valued invariant: it equals the identity loop exactly when (a) and (b) commute on the declared domain.
09.S1.f — Holonomy residual and pinned metrics
Fix a pinned metric (d_\pi) on (\mathcal{R}A) (or on its normal forms), and a pinned canonicalization operator (\mathrm{NF}\pi). Define the holonomy residual of a loop (L) on a test set (U\subseteq\mathrm{Dom}(L)) by[\boxed{\mathrm{Res}\pi(L;U):=\sup{x\in U}\ d_\pi!\big(\mathrm{NF}\pi(T_L(x)),\ \mathrm{NF}\pi(x)\big).}]In corridors where equality is fingerprint equality, (d_\pi) may be the discrete metric on pinned fingerprints:[d_\pi(u,v):=\begin{cases}0,& \mathrm{fp}\pi(u)=\mathrm{fp}\pi(v),\1,& \text{otherwise}.\end{cases}]The corridor profile pins which metric is authoritative for each invariant family.
09.S1.g — SpinReceipt (commutation receipt artifact)
A SpinReceipt is the minimal proof-carrying artifact that records a measured spin loop (or general path-difference loop) under a corridor:[\boxed{\mathsf{SR}:=(A,\ \mathfrak{C},\ a,\ b,\ \mathrm{Spin}(a,b),\ U,\ d_\pi,\ \mathbf{b},\ \mathrm{Res}_\pi,\ \tau,\ \mathsf{RC},\ \mathsf{W},\ \mathsf{RL?},\ \mathsf{EP?},\ \mathsf{FW?}).}]A SpinReceipt is a routable object. A route planner may require SpinReceipts at planning time (commutation gating), and may attach them to lift chains, tunnel schedules, and lens-swap sequences as mandatory commutation evidence.
09.S2 — Operators
09.S2.a — Commutation check as a loop-evaluation operator
Define the commutation-check operator[\boxed{\mathrm{CheckComm}\mathfrak{C}(a,b;U):=\mathrm{Eval}\mathfrak{C}\big(\mathrm{Spin}(a,b);\ U\big),}]where (\mathrm{Eval}_\mathfrak{C}) is the corridor’s deterministic evaluator producing an outcome[\mathsf{Out}=(\tau,\mathsf{RC},\mathsf{W},\mathsf{RL?},\mathsf{EP?},\mathsf{FW?},\mathrm{BudgetUse},\mathrm{Obligations}).]The evaluator is required to:
compute (\mathrm{Res}_\pi(\mathrm{Spin}(a,b);U)),
charge commutation residual against (\kappa),
charge any approximation drift against (\beta),
charge search/replay cost against (\chi),
produce (\mathrm{OK}) only under replay closure and exact invariant satisfaction.
09.S2.b — Holonomy witness for two routes
Given two certified paths (P,Q:A\rightharpoonup B) with declared evaluation set (U\subseteq\mathrm{Dom}(P)\cap\mathrm{Dom}(Q)), define:[\boxed{\mathrm{Hol}\mathfrak{C}(P,Q;U):=\mathrm{Eval}\mathfrak{C}\big(\mathrm{Loop}(P,Q);\ U\big),}]when (Q^{-1}) is defined and certified on (T_P(U)).
This operator is the universal mechanism for:
detecting route disagreement,
producing a witness of the disagreement,
classifying the disagreement under budgets,
and generating repair obligations (strengthen invariants, refine domains, migrate profiles, or quarantine).
09.S2.c — Conjugation transport of operators across lenses
Holonomy and spin are defined on endomorphisms of a single endpoint. For cross-lens operator families, define operator transport by conjugation.
Let (u:\ A\rightharpoonup B) be an invertible certified transport and let (b:\ B\rightharpoonup B) be an endomorphism. Define the pullback of (b) to (A) by[\boxed{u^\ast b:=u^{-1}\circ b\circ u:\ A\rightharpoonup A.}]Define the pushforward of (a:\ A\rightharpoonup A) to (B) by[\boxed{u_\ast a:=u\circ a\circ u^{-1}:\ B\rightharpoonup B.}]Conjugation makes operator commutation testable “in one space” even when the original operators live naturally in different lenses.
09.S2.d — Holonomy class and loop normalization
A corridor may pin a loop normal form (\mathrm{NFLoop}_\pi) that canonicalizes a loop path (e.g., reduces adjacent inverse pairs, eliminates identity edges, normalizes edge ordering under pinned tie-break).
Define the holonomy class of a loop (L) as:[\boxed{[L]\pi := \mathrm{NFLoop}\pi(L).}]Loop normalization is mandatory whenever receipts are deduplicated, indexed, or used as route constraints; without normalization, identical holonomy content can fragment across multiple syntactic loops.
09.S3 — Invariants
09.S3.a — Path-independence ⇔ trivial holonomy
For evaluable routes (P,Q:A\rightharpoonup B) on test set (U), path-independence under corridor invariants is equivalent to trivial holonomy:[\mathrm{Res}\pi(\mathrm{Loop}(P,Q);U)=0\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad\mathrm{NF}\pi(T_P(x))=\mathrm{NF}_\pi(T_Q(x))\ \ \forall x\in U.]Thus, holonomy is the canonical witness of path dependence.
09.S3.b — Spin triviality ⇔ commutation
For endomorphisms (a,b:A\rightharpoonup A) with certified inverses on a declared common domain:[\mathrm{Res}\pi(\mathrm{Spin}(a,b);U)=0\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad\mathrm{NF}\pi(a(b(x)))=\mathrm{NF}_\pi(b(a(x)))\ \ \forall x\in U.]
09.S3.c — Conjugacy invariance of holonomy magnitude
Let (u:A\rightharpoonup B) be an invertible certified transport. For any loop (L) at (B), define the conjugated loop (u^\ast L:=u^{-1}\circ L\circ u) at (A). If the corridor pins metrics compatible under transport (i.e., (d_\pi) is transport-invariant on the declared domain), then:[\mathrm{Res}\pi(L;U)=\mathrm{Res}\pi(u^\ast L;\ u^{-1}(U)).]This is the formal statement that holonomy is a geometric invariant of the underlying structure, not an artifact of lens choice, when transports are certified as equivalences.
09.S3.d — Budget monotonicity and route-level holonomy control
Corridor budgets impose monotone constraints:
(\kappa) bounds commutation residuals (spin magnitude),
(\beta) bounds approximation drift,
(\chi) bounds loop search and replay cost,
(\delta) bounds recursion depth for receipts that require nested verification.
For any composed loop (L=L_1\circ L_2), corridor-defined aggregation rules imply:[\mathrm{Res}\pi(L;U)\ \text{is bounded above by a pinned function of}\ \mathrm{Res}\pi(L_1;U)\ \text{and}\ \mathrm{Res}_\pi(L_2;U).]The corridor pins whether residuals are summed, maxed, or combined by a mixed rule; the combination semantics are part of meaning and must be pinned.
09.S4 — Protocols and Algorithms
09.S4.a — SpinReceipt construction protocol
Given (A,\mathfrak{C},a,b,U):
Domain intersection. Compute and certify a domain (U\subseteq \mathrm{Dom}(a)\cap\mathrm{Dom}(b)\cap\mathrm{Dom}(a^{-1})\cap\mathrm{Dom}(b^{-1})) sufficient for evaluation.
Loop formation. Construct (L:=\mathrm{Spin}(a,b)=a\circ b\circ a^{-1}\circ b^{-1}).
Replay capsule. Produce (\mathsf{RC}) that deterministically replays:
evaluation set construction,
map application order,
canonicalization,
metric computation,
classification under ((\kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi)).
Residual computation. Compute (\mathrm{Res}_\pi(L;U)), and any auxiliary commutator diagnostics pinned by the corridor.
Truth typing. Output:
(\mathrm{OK}) iff residual is (0) under the corridor’s exact metric and replay closes;
(\mathrm{NEAR}) iff residual (\le\kappa) (and any drift (\le\beta)) with a ResidualLedger;
(\mathrm{AMBIG}) iff the corridor can bound ambiguity (finite candidates) with an EvidencePlan;
(\mathrm{FAIL}) otherwise with a FailureWitness.
Indexing. Store ([L]_\pi) in the SpinAtlas (receipt registry), keyed by pinned digests of (A,\mathfrak{C},a,b,\pi).
09.S4.b — Path-difference holonomy receipt (route comparison)
Given two routes (P,Q:A\rightharpoonup B) and a test set (U\subseteq\mathrm{Dom}(P)\cap\mathrm{Dom}(Q)), construct:[L:=\mathrm{Loop}(P,Q)=Q^{-1}\circ P:\ A\rightharpoonup A]and evaluate as in 09.S4.a. This yields a RouteHolonomyReceipt that can be used to:
certify that two routes are equivalent (OK),
disclose bounded disagreement (NEAR) with scope,
produce an evidence plan to disambiguate (AMBIG),
or certify failure and fence the route (FAIL).
09.S4.c — Canonical commutation receipt template library
Corridors may require receipts for specific generator pairs, including (non-exhaustive):
Lift–Spin receipts: commutation between scale lifts and circle/tunnel steps.
Axis-order receipts: commutation between per-axis steps (\mathrm{Step}{\delta_i}) and (\mathrm{Step}{\delta_j}) under pinned multi-axis scheduling.
DUAL-chain receipts: commutation receipts validating that alternative adjacency lift chains induce equivalent semantics (or bounded residual).
Snap–Transport receipts: receipts that snapping into hub corridors does not change coarse hub class under pinned truncations, beyond budget.
Each template fixes:
generator identifiers (by digest),
declared test sets,
mandatory invariants,
and required truth threshold for routability.
09.S4.d — Reference implementation skeleton (loop receipts)
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Callable, List, Optional, Tuple, Literal, Dict, Any
Truth = Literal["OK","NEAR","AMBIG","FAIL"]
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Budget:
kappa: float
beta: float
delta: int
chi: int
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class ResidualLedger:
metric_id: str
bound: float
scope: Tuple[str, ...]
obligations: Tuple[str, ...]
replay_ptr: str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class EvidencePlan:
candidates: Tuple[str, ...]
discriminators: Tuple[str, ...]
routes: Tuple[str, ...]
promotion_rules: Tuple[str, ...]
replay_ptrs: Tuple[str, ...]
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class FailureWitness:
reason: str
repro_ptr: str
counterexample_ptr: Optional[str]
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Outcome:
truth: Truth
replay_ptr: str
witness_ptrs: Tuple[str, ...]
residual_ledger: Optional[ResidualLedger]
evidence_plan: Optional[EvidencePlan]
failure_witness: Optional[FailureWitness]
budget_use: Budget
obligations: Tuple[str, ...]
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class LoopSpec:
loop_id: str
# callable maps on a shared state type; in the manuscript, these are typed partial maps
fwd: Callable[[Any], Any]
inv: Callable[[Any], Any] # inverse on declared domain
domain_pred: Callable[[Any], bool] # decides membership in declared evaluation domain
def spin_loop(a: LoopSpec, b: LoopSpec) -> LoopSpec:
def fwd(x):
return a.fwd(b.fwd(a.inv(b.inv(x))))
def inv(x):
# inverse of commutator is commutator with swapped order: b a b^{-1} a^{-1}
return b.fwd(a.fwd(b.inv(a.inv(x))))
def dom(x):
return a.domain_pred(x) and b.domain_pred(x)
return LoopSpec(loop_id=f"Spin({a.loop_id},{b.loop_id})", fwd=fwd, inv=inv, domain_pred=dom)
def holonomy_residual(loop: LoopSpec, U: List[Any], NF: Callable[[Any], Any], dist: Callable[[Any,Any], float]) -> float:
r = 0.0
for x in U:
if not loop.domain_pred(x):
continue
y = NF(loop.fwd(x))
x0 = NF(x)
r = max(r, dist(y, x0))
return r
def classify_spin(loop: LoopSpec, U: List[Any], NF, dist, budget: Budget, replay_ptr: str, witness_ptrs: List[str]) -> Outcome:
r = holonomy_residual(loop, U, NF, dist)
# budget charging: treat r as commutation residual (kappa) and also drift (beta) if the corridor chooses
kappa_use = r
beta_use = 0.0
chi_use = len(U) # placeholder; real corridors charge replay cost, search, and verification
if r == 0.0:
return Outcome("OK", replay_ptr, tuple(witness_ptrs), None, None, None,
Budget(kappa_use, beta_use, 0, chi_use), tuple())
if r <= budget.kappa:
rl = ResidualLedger(metric_id="METRIC_PINNED", bound=r, scope=(loop.loop_id,),
obligations=("PROMOTE_BY_TIGHTENING_OR_REFINEMENT",), replay_ptr=replay_ptr)
return Outcome("NEAR", replay_ptr, tuple(witness_ptrs), rl, None, None,
Budget(kappa_use, beta_use, 0, chi_use), rl.obligations)
fw = FailureWitness(reason="Spin residual exceeds kappa budget", repro_ptr=replay_ptr, counterexample_ptr=None)
return Outcome("FAIL", replay_ptr, tuple(witness_ptrs), None, None, fw,
Budget(kappa_use, beta_use, 0, chi_use), tuple())
❀ Flower — Continuous Spin, Holonomy, and Curvature as the Geometry of Noncommutation
09.F1 — Holonomy from flows and connections
Let (\mathcal{M}) be a smooth state manifold (e.g., (\mathbb{T}^d) or a smooth model space whose discretizations produce the Square carriers). Let (A,B) be (possibly unbounded) generators of flows on (\mathcal{M}), with flow maps[\Phi_A^t:=e^{tA},\qquad \Phi_B^t:=e^{tB}.]Noncommutation is measured by the Lie bracket ([A,B]), and holonomy is the integrated manifestation of that bracket along loops.
09.F2 — Spin loop as a commutator of exponentials
Define the infinitesimal spin loop at step (\Delta t) by the commutator of the two flows:[\boxed{\mathrm{Spin}_{\Delta t}(A,B):=e^{\Delta t A},e^{\Delta t B},e^{-\Delta t A},e^{-\Delta t B}.}]This is a loop in the diffeomorphism group (or semigroup, when only partial inverses exist) acting on (\mathcal{M}).
When the Baker–Campbell–Hausdorff expansion is valid on a corridor domain, the leading-order holonomy is:[\boxed{\mathrm{Spin}_{\Delta t}(A,B)=\exp!\left(\Delta t^2 [A,B] + O(\Delta t^3)\right).}]Thus, the commutator bracket ([A,B]) is the curvature density controlling spin at small steps.
09.F3 — Holonomy as curvature integrated over a loop
Let a path (\gamma:[0,1]\to\mathcal{M}) be generated by a time-dependent vector field (V(t)). A connection-like transport rule (pinned by corridor policy) defines parallel transport along (\gamma). The holonomy of a closed loop (\gamma) is the induced endomorphism on the fiber (or on the state space when the transport is intrinsic).
Spin receipts in the discrete HD‑SCT graph correspond to sampled holonomy of such loop transports; the pinned commutation budget (\kappa) is a discrete corridor bound on curvature-integral magnitude.
09.F4 — Corridor geometry: spin‑kill and curvature damping
A corridor may enforce a spin-kill constraint: only allow operator schedules whose commutator residual is bounded or whose higher-order symmetric compositions cancel leading curvature terms.
Canonical examples include:
Symmetric splitting schedules that reduce leading-order spin accumulation (e.g., Strang-type symmetrizations), and
Curvature damping rules that refine resolution or change charts when spin receipts exceed (\kappa).
In HD‑SCT, these are realized as route constraints requiring specific SpinReceipts to be (\mathrm{OK}) or (\mathrm{NEAR}) before a composite schedule is admitted as routable.
☁ Cloud — Spin as a Random Variable and Receipts as Confidence-Bearing Evidence
