09.C1 — Noisy evaluation and probabilistic holonomy
When measurements, floating representations, or stochastic approximations enter, loop evaluation yields a random residual (\widehat{\mathrm{Res}}\pi(L;U)). Under a pinned noise model, define:[\widehat{r}:=\widehat{\mathrm{Res}}\pi(L;U),\qquadr:=\mathbb{E}[\widehat{r}],\qquad\mathrm{Var}(\widehat{r})\ \text{pinned or estimated}.]A corridor must pin the inference rule mapping (\widehat{r}) into truth typing; absent pinned inference, the outcome is (\mathrm{AMBIG}).
09.C2 — Probabilistic receipts: confidence and risk envelopes
A ProbabilisticSpinReceipt extends (\mathsf{SR}) with confidence structure:
estimator specification,
confidence intervals for residual,
sample size and sampling plan digest,
failure probabilities or tail bounds,
replay recipe reproducing the estimator and randomness control (seed pinning or distribution pinning).
Truth typing rules remain discrete:
(\mathrm{OK}) requires deterministic zero residual under pinned exactness (or a pinned probabilistic notion of “almost surely zero” that is itself replayable and publishable),
(\mathrm{NEAR}) requires bounded residual with disclosed confidence and scope,
(\mathrm{AMBIG}) requires a bounded candidate set (e.g., multiple plausible holonomy magnitudes due to insufficient samples) and an evidence plan,
(\mathrm{FAIL}) requires a reproducible violation beyond budgets or a reproducible inability to bound risk under (\chi).
09.C3 — Uncertainty propagation through routes
Given a route (P) composed of edges with outcomes (\tau_i), the route truth is the meet (\bigwedge_i\tau_i). For spin receipts, uncertainty propagates as:
any required commutation receipt typed (\mathrm{FAIL}) blocks the route,
(\mathrm{AMBIG}) receipts prevent semantic rewriting and force evidence planning,
(\mathrm{NEAR}) receipts impose mandatory residual disclosures and downstream obligations.
Thus probabilistic holonomy is routable only to the extent that the corridor allows NEAR and that disclosures are carried.
09.C4 — Statistical discriminators for AMBIG holonomy
When a loop is typed (\mathrm{AMBIG}), the evidence plan typically specifies discriminators such as:
refinement tests (increase (k) or (B_d) and re-evaluate spin),
domain restriction tests (evaluate on a smaller corridor subset),
schedule changes (alternate generator orderings and compare receipts),
cross-lens conjugacy checks (transport loop to a different lens and re-measure under a transport-invariant metric).
All discriminators must be finite and (\chi)-bounded to remain (\mathrm{AMBIG}); otherwise the corridor must type (\mathrm{FAIL}).
✶ Fractal — Spin Accumulation Across Scale and Governance by Receipts
09.R1 — Spin growth and path dependence under repeated composition
Even when each individual step appears corridor-close, repeated noncommutation can accumulate into macroscopic drift. Let (a,b) be two endomorphisms and consider repeated schedules such as ((ab)^n) versus ((ba)^n). The discrepancy is governed by repeated commutator insertions:[(ab)^n = (ba)^n \cdot \prod_{j=1}^{n-1} \mathrm{Spin}(a,b)^{\theta_j},]for corridor-pinned exponents (\theta_j) determined by group identities on the admissible domain. The essential point is that spin receipts must be treated as first-class scale-governance objects: a small nonzero holonomy can become large after many compositions unless the corridor enforces damping, schedule symmetrization, or refinement.
09.R2 — Holonomy localization and curvature concentration
Spin is not generally uniform across state space. The corridor therefore permits localized receipts:
evaluate on structured test sets (U) (hub meshes, carry hyperplanes, station partitions),
compute scope-limited residual ledgers,
and attach these to routes that traverse the same scope.
This yields a holonomy atlas: a map from operator pairs and scopes to certified receipts. Curvature is treated as concentrated where commutators are large (e.g., on boundary loci such as carry sets, aliasing corridors, or hub transitions), and the atlas supports targeted patching.
09.R3 — Governance: commutation receipts as non-negotiable artifacts
A transport planner is permitted to assert path equivalence only via a holonomy witness:
Two distinct routes are equivalent in a corridor only if the path-difference loop receipt is (\mathrm{OK}) (or (\mathrm{NEAR}) when the corridor permits NEAR rewriting with disclosures and obligations).
Non-adjacent representation swaps or composite lift chains require commutation receipts for the reorderings they implicitly assume.
Any claim of “commutes” without a SpinReceipt (or an explicitly referenced previously certified receipt in the atlas) is typed (\mathrm{AMBIG}) or (\mathrm{FAIL}) according to corridor policy.
Receipts therefore serve as the governance layer that replaces informal “should commute” intuition with certified loop evidence.
09.R4 — Repair loop: spin‑kill, refinement, and migration
When a required SpinReceipt is not (\mathrm{OK}), corridor-governed repair proceeds by the minimal admissible option:
Promotion repair (NEAR→OK): refine resolution, tighten domain, strengthen invariants, or change schedule to reduce residual to zero; reissue receipt with replay closure.
Disambiguation repair (AMBIG): execute evidence plan discriminators to produce a unique candidate receipt and re-evaluate.
Meaning evolution (MIGRATE): if the only way to reconcile is to change pinned profiles (normal forms, metrics, operator definitions), produce an explicit migration with compatibility matrix and regressions; receipts bind to the migrated profiles.
Quarantine (FAIL): if residual violates budgets or replay fails, fence routes that depend on the failed commutation and store a failure witness; future routing must avoid the fenced region unless repaired or migrated.
This closes the holonomy governance loop: spin is measured, typed, routed, and either controlled or fenced.
Ch09 — Spin and Holonomy as Path-Dependence Witness
Ch10 — Meta-Zero and Snap
Alternating projections → canonical representative + residual ledger
Let (\mathsf X) be a complete inner-product state space (finite-dimensional (\mathbb{R}^n), (\mathbb{C}^n), or a separable Hilbert space) equipped with norm (|\cdot|). Let (\mathfrak G) be the directed multigraph of representation changes available inside HD‑SCT at fixed ((d,k)) (square/circle/triangle carriers at a locked depth), and let each oriented edge (e: X \to Y) be equipped with a forward map (f_e: X\to Y) and a backward map (g_e: Y\to X) (possibly approximate or corridor‑restricted).
10.0 Global primitives (used by all lenses)
10.0.1 Zero corridors (per pair)
For any pair ((X\leftrightarrow Y)) with forward (f:X\to Y) and backward (g:Y\to X), define the zero corridor on (X) as the fixed‑set of the round‑trip map:[Z_X ;:=; \mathrm{Fix}(g\circ f);=;{x\in X:; g(f(x))=x}.]Equivalently, (Z_Y:=\mathrm{Fix}(f\circ g)) on (Y). These sets are the maximal corridors on which the “becoming” (X\to Y\to X) is lossless (exactly reversible).
For any (x\in X), define its distance‑to‑zero residual (a corridor‑exit witness):[r_{(f,g)}(x);:=;\bigl|x-(g\circ f)(x)\bigr|.]A zero corridor certificate is a bound (r_{(f,g)}(x)\le \beta_{(f,g)}) under a pinned metric; exceeding the bound is corridor violation.
10.0.2 The meta‑zero intersection
HD‑SCT carries multiple logically independent corridor families. The core meta‑zero (the “zero point of everything”) is the intersection of the principal corridor families:[\mathcal Z_\star;:=; Z_{\text{carrier}}\cap Z_{\text{Nyquist}}\cap Z_{\Pi}\cap Z_{\text{spec}}\cap Z_{\text{spin}}.]On (\mathcal Z_\star), all intended rotations commute (up to the chosen tolerances), and all cross‑lens transports become genuine changes of coordinates rather than lossy reinterpretations.
10.0.3 Corridor projectors and fixed‑set enforcement
A corridor projector is any deterministic map (\mathcal P:\mathsf X\to\mathsf X) such that (\mathrm{Fix}(\mathcal P)=Z) for a corridor set (Z\subseteq\mathsf X), together with a residual functional (r_{\mathcal P}(x):=|x-\mathcal P(x)|) (or a pinned equivalent).
Key corridor‑enforcement gates used throughout the framework include:
Bandlimit / alias‑kill gate: (\mathcal P_B).
Representability gate: (\Pi_h = R_h S_h).
Low‑band “same‑physics” spectral gate: (P_{\Lambda}) (or (P_{\le\Lambda})).
Spin‑kill / commutator‑damping gate: (\mathcal P_{\text{spin},\varepsilon}), projecting near (\ker([D,\Omega])) (or the appropriate holonomy‑null corridor in HD‑SCT).
These gates need not commute. The point of this chapter is to canonically reconcile them.
10.0.4 The Snap operator (canonical corridor lock)
Fix a deterministic ordered gate list (\mathbf P=(P_1,\dots,P_m)), with each (P_i) enforcing one corridor family. Define the one‑step composite:[T ;:=; P_m\circ\cdots\circ P_1,]and define the Snap (corridor‑lock) output as the fixed‑point of alternating projections (when the limit exists):[\psi_\star ;:=; \lim_{n\to\infty}T^n(\psi).]A canonical Snap engine returns (\psi_\star) and a structured residual ledger containing: path defects (|\Delta|), alias leakage, rank/conditioning witnesses, and spin magnitude (plus any additional pinned residual metrics mandated by corridor policy).
10.1 ■ Square lens
10.1.1 Atoms: square‑carrier meta‑zero as fixed corridors
Let (\mathsf X_\square(d,k)) denote the square carrier at locked dimension‑depth, with pinned resolution parameter (h=h(d,k)) (encoding the discrete sampling scale). The square lens contributes two structurally central corridor constraints:
Projection‑zero / representability corridor.Let (S_h:\mathsf X\to\mathsf X_\square) be the sampling/discretization map and (R_h:\mathsf X_\square\to\mathsf X) a reconstruction/lift map (both pinned). Define[\Pi_h := R_hS_h:\mathsf X\to\mathsf X,\qquadZ_{\Pi}:=\mathrm{Fix}(\Pi_h).]Then (Z_{\Pi}) is precisely the subspace of states that are exactly representable at resolution (h).
Carrier‑zero corridor.Square legality requires the carrier itself to be stable under the planned rotations (boundedness/coercivity constants for the transforms in scope). Carrier‑zero is the shared legality space in which basis rotations and transports are well‑posed.
For each declared square edge (e) with maps ((f_e,g_e)), define the corresponding square zero corridor (Z_e=\mathrm{Fix}(g_e\circ f_e)), and treat[Z_\square ;:=;\bigcap_{e\in\mathfrak G_\square} Z_e]as the square‑local feasibility domain. This is the square contribution to (\mathcal Z_\star) (prior to spectral and spin constraints). The square “distance‑to‑zero” witness is the per‑edge residual (r_e(x)=|x-(g_e\circ f_e)(x)|).
10.1.2 Rotations: corridor‑lock as a deterministic projector stack
A square‑compatible Snap engine is built as a projector stack (an operator registry plus a deterministic script), with ordering treated as a first‑class, pinned parameter because noncommuting gates imply order sensitivity.
A canonical baseline stack is the four‑gate chain[T ;=; \mathcal P_{\text{spin},\varepsilon}\circ P_{\Lambda}\circ \Pi_h\circ \mathcal P_B,]understood as an operator on the chosen carrier for the current route (square state, joint square×circle state, or the full product state—depending on which corridors are being locked in the current segment).
Deterministic Snap iteration.Given (\psi^{(0)}=\psi), iterate[\psi^{(n+1)}=T(\psi^{(n)}),\qquad n=0,1,2,\dots]until a pinned stopping rule fires. The Snap output is (\psi_\star=\psi^{(n_\star)}) together with a ledger (defined below), and the route’s truth classification is computed from that ledger.
Noncommutation control (relaxed iteration).When strict cycling exhibits oscillation, use a pinned relaxation parameter (\lambda\in(0,1]):[\psi^{(n+1)} ;=; (1-\lambda)\psi^{(n)}+\lambda,T(\psi^{(n)}),]with (\lambda) declared in the corridor profile (and therefore replayable). Any schedule adaptation that changes decode‑relevant behavior must be encoded or deterministically derivable under pinned rules; hidden knobs are illegal.
Implementation interface (square core).A corridor projector is implemented as:
a pinned GateID,
a deterministic apply(·) map,
a pinned residual metric (\mathrm{MetricID}) and digest,
a pinned bound (\beta) and scope rules,
and an optional witness generator (rank tests, conditioning tests, commutator estimates).
A Snap script is:[\mathsf{Script}=(\mathrm{GateSeq},\lambda,\mathrm{StopRule},\mathrm{RollbackRule},\mathrm{Pins}).]Rollback and re‑lock are defined as first‑class protocols in the snap script (not ad‑hoc interventions).
10.1.3 Shadows: residual ledger, blame assignment, and legality
Because gates do not perfectly commute, the Snap engine must quantify which corridor(s) are failing and by how much. The square lens therefore requires a residual ledger per projector, plus blame attribution keyed to corridor families (representability, rank stability, commutation, etc.).
A residual ledger must be a canonical evidence object representing bounded approximation. A compliant ledger schema includes:[\mathsf{RL}:=(\mathrm{RLID},\mathrm{MetricID},\mathrm{MetricDigest},\mathrm{Bound},\mathrm{Value},\mathrm{Scope},\mathrm{Expiry},\mathrm{CalibrationRef},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{IssuedAtPulse}),]where (\mathrm{Value}=r) is the measured residual and admissibility requires (r\le \mathrm{Bound}) under the pinned metric; scope explicitly binds which atoms/edges the residual applies to; expiry encodes when recalibration/promotion is required; and (\mathrm{ReplayPtr}) reproduces the measurement deterministically.
Required square residual channels (minimum).
Representability residual: (r_{\Pi}(\psi):=|\psi-\Pi_h\psi|).
Rank/conditioning witnesses: stability constants, kernel/quotient evidence, or explicit conditioning numbers (as pinned by the corridor profile).
Commutation residuals: for any commuting square enforced by the corridor profile, compute the defect[\Delta := f-h\circ g,]and record (|\Delta(\cdot)|) under pinned metric. Residuals bounded by (\beta) yield NEAR ledgers; exceeding pinned (\kappa) yields FAIL/CONFLICT under replay discipline.
Legality rule (NEAR is not free).NEAR handling is permitted only with residual ledger, scope, and replayable measurement; NEAR must propagate into publication disclosures when applicable.Lossy modes require residual ledgers and disclosures; otherwise the route is illegal.
10.1.4 Patches: corridor tightening, rollback, and empty‑intersection recovery
Square patching is policy‑driven:
Corridor tightening/loosening rules.Each corridor family carries threshold selection rules: tighten when residuals indicate structural drift; loosen only if the corridor profile explicitly permits widening (and such widening must trigger MIGRATE if it changes certified semantics).
Deterministic snap scripts.Operator ordering, relaxation, stopping criteria, and rollback rules are pinned. Determinism is mandatory: any adaptation that changes decode semantics must be encoded and replayable.
Intersection feasibility and fallback.Meta‑zero is an intersection corridor. If the intersection is empty (or empirically infeasible under pinned budgets), the engine must:
certify infeasibility within bounded search budget, and
compute a nearest feasible corridor candidate (a best‑effort snapped point minimizing a pinned penalty functional), emitting NEAR/AMBIG with an evidence plan rather than pretending OK.
Replay harness and transcript discipline.All corridor evaluations must be reproducible under replay; transcripts record corridor choice, pins, witnesses, residuals, budgets, truth outcome (\tau), and obligations/fences, and are append‑only. Replay capsules reproduce the entire evaluation deterministically under pins.
10.2 ◯ Circle lens
10.2.1 Atoms: hub meshes and phase‑space canonicalization
Let (\mathbb T^d) be the (d)-torus with wrapped metric (\mathrm{dist}{\mathbb T}) (coordinate‑wise circular distance combined by a pinned norm). Let (\mathcal H^d\subset \mathbb T^d) be the pinned hub mesh (the hub carrier used by tunneling and station logic). Define the circle Snap‑to‑hub operator:[\mathrm{Snap}{\mathcal H}(\phi);:=;\arg\min_{q\in \mathcal H^d}\mathrm{dist}_{\mathbb T}(\phi,q).]This is the circle’s canonical “collapse to the nearest allowed phase class.”
The circle residual is the phase distance to the chosen hub:[r_{\mathcal H}(\phi):=\mathrm{dist}{\mathbb T}!\bigl(\phi,\mathrm{Snap}{\mathcal H}(\phi)\bigr),]with deterministic tie‑break if multiple hubs attain the same minimum.
A hierarchical (fractal) hub mesh may be indexed by octave/level (n), with refinement (\mathcal H_n\subset\mathbb T^d) growing by depth; multi‑step convergence occurs when hub sets are hierarchical rather than coarse. This is the operational mechanism behind multi‑step fractal convergence under repeated snapping.
10.2.2 Rotations: circle gates inside the global Snap script
Circle participates in the global corridor lock through two gate families:
Hub‑snap gate (P_{\mathcal H}).Apply (\mathrm{Snap}_{\mathcal H}) (or its (d)-axis version) to enforce hub‑preserving feasibility.
Nyquist / visibility gates.Circle legality depends on whether circle resolution is sufficient for higher‑dimensional structure. This is encoded as a Nyquist‑type corridor: “injective fold/unfold” requires no alias overlap and therefore a sufficient circle carrier resolution. Nyquist‑zero is explicitly treated as a core zero corridor family.
Within a unified Snap stack, the circle’s gates appear either:
explicitly as (P_{\mathcal H}) and a circle‑Nyquist projector (\mathcal P_{\text{Nyq}}), or
implicitly via the bandlimit gate (\mathcal P_B) and low‑band gate (P_\Lambda) (when circle legality is enforced as spectral window legality).
10.2.3 Shadows: alias/leakage and phase residual accounting
The circle lens records:
Hub residual (r_{\mathcal H}) (distance to nearest hub).
Nyquist/alias leakage monitors, i.e., evidence that the circle carrier is too coarse for the present high‑D structure, producing many‑to‑one collapse. Nyquist violation is a first‑class obstruction and is explicitly tracked as aliasing/leakage in the global ledger output.
All circle residuals are emitted as ResidualLedger objects with pinned metric digests, bound, scope (axes, station windows, affected transports), expiry, and replay pointer (reproducing hub selection and distance computation).
10.2.4 Patches: refine resolution, refine hubs, checkpoint alignment
Circle patching is constrained by legality:
If Nyquist residuals or alias monitors fail, the only legal repair is to increase carrier resolution (raise circle station resolution (N), refine (\mathcal H^d), or narrow the enforced band window) under an encoded and replayable corridor update.
If the hub mesh is refined adaptively, checkpoint boundaries must be explicit: within any independently decodable segment, alignment regime must remain stable (phase bin rules and schedule selection fixed); inter‑segment changes require checkpoints restoring phase state and pins.
10.3 △ Triangle lens
10.3.1 Atoms: corridor policy as a projector‑selectable constraint
Triangle is the corridor‑policy layer: it selects which corridors are pinned as admissible routes (global vs per‑axis pinning, and how “visibility corridors” are interpreted). In Snap terms, triangle contributes:
a discrete policy state (\tau) (global (\in{A,B}) or per‑axis (\in{A,B}^d)), and
a policy‑constraint set (Z_\triangle(\tau)\subseteq\mathsf X) defining which transports and which gate parameters are legal.
Triangle’s meta‑zero contribution is the intersection of “policy‑consistent” corridors:[Z_{\triangle} ;:=; \bigcap_{\text{declared policy constraints}} Z_{\triangle,i}(\tau).]This is enforced by a deterministic policy gate (P_\triangle) that updates or validates (\tau) under pinned tie‑break.
10.3.2 Rotations: policy snap as constrained minimization with deterministic tie‑break
Triangle’s gate is not a metric projection in a continuous space; it is a selection operator over a finite policy set.
Given a candidate state (\psi), define a pinned objective (policy feasibility + residual cost):[\mathcal J_\triangle(\tau;\psi);:=;\sum_{i\in\mathcal I_\triangle} w_i, r_i!\bigl(P_i^{(\tau)}(\psi)\bigr)^2;+;\sum_{b\in\mathcal B_\triangle} \mathbf 1{\text{budget }b\text{ violated under }\tau},]where (P_i^{(\tau)}) are the gates whose parameters depend on (\tau), and (\mathcal B_\triangle) are pinned corridor budgets. Triangle snap chooses:[\tau_\star ;:=; \operatorname*{argmin}{\tau\in\mathcal T{\text{pinned}}}\mathcal J_\triangle(\tau;\psi),]breaking ties by a pinned total order on (\mathcal T_{\text{pinned}}) (so the route is replayable and verifier‑consistent). Any adaptive choice that changes decode‑relevant behavior must be encoded/replayable; otherwise it is illegal.
The triangle output is ((\tau_\star,\psi)) plus (i) the policy regret gap (difference to second best), and (ii) a scope‑bound statement of which transports were excluded by the policy.
10.3.3 Shadows: ambiguity witnesses and AMBIG discipline
Triangle is where “multiple consistent stories” appear. A corridor lock is not allowed to silently choose among multiple incompatible policy explanations without emitting AMBIG or NEAR evidence.
Define the policy ambiguity witness:[\mathrm{gap}(\psi);:=;\mathcal J_\triangle(\tau_{(2)};\psi)-\mathcal J_\triangle(\tau_{(1)};\psi),]where (\tau_{(1)}) and (\tau_{(2)}) are the best and second‑best pinned candidates. If (\mathrm{gap}(\psi)) is below a pinned threshold and the downstream artifacts depend on the choice, the correct outcome is AMBIG (with an evidence plan) rather than a hidden tie‑break. Unknown structure (insufficient metadata for policy selection) must be treated as AMBIG with a bounded evidence plan.
10.3.4 Patches: pin corridor mode, propagate disclosures, quarantine conflicts
Triangle patching is governance:
If a segment declares lossless behavior, any unaccounted residual loss yields FAIL; lossy mode requires residual ledger and disclosure, otherwise illegal.
If policy computations disagree under identical pins (verifier mismatch), classify CONFLICT and quarantine the route; conflict packets must be reproducible and fenced.
10.4 ✶ Fractal lens
10.4.1 Atoms: meta‑zero as intersection + invariance fixed point
Fractal is the global reconciliation layer. It treats meta‑zero as:
Intersection of all corridors (\mathcal Z_\star=\bigcap Z) (explicitly, the intersection of the corridor families listed in (\mathcal Z_\star)).
Fixed point of the global transform group (the “true shared object‑space”): the state that is invariant under the legal symmetry group of declared becomings. In operational terms, the zero point is the set of states for which the defect vector is (exactly or tolerably) zero, and the commuting/holonomy tests collapse. The framework packages these defects as explicit operators (commutators, overlaps, kernels, divergences), so “failure” becomes a measurable object rather than an anecdote.
10.4.2 Rotations: alternating projections across levels (multilevel Snap)
Fractal snap is the alternating projection engine:
Single‑level alternating projection.Use (T=P_m\circ\cdots\circ P_1) and iterate to a fixed point (\psi_\star=\lim_{n\to\infty}T^n(\psi)). This is the canonical corridor lock definition when gates do not commute.
Multilevel (coarse‑to‑fine) Snap.When (\mathcal Z_\star) is difficult at full resolution, enforce corridors on a scale ladder ((h_0>h_1>\cdots>h_L)), using coarse snaps to enter the correct basin, then refining while re‑locking constraints. This is explicitly treated as “adaptive refinement to improve intersection pushing,” with multilevel scheduling as a first‑class patch path.
All adaptive refinement decisions that change decode‑relevant behavior must be encoded/replayable under the corridor profile; otherwise the snap is not certifiable.
10.4.3 Shadows: convergence monitors, holonomy collapse, scale maps
Fractal shadows are convergence and path‑dependence diagnostics:
Snap convergence curves: monotone decrease of pinned residual aggregates, plateau detection (structural obstruction), and cycle detection (nonconvergence).
Holonomy/spin collapse: spin residual is an explicit channel in the global output ledger; successful snapping drives spin toward the spin‑zero corridor by the spin‑kill gate (\mathcal P_{\text{spin},\varepsilon}).
Scale‑dependent success/failure maps: record at which scales each corridor can be simultaneously satisfied; this is the falsifiable signature of whether (\mathcal Z_\star) is nonempty under the pinned profile.
All such diagnostics are emitted as ResidualLedger objects (pinned metrics, bounds, scope, expiry, calibration, replay pointers).
10.4.4 Patches: certify intersection, or compute nearest feasible corridor (with certificates)
Fractal patching completes the contract of Snap:
Intersection certification (OK).If the ledger shows all corridor residuals at or below pinned bounds, and replay reproduces the same truth classifications, emit OK with a transcript and certificate pack (ReplayCert, ResidualCert, and any domain‑specific certificates required by the corridor profile). Truth outcomes must reproduce under replay; otherwise the corridor engine is invalid for OK.
Nearest feasible corridor (NEAR) when (\mathcal Z_\star) is empty or unreachable.If the intersection is empty or not achieved within bounded iteration cost, compute a nearest‑feasible approximation (minimizing a pinned penalty functional over corridor distances), emit NEAR with a residual ledger, scope, expiry, and promotion obligations; NEAR without ledger/scope/replay is forbidden.
AMBIG when structure is underdetermined.If corridor choice or policy selection depends on unknown structure or missing pins, emit AMBIG with a bounded evidence plan; do not guess.
FAIL/CONFLICT when budgets are exceeded or verifiers disagree.If commutation residual exceeds (\kappa) under replay, emit FAIL (deterministic illegality) or CONFLICT (reproducible disagreement). Conflicts are quarantined and routed with conflict packets and fences, not silently absorbed.
Ch10 — Meta-Zero and Snap
Ch11 — Router Contract (≤6 hubs, deterministic order)
HD‑SCT route planning outputs replayable artifacts
□ Square — The Deterministic Router as a Pure Bounded Compiler
11.S1 — Objects
11.S1.a — Address space and strict parsing
Let (\mathsf{Addr}) be the set of globally addressable atoms. A target is a string-encoded address (v\in\mathsf{Addr}) whose grammar is pinned and strictly parsed by the canonical parser (the parse is not heuristic and is not user‑dependent). The strict parse returns a record[\mathsf{PA}=\mathrm{Parse}(v);:=;(\mathrm{Kind},\mathrm{Lens},\mathrm{Facet},\mathrm{ChapterIdx?},\mathrm{StationHeader?},\mathrm{LocalPath},\mathrm{ScopeTag?})]with (\mathrm{Kind}\in{\mathrm{Ch},\mathrm{App}}). The station header is present for chapter targets and is treated as an address-derived invariant carried inside the route plan as an explicit value (never recomputed implicitly during execution).
For chapter targets, the parsed record exposes the canonical station indices[(\alpha,\rho,\nu,\omega)\in {0,\dots,6}\times{0,1,2}\times{\mathrm{Su},\mathrm{Me},\mathrm{Sa}}\times{0,\dots,20},]derived from the chapter index and pinned station rules. The router treats ((\alpha,\rho,\nu,\omega)) as inputs to hub selection only through pinned rules in the router profile. (In particular, the router is not permitted to infer additional semantics from chapter titles or prose.)
11.S1.b — Truth lattice and routing intents
Let the corridor truth lattice be[\mathbb{T}:={\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL}}.]The router accepts an initial truth estimate (\tau_0\in\mathbb{T}) and an intent[\mathsf{Intent}\in\mathcal{I},]where (\mathcal{I}) is a closed, pinned set of task intents (e.g., VERIFY/BUILD/MIGRATE/RESOLVE/PUBLISH). Task intents define additional required hubs (intent hubs) and obligations but do not alter the core boundedness or determinism contract.
11.S1.c — Hub universe and mandatory signature
Let (\mathcal{H}) be the finite hub universe (appendix hubs). A hub ride is a sequence in (\mathcal{H}) culminating at the target.
A distinguished subset[\boxed{\Sigma:={\mathrm{AppA},\mathrm{AppI},\mathrm{AppM}}}]is the mandatory verification signature. Any route plan intended to certify (\mathrm{OK}) must include (\Sigma); (\Sigma) is never droppable under hub-cap enforcement.
Operationally (and deterministically), the signature hubs are interpreted as:
(\mathrm{AppA}): strict parsing + canonicalization (grammar correctness; canonical bytes hooks),
(\mathrm{AppI}): corridor truth typing + budget admissibility evaluation,
(\mathrm{AppM}): replay closure execution and environment pin validation.These roles are fixed as part of the router contract: the route may add hubs, but cannot remove the signature responsibilities without declaring a different corridor and emitting a non‑OK truth type.
11.S1.d — RouterProfile (pinned)
A RouterProfile (\pi_R) is a pinned data object whose digest (\mathrm{RouterProfileDigest}) is included in every route’s replay pointer. The profile pins, at minimum:
hub selection tables (LensBase, FacetBase, ArcHub),
mandatory signature (\Sigma),
truth overlay rules (AppJ/AppL/AppK insertion),
hub cap and deterministic drop policy,
canonical hub ordering policy, and
deterministic tie-break rules for ambiguous selections.The router output is a replayable artifact, and every route includes (\mathrm{RouterProfileDigest}) in its replay pointer.
11.S1.e — Deterministic base hub selectors
The router profile supplies deterministic selectors; canonical examples include:
LensBase. A pinned map[\mathrm{LensBase}:{S,F,C,R}\to\mathcal{H},]e.g.[S\mapsto\mathrm{AppC},\quad F\mapsto\mathrm{AppE},\quad C\mapsto\mathrm{AppI},\quad R\mapsto\mathrm{AppM}.]
FacetBase. A pinned map[\mathrm{FacetBase}:{1,2,3,4}\to\mathcal{H},]e.g.[1\mapsto\mathrm{AppA},\quad 2\mapsto\mathrm{AppB},\quad 3\mapsto\mathrm{AppH},\quad 4\mapsto\mathrm{AppM}.]
ArcHub. For chapter targets, a pinned selector[\mathrm{ArcHub}:{0,\dots,6}\to\mathcal{H},]e.g.[0\mapsto\mathrm{AppA},\ 1\mapsto\mathrm{AppC},\ 2\mapsto\mathrm{AppE},\ 3\mapsto\mathrm{AppF},\ 4\mapsto\mathrm{AppG},\ 5\mapsto\mathrm{AppN},\ 6\mapsto\mathrm{AppP}.]
The profile may refine ArcHub to depend on lane (\nu) (or other station header fields) provided the dependence is explicitly pinned and deterministic; any such refinement is part of (\pi_R) and therefore replayable.
11.S1.f — Truth overlay rail
The router profile pins a deterministic overlay selector[\mathrm{Rail}:\mathcal{I}\times\mathbb{T}\to \mathcal{H}\cup{\varnothing},]such that the presence of a non‑OK truth class inserts a dedicated hub:[\mathrm{NEAR}\Rightarrow \mathrm{AppJ},\qquad\mathrm{AMBIG}\Rightarrow \mathrm{AppL},\qquad\mathrm{FAIL/CONFLICT}\Rightarrow \mathrm{AppK},]and (\mathrm{OK}) inserts nothing (optionally inserting (\mathrm{AppO}) under publish intent, if pinned).
Overlay hubs are mandatory when their truth class occurs, unless the active corridor explicitly forbids the corresponding truth class for the given intent (e.g., forbidding AMBIG on a production-critical ride). Such forbiddance must be pinned and is interpreted as a routing legality constraint (not a soft preference).
11.S1.g — HubCap and DropLog
A hub ride is bounded by a hard cap:[\boxed{\mathrm{HubCap}:=6}]interpreted as “maximum number of unique hubs visited before the target.” Duplicate hubs do not count; duplicates are removed by deterministic compression.
When the cap would be exceeded, the router must apply a deterministic drop policy and must emit a DropLog recording all cap-enforced drops. No “best effort route” is permitted without a DropLog and truth typing that reflects the drops and any resulting loss of certainty.
A DropLog is a record:[\mathsf{DL}:=(\mathrm{Cap},\mathrm{Dropped},\mathrm{Reasons},\mathrm{RedundancyWitnesses?},\mathrm{TruthImpact}),]where:
(\mathrm{Dropped}\subseteq \mathcal{H}) is an ordered list (in drop order),
(\mathrm{Reasons}) includes “cap enforcement” and any redundancy facts used,
(\mathrm{TruthImpact}) records the deterministic downgrade rule (typically to AMBIG unless a redundancy proof is supplied and replay-verified).
11.S1.h — RoutePlan (replayable artifact)
A RoutePlan is the executable routing unit. It is a graph object: addressable, replayable, diffable, and auditable. Define[\boxed{\mathsf{RP}:=(\mathrm{Intent},\mathrm{Target},\mathrm{Scope},\mathrm{StationHeader?},\mathrm{HubsSeq},\tau_0,\mathsf{Pins},\mathsf{Obligations},\mathsf{DropLog}).}]Equivalently (with (\mathrm{StationHeader?}) absorbed into (\mathrm{Target}) for appendix targets), a canonical minimal schema is:[\mathsf{RP}:=(\mathrm{Target},\mathrm{StationHeader?},\mathrm{HubsSeq},\tau_0,\mathsf{Obligations},\mathsf{DropLog},\mathsf{Pins},\mathsf{Scope}).]
The pinned set (\mathsf{Pins}) includes, at minimum:
(\mathrm{GrammarDigest}) and (\mathrm{CanonBytesDigest}) for strict parsing and canonicalization,
(\mathrm{RouterProfileDigest}) and (\mathrm{CorridorProfileDigest}),
(\mathrm{EnvPinsDigest}) for replay environment closure,plus any domain-specific pins required by the intent (kernel/phase/bridge/control/lawpack/container/bundle schemas). Missing required pins deterministically forces AMBIG (recoverable) or FAIL (illegal) under the active corridor rules.
11.S2 — Laws
11.S2.a — Router purity law
Route planning is a pure function:[\boxed{\mathrm{Route}(v,\mathsf{Intent},\tau_0;\pi_R,\pi_C,\mathsf{Pins})\ \to\ \mathsf{RP},}]where all inputs are pinned and addressable. The router must not depend on ambient time, user behavior, mutable caches, network state, or any unpinned environment variable. Any deviation is nondeterminism and is classified as FAIL/CONFLICT under the corridor truth policy.
11.S2.b — Bounded routing law (HubCap)
All route plans must obey:
(#{\text{unique hubs before target}}\le 6),
(\Sigma={\mathrm{AppA},\mathrm{AppI},\mathrm{AppM}}) is enforced and never dropped,
hub ordering is deterministic,
cap enforcement is deterministic and produces a DropLog.This boundedness is a structural safety property: it prevents route explosion and keeps the abstract executable.
If a route cannot be constructed within cap while satisfying mandatory signature and mandatory overlay hubs, the router must either deterministically replace lower-priority hubs or classify AMBIG/FAIL with explicit obligations (evidence tasks, repinning tasks, or repairs). No best-effort behavior is permitted without DropLog and truth typing.
11.S2.c — Deterministic ordering law
The router profile pins a canonical ordering policy. A canonical hub sequence rule is:[\boxed{\mathrm{AppA}\ \prec\ \mathrm{ArcHub}\ \prec\ \mathrm{LensBase}\ \prec\ \mathrm{FacetBase}\ \prec\ \mathrm{OverlayHub}\ \prec\ \mathrm{AppI}\ \prec\ \mathrm{AppM}\ \prec\ \mathrm{Target}.}]Absent hubs are removed; duplicates are compressed deterministically.
11.S2.d — Overlay insertion law
Truth overlays are inserted deterministically:[\mathrm{OK}\Rightarrow \varnothing\ (\text{optionally } \mathrm{AppO}\text{ if publish intent is pinned}),\quad\mathrm{NEAR}\Rightarrow \mathrm{AppJ},\quad\mathrm{AMBIG}\Rightarrow \mathrm{AppL},\quad\mathrm{FAIL/CONFLICT}\Rightarrow \mathrm{AppK}.]Overlay insertion is part of the hub set prior to cap enforcement; if the overlay causes cap pressure, other optional hubs must be deterministically dropped (and the drop must be logged).
11.S2.e — Base transfer set law
For chapter targets (v=\mathrm{ChXX}\langle dddd\rangle.Lf.t), define the base transfer set:[T(v):={\mathrm{LensBase}(L),\ \mathrm{FacetBase}(f),\ \mathrm{ArcHub}(\alpha)}\ \ \text{(dedupe)}.]For appendix targets (v=\mathrm{AppX}.Lf.t), define:[T(v):={\mathrm{LensBase}(L),\ \mathrm{FacetBase}(f)}\ \ \text{(dedupe)}.]The route hub set begins from (T(v)\cup \Sigma\cup {\mathrm{Rail}(\mathsf{Intent},\tau_0)}\cup \mathrm{IntentHub}(\mathsf{Intent})), then applies deterministic cap enforcement and ordering. These constructions are pinned by the router profile.
11.S2.f — Optimization cannot change semantics
Any route optimization is permitted only if it does not alter semantics. Allowed optimizations include:
removing duplicate hub visits,
reordering commutative hub visits only when equivalence is witnessed (rare),
caching validated pins and proofs.Optimization may not add or drop required hubs, may not change truth classification, may not bypass pin validation, and may not bypass quarantine. Any optimization must be recorded in the transcript and pinned by engine version.
11.S2.g — INTER scope pinning law
If (\mathrm{Scope}=\mathrm{INTER}), then the route crosses manuscripts. INTER edges must pin:
both manuscript identifiers,
both manifests/policy digests,
required profile digests (router/corridor/grammar),
compatibility/migration layers if versions differ.Without these pins, an INTER link is AMBIG/FAIL and cannot be OK.
11.S3 — Constructions and Algorithms
11.S3.a — Router contract algorithm
Let inputs be ((v,\mathsf{Intent},\tau_0,\pi_R,\pi_C,\mathsf{Pins})). The router computes (\mathsf{RP}) as follows:
Strict parse.[\mathsf{PA}\leftarrow \mathrm{Parse}(v)]and if parsing fails under the pinned grammar, output (\tau=\mathrm{FAIL}) with an explicit parse failure witness (no heuristic recovery is permitted for an OK ride). The parse step is attributed to (\mathrm{AppA}) in the canonical ordering.
Compute base hub candidates (H).Initialize (H\leftarrow \varnothing). Add the pinned base hubs:[H\leftarrow H\cup{\mathrm{LensBase}(\mathsf{PA.Lens})}\cup{\mathrm{FacetBase}(\mathsf{PA.Facet})}.]If (\mathsf{PA.Kind}=\mathrm{Ch}), compute the arc index (\alpha) from the pinned station header rule and add (\mathrm{ArcHub}(\alpha)).
Enforce mandatory signature.[H\leftarrow H\cup\Sigma.]
Add intent hubs and truth overlay hub.Compute (H_{\mathrm{intent}}=\mathrm{IntentHub}(\mathsf{Intent})) (a pinned, small set; typically (\le 2)), and add. Compute (h_{\mathrm{rail}}=\mathrm{Rail}(\mathsf{Intent},\tau_0)) and add if nonempty.
Deduplicate.Convert to a deterministic hub multiset representation and compress duplicates; duplicates do not count against the cap. Deduplication must preserve the deterministic priority ordering that will later be used for dropping and ordering. (Dedup is not “dropping”; it is canonicalization.)
Enforce HubCap via deterministic drop.Apply deterministic cap enforcement:[(H,\mathsf{DL},\tau_1)\leftarrow \mathrm{EnforceCap}(H;\pi_R,\tau_0),]where (\tau_1) is (\tau_0) possibly downgraded (typically to AMBIG) if cap-enforced drops occur without redundancy witnesses. (\Sigma) is never droppable. Every cap-enforced drop is recorded in (\mathsf{DL}).
Deterministic ordering.Compute the hub sequence:[\mathrm{HubsSeq}\leftarrow \mathrm{Order}(H,\mathsf{PA};\pi_R),]consistent with the canonical ordering policy. Then append the target (v).
Compute obligations.Compute an explicit finite list of obligations (\mathsf{Obligations}) determined by ((\mathsf{Intent},\tau_1,\mathsf{PA},\pi_C)). Obligations are addressable evidence tasks for promotion and verification (e.g., evidence plan tasks for AMBIG, residual ledger tasks for NEAR, conflict packet tasks for FAIL).
Emit RoutePlan.Return:[\mathsf{RP}:=(\mathsf{Intent},v,\mathrm{Scope},\mathsf{PA.StationHeader?},\mathrm{HubsSeq},\tau_1,\mathsf{Pins},\mathsf{Obligations},\mathsf{DL}).]The RoutePlan includes the pinned digests necessary for replay and audit; in particular, every route includes (\mathrm{RouterProfileDigest}) in its replay pointer inputs.
11.S3.b — Deterministic cap enforcement with redundancy witnesses
Cap enforcement must be deterministic and profile-pinned. A canonical construction is:
Let (H) be the deduped hub set. Partition:[H = H_{\mathrm{must}}\ \dot\cup\ H_{\mathrm{opt}},\qquadH_{\mathrm{must}}:=\Sigma\cup H_{\mathrm{rail}}^{\mathrm{mandatory}},]where (H_{\mathrm{rail}}^{\mathrm{mandatory}}) contains the truth overlay hub when (\tau_0\neq \mathrm{OK}) and when the corridor permits that truth class.
If (|H_{\mathrm{must}}|>6), then the route cannot be satisfied under the hub-cap constraint; the router must output (\mathrm{FAIL}) (or (\mathrm{AMBIG}) with an explicit repinning obligation, if the corridor allows recovery by changing profiles). This is not an optimization problem; it is a legality failure under a pinned contract.
Otherwise, define a deterministic priority order (\prec_{\mathrm{drop}}) over optional hubs (H_{\mathrm{opt}}), pinned by (\pi_R). Apply the drop policy until (|H|\le 6). Canonical pinned drop rules include:
drop publish-only hub (\mathrm{AppO}) first,
drop (\mathrm{FacetBase}) if redundant with (\mathrm{LensBase}+\mathrm{ArcHub}+\Sigma),
drop (\mathrm{LensBase}) if redundant with (\mathrm{ArcHub}+\Sigma),
drop (\mathrm{ArcHub}) only if forced,with all drops recorded and with truth typically downgraded to AMBIG unless redundancy is witnessed and replay-verified.
A redundancy witness is a replayable certificate that the obligations discharged by the dropped hub are already discharged (or rendered unnecessary) by the remaining hubs under the pinned corridor. Without such a witness, a cap-enforced drop introduces underdetermination and must be represented as AMBIG unless the corridor forbids AMBIG (in which case the route is FAIL).
11.S3.c — Deterministic ordering function
Given the final hub set (H) and parsed address (\mathsf{PA}), the ordering function constructs the canonical sequence by filtering a pinned template:
[\mathrm{Template}(\mathsf{PA},\tau_0):=\bigl[\mathrm{AppA},\ \mathrm{ArcHub}(\alpha)?,\ \mathrm{LensBase}(L),\ \mathrm{FacetBase}(f),\ \mathrm{Rail}(\mathsf{Intent},\tau_0)?,\ \mathrm{AppI},\ \mathrm{AppM}\bigr].]The ordered hub sequence is:[\mathrm{HubsSeq}:=\mathrm{Compress}\Bigl(\bigl[h\in\mathrm{Template}: h\in H\bigr]\Bigr),]where (\mathrm{Compress}) removes duplicates while preserving first occurrence. This matches the canonical ordering policy (“then remove absent hubs and compress duplicates”).
11.S3.d — Obligations constructor (minimal contract)
Obligations are explicit addressable tasks. A minimal obligation set is:
Always include:
(\mathrm{Obl.ParseCanon}) (AppA): strict parse, canonicalization, and digest hooks,
(\mathrm{Obl.CorridorType}) (AppI): admissibility + budgets + truth typing,
(\mathrm{Obl.ReplayClose}) (AppM): execute replay capsules and verify pinned digests.
If (\tau_0=\mathrm{NEAR}): include (\mathrm{Obl.ResidualLedger}) (AppJ) and drift envelope disclosures.
If (\tau_0=\mathrm{AMBIG}): include (\mathrm{Obl.EvidencePlan}) (AppL) with bounded candidates and discriminators.
If (\tau_0=\mathrm{FAIL/CONFLICT}): include (\mathrm{Obl.ConflictPacket}) (AppK) and fence propagation tasks.
This obligation contract is structural: later domain expansions may add obligations, but cannot remove or weaken the mandatory signature obligations without changing the corridor profile (which forces a pinned migration rather than an implicit rewrite).
11.S3.e — Reference implementation (router compiler)
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import FrozenSet, Optional, Tuple, Literal, Dict, List
Truth = Literal["OK", "NEAR", "AMBIG", "FAIL", "CONFLICT"]
Scope = Literal["LOCAL", "INTER"]
Hub = str # e.g., "AppA", "AppI", "AppM", ...
Lens = Literal["S", "F", "C", "R"]
Intent = str # pinned enum in RouterProfile
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class StationHeader:
arc: int # α
rot: int # ρ
lane: str # ν
omega: int # ω
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class ParsedAddr:
kind: Literal["Ch", "App"]
lens: Lens
facet: int
is_chapter: bool
station: Optional[StationHeader]
scope: Scope
raw: str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class DropRecord:
hub: Hub
reason: str
redundancy_witness_ptr: Optional[str] = None
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class DropLog:
cap: int
dropped: Tuple[DropRecord, ...]
truth_impact: Truth
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class RouterProfile:
digest: str
hub_cap: int # must be 6 under this contract
mandatory_signature: FrozenSet[Hub] # Σ
lens_base: Dict[Lens, Hub]
facet_base: Dict[int, Hub]
arc_hub: Dict[int, Hub] # α -> hub
# rail(Truth, Intent) -> optional overlay hub (or None)
overlay: Dict[Tuple[Truth, Intent], Optional[Hub]]
# deterministic template order (before filtering)
canonical_template: Tuple[str, ...]
# deterministic drop priority list for optional hubs (lowest priority first)
drop_priority: Tuple[Hub, ...]
# policy: if a cap-enforced drop happens without redundancy witness, downgrade to AMBIG
downgrade_on_unwitnessed_drop: bool = True
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Pins:
grammar_digest: str
canon_bytes_digest: str
corridor_profile_digest: str
router_profile_digest: str
env_pins_digest: str
extra: Tuple[Tuple[str, str], ...] = ()
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class RoutePlan:
intent: Intent
target: str
scope: Scope
station_header: Optional[StationHeader]
hubs_seq: Tuple[Hub, ...] # ≤6 unique hubs before target
tau0: Truth
pins: Pins
obligations: Tuple[str, ...]
droplog: Optional[DropLog]
def parse_addr_strict(addr: str) -> ParsedAddr:
"""
Placeholder strict parser; in the manuscript, this is the pinned grammar.
Must be deterministic and reject malformed addresses (no heuristics).
"""
raise NotImplementedError
def truth_overlay(intent: Intent, tau0: Truth, rp: RouterProfile) -> Optional[Hub]:
return rp.overlay.get((tau0, intent), None)
def enforce_cap(hubs: List[Hub], rp: RouterProfile, tau0: Truth) -> Tuple[List[Hub], Optional[DropLog], Truth]:
# Stable dedupe in current order
seen = set()
deduped: List[Hub] = []
for h in hubs:
if h not in seen:
seen.add(h)
deduped.append(h)
must = set(rp.mandatory_signature)
# Overlay hubs are treated as must if present
# (The corridor may forbid some truths; forbiddance must be encoded upstream as FAIL.)
# Here we treat any overlay hub already included as mandatory to keep.
for h in deduped:
if h in {"AppJ", "AppL", "AppK"}:
must.add(h)
if len(must) > rp.hub_cap:
# Cannot satisfy cap with mandatory hubs: classify FAIL (or CONFLICT) deterministically
dl = DropLog(cap=rp.hub_cap, dropped=tuple(), truth_impact="FAIL")
return list(must), dl, "FAIL"
drops: List[DropRecord] = []
truth_out: Truth = tau0
# Deterministic drop: remove optional hubs in pinned priority order until within cap.
# Never drop must hubs.
while len(deduped) > rp.hub_cap:
dropped_any = False
for candidate in rp.drop_priority:
if candidate in deduped and candidate not in must:
deduped.remove(candidate)
drops.append(DropRecord(hub=candidate, reason="cap_enforcement"))
dropped_any = True
break
if not dropped_any:
# No droppable hub available: deterministic failure
dl = DropLog(cap=rp.hub_cap, dropped=tuple(drops), truth_impact="FAIL")
return deduped, dl, "FAIL"
if drops:
if rp.downgrade_on_unwitnessed_drop and truth_out == "OK":
truth_out = "AMBIG"
dl = DropLog(cap=rp.hub_cap, dropped=tuple(drops), truth_impact=truth_out)
return deduped, dl, truth_out
return deduped, None, truth_out
def order_hubs_deterministically(hubs_set: FrozenSet[Hub], pa: ParsedAddr, intent: Intent, tau0: Truth, rp: RouterProfile) -> Tuple[Hub, ...]:
# Build templated hubs (string tokens allow placeholder names in canonical_template)
computed: Dict[str, Optional[Hub]] = {
"AppA": "AppA",
"ArcHub": rp.arc_hub.get(pa.station.arc) if (pa.is_chapter and pa.station is not None) else None,
"LensBase": rp.lens_base.get(pa.lens),
"FacetBase": rp.facet_base.get(pa.facet),
"Overlay": truth_overlay(intent, tau0, rp),
"AppI": "AppI",
"AppM": "AppM",
}
seq: List[Hub] = []
seen = set()
for token in rp.canonical_template:
h = computed.get(token, token) # allow direct hub names or tokens
if h is None:
continue
if h in hubs_set and h not in seen:
seen.add(h)
seq.append(h)
return tuple(seq)
def compute_obligations(intent: Intent, tau0: Truth) -> Tuple[str, ...]:
obls = ["Obl.ParseCanon(AppA)", "Obl.CorridorType(AppI)", "Obl.ReplayClose(AppM)"]
if tau0 == "NEAR":
obls.append("Obl.ResidualLedger(AppJ)")
elif tau0 == "AMBIG":
obls.append("Obl.EvidencePlan(AppL)")
elif tau0 in ("FAIL", "CONFLICT"):
obls.append("Obl.ConflictPacket(AppK)")
# intent-specific obligations can be added deterministically by a pinned table
return tuple(obls)
def route(addr: str, intent: Intent, tau0: Truth, rp: RouterProfile, pins: Pins) -> RoutePlan:
pa = parse_addr_strict(addr)
hubs: List[Hub] = []
# Base hubs from lens/facet
hubs.append(rp.lens_base[pa.lens])
hubs.append(rp.facet_base[pa.facet])
# Arc hub for chapters
if pa.is_chapter and pa.station is not None:
hubs.append(rp.arc_hub[pa.station.arc])
# Enforce mandatory Σ
hubs.extend(list(rp.mandatory_signature))
# Truth overlay
overlay_hub = truth_overlay(intent, tau0, rp)
if overlay_hub is not None:
hubs.append(overlay_hub)
# Cap enforcement
hubs2, droplog, tau1 = enforce_cap(hubs, rp, tau0)
# Ordering
hubs_seq = order_hubs_deterministically(frozenset(hubs2), pa, intent, tau1, rp)
# Obligations
obligations = compute_obligations(intent, tau1)
return RoutePlan(intent=intent, target=addr, scope=pa.scope, station_header=pa.station,
hubs_seq=hubs_seq, tau0=tau1, pins=pins, obligations=obligations, droplog=droplog)
The reference implementation is intentionally structured so that every degree of freedom (tables, ordering, drop priority, overlay mapping) is pinned inside the router profile, ensuring router purity and replayability. The hub cap is enforced as a hard contract; drops are logged; and cap‑enforced unwitnessed drops deterministically degrade intended truth to AMBIG (or FAIL if the corridor forbids AMBIG).
11.S4 — Route execution outputs (replayable artifacts)
11.S4.a — Metro ride execution engine
Given a RoutePlan (\mathsf{RP}), the execution engine performs:
visit hubs in (\mathrm{HubsSeq}) order,
perform hub-specific normalizations and validations (parsing, corridor checks, replay),
gather witnesses and replay capsules,
evaluate truth typing under the corridor,
emit an execution transcript.
The engine output is deterministic and replayable. Any divergence under identical pins is a determinism failure and must be quarantined as FAIL/CONFLICT under the corridor truth rules.
11.S4.b — Transcript schema (minimum)
An execution transcript (\mathsf{Tx}) is an append-only record:[\mathsf{Tx}:=(\mathsf{RP},\mathrm{HubVisits},\mathrm{WitnessPtrs},\mathrm{ReplayPtrs},\tau_{\mathrm{final}},\mathrm{BudgetsUsed},\mathrm{ObligationsClosed},\mathrm{ObligationsOpened},\mathrm{EngineVer}).]Each hub visit record includes:
hub identifier,
inputs (digests of pulled artifacts),
performed actions (schema-bound operations),
produced outputs (digests),
witness and replay pointers,
any truth transitions (promotion/downgrade triggers).
Transcripts are governance-ready artifacts; route plans and transcripts are the executable substrate of cross-reference semantics.
❀ Flower — Canonical Ride Selection as Constraint Projection with Lexicographic Minimality
11.F1 — The constraint system
Let the router constraints be:
(C_{\Sigma}): include (\Sigma),
(C_{\mathrm{cap}}): (\le 6) unique hubs pre-target,
(C_{\mathrm{rail}}): include mandatory overlay hub induced by ((\mathsf{Intent},\tau_0)),
(C_{\mathrm{base}}): include base hubs induced by (\mathrm{LensBase},\mathrm{FacetBase},\mathrm{ArcHub}) (as applicable),
(C_{\mathrm{order}}): impose canonical ordering.
A candidate hub ride is a finite sequence (\mathbf{h}\in\mathcal{H}^{\le 6}). The router contract is equivalently the computation of a canonical feasible point of this constraint system under pinned tie-break rules.
11.F2 — Alternating projection interpretation
Define projectors on a “hub multiset space”:
(P_{\Sigma}): add (\Sigma),
(P_{\mathrm{rail}}): add the overlay hub induced by ((\mathsf{Intent},\tau_0)),
(P_{\mathrm{base}}): add base hubs induced by the parsed address,
(P_{\mathrm{cap}}): apply deterministic cap enforcement with DropLog,
(P_{\mathrm{order}}): map multiset to ordered sequence via canonical ordering template and compression.
Then the router is the finite composition:[\mathbf{h}\star = P{\mathrm{order}}\circ P_{\mathrm{cap}}\circ P_{\mathrm{rail}}\circ P_{\Sigma}\circ P_{\mathrm{base}}(\varnothing),]with the understanding that each projector is deterministic under (\pi_R). The “projection” language here is not analytic; it is the formal statement that routing is constraint satisfaction via deterministic normalization.
11.F3 — Lexicographic minimality and deterministic tie-break
Whenever multiple feasible rides exist (e.g., due to optional intent hubs or alternative ArcHub refinements), the router selects the unique ride minimizing a pinned lexicographic objective:[\min_{\mathbf{h}\in\mathcal{F}}\ \Bigl(\mathrm{CapViol}(\mathbf{h}),\ \mathrm{DropCount}(\mathbf{h}),\ \mathrm{DropPriorityScore}(\mathbf{h}),\ \mathrm{OrderKey}(\mathbf{h})\Bigr),]where (\mathcal{F}) is the feasible set given the pinned base hubs and mandatory signature/rail constraints. This objective must be pinned as part of (\pi_R) (or equivalently realized by pinned deterministic drop+order functions). Any unpinned tie-break introduces nondeterminism and violates the router purity law.
11.F4 — Ride equivalence and witnessed commutation
If an optimization proposes a different hub visit ordering, it is legal only if commutation is witnessed. In this chapter’s contract, this means: the engine may reorder only when it possesses a replayable equivalence witness that the reordered ride yields identical outputs and identical truth typing under pinned profiles. Otherwise the canonical ordering stands. This enforces the rule that reordering commutative hub visits is rare and must be witnessed; it cannot be assumed.
☁ Cloud — Uncertainty Discipline, AMBIG Plans, and Determinism Under Missing Pins
11.C1 — Missing prerequisites implies AMBIG plan
If any required prerequisite is missing (missing required profile digests, missing manifests for INTER edges, missing replay environment pins), the router and/or execution engine must output AMBIG (recoverable) with:
bounded candidate set if applicable,
an explicit evidence plan and obligations,
insertion of (\mathrm{AppL}) via the overlay rail,and must not claim OK. This is a routing law, not a stylistic preference.
11.C2 — Determinism under uncertainty
Uncertainty is represented as explicit artifacts (evidence plans, candidate sets, obligations), never as randomness. Any sampling, randomized tie-break, or nondeterministic cache use is illegal unless pinned by a reproducible seed and an explicit inference rule (and such pinning becomes part of the corridor profile and replay capsule, not an implicit engine behavior). This is a corollary of router purity: identical pins imply identical routes and identical artifacts.
11.C3 — Truth overlays as routable uncertainty channels
Truth overlays turn epistemic states into routable destinations:
NEAR routes through (\mathrm{AppJ}) to emit residual ledgers and drift envelopes,
AMBIG routes through (\mathrm{AppL}) to emit evidence plans and discriminator routes,
FAIL/CONFLICT routes through (\mathrm{AppK}) to fence contradictions and package conflict receipts.Overlay insertion is deterministic and profile-pinned; omission of a required overlay hub is illegal unless the corridor forbids that truth class for the ride.
11.C4 — Cap-induced ambiguity and DropLog semantics
When cap enforcement forces a drop of an optional hub, the route’s epistemic status changes unless redundancy is witnessed. The contract requires:
DropLog emission,
deterministic downgrade (typically to AMBIG),
obligations specifying which evidence would re-enable the dropped hub or prove redundancy.This is the mechanism by which bounded routing remains sound: it never pretends completeness when completeness could not be achieved within the cap.
✶ Fractal — RoutePlans as Composable Units of Corpus Execution
11.R1 — RoutePlan composability and task rides
A RoutePlan is not merely navigation; it is a composable execution unit. Task-based rides are deterministic templates specialized by router rules and truth overlays, for example:[\begin{aligned}\mathrm{VERIFY}&:\ \mathrm{AppA}\to\mathrm{AppI}\to\mathrm{AppM}\to\mathrm{Targets},\\mathrm{BUILD}&:\ \mathrm{AppA}\to\mathrm{AppH}\to\mathrm{AppC}\to\mathrm{AppM}\to\mathrm{Targets},\\mathrm{MIGRATE}&:\ \mathrm{AppA}\to\mathrm{AppD}\to\mathrm{AppB}\to\mathrm{AppM}\to\mathrm{AppO},\\mathrm{RESOLVE}&:\ \mathrm{AppA}\to\mathrm{AppK}\to\mathrm{AppM}\to\mathrm{AppB},\\mathrm{PUBLISH}&:\ \mathrm{AppA}\to\mathrm{AppO}\to\mathrm{AppM}\to\mathrm{AppD}\to\mathrm{AppP}.\end{aligned}]These are not informal reading suggestions; they are deterministic ride templates executed by the engine, producing transcripts and replay artifacts.
11.R2 — Narrative compilation as a deterministic list of RoutePlans
A narrative is valid only insofar as it compiles to a finite set of RoutePlans and their certificates. A narrative compiler is therefore a deterministic procedure:[(\mathsf{Intent},\mathrm{Targets})\ \mapsto\ \bigl[\mathsf{RP}_1,\dots,\mathsf{RP}_N\bigr],]with explicit address citations and truth typing. Claims unsupported by OK routes must remain AMBIG and must cite evidence plans and discriminator routes. This embeds “documentation” into the same proof-carrying graph substrate as transport legality, ensuring the manuscript remains executable rather than rhetorical.
11.R3 — Certificates for router conformance
Router correctness is witnessed by explicit certificates. A minimal certificate suite includes:
RouterDeterminismCert: witness that router outputs identical hub sequences and DropLogs under identical pins, that mandatory signature is enforced, and that cap enforcement is deterministic.
HubCapCert: witness that all route plans respect (\le 6) unique hubs pre-target, that any cap enforcement is recorded in DropLog, and that violations are classified AMBIG/FAIL (never silently ignored).
EngineReplayCert: witness that execution transcripts replay under pinned profiles reproducing identical outputs and identical fingerprints for all edges typed OK; any mismatch forces FAIL/CONFLICT quarantine under the corridor policy. (This cert binds the router contract to the replay contract.)
Certificates are addressable artifacts and can themselves be targets of RoutePlans.
11.R4 — Optional cross-scope tunneling under pinned gateways
If cross-corpus tunneling is enabled, it must be declared via a pinned gateway profile:
deterministic mapping between scopes,
replayable and auditable,
never bypassing corridor truth typing or pin validation.Otherwise tunneling is forbidden. This prevents hidden jumps that violate router purity and auditability.
Ch11 — Router Contract (≤6 hubs, deterministic order)
Ch12 — Certificates (ReplayCert, RegressionCert, ExportCert)
Defines HD‑SCT witness bundles + replay harness expectations (import‑verifiable)
12.0 Preliminaries: canonical bytes, digests, and subject closure
12.0.1 Canonical bytes and pinned hash
Fix a pinned hash algorithm (\mathsf{HashAlg}) with hash function[H:{0,1}^\star \to {0,1}^{\ell}.]Every certifiable object (X) in HD‑SCT admits a pinned canonical encoding (\mathrm{Enc}(X)\in{0,1}^\star) (sorted keys, canonical integers, canonical list ordering, and pinned byte ordering rules). The fingerprint of (X) is[\mathrm{fp}(X);:=;H(\mathrm{Enc}(X)).]Any change to (\mathrm{Enc}) rules is a schema change and must be routed as a MIGRATE‑managed change at the publication/import layer; it cannot be treated as “harmless formatting.”
12.0.2 Subjects, scopes, and dependency closure
Let (\mathcal{G}) be the HD‑SCT corpus graph of atoms/edges, each addressable by a (\mathrm{GlobalAddr}). A certificate subject is one of:
an atom (a\in\mathrm{Atoms}(\mathcal{G})),
an edge (e\in\mathrm{Edges}(\mathcal{G})),
a profile object (router/corridor/kernel/phase/bridge/control/container schemas),
a replay capsule (\mathsf{RC}),
a regression suite (\mathsf{RS}),
an export bundle (\mathsf{EB}),
or a finite subject set (S\subseteq\mathrm{Subjects}) (closure‑certs).
Each certificate is parameterized by (\mathrm{Scope}\in{\mathrm{LOCAL},\mathrm{INTER}}). INTER subjects must include the precise manifest digests and profile digests for both sides of the crossing in their pinned requirements; missing inter‑pins prevents OK certification.
Define a pinned dependency function (\mathrm{Deps}(\cdot)) returning the finite set of prerequisite objects required to verify a subject under the active corridor class. The verification closure of subject (S) is[\mathrm{Cl}(S);:=;S;\cup;\mathrm{Deps}(S);\cup;\mathrm{Deps}(\mathrm{Deps}(S));\cup\cdots]which is required to stabilize to a finite set under bounded corridors. Export and certificate packaging is defined on (\mathrm{Cl}(S)).
12.0.3 Proof‑carrying determinism as an operational law
HD‑SCT treats replay determinism as the operational definition of verified truth: identical pins and inputs imply identical outputs and identical fingerprints; any mismatch under identical pins is a deterministic failure or a reproducible contradiction, and cannot be ignored.A claim is OK only if required witness artifacts exist, required replays close, pins validate, budgets are satisfied, and no fences are violated.
Certificates are the formalization of this law into import‑verifiable bundles.
12.1 ReplayCapsule and the replay harness contract
12.1.1 ReplayCapsule (\mathsf{RC}): the minimal import‑verifiable verifier packet
A ReplayCapsule is the smallest self‑contained unit enabling an independent verifier to re‑run a claim check deterministically. Define:[\boxed{\mathsf{RC}:=(\mathrm{RCID},\mathrm{TargetAddr},\mathrm{Scope},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{EnvPins},\mathrm{Seeds},\mathrm{Inputs},\mathrm{Steps},\mathrm{ExpectedDigests},\mathrm{OutputsSpec},\mathrm{LogsSpec},\mathrm{SchemaVer})}]where:
(\mathrm{TargetAddr}) is the (\mathrm{GlobalAddr}) node/edge being verified,
(\mathrm{Pins}) includes all profile digests required to interpret the claim (router/corridor/grammar/canonbytes/kernel/phase/bridge/control/container schema),
(\mathrm{EnvPins}) pins runtime/platform/dependency behavior sufficient for deterministic replay,
(\mathrm{Seeds}) pins any randomness (empty if randomness is forbidden for the capsule class),
(\mathrm{Inputs}) are embedded canonical bytes or digest‑referenced canonical bytes,
(\mathrm{Steps}) is a deterministic execution recipe,
(\mathrm{ExpectedDigests}) are intermediate and final digests binding the claimed outcome,
(\mathrm{OutputsSpec}) and (\mathrm{LogsSpec}) pin output/log canonicalization.A capsule is self‑contained relative to determinism: everything that can affect the outcome must be pinned or embedded; otherwise it cannot certify OK.
A canonical schema requires (unless policy explicitly permits omission):[{\mathrm{TargetAddr},\ \mathrm{RouterProfileDigest},\ \mathrm{CorridorProfileDigest},\ \mathrm{EnvPins},\ \mathrm{Seeds},\ \mathrm{Inputs},\ \mathrm{Steps},\ \mathrm{ExpectedDigests},\ \mathrm{Outputs},\ \mathrm{Logs}}.]
12.1.2 ReplayRecipe (\mathsf{RRc}) and strict ordering
Define the replay program carried inside (\mathsf{RC}) as:[\mathsf{RRc}:=(\mathrm{StepList},\mathrm{StepPins},\mathrm{StepDigests},\mathrm{OrderingPolicy})]where:
(\mathrm{StepList}=(s_1,\dots,s_n)) is a sequence of named steps (parse, canonicalize, compute NF, apply kernel, decode stream, compute digest, compare),
(\mathrm{StepPins}) lists required profile digests per step,
(\mathrm{StepDigests}) optionally pins intermediate digests for localization,
(\mathrm{OrderingPolicy}) is pinned; steps execute in strict order.The recipe forbids best‑effort skipping; if a step cannot run, outcome is AMBIG/FAIL according to the corridor policy.
12.1.3 EnvironmentPin (\mathsf{EPn}) and numeric determinism
An EnvironmentPin is the minimal set of version identifiers needed to make replay deterministic across machines:[\mathsf{EPn}:=(\mathrm{OSID},\mathrm{ArchID},\mathrm{RuntimeID},\mathrm{LibDigests},\mathrm{Compiler/VMID?},\mathrm{FloatingPolicy},\mathrm{EndianPolicy},\mathrm{SchemaPins}).]Missing environment pins prevent OK certification; at best the result is AMBIG (recoverable) or FAIL (policy forbids).
12.1.4 DeterminismChecklist (\mathsf{DCk}): what must be pinned
A DeterminismChecklist is an explicit list of “knobs that must be pinned” for a capsule class:[\mathsf{DCk}:=(\mathrm{CapsuleClass},\mathrm{RequiredPins},\mathrm{OptionalPins},\mathrm{ForbiddenUnpinned},\mathrm{FallbackPolicy}),]including forbidden unpinned dependencies such as unpinned RNG, time dependence, network dependence, or unspecified platform behavior. (\mathsf{DCk}) is itself pinned by digest and referenced by verifiers.
12.1.5 Verifier engine (V): deterministic replay execution and failure classification
Fix a pinned verifier engine version (\mathrm{VerifierVer}). The verifier executes (\mathsf{RC}) as a deterministic state machine whose internal state includes step index, loaded pins, loaded inputs, digest accumulator, transcript buffer, and budget counters (\chi).
Given (\mathsf{RC}), (V) must:
validate pins via the registry snapshot (existence, digest match, not revoked),
validate schema versions (capsule schema, container schema),
load inputs (embedded or fetched by digest under pinned policy),
execute steps in order producing intermediate digests,
compare observed digests to (\mathrm{ExpectedDigests}),
emit a canonical transcript and a truth classification under corridor mapping.
Mismatch handling is strict:
FAIL if mismatch is deterministic under a pinned environment,
CONFLICT if mismatches disagree across independently pinned replays (fork indicator),
AMBIG only if evaluation cannot be completed due to missing pins/inputs and recovery is permitted.Mismatch cannot be ignored or downgraded to OK.
12.2 Certificate algebra: types, schemas, and verification semantics
12.2.1 Certificate object (\mathsf{Cert})
A certificate is a replay‑verifiable witness object with a typed claim. Define:[\boxed{\mathsf{Cert}:=(\mathrm{CertID},\mathrm{CertType},\mathrm{Subject},\mathrm{Scope},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{EnvPins},\mathrm{Claims},\mathrm{WitnessRefs},\mathrm{ReplayRefs},\mathrm{ExpectedDigests},\mathrm{Budgets},\mathrm{TranscriptDigest},\mathrm{IssuedAtPulse},\mathrm{Prev?},\mathrm{Signatures?},\mathrm{SchemaVer})}]with:
(\mathrm{CertType}\in{\mathrm{ReplayCert},\mathrm{RegressionCert},\mathrm{ExportCert}}),
(\mathrm{Subject}) an addressable subject set or single subject,
(\mathrm{WitnessRefs}) references to required witnesses (tests, measurement logs, diffs),
(\mathrm{ReplayRefs}) references to (\mathsf{RC}) objects required for verification,
(\mathrm{ExpectedDigests}) binding certificate‑level outputs (not only subject outputs),
(\mathrm{Budgets}) binding maximum allowable verification cost,
(\mathrm{TranscriptDigest}) binding the canonical verifier transcript emitted during certification,
(\mathrm{Signatures?}) optional signatures under a pinned signature discipline.
A certificate is valid only if its verification reduces to deterministic replay execution(s) plus deterministic ledger checks, all under pinned profiles and environment.
12.2.2 Import‑verifiable certificates
A certificate is import‑verifiable if an independent verifier can validate it without privileged access: all required pins, inputs, witnesses, and replays are embedded or content‑addressed by digest and included in the import closure, and the verification procedure is fully specified and deterministic.
Formally, let (\mathsf{Bundle}) be an importable package (see §12.4). A certificate (\mathsf{Cert}) is import‑verifiable within (\mathsf{Bundle}) if:[\mathrm{Cl}({\mathsf{Cert}})\subseteq \mathrm{Contents}(\mathsf{Bundle})]and if executing the pinned verification algorithm on (\mathsf{Bundle}) yields the same transcript digest and same truth mapping across all conformant environments satisfying (\mathrm{EnvPins}).
12.3 ReplayCert: replay closure as a certificate
12.3.1 ReplayCert: definition
A ReplayCert attests that replay verification closes for a subject (or subject set) under pinned environment and pins.
Define a ReplayCert for subject (S) as:[\boxed{\mathsf{ReplayCert}(S):=(\mathrm{CertID},\mathrm{Subject}=S,\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{EnvPins},\mathrm{RCSet},\mathrm{RCExpected},\mathrm{OutputsDigest},\mathrm{TranscriptDigest},\mathrm{Budgets},\mathrm{Result},\mathrm{IssuedAtPulse},\mathrm{SchemaVer})}]where:
(\mathrm{RCSet}={\mathsf{RC}_1,\dots,\mathsf{RC}_m}) is the required capsule set for (S) under the active corridor,
(\mathrm{RCExpected}) binds each capsule fingerprint (\mathrm{fp}(\mathsf{RC}_i)) and its expected digest map,
(\mathrm{OutputsDigest}) binds the final aggregated outputs (e.g., subject fingerprints, registry entries, or explicit atom digests),
(\mathrm{Result}\in{\mathrm{PASS},\mathrm{QUARANTINE},\mathrm{REJECT}}) is computed deterministically from the capsule outcomes and fence policies.
Replay closure is an operational requirement for OK: without replay closure, the strongest admissible truth class is AMBIG (or FAIL in strict corridors).
12.3.2 ReplayCert verification algorithm
Let (V) be the pinned verifier engine. Verification of (\mathsf{ReplayCert}(S)) is:
Pin validation. Verify (\mathrm{Pins}) against the registry snapshot: required digests exist, match, and are not revoked.
Capsule integrity. For each (\mathsf{RC}_i\in \mathrm{RCSet}), verify:
(\mathrm{fp}(\mathsf{RC}_i)) matches (\mathrm{RCExpected}),
all required pins/inputs present (relative to (\mathsf{DCk}) for the capsule class). Missing required pins prohibits OK closure.
Deterministic execution. Execute each capsule with (V), respecting per‑capsule and global budget counters (\chi). Record observed intermediate/final digests and the deterministic failure classifier output.
Digest equality checks. Compare observed digests to (\mathrm{ExpectedDigests}). Apply mismatch rule:
deterministic mismatch (\Rightarrow) FAIL/REJECT,
cross‑environment mismatch disagreement (\Rightarrow) CONFLICT/QUARANTINE,
missing inputs/pins with permitted recovery (\Rightarrow) AMBIG/QUARANTINE.
Transcript binding. Compute the canonical transcript digest and compare to (\mathrm{TranscriptDigest}).
Output digest binding. Compute (\mathrm{OutputsDigest}) from the verified outputs and compare to the certificate’s value.
Acceptance requires PASS plus full transcript/output digest match. Any failure produces a deterministic quarantine/reject classification and an obligation packet (repair, migration, or conflict packet) according to corridor rules.
12.3.3 ReplayCert construction algorithm
Given subject (S) and corridor profile (\pi_C), the constructor:
computes required capsule set (\mathrm{RCSet}) under the corridor’s closure class;
materializes all required inputs/witnesses into content‑addressed storage;
runs (V) to produce transcripts and observed digests;
packages the resulting (\mathsf{ReplayCert}(S)) with transcript digest, output digest, and budget consumption;
appends the certificate as an immutable artifact (superseding occurs by new cert, not rewrite).
Replay transcripts are append‑only; corrections occur as new transcripts and new capsules rather than retro‑editing.
12.4 RegressionCert: deterministic regression suites as certificates
12.4.1 Regression suite object (\mathsf{RS})
A Regression Suite is a finite set of replay capsules and fixtures designed to cover edge cases for a subject class. Define:[\boxed{\mathsf{RS}:=(\mathrm{RSID},\mathrm{SubjectClass},\mathrm{Scope},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{EnvPins},\mathrm{FixtureIndex},\mathrm{CapsuleIndex},\mathrm{ExpectedDigests},\mathrm{CoverageSpec},\mathrm{Budgets},\mathrm{SchemaVer})}]where:
(\mathrm{FixtureIndex}) content‑addresses each fixture by digest and describes its role (normal, adversarial, boundary, migration‑compat),
(\mathrm{CapsuleIndex}) lists (\mathsf{RC}) objects built from fixtures,
(\mathrm{CoverageSpec}) pins the minimal required categories and corner cases for the subject class.
Regression suites are required to be deterministic: fixtures may be randomized only under pinned seeds and pinned RNG policy. Missing coverage implies that claims relying on uncovered corners cannot be upgraded to OK without explicit caveat routing.
12.4.2 RegressionCert: definition
A RegressionCert attests that a regression suite (\mathsf{RS}) passes under deterministic replay and produces pinned expected digests.
Define:[\boxed{\mathsf{RegressionCert}(\mathsf{RS}):=(\mathrm{CertID},\mathrm{RSID},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{EnvPins},\mathrm{RunTranscriptDigest},\mathrm{PassSetDigest},\mathrm{FailSetDigest},\mathrm{CoverageDigest},\mathrm{BudgetsUsed},\mathrm{Result},\mathrm{IssuedAtPulse},\mathrm{SchemaVer})}]where:
(\mathrm{Result}\in{\mathrm{PASS},\mathrm{FAIL},\mathrm{CONFLICT}}),
(\mathrm{PassSetDigest}) binds the set of passing capsule fingerprints,
(\mathrm{FailSetDigest}) binds failing capsules plus minimal failure witnesses,
(\mathrm{CoverageDigest}) binds the coverage evaluation (which categories were exercised and satisfied).
Regression failures trigger quarantine of affected profiles/capsules/cert classes; affected routes cannot remain OK until repaired or migrated.
12.4.3 Regression harness expectations
The regression harness is a replay harness specialized to suites:
validate suite pins and schema versions;
load fixtures deterministically;
execute each suite capsule under (V) with pinned budgets (\chi);
collect transcripts and failure witnesses;
compute the deterministic coverage evaluation;
output a regression transcript and (\mathsf{RegressionCert}).
Importers must not accept regressions “as declared”; they re‑run regression verification (or re‑run a pinned representative subset when policy permits and the suite supplies coverage‑preserving certificates).
12.5 ExportCert: deterministic export and import‑verifiable closure
12.5.1 ExportBundle (\mathsf{EB}): proof‑carrying publication package
An ExportBundle is a proof‑carrying package that can be imported and independently verified. Define:[\boxed{\mathsf{EB}:=(\mathrm{BundleID},\mathrm{BundleSchemaID},\mathrm{Manifest},\mathrm{Index},\mathrm{PayloadSections},\mathrm{WitnessSections},\mathrm{ReplaySections},\mathrm{Disclosures},\mathrm{Fences},\mathrm{Revocations},\mathrm{Signatures},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{Digests})}]with canonical components:
(\mathrm{Manifest}): sorted keys, canonical encoding, digests for all sections,
(\mathrm{Index}): atom‑granular map (\mathrm{GlobalAddr}\to) offsets/digests,
(\mathrm{PayloadSections}): serialized atoms/tiles, edge lists, profiles, topology packs, container bytes,
(\mathrm{WitnessSections}): tests/diffs/logs/measurement artifacts,
(\mathrm{ReplaySections}): replay capsules required for verifying OK/NEAR claims in scope,
(\mathrm{Disclosures}): NEAR residual disclosures and explicit AMBIG fences,
(\mathrm{Fences/Revocations}): quarantine fences and revocation receipts,
(\mathrm{Pins}): router/corridor/grammar/canonbytes and all referenced profile digests,
(\mathrm{Digests}): per‑section and overall digests with pinned hash algorithm.Determinism requirement: the same target set and pins must produce identical bundle bytes (modulo signature nonces only if policy allows, and such nonces must be pinned/encoded).
12.5.2 ImportVerifier (\mathsf{IV}): deterministic accept/quarantine/reject
An ImportVerifier is the deterministic procedure for accepting, quarantining, or rejecting bundles:[\boxed{\mathsf{IV}:=(\mathrm{VerifierID},\mathfrak{C}_{\mathrm{import}},\mathrm{PinPolicy},\mathrm{ReplayPolicy},\mathrm{DiffPolicy},\mathrm{FencePolicy},\mathrm{SignaturePolicy},\mathrm{CompatPolicy},\mathrm{Pins})}]and must:
validate bundle pins against the registry snapshot,
validate signatures if required,
run required replay capsules,
enforce fences and revocations,
compute atom‑granular diffs vs local corpus state,
output a deterministic verdict (\in{\mathrm{ACCEPT},\mathrm{QUARANTINE},\mathrm{REJECT}}) with a transcript.
Import acceptance requires validating pins, replaying required capsules, and matching expected digests and fingerprints; skipping required replays yields quarantine/reject per policy.
12.5.3 ExportCert: definition
An ExportCert attests that an export bundle is deterministic, complete with respect to its declared closure, and import‑verifiable under the pinned import verifier.
Define:[\boxed{\mathsf{ExportCert}(\mathsf{EB}):=(\mathrm{CertID},\mathrm{BundleID},\mathrm{BundleDigest},\mathrm{ManifestDigest},\mathrm{IndexDigest},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{ImportVerifierID},\mathrm{ImportTranscriptDigest},\mathrm{ReplayCoverageDigest},\mathrm{DisclosureDigest},\mathrm{FenceDigest},\mathrm{SignatureDigest?},\mathrm{Result},\mathrm{IssuedAtPulse},\mathrm{SchemaVer})}]where:
(\mathrm{BundleDigest}:=H(\mathrm{Enc}(\mathsf{EB}))),
(\mathrm{ReplayCoverageDigest}) binds the set of RCs included and required by corridor closure for the bundle’s declared claim classes,
(\mathrm{DisclosureDigest}) binds required NEAR disclosures and AMBIG fences,
(\mathrm{FenceDigest}) binds quarantine and revocation enforcement artifacts.
12.5.4 ExportCert verification algorithm (import‑verifiable)
Given (\mathsf{EB}), (\mathsf{ExportCert}(\mathsf{EB})), and pinned (\mathsf{IV}):
Bundle integrity checks. Verify bundle parses under schema, digests verify, index matches payload sections, pins complete, deterministic layout rules satisfied.
Signature validation (if required). Verify signature semantics under pinned signature spec and canonical signed‑bytes rule.
Pin validation and registry binding. Validate all profile digests referenced by the bundle. Bundles lacking required pins are rejected/quarantined per corridor policy; silent fallback is forbidden.
Replay coverage closure. Compute the set of required replays for the bundle’s in‑scope claims (critical subjects under the corridor closure class) and verify that (\mathsf{EB}) contains those replay capsules and their required inputs. Missing required replay coverage implies QUARANTINE/REJECT per policy; it cannot be OK.
Import replay execution. Execute the import pipeline: verify integrity/pins, run required replays, apply fences and revocations, compute diffs, emit a deterministic import transcript and verdict.
Transcript binding. Compare the observed import transcript digest to (\mathrm{ImportTranscriptDigest}) in (\mathsf{ExportCert}). Any divergence indicates nondeterminism, missing pins, or schema drift and triggers QUARANTINE/FAIL under the corridor.
12.5.5 ExportCert construction algorithm (deterministic export)
Given target subject set (S), corridor profile (\pi_C), and bundle schema profile (\pi_O), the exporter:
computes (\mathrm{Cl}(S)) under the bundle closure rules;
serializes payloads and witnesses deterministically (address ordering by (\mathrm{GlobalAddr}));
includes replay capsules required for verifying OK/NEAR claims in scope;
includes required disclosures and fences;
computes manifest/index/digests deterministically;
applies signatures under a pinned signature discipline (if enabled);
runs the pinned import verifier on the produced bytes to produce (\mathrm{ImportTranscriptDigest});
emits (\mathsf{ExportCert}(\mathsf{EB})) binding the output.Publishing cannot hide missing evidence; AMBIG must remain fenced and explicit.
12.6 Witness bundles: certificate‑complete proof packs for HD‑SCT routes
12.6.1 WitnessBundle (\mathsf{WB}): typed bundle of certifiable artifacts
A WitnessBundle is a minimal certificate‑complete pack for a declared subject set (S). Define:[\boxed{\mathsf{WB}(S):=(\mathrm{WBID},\mathrm{Subjects}=S,\mathrm{Scope},\mathrm{Pins},\mathrm{Witnesses},\mathrm{ReplayCapsules},\mathrm{RegressionSuites},\mathrm{Certificates},\mathrm{Transcripts},\mathrm{Disclosures},\mathrm{Fences},\mathrm{Revocations},\mathrm{SchemaVer})}]with the closure constraint:[\mathrm{Cl}(S)\ \subseteq\ \mathrm{Contents}(\mathsf{WB}(S)).]The witness bundle may be embedded in (\mathsf{EB}) as (\mathrm{WitnessSections}\cup\mathrm{ReplaySections}) and is required for import‑verifiable publication.
12.6.2 Minimal certificate set for publishable claims
