Let (S) be the bundle’s declared claims in scope. A publish corridor that permits OK for (S) requires, at minimum:
(\mathsf{ReplayCert}(S)) binding closure of required capsules,
(\mathsf{RegressionCert}(\mathsf{RS}_{\mathrm{critical}})) for each critical verifier/profile class used in claims,
(\mathsf{ExportCert}(\mathsf{EB})) binding deterministic export and import‑verifiable acceptance behavior.
If any required certificate is absent, the highest admissible truth class for affected claims is AMBIG or NEAR (if bounded approximation is explicitly declared and certified), and publication must carry corresponding fences/disclosures.
12.6.3 Relationship to NEAR and residual disclosures
When a claim is NEAR, the witness bundle must include residual‑ledger evidence and measurement replays sufficient to validate bounded approximation under pinned metrics and calibration. NEAR is valid only when the replay capsule explicitly declares the approximation envelope and residual metrics; otherwise NEAR cannot be produced.
12.6.4 Deterministic deltas, supersession, and append‑only certificates
Certificates are append‑only: a certificate may be superseded by later certificates, but never overwritten. Supersession is represented as an explicit edge (\mathrm{Prev?}) and is itself subject to replay verification if it changes routability (e.g., revocation or quarantine propagation).
12.7 Reference implementation: certificate schemas and verifier APIs
from __future__ import annotations

Digest = str # hex/base64 per pinned HashAlg

A conformant implementation must provide deterministic constructors and verifiers for these objects and must bind canonical encodings to digests under pinned schema versions; any mismatch is a replay failure and cannot certify OK.
Ch12 — Certificates (ReplayCert, RegressionCert, ExportCert)
Ch13 — Cross-Dimensional Metro (B_d ring + gear stacks)
The refined metro ring (B_d = 15\cdot 3^{d-1}) and multi-gear projections across dimension
□ Square — The (B_d) Metro Ring as a Triadic Refinement Tower
13.S1 — The (B_d) ring
13.S1.1 — Definition of the cross-dimensional metro ring
For each dimension (d\in\mathbb{N}{\ge 1}), define the cross-dimensional metro ring size[\boxed{B_d := 15\cdot 3^{,d-1}.}]Define the (B_d) metro ring as the cyclically ordered index set[\boxed{\Sigma{B_d} := {0,1,\dots,B_d-1},}]equipped with the cyclic adjacency relation (u\sim u\pm 1 \ (\mathrm{mod}\ B_d)).
The case (d=1) recovers the base metro ring (\Sigma_{15}). For each increment in dimension, the metro ring refines by a factor of (3):[\boxed{B_{d+1} = 3B_d.}]
13.S1.2 — Macro-stations and internal phase strata
The (B_d) ring is a refinement of the 15-station metro. Define the macro-station width[\boxed{W_d := \frac{B_d}{15} = 3^{d-1}.}]Define the macro-station projection[\boxed{\pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d)}:\Sigma_{B_d}\to\Sigma_{15},\qquad\pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d)}(u):=\left\lfloor \frac{u}{W_d}\right\rfloor}](where (\Sigma_{15}={0,\dots,14})). Thus the 15 macro-stations are the contiguous blocks[\boxed{\mathcal{B}{d}(\sigma) := {\sigma W_d,\ \sigma W_d +1,\ \dots,\ (\sigma+1)W_d -1},\qquad \sigma\in\Sigma{15}.}]
Define the internal stratum coordinate[\boxed{\pi_{\mathrm{str}}^{(d)}:\Sigma_{B_d}\to\Sigma_{W_d},\qquad\pi_{\mathrm{str}}^{(d)}(u):=u-\pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d)}(u),W_d.}]Equivalently, (\pi_{\mathrm{str}}^{(d)}(u)=u\ \mathrm{mod}\ W_d) using canonical representatives in (\Sigma_{W_d}).
Every (u\in \Sigma_{B_d}) admits a unique decomposition[\boxed{u = W_d\cdot \sigma ;+; \gamma\qquad\text{with }\sigma=\pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d)}(u)\in\Sigma_{15},\ \gamma=\pi_{\mathrm{str}}^{(d)}(u)\in\Sigma_{W_d}.}]
13.S1.3 — Interpretation: “15 stations × (3^{d-1}) strata”
The (B_d) ring is a structured carrier that simultaneously encodes:
a metro station (\sigma\in\Sigma_{15}) (the 15-station powerset carrier), and
an internal phase stratum (\gamma\in\Sigma_{3^{d-1}}) (the dimension-induced stratification).
The meaning of “internal stratum” is pinned by the active corridor profile: it represents the discretized relative-triangle-phase (or an equivalent stratification variable) that becomes necessary to keep higher-dimensional cycles visible rather than aliased.
13.S2 — Gear stacks: ternary factorization of the stratum coordinate
13.S2.1 — Ternary digit stack (gear stack)
Because (W_d=3^{d-1}), the stratum coordinate (\gamma\in\Sigma_{W_d}) has a canonical ternary expansion. Define the gear digits[\boxed{\mathrm{digits}{d}(\gamma) = (t_1,t_2,\dots,t{d-1})\in{0,1,2}^{d-1}}]by the unique equality[\boxed{\gamma = \sum_{i=1}^{d-1} t_i\cdot 3^{,d-1-i}.}]Equivalently, (t_1) is the most significant ternary digit and (t_{d-1}) is the least significant ternary digit.
Define the gear-stack decomposition map[\boxed{\mathsf{GS}d:\Sigma{B_d}\to \Sigma_{15}\times{0,1,2}^{d-1}}]by[\boxed{\mathsf{GS}d(u) := \bigl(\sigma,\ t_1,\dots,t{d-1}\bigr)\quad\text{where}\quad\sigma=\pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d)}(u),\ \ (t_1,\dots,t_{d-1})=\mathrm{digits}d(\pi{\mathrm{str}}^{(d)}(u)).}]
Define its inverse reconstruction map[\boxed{\mathsf{GS}d^{-1}(\sigma,t_1,\dots,t{d-1}) := \sigma W_d + \sum_{i=1}^{d-1} t_i\cdot 3^{,d-1-i}.}]
Proposition 13.S2.1 (Bijection).(\mathsf{GS}d) is a bijection with inverse (\mathsf{GS}d^{-1}). Consequently,[\Sigma{B_d}\cong \Sigma{15}\times{0,1,2}^{d-1}]as finite sets, and the (B_d) ring is a 15-station metro with a ((d-1))-layer ternary gear stack inside each station.
13.S2.2 — Relative triangle-phase model and the (3^{d-1}) count
Let (\tau=(\tau_1,\dots,\tau_d)\in(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d) denote a per-axis triangle-phase assignment. Let (\Delta\subset(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d) be the diagonal subgroup[\Delta := {(a,a,\dots,a):a\in\mathbb{Z}_3}.]Define the relative phase class ([\tau]\in (\mathbb{Z}_3)^d/\Delta). Then[\left|(\mathbb{Z}3)^d/\Delta\right| = 3^{d-1}.]A corridor may pin an identification between internal strata (\gamma\in\Sigma{3^{d-1}}) and relative phase classes ([\tau]). A canonical gauge choice is:
pick the unique representative with (\tau_d=0), and
encode ((\tau_1,\dots,\tau_{d-1})\in(\mathbb{Z}_3)^{d-1}) into (\gamma) by ternary positional encoding.
Under this gauge, the gear digits ((t_1,\dots,t_{d-1})) are the stored relative phase coordinates.
13.S3 — Multi-gear projections between dimensions
13.S3.1 — One-step dimension projection
Because (B_{d+1}=3B_d), (\Sigma_{B_{d+1}}) refines (\Sigma_{B_d}) by splitting each cell into three subcells.
Define the one-step projection[\boxed{\pi_{d+1\to d}:\Sigma_{B_{d+1}}\to \Sigma_{B_d},\qquad\pi_{d+1\to d}(u):=\left\lfloor\frac{u}{3}\right\rfloor.}]This is the canonical “forget the last ternary digit” map: it groups consecutive triples ({3v,3v+1,3v+2}) into (v).
Proposition 13.S3.1 (Station preservation).For all (u\in\Sigma_{B_{d+1}}),[\pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d)}(\pi_{d+1\to d}(u)) = \pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d+1)}(u).]Thus the macro-station (\sigma\in\Sigma_{15}) is invariant under dimension projection.
Proposition 13.S3.2 (Stratum truncation).If (\mathsf{GS}{d+1}(u)=(\sigma,t_1,\dots,t_d)), then[\mathsf{GS}{d}\bigl(\pi_{d+1\to d}(u)\bigr) = (\sigma,t_1,\dots,t_{d-1}).]The projection drops the last gear digit.
13.S3.2 — Multi-step dimension projection (multi-gear projection)
For (d\ge d'\ge 1), define the multi-step projection[\boxed{\pi_{d\to d'}:\Sigma_{B_d}\to\Sigma_{B_{d'}},\qquad\pi_{d\to d'}(u):=\left\lfloor \frac{u}{3^{d-d'}}\right\rfloor.}]This coarsens by removing the finest ((d-d')) ternary digits of the internal stratum coordinate.
Proposition 13.S3.3 (Functoriality).For all (d\ge d'\ge d''\ge 1),[\boxed{\pi_{d\to d''} = \pi_{d'\to d''}\circ \pi_{d\to d'}.}]Proposition 13.S3.4 (Fiber size).For each (v\in\Sigma_{B_{d'}}), the fiber has cardinality[\left|\pi_{d\to d'}^{-1}(v)\right| = 3^{d-d'}.]
13.S3.3 — Multi-gear readout as a tower of consistent indices
Given (u\in\Sigma_{B_d}), define the multi-gear readout[\boxed{\mathsf{MG}d(u):=\bigl(u^{(1)},u^{(2)},\dots,u^{(d)}\bigr)\quad\text{where}\quadu^{(r)}:=\pi{d\to r}(u)\in\Sigma_{B_r}.}]Then[\boxed{u^{(r)}=\pi_{r+1\to r}\bigl(u^{(r+1)}\bigr)\quad\text{for all }r=1,\dots,d-1,}]so the tower is internally consistent.
Conversely, any tower ((u^{(1)},\dots,u^{(d)})) satisfying the consistency constraints uniquely determines (u=u^{(d)}).
13.S4 — Multi-gear lifts and gear-stack fibers
13.S4.1 — One-step lift (three refinement choices)
Define the one-step lift family[\boxed{\lambda_{d\to d+1}^{(t)}:\Sigma_{B_d}\to\Sigma_{B_{d+1}},\qquad\lambda_{d\to d+1}^{(t)}(u) := 3u + t,\qquad t\in{0,1,2}.}]Each (u\in\Sigma_{B_d}) has exactly three children in (\Sigma_{B_{d+1}}):[\boxed{\pi_{d+1\to d}^{-1}(u)={3u,\ 3u+1,\ 3u+2}.}]
Proposition 13.S4.1 (Right inverse).For all (u\in\Sigma_{B_d}) and (t\in{0,1,2}),[\boxed{\pi_{d+1\to d}\bigl(\lambda_{d\to d+1}^{(t)}(u)\bigr)=u.}]
Proposition 13.S4.2 (Digit append).If (\mathsf{GS}d(u)=(\sigma,t_1,\dots,t{d-1})), then[\mathsf{GS}{d+1}\bigl(\lambda{d\to d+1}^{(t)}(u)\bigr)=(\sigma,t_1,\dots,t_{d-1},t).]Thus the one-step lift appends exactly one ternary gear digit.
13.S4.2 — Multi-step lifts
For (d>d'), define the multi-step lift family[\boxed{\lambda_{d'\to d}^{(\mathbf{t})}(u):=3^{d-d'}u + \mathrm{code}(\mathbf{t}),\qquad\mathbf{t}\in{0,1,2}^{d-d'}.}]Here (\mathrm{code}(\mathbf{t})\in{0,\dots,3^{d-d'}-1}) is the ternary integer whose digits are (\mathbf{t}) (most significant first).
Then[\boxed{\pi_{d\to d'}\bigl(\lambda_{d'\to d}^{(\mathbf{t})}(u)\bigr)=u,}]and the lift appends the digit block (\mathbf{t}) to the gear-stack representation.
13.S4.3 — Deterministic lift selection (pinned policy)
A lift (\lambda^{(t)}) is not canonical until (t) is specified. The digit choice (t) is a meaning-bearing decision because it selects a stratum of the refined ring. Therefore:
the selection rule (t=\mathsf{LiftDigit}(u;\pi_{\triangle},\pi_{\mathrm{corr}})) must be pinned by digest,
its inputs must be explicit and replayable, and
its output must be recorded as part of any certified transport or routing plan that uses the lift.
If multiple digit choices are admissible under corridor constraints, then either:
the corridor pins a deterministic tie-break (yielding (\mathrm{OK}) for the choice), or
the route is (\mathrm{AMBIG}) and must emit a bounded candidate set ({t=0,1,2}) together with discriminators that select the intended stratum.
13.S5 — The ring as a discretization of (S^1)
13.S5.1 — Phase quantization into (\Sigma_{B_d})
Let (\phi\in [0,1)) be a circle phase. Define the (B_d) quantizer[\boxed{Q_d(\phi) := \left\lfloor B_d,\phi \right\rfloor \in \Sigma_{B_d}.}]Define the macro-station index[\boxed{\sigma(\phi):=\left\lfloor 15,\phi\right\rfloor \in \Sigma_{15}.}]Because (B_d=15W_d), for all (\phi) not on a macro-station boundary (i.e., (15\phi\notin\mathbb{Z})),[\boxed{\pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d)}\bigl(Q_d(\phi)\bigr) = \sigma(\phi).}]The internal stratum is the (W_d)-quantization of the fractional position within the macro-station interval:[\boxed{\gamma(\phi):= Q_d(\phi) - W_d,\sigma(\phi)= \left\lfloor W_d\cdot \mathrm{frac}(15\phi)\right\rfloor.}]A boundary policy is required to define (Q_d) on boundary points. The boundary policy is part of the corridor pins; absent a pinned boundary policy, cross-dimensional projections involving quantized phases are (\mathrm{AMBIG}).
13.S5.2 — Compatibility of quantization with dimension projection
For (d\ge d'\ge 1), define the quantizer (Q_{d'}(\phi)=\lfloor B_{d'}\phi\rfloor). If (\phi) avoids refinement boundaries at scale (B_d), then[\boxed{Q_{d'}(\phi) = \pi_{d\to d'}\bigl(Q_d(\phi)\bigr).}]This expresses the defining property of the refinement tower: coarsening by grouping triples agrees with direct coarser quantization, except at pinned boundary cases which must be resolved deterministically.
13.S6 — Minimality of (B_d) under stratified metro requirements
13.S6.1 — Stratified station requirement
Fix dimension (d). Assume:
The metro requires 15 macro-stations (\sigma\in\Sigma_{15}).
Each macro-station must support (S_d) distinguishable internal strata, where (S_d=3^{d-1}) is the pinned stratification count (e.g., relative triangle-phase classes).
The discretization of the circle is required to assign a unique discrete cell to each pair ((\sigma,\mathrm{stratum})) while preserving contiguity of macro-stations as blocks (each station occupies a contiguous interval).
Under these requirements, any admissible discretization must have at least (15\cdot S_d) cells, and the block-refinement construction achieves equality.
Theorem 13.S6.1 (Minimality).Any discretization satisfying the stratified station requirement must have[N \ge 15\cdot 3^{d-1}.]Moreover, (N=B_d) is achievable by subdividing each of the 15 station intervals into (3^{d-1}) equal subintervals, yielding the (B_d) metro ring (\Sigma_{B_d}).
❀ Flower — Geometric Interpretation: A Triadic Covering Tower of the Circle
13.F1 — The refinement tower as coverings of (S^1)
Let (S^1=\mathbb{R}/\mathbb{Z}). The discretization at dimension (d) is the partition of (S^1) into (B_d) equal arcs:[I_u^{(d)} := \left[\frac{u}{B_d},\frac{u+1}{B_d}\right),\qquad u\in\Sigma_{B_d}.]The one-step projection (\pi_{d+1\to d}) is the triadic covering map on indices: it groups three consecutive fine arcs into one coarse arc. The lift maps (\lambda_{d\to d+1}^{(t)}) select one of the three subarcs inside a coarse arc.
Thus, for each (d), the discretized metro ring is a cyclic refinement of the same underlying circle:[S^1 \xrightarrow{Q_d} \Sigma_{B_d}\quad\text{with}\quad\Sigma_{B_d}\xrightarrow{\pi_{d\to d'}}\Sigma_{B_{d'}} \ \text{for}\ d\ge d'.]
13.F2 — Gear stacks as triadic addresses within each station
Each macro-station interval has width (1/15). Inside a macro-station, the internal stratum coordinate (\gamma\in\Sigma_{3^{d-1}}) corresponds to a triadic refinement address of depth ((d-1)). The gear digits ((t_1,\dots,t_{d-1})) are the triadic address of the subinterval:[\left[\frac{\sigma}{15} + \frac{\gamma}{15\cdot 3^{d-1}}, \ \frac{\sigma}{15} + \frac{\gamma+1}{15\cdot 3^{d-1}} \right).]Multi-gear projection is geometric truncation of the triadic address; multi-gear lift is geometric extension by appending one triadic digit.
13.F3 — Relative-phase stratification as a quotient geometry
When triangle-phase is per-axis (\tau\in(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d) but only relative phase is physically discriminable, the quotient ((\mathbb{Z}_3)^d/\Delta) yields (3^{d-1}) strata. The triadic refinement depth ((d-1)) encodes exactly the stratification needed to lift the metro into dimension (d) without collapsing distinct relative-phase regimes into the same discrete cell.
☁ Cloud — Legality, Truth Typing, and Failure Modes for Projections and Lifts
13.C1 — Projection and lift claims are certified transforms
A projection or lift is a meaning-bearing transform only when its rule is pinned and its execution is replayable. Define a projection claim[\mathsf{Claim}{\pi} := (\text{src}=\Sigma{B_d},\ \text{dst}=\Sigma_{B_{d'}},\ \text{map}=\pi_{d\to d'},\ \text{pins},\ \text{domain},\ \text{corridor}),]and analogously for lift claims (\lambda^{(t)}). A claim is eligible for (\mathrm{OK}) only if:
the digits/order conventions are pinned,
boundary policy is pinned (if phases (\phi) are inputs),
deterministic replay reproduces identical outputs and identical digests, and
any additional corridor invariants (station preservation, stratum policy constraints, hub constraints) are verified.
13.C2 — Truth typing for lift-digit choice
When projecting from (d) to (d+1), there are three lifts (\lambda^{(0)},\lambda^{(1)},\lambda^{(2)}). The digit selection is governed by corridor constraints:
OK: the lift digit (t) is uniquely determined by pinned policy, or the corridor explicitly pins (t) as part of the claim input.
AMBIG: multiple digits are admissible and no pinned tie-break exists; the outcome must include a bounded candidate set ({t}\subseteq{0,1,2}) and an evidence plan that selects (t).
FAIL: the digit choice violates corridor invariants (e.g., violates a pinned corridor that forbids certain strata for the current target), or the policy is missing but required.
NEAR: permitted only if the corridor explicitly allows approximate digit selection under a metric and a residual ledger (rare for discrete digit selection; generally disallowed).
13.C3 — Boundary ambiguity for phase quantization
If an input phase (\phi) lies on a quantization boundary (e.g., (B_d\phi\in\mathbb{Z})), then (Q_d(\phi)) depends on boundary conventions. Without pinned boundary conventions, the correct truth type is (\mathrm{AMBIG}) (bounded ambiguity among at most two indices). With pinned boundary conventions, the quantizer is deterministic and may be (\mathrm{OK}).
A corridor that permits quantized-phase operations must specify:
interval conventions (half-open policy),
numeric representation policy (rational canonical form or pinned float policy), and
replay rules for boundary cases.
13.C4 — Aliasing failure as insufficient stratification
If a system attempts to interpret a (d)-dimensional stratified state using a ring (N<B_d), then multiple strata must collapse into the same discrete cell. This is an aliasing failure mode:
If the collapsed fiber is bounded and explicitly enumerated, the correct type is (\mathrm{AMBIG}) with a bounded candidate set and an evidence plan.
If the fiber is unbounded under the corridor’s admissible state class (or cannot be enumerated within budget (\chi)), the correct type is (\mathrm{FAIL}).
✶ Fractal — Gear-Stack Atlases, Replay Harness Expectations, and Regression Obligations
13.R1 — The gear-stack atlas across dimensions
Define the gear-stack atlas at dimension (d) as the collection of all certified maps:
(\pi_{d\to d'}) for all (d'\le d),
(\lambda_{d'\to d}^{(\mathbf{t})}) families with pinned digit policies,
(\mathsf{GS}_d) and (\mathsf{GS}_d^{-1}),together with replay capsules and regression suites verifying:
station preservation under projection,
digit append/truncation laws,
functoriality (\pi_{d\to d''}=\pi_{d'\to d''}\circ\pi_{d\to d'}), and
deterministic behavior under pinned boundary policy.
This atlas is a necessary substrate for any cross-dimensional routing that intends to be replay-verifiable.
13.R2 — Replay harness expectations for (B_d) projections and lifts
A conformant replay harness must provide deterministic routines for:
Index normalization into (\Sigma_{B_d}) canonical representatives.
Macro-station computation (\pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d)}) and stratum computation (\pi_{\mathrm{str}}^{(d)}).
Digit extraction (\mathrm{digits}_d) and reconstruction.
Projection verification for (\pi_{d\to d'}).
Lift verification for (\lambda^{(t)}) with pinned digit selection rules.
Round-trip laws: (\pi_{d+1\to d}\circ \lambda_{d\to d+1}^{(t)}=\mathrm{Id}), and tower consistency.
Boundary policy tests if phase quantization is part of the subject.
All verifier outputs must be digest-bound and reproducible under pinned environment pins.
13.R3 — Regression suite obligations (minimum fixtures)
A minimal regression suite for cross-dimensional metro must include fixtures for:
All macro-station boundaries: values of (u) at (\sigma W_d) and ((\sigma+1)W_d-1).
All lift digits: for each (t\in{0,1,2}), verify digit append law and right-inverse law.
Multi-step functoriality: random (u) and multiple (d') verifying (\pi_{d\to d''}=\pi_{d'\to d''}\circ\pi_{d\to d'}).
Digit stack extremes: (\gamma=0) (all digits zero) and (\gamma=3^{d-1}-1) (all digits two).
Phase boundary cases: if (Q_d) is used, test boundary points under the pinned boundary convention.
Failures must produce deterministic failure witnesses; unresolved ambiguity must produce evidence plans; all artifacts must be exportable and import-verifiable.
13.R4 — Reference implementation (projection/lift/digit stack)
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import List, Tuple, Literal
Digit = Literal[0, 1, 2]
def B(d: int) -> int:
assert d >= 1
return 15 * (3 ** (d - 1))
def W(d: int) -> int:
assert d >= 1
return 3 ** (d - 1)
def proj_dim(u: int, d: int, d2: int) -> int:
"""
Projection π_{d→d2} on indices, grouping triadic refinements.
u is assumed canonical in [0, B(d)-1].
"""
assert 1 <= d2 <= d
return u // (3 ** (d - d2))
def lift_dim(u: int, d: int, t: Digit) -> int:
"""
One-step lift λ_{d→d+1}^{(t)}.
"""
assert d >= 1
return 3 * u + int(t)
def station(u: int, d: int) -> int:
"""
Macro-station projection π_st^{(d)}(u) in {0,...,14}.
"""
return u // W(d)
def stratum(u: int, d: int) -> int:
"""
Stratum projection π_str^{(d)}(u) in {0,...,W(d)-1}.
"""
return u - station(u, d) * W(d)
def digits_stratum(gamma: int, d: int) -> Tuple[Digit, ...]:
"""
Convert gamma in [0, 3^{d-1}-1] to (t1,...,t_{d-1}) in base 3.
Most significant digit first. For d=1, returns empty tuple.
"""
assert d >= 1
if d == 1:
return tuple()
out: List[Digit] = []
rem = gamma
for i in range(d - 1):
place = 3 ** (d - 2 - i)
ti = rem // place
rem = rem - ti * place
out.append(ti) # type: ignore
return tuple(out) # type: ignore
def undigits_stratum(ts: Tuple[Digit, ...]) -> int:
"""
Convert (t1,...,t_{m}) in base 3 to integer gamma.
"""
m = len(ts)
gamma = 0
for i, ti in enumerate(ts):
place = 3 ** (m - 1 - i)
gamma += int(ti) * place
return gamma
def gear_stack(u: int, d: int) -> Tuple[int, Tuple[Digit, ...]]:
"""
Returns (sigma, (t1,...,t_{d-1})) for u in Σ_{B_d}.
"""
sigma = station(u, d)
gamma = stratum(u, d)
ts = digits_stratum(gamma, d)
return sigma, ts
def from_gear_stack(sigma: int, ts: Tuple[Digit, ...], d: int) -> int:
"""
Inverse reconstruction GS_d^{-1}.
"""
assert 0 <= sigma <= 14
assert len(ts) == max(0, d - 1)
gamma = undigits_stratum(ts)
assert 0 <= gamma < W(d)
return sigma * W(d) + gamma
def multi_gear(u: int, d: int) -> Tuple[int, ...]:
"""
Multi-gear readout MG_d(u) = (u^{(1)},...,u^{(d)}).
"""
return tuple(proj_dim(u, d, r) for r in range(1, d + 1))
Ch13 — Cross-Dimensional Metro (B_d ring + gear stacks)
Ch14 — The Holographic Compiler Interface (Seed → State → Navigation)
The aether seed as an invariant object and its instantiation into HD‑SCT state and deterministic navigation
□ Square — Formal Interface: aether seed, compilation, and routable artifacts
14.S1 Aether seed as a typed invariant object
14.S1.1 Seed as canonical semantic object, not surface syntax
An aether seed is the canonical semantic object from which all lens-representations are compiled. It is not a string, not a rendered equation, and not a file layout. It is a typed invariant structure supporting deterministic compilation.
Define a seed (\mathcal{A}) as the tuple[\boxed{\mathcal{A}:=\bigl(\mathcal{V},\mathcal{O},\mathcal{T},\mathcal{R},\mathcal{I},\mathcal{U},\mathcal{G}\bigr)}]where:
(\mathcal{V}) is a finite set of symbols (variables, constants, parameters, fields, random variables, operators).
(\mathcal{O}) is a finite set of operators (function symbols) with arities and evaluation classes (algebraic, differential, integral, stochastic, functional, multiscale).
(\mathcal{T}) is a type system specifying base types and constructors (scalars, vectors, tensors, fields on manifolds, measures, distributions, operators, scale-families, code objects), together with well-formedness judgments for terms.
(\mathcal{R}) is a finite set of relations (axioms/constraints) expressed as typed equalities/inequalities/implications between well-typed terms.
(\mathcal{I}) is a finite set of invariants that must be preserved by admissible representation changes (dimensional consistency, conservation laws, symmetries, normal-form equivalence, decode equivalence, commutation receipts, corridor legality).
(\mathcal{U}) is a unit/gauge discipline (units, dimensional annotations, gauge choices, and any quotient identifications that define semantic equivalence classes).
(\mathcal{G}) is a finite set of gauge freedoms and canonicalization constraints specifying which degrees of freedom are semantic and which are representational.
The role of (\mathcal{G}) is to make “same seed” well-defined. If two surface forms differ only by allowed gauge transformations, they compile to the same canonical seed.
14.S1.2 Term-graph representation and alpha-canonicalization
Let (\mathrm{Term}(\mathcal{A})) be the set of well-typed terms over ((\mathcal{V},\mathcal{O},\mathcal{T})). To avoid dependence on symbol names and syntactic formatting, the seed is represented as a typed term graph:
[\boxed{\mathsf{TG}(\mathcal{A}) := (N,E,\mathrm{op},\mathrm{ty},\mathrm{ann})}]where (N) are nodes (subterms), (E\subseteq N\times N) are directed edges (argument links), (\mathrm{op}) assigns an operator label to each internal node, (\mathrm{ty}) assigns a type to each node, and (\mathrm{ann}) stores canonical annotations (units, domains, axis tags, scale tags, measure tags).
A seed (\mathcal{A}) is canonical if:
its term graph is acyclic (or if cyclic, the cycle semantics are explicitly typed and pinned),
all binders (integrals, sums, expectations) are alpha-canonicalized,
node ordering is canonical (topological order with pinned tie-break), and
every semantic degree of freedom is represented explicitly in (\mathcal{G}), with a pinned canonical gauge selection.
Define the seed canonical bytes (\mathrm{Enc}(\mathcal{A})) by a pinned encoding schema, and define the seed identifier[\boxed{\mathrm{SeedID}(\mathcal{A}) := H(\mathrm{Enc}(\mathcal{A})).}]All compiled artifacts produced from (\mathcal{A}) are required to carry (\mathrm{SeedID}(\mathcal{A})) as a primary pin.
14.S1.3 Seed equivalence and semantic equality
Let (\sim_{\mathcal{G}}) be the equivalence relation generated by the allowed gauge transformations and definitional equalities specified in (\mathcal{G}). Two seeds (\mathcal{A},\mathcal{A}') are semantically equal if:[\boxed{\mathcal{A}\equiv \mathcal{A}' \quad \Longleftrightarrow \quad \mathcal{A}\sim_{\mathcal{G}}\mathcal{A}'.}]Canonicalization selects a unique representative (\mathrm{CanSeed}(\mathcal{A})) in each equivalence class. The compiler interface is defined on canonical seeds.
14.S2 The compiler pipeline: Seed → State → Navigation
14.S2.1 The compiler as a pure function of pinned inputs
Fix pinned profiles:
a CorridorProfile (\mathfrak{C}) (truth typing, budgets, legality),
a RouterProfile (\pi_R) (≤6 hubs, deterministic order),
a BuildProfile (\pi_B) (dimension-depth lock policy, resolution policy, boundary policy, normalization policy, export policy),
an EnvironmentPin (\mathsf{EPn}) (replay determinism requirements).
The holographic compiler is the pure function[\boxed{\mathrm{Compile}:\ (\mathcal{A},\pi_B,\mathfrak{C},\pi_R,\mathsf{EPn})\ \longrightarrow\ \mathsf{Program}}]where (\mathsf{Program}) is an addressable, replayable package containing:
instantiated HD‑SCT state objects across chosen ((d,k)),
certified transform edges and receipts needed to move between states,
navigation indices and router-ready graph structures, and
certificate bundles for replay/import verification.
Purity requirement: compilation must not depend on unpinned randomness, clock time, network state, or mutable caches. Any such dependency forces (\mathrm{AMBIG}) or (\mathrm{FAIL}) under corridor policy.
14.S2.2 HD‑SCT state as a four-carrier object
For each locked dimension/scale pair ((d,k)), define the HD‑SCT state space[\boxed{\mathsf{HDState}(d,k):= \mathsf{SqState}(d,k)\ \times\ \mathsf{CiState}(d,k)\ \times\ \mathsf{TrState}(d,k)\ \times\ \mathsf{FrState}(d,k).}]An instantiated state is[\boxed{\mathbf{x}{d,k}:=\bigl(x^\square{d,k},x^\circ_{d,k},x^\triangle_{d,k},x^{\mathfrak{f}}_{d,k}\bigr)\in\mathsf{HDState}(d,k).}]
The seed-to-state instantiator is the function[\boxed{\mathrm{Instantiate}:\ (\mathcal{A},d,k;\pi_B,\mathfrak{C})\ \longrightarrow\ \mathbf{x}_{d,k}\ \text{ plus ledgers and receipts}.}]
(i) Square carrier (\mathsf{SqState}(d,k)).This is the discrete address/structure carrier at locked depth. It must include:
the locked dimension/scale tags ((d,k)),
the square resolution policy (per-axis minimums, lock constraints),
a canonical normal form object for square addresses/tiles,
any square-encoded invariants derived from (\mathcal{A}) (symbol/type placements, adjacency constraints, operator wiring constraints).
(ii) Circle carrier (\mathsf{CiState}(d,k)).This is the phase/metro carrier associated to (\mathbb{T}^d) and the refined metro ring. It must include:
an axis-phase vector (\phi\in\mathbb{T}^d) or a discrete hub index in a pinned hub mesh (\mathcal{H}^d),
a metro index (u\in\Sigma_{B_d}) where[\boxed{B_d=15\cdot 3^{d-1}},]
the boundary policy and quantization policy binding (\phi) to (u) (or declaring the relationship as approximate with a residual ledger).
(iii) Triangle carrier (\mathsf{TrState}(d,k)).This is the pinned corridor-policy state governing which corridors and routes are admissible (e.g., global vs per-axis triangle mode, pinned corridor selections, digit/lift selection policies). It must include:
the triangle mode (\tau) (global or per-axis),
the lift-digit policy binding triadic refinement choices to admissible states,
policy witnesses for any forced choices (or evidence plans if not uniquely determined).
(iv) Fractal carrier (\mathsf{FrState}(d,k)).This is the multiscale and cross-dimensional coherence carrier. It must include:
the scale ladder and lift/projection receipts,
Snap/meta-zero canonical representatives and residual ledgers,
holonomy/spin receipts required for schedule commutation claims,
certificate references needed to replay all above.
Each carrier is an object with canonical bytes and a digest. The full state digest is the digest of the product encoding under pinned ordering.
14.S2.3 Seed invariance law across carriers
Compilation is valid only if the instantiated carriers remain attached to the same seed.
For each lens (L\in{\square,\circ,\triangle,\mathfrak{f}}), define a deterministic evaluator[\mathrm{Eval}_L:\ \mathsf{LState}(d,k)\ \rightharpoonup\ \mathcal{A}]and a deterministic encoder[\mathrm{Enc}_L:\ \mathcal{A}\ \rightharpoonup\ \mathsf{LState}(d,k),]both pinned by profile digests and boundary policies.
Define the seed invariance defect for lens (L) by[\Delta_L(\mathcal{A};d,k):= \mathrm{Dist}_{\mathcal{A}}!\bigl(\mathrm{Eval}_L(\mathrm{Enc}L(\mathcal{A})),\ \mathcal{A}\bigr),]where (\mathrm{Dist}{\mathcal{A}}) is a pinned seed-distance functional (often discrete: (0) if canonical seed ID matches; (1) otherwise; or structural diff metrics when a corridor permits NEAR).
Seed invariance requirement.A compiled program may claim (\mathrm{OK}) attachment to seed (\mathcal{A}) at ((d,k)) only if:[\boxed{\Delta_L(\mathcal{A};d,k)=0\quad\text{for all required lenses }L}]and all associated replays close. If (\Delta_L) is bounded but nonzero, the compiler must emit a residual ledger and type the attachment (\mathrm{NEAR}) or (\mathrm{AMBIG}) under corridor rules.
14.S3 Snap-closure as the canonical state selector
Seed instantiation is not generally unique because multiple representations and corridor constraints do not necessarily commute. The compiler therefore selects canonical representatives by Snap/meta-zero closure.
Fix a pinned gate list (\mathbf{P}=(P_1,\dots,P_m)) acting on a product carrier (\mathsf{X}) that includes the necessary components of (\mathsf{HDState}(d,k)). Define the composite gate[T:=P_m\circ\cdots\circ P_1.]The Snap closure is:[\boxed{\mathrm{Snap}{\pi_B,\mathfrak{C}}(\mathbf{x}):=\lim{n\to\infty}T^n(\mathbf{x})}]when the limit exists under the pinned stopping rule and within the pinned computational budget (\chi). The Snap output is:[\boxed{\bigl(\mathbf{x}^\star,\ \mathsf{RL},\ \mathsf{SR},\ \mathsf{RC}\bigr)}]where:
(\mathbf{x}^\star) is the canonical representative,
(\mathsf{RL}) is the residual ledger bundle (per-gate defects, alias leakage, boundary defects),
(\mathsf{SR}) is the set of required spin/holonomy receipts (when commutation constraints are part of the corridor),
(\mathsf{RC}) is the replay capsule ensuring determinism of the Snap computation.
The compiler must treat Snap as a first-class compilation stage: it is not an optimization, and it is not optional when canonical representatives are required for navigation or export.
14.S4 Navigation as a compiled interface: queries, routes, and artifacts
14.S4.1 Navigation objects: targets, intents, and start contexts
Navigation operates on the compiled program (\mathsf{Program}) by issuing a navigation query[\boxed{\mathsf{NavQ}:=(\mathrm{SeedID},\mathrm{Ctx},\mathrm{Target},\mathsf{Intent},\tau_0,\mathsf{Pins})}]where:
(\mathrm{Ctx}) identifies the current ((d,k)) (or a set of candidate ((d,k)) contexts),
(\mathrm{Target}) is a strict address in the HD‑SCT address grammar,
(\mathsf{Intent}) is a pinned intent class,
(\tau_0\in{\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL}}) is the initial truth state,
(\mathsf{Pins}) pins router/corridor profiles and environment.
Navigation outputs a RoutePlan (≤6 hubs, deterministic order) together with replayable artifacts:[\boxed{\mathrm{Navigate}(\mathsf{NavQ})\ \longrightarrow(\mathsf{RP},\ \mathsf{Tx},\ \mathsf{Out},\ \mathsf{RC}_{\mathrm{nav}})}]where:
(\mathsf{RP}) is the deterministic hub ride to the target,
(\mathsf{Tx}) is the execution transcript (append-only),
(\mathsf{Out}) is the corridor truth-typed outcome bundle,
(\mathsf{RC}_{\mathrm{nav}}) is a replay capsule for route selection and execution.
14.S4.2 The compiled navigation index
To guarantee deterministic routing without heuristic search explosion, the compiler emits a navigation index. Define:[\boxed{\mathsf{NavIndex}:=(\mathrm{AddrIndex},\mathrm{HubIndex},\mathrm{RingIndex},\mathrm{LiftIndex},\mathrm{ReceiptIndex},\mathrm{FenceIndex})}]where:
(\mathrm{AddrIndex}) maps addresses to canonical nodes in the compiled graph.
(\mathrm{HubIndex}) maps target classes to router base hubs and intent overlays under (\pi_R).
(\mathrm{RingIndex}) maps circle-phase or metro objects to (u\in\Sigma_{B_d}), plus macro-station (\sigma\in\Sigma_{15}) and gear digits.
(\mathrm{LiftIndex}) stores available lift/projection families between dimensions (including digit selection policies and admissibility).
(\mathrm{ReceiptIndex}) stores spin/holonomy receipts and their scopes.
(\mathrm{FenceIndex}) stores quarantines, revocations, and conflict packets.
The router and executor are required to operate only on the index and pinned profiles; they must not re-infer semantics from prose or from mutable state.
14.S4.3 The router/engine artifact contract
For any navigation output, the compiler and executor must emit a minimal bundle:[\boxed{\mathsf{NavBundle}:= (\mathsf{RP},\mathsf{Tx},\mathsf{Out},\mathrm{SeedID},\mathrm{StateDigests},\mathrm{ProfileDigests},\mathrm{BudgetUse})}]with strict requirements:
Deterministic hub order pinned by (\pi_R).
≤6 unique hubs before the target (dedupe does not count as dropping).
Truth overlay hubs inserted deterministically according to (\tau_0) and corridor policy.
Replay closure: the navigation selection and execution transcript must be reproducible under pinned environment pins.
Import verifiability: when exported, the bundle includes enough closure artifacts (capsules, witnesses, profiles) for an external verifier to reproduce the outcome.
If any requirement fails, the navigation output must be typed (\mathrm{AMBIG}) or (\mathrm{FAIL}), never (\mathrm{OK}).
14.S5 Program output: the compiled package and certificate expectations
Define the compiler output as[\boxed{\mathsf{Program}:=(\mathrm{SeedID},\mathrm{Manifests},\mathrm{Profiles},\mathrm{States},\mathrm{Graph},\mathrm{NavIndex},\mathrm{Receipts},\mathrm{Ledgers},\mathrm{Certificates},\mathrm{Exports})}]where:
(\mathrm{States}) contains instantiated (\mathbf{x}^\star_{d,k}) for required ((d,k)) contexts, each with Snap closure and state digest.
(\mathrm{Graph}) is the certified transform graph over these states (edges typed by corridor legality and carrying outcomes).
(\mathrm{Receipts}) includes commutation receipts (spin/holonomy), lift/projection receipts, and any legality witnesses required by the corridor.
(\mathrm{Ledgers}) includes residual ledgers for NEAR or Snap defects.
(\mathrm{Certificates}) includes replay certificates, regression certificates, and export certificates required for import-verifiable publication.
(\mathrm{Exports}) includes export bundles and their import verification transcripts.
A program is eligible for publication corridors only when its certificate set is complete for the declared scope.
14.S6 Reference interface specification and data model
14.S6.1 Minimal type signatures
Let (\mathrm{Bytes}) be byte strings and (\mathrm{Digest}) be digests under pinned (H). Define canonical interfaces:
Seed canonicalization:[\mathrm{CanSeed}:\ \mathrm{SeedInput}\to \mathcal{A}]
State instantiation:[\mathrm{Instantiate}:\ (\mathcal{A},d,k;\pi_B,\mathfrak{C})\to \mathbf{x}_{d,k}\times \mathsf{Out}]
Snap closure:[\mathrm{Snap}:\ (\mathbf{x}{d,k};\pi_B,\mathfrak{C})\to \mathbf{x}^\star{d,k}\times \mathsf{Out}]
Navigation compilation:[\mathrm{BuildNavIndex}:\ (\mathsf{Program};\pi_R,\mathfrak{C})\to \mathsf{NavIndex}]
Navigation query execution:[\mathrm{Navigate}:\ (\mathsf{Program},\mathsf{NavQ})\to \mathsf{NavBundle}]
Export:[\mathrm{Export}:\ (\mathsf{Program},S;\pi_B,\mathfrak{C})\to \mathsf{ExportBundle}\times \mathsf{ExportCert}]
All functions are deterministic given their pinned profiles and environment pins.
14.S6.2 Reference implementation skeleton (compiler core)
from __future__ import annotations
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Any, Dict, List, Optional, Tuple, Literal, FrozenSet, Callable
Truth = Literal["OK", "NEAR", "AMBIG", "FAIL", "CONFLICT"]
Lens = Literal["SQUARE", "CIRCLE", "TRIANGLE", "FRACTAL"]
Digest = str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class EnvPins:
os_id: str
arch_id: str
runtime_id: str
lib_digests: Tuple[Tuple[str, Digest], ...]
float_policy: str
endian_policy: str
schema_pins: Tuple[Tuple[str, str], ...]
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class CorridorProfile:
digest: Digest
truth_threshold: Truth
budget_kappa: float
budget_beta: float
budget_delta: int
budget_chi: int
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class RouterProfile:
digest: Digest
hub_cap: int # must be 6 for the contract
mandatory_signature: FrozenSet[str] # e.g., {"AppA","AppI","AppM"}
# plus deterministic tables (lens/facet/arc/overlay/drop priorities)
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class BuildProfile:
digest: Digest
dim_lock_policy: str
resolution_policy: str
boundary_policy: str
snap_script_digest: Digest
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class AetherSeed:
seed_id: Digest
# canonical term-graph + types + invariants + gauge constraints
payload_digest: Digest
schema_ver: str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class ResidualLedger:
metric_id: str
value: float
bound: float
scope: Tuple[str, ...]
replay_ptr: str
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Outcome:
truth: Truth
replay_ptr: Optional[str]
witness_ptrs: Tuple[str, ...]
residuals: Tuple[ResidualLedger, ...]
obligations: Tuple[str, ...]
budget_use: Tuple[float, float, int, int] # (kappa,beta,delta,chi)
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class SquareState:
d: int
k: int
digest: Digest
nf_profile: Digest
data_digest: Digest
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class CircleState:
d: int
k: int
digest: Digest
B_d: int
u: int # metro index in Σ_{B_d}
phi_digest: Optional[Digest]
hub_digest: Optional[Digest]
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class TriangleState:
d: int
k: int
digest: Digest
mode: str # pinned mode spec
lift_digit_policy: Digest
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class FractalState:
d: int
k: int
digest: Digest
scale_ladder_digest: Digest
receipts_digest: Digest
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class HDState:
d: int
k: int
seed_id: Digest
square: SquareState
circle: CircleState
triangle: TriangleState
fractal: FractalState
digest: Digest
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class NavIndex:
digest: Digest
addr_index_digest: Digest
hub_index_digest: Digest
ring_index_digest: Digest
lift_index_digest: Digest
receipt_index_digest: Digest
fence_index_digest: Digest
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class Program:
seed_id: Digest
build_profile: Digest
corridor_profile: Digest
router_profile: Digest
env_pins: EnvPins
states: Tuple[HDState, ...]
graph_digest: Digest
nav_index: NavIndex
certificates_digest: Digest
def compile_seed(seed: AetherSeed,
bp: BuildProfile,
C: CorridorProfile,
R: RouterProfile,
env: EnvPins,
instantiate: Callable[[AetherSeed,int,int,BuildProfile,CorridorProfile,EnvPins], Tuple[HDState, Outcome]],
build_nav_index: Callable[[Tuple[HDState,...], BuildProfile, CorridorProfile, RouterProfile], NavIndex],
build_graph: Callable[[Tuple[HDState,...], CorridorProfile], Digest],
build_certs: Callable[[Tuple[HDState,...], Digest, NavIndex, BuildProfile, CorridorProfile, RouterProfile, EnvPins], Digest]
) -> Program:
"""
Deterministic compiler entrypoint: Seed → States → Graph/Index → Certificates.
All variability must be pinned by digests in bp, C, R, env.
"""
# Dimension-depth selection is pinned by bp.dim_lock_policy; example: compile a minimal ladder
# (d0,k0) plus a fixed number of locked lifts. Here we stub a pinned set:
dk_targets = [(1, 0), (2, 1), (3, 2)] # placeholder; must be derived deterministically
states: List[HDState] = []
outcomes: List[Outcome] = []
for d, k in dk_targets:
st, out = instantiate(seed, d, k, bp, C, env)
states.append(st)
outcomes.append(out)
# Graph and index depend only on compiled states and pinned profiles.
graph_digest = build_graph(tuple(states), C)
nav_index = build_nav_index(tuple(states), bp, C, R)
# Certificates bind replay closure, regressions, and export readiness.
certs_digest = build_certs(tuple(states), graph_digest, nav_index, bp, C, R, env)
return Program(
seed_id=seed.seed_id,
build_profile=bp.digest,
corridor_profile=C.digest,
router_profile=R.digest,
env_pins=env,
states=tuple(states),
graph_digest=graph_digest,
nav_index=nav_index,
certificates_digest=certs_digest,
)
This skeleton is intentionally strict: all degrees of freedom must be pinned by profile digests and environment pins, and every artifact must be content-addressed. An implementation may extend the schema, but it may not weaken determinism, replay closure, or truth typing.
❀ Flower — Geometric meaning: seed as coordinate-free object, state as charted representative, navigation as path selection
14.F1 Seed as an equivalence class in a moduli space
The aether seed (\mathcal{A}) may be regarded as a coordinate-free object: a point in a moduli space of typed relations modulo gauge. Each lens (L) provides a chart (a representational coordinate system) on (a portion of) that moduli space. Encoding (\mathrm{Enc}_L) selects a chart representative; evaluation (\mathrm{Eval}_L) maps back to the coordinate-free object.
In this interpretation:
seed invariance is chart-independence,
Snap/meta-zero is canonical gauge fixing plus intersection of admissible corridor constraints,
residual ledgers quantify failure to lie exactly in the intersection (distance-to-corridor).
14.F2 State as a fibered structure over seed
For fixed ((d,k)), the state space (\mathsf{HDState}(d,k)) is a fibered product of carriers:[\mathsf{HDState}(d,k)\ \longrightarrow\ \mathcal{A},]where the projection is “evaluate back to seed.” The fiber over (\mathcal{A}) contains all representations consistent with (\mathcal{A}) under pinned legality. Snap selects a canonical section of this fibration (or a best-approximate section, recorded as NEAR).
14.F3 Cross-dimensional metro as a refinement tower of the circle
The circle component of state binds a geometric phase object to the refined metro ring (\Sigma_{B_d}). The refinement law (B_{d+1}=3B_d) is a tower of coverings of the base 15-station circle partition. Gear-stack digits are the discrete internal coordinates within each macro-station induced by relative phase stratification.
Thus “Seed → State” includes selecting a consistent refinement level for the seed’s dimensional deployment, and “State → Navigation” uses this consistent refinement to avoid aliasing and to keep higher-dimensional cycles visible.
14.F4 Navigation as homotopy-aware routing with receipts
When navigation asserts equivalence of two routes, that assertion is a holonomy statement. The compiled program therefore treats spin/holonomy receipts as geometric witnesses: they certify path-independence (or quantify the defect) under corridor metrics. Navigation is thereby a geometric process with explicit loop evidence, not an informal choice of links.
☁ Cloud — Uncertainty: partial seeds, NEAR instantiation, and AMBIG navigation plans
14.C1 Partial seeds and evidence plans
If the input seed is missing required typing, gauge constraints, boundary policies, or legality pins, canonicalization cannot produce a unique (\mathcal{A}). In this case, compilation must return (\mathrm{AMBIG}) with:
a bounded candidate set of completions ({\mathcal{A}_1,\dots,\mathcal{A}_m}) (when enumerable within (\chi)), and
an evidence plan specifying discriminators that collapse ambiguity (additional typing facts, unit constraints, corridor selections, or canonical gauge selections).
The compiler is forbidden to guess missing constraints while claiming OK.
14.C2 NEAR instantiation and residual disclosure
If the seed is canonical but exact corridor intersection is not achievable (Snap does not reach zero defect within budgets), compilation may emit (\mathrm{NEAR}) state with residual ledger bundle (\mathsf{RL}). NEAR is admissible only if:
all residuals are computed under pinned metrics,
bounds are explicit,
scope is explicit (which parts of state/navigation are affected), and
replay capsules reproduce the residual computation.
NEAR states must be treated as first-class: navigation that depends on them must propagate residual disclosures and may be forbidden under strict corridors (e.g., publication).
14.C3 Probabilistic seeds and pinned inference rules
If the seed includes stochastic components (random variables, distributions, empirical measures), the seed is still an invariant object only if its probabilistic semantics are pinned:
distribution families and parameters,
sampling policies (if any),
estimator definitions (if approximate),
and replay policies (seeds/RNG discipline).
Absent pinned inference rules, probabilistic compilation cannot be import-verifiable and must be typed AMBIG/FAIL under strict corridors.
14.C4 Navigation under uncertainty is routable, not suppressed
Uncertainty in compilation and navigation is represented by routable truth typing:
(\mathrm{AMBIG}) produces evidence-plan routes rather than semantic routes,
(\mathrm{NEAR}) produces residual-ledger routes with explicit disclosures,
(\mathrm{FAIL}) produces fences and conflict packets,
(\mathrm{OK}) produces publishable routes.
This turns “compiler uncertainty” into explicit graph content.
✶ Fractal — Multiscale compilation: locked lifts, gear stacks, and certificate-complete export
14.R1 Locked lift ladder as the canonical dimension-depth schedule
A build profile (\pi_B) pins a dimension-depth ladder[(d_0,k_0)\ \leadsto\ (d_1,k_1)\ \leadsto\ \cdots\ \leadsto\ (d_m,k_m)]typically by a locked law such as ((d,k)\mapsto(d+1,k+1)). Compilation must produce:
states at each rung,
lift/projection maps between rungs,
receipts verifying functoriality and station preservation,
and regression fixtures covering boundary and alias cases.
This is the cross-dimensional backbone that makes a seed “holographically coherent” across dimensions.
14.R2 Gear-stack coherence constraints
For each rung (d), the circle carrier uses (\Sigma_{B_d}) with (B_d=15\cdot 3^{d-1}). Cross-dimensional coherence requires:
projection compatibility across rungs (dropping gear digits by triadic coarsening),
lift choice policies pinned by triangle carrier state,
and boundary policies pinned for quantization and digit selection.
Any failure of coherence yields nontrivial fibers (ambiguity) or aliasing (failure), and must be typed accordingly.
14.R3 Compiler output must be certificate-complete for its declared claims
A compiled program intended for import-verifiable sharing must include certificate bundles that bind:
replay closure for critical state instantiation and navigation,
regression coverage for key transforms, boundary rules, and lift/projection laws,
export determinism and import verification transcripts.
The compiler interface therefore treats certificates as output of compilation, not as external paperwork. Export without certificates is not a “release”; it is an explicitly non-verifiable draft package, and its truth claims must be bounded accordingly.
14.R4 Incremental compilation and supersession without semantic drift
Because certificates and state objects are content-addressed, the compiler supports incremental rebuild:
unchanged seed and profiles imply unchanged digests,
changed profiles require explicit MIGRATE semantics and compatibility receipts,
supersession occurs by new artifacts linked to previous ones, never by overwriting.
This establishes the holographic compiler as an append-only, replay-verifiable “build system for meaning.”
Ch14 — The Holographic Compiler Interface (Seed → State → Navigation)
Ch15⟨0032⟩ — Defect Skeletons and Trigger Laws
[Arc 4 | Rot 1 | △Lane Su | ω=14]Workflow role: trigger loci, measurable laws, counterexamples, boundary repair discipline.Primary hubs: AppA (canonical encoding), AppD (pins), AppG (corridor budgets), AppC (kernels/phases), AppI (measurement/logging), AppM (repair search), AppK/AppO (fences/quarantine).
15.0 Mechanization Thesis
From this chapter forward, “failure” is not narrative. A failure is a structured, typed artifact whose semantics are enforced by pinned encodings, deterministic replay, measurable trigger laws, and explicit repair legality.
A failure instance is represented by the minimal quintuple:[\mathcal{F} ;=; (\mathrm{DS}, \mathrm{TL}, \mathrm{MS}, \mathrm{RS}, \mathrm{CE?})]where:
DefectSkeleton (DS) is the minimal witness class explaining a disagreement between two purportedly equivalent routes/representations.
TriggerLaw (TL) is the deterministic predicate over pinned state and event stream that decides whether the DS can manifest.
MeasurementSpec (MS) is the bounded, ordered, redactable emission contract sufficient to reproduce/classify/repair-search the defect.
RepairSpec (RS) is the constrained set of legal repair operations (append-only) and budgets/exit criteria.
CounterexampleArtifact (CE) is mandatory when TL triggers and RS cannot produce OK/NEAR under corridor budgets, or when repair is disallowed by boundary discipline.
A mechanized defect is routable to certificates and replay harnesses without additional prose, and all decisions (triggering, typing, repair legality) are derivable by deterministic algorithms from pinned artifacts.
15.1 Foundations: Pins, Canonical Encoding, and Deterministic Replays
15.1.1 Pinned Canonical Encoding
All types introduced in this chapter are pinned, serializable types with canonical encodings governed by AppA/AppD.
Let (\mathrm{Enc}_A(T)) denote the AppA canonical encoding for instances of type (T).
Let (\mathrm{Digest}(\cdot)) denote the pinned digest function (\mathsf{H}) (algorithm identifier + domain separation are part of the pin set).
Canonical encoding requirements. For any type (T) defined in this chapter:
Totality. (\mathrm{Enc}_A) is defined for all well-formed values of (T).
Determinism. If (x=y) as values, then (\mathrm{Enc}_A(x)) is bitwise identical to (\mathrm{Enc}_A(y)).
Canonical key ordering. All map/object key orderings are canonical (fixed ordering by tag/field-id), all lists requiring canonicality must be sorted by pinned comparator.
No ambient dependence. Encoding depends only on value content and pins (not wall-clock time, locale, platform specifics).
Each artifact carries a PinSet reference:
PinSet: a record of immutable identifiers controlling canonicalization, schema, kernel versions, determinism profile, redaction profile, and digest algorithm identifiers.
PinSetDigest: (\mathrm{Digest}(\mathrm{Enc}_A(\text{PinSet}))).
15.1.2 Pinned State and Event Streams
PinnedState is the minimal closure of artifacts required to interpret and replay a claim:
canonical forms (Ch05/AppA),
interpretation pins (AppD),
kernel/phase profiles (AppC),
corridor budgets and typing rules (AppG),
measurement/logging profile (AppI).
EventStream is an ordered sequence of records emitted under an MS:[\mathcal{E} = (e_0, e_1, \dots, e_{n-1})]where ordering is a total order defined by MS (not by ingestion time).
A Replay is the deterministic evaluation of:
canonical normalizers,
defect extraction,
TL evaluation,
repair attempt,
certificates verification,
using only ((\text{PinnedState}, \mathcal{E}, \text{Inputs})) and pinned tie-break rules.
15.2 Required Objects: Canonical Types
All required objects are defined as pinned, serializable types. Each type below includes:
canonical fields and invariants,
deterministic ordering constraints,
required digests.
15.2.1 Shared Primitive Types
Addressing primitives.
CorpusID: bytes16 (pinned identifier).
NodeID: bytes16.
EdgeID: bytes16.
FieldPath: canonical UTF-8 path with pinned normalization (AppA).
TimeIndex: u64 logical index (not wall-clock).
Address is a sum type:
AtomAddress = ({\text{corpus}: \text{CorpusID}, \text{node}: \text{NodeID}, \text{field}: \text{FieldPath}, \text{time}: \text{TimeIndex}})
EdgeAddress = ({\text{corpus}: \text{CorpusID}, \text{edge}: \text{EdgeID}, \text{time}: \text{TimeIndex}})
The canonical ordering on addresses is a pinned lexicographic order:[(\text{tag}, \text{corpus}, \text{node/edge}, \text{field?}, \text{time})]where tag orders AtomAddress < EdgeAddress (pinned).
Kernel/phase/control.
KernelID: bytes16.
PhaseID: enum ({\mathbf{P}, \mathbf{Q}, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{C}}) (stage injection points).
ControlProfileDigest: bytes32 digest of pinned control parameters.
Corridor typing.
TruthType: enum ({\mathbf{OK}, \mathbf{NEAR}, \mathbf{AMBIG}, \mathbf{FAIL}}) with pinned preorder:[\mathbf{OK} \succ \mathbf{NEAR} \succ \mathbf{AMBIG} \succ \mathbf{FAIL}.]
Corridor budgets.
BudgetVector: a fixed-key map (canonical field order) of nonnegative integers (u64):
measurement_budget_bytes,
measurement_budget_records,
repair_budget_steps,
repair_budget_search,
kernel_budget (optional, pinned by AppC),
quarantine_budget (optional, pinned by AppK/AppO).
CorridorClass: enum ({\mathbf{OK_CORRIDOR}, \mathbf{NEAR_CORRIDOR}, \mathbf{AMBIG_CORRIDOR}, \mathbf{FAIL_CORRIDOR}}).
Difference operator.
DiffOpID: bytes16 (pinned).
DiffReportDigest: bytes32.
A DifferenceOperator is a record:
diff_op_id: DiffOpID,
params_digest: bytes32 (digest of pinned params),
output_kind: enum (STRUCTURAL, SEMANTIC, TYPING, MIGRATION),
normalization_pins_digest: bytes32,
comparator_pins_digest: bytes32.
Its semantics are:[\mathrm{DiffOp}(L,R) \mapsto (\text{DiffReport}, \text{DiffReportDigest})]where DiffReport is not required to be stored in DS; DS stores the operator identity plus digests, and MS defines how to log any necessary report fragments.
15.3 DefectSkeleton (DS)
15.3.1 Definition
A DefectSkeleton is the minimal witness class explaining why two routes/representations disagree.
DefectSkeleton is a pinned serializable record:
ds_version: u32 (pinned),
pins_digest: PinSetDigest,
ds_kind: DSKind,
left_ref: ArtifactRef,
right_ref: ArtifactRef,
involved_addresses: sorted unique list[Address],
transform_context: TransformContext,
budget_context: BudgetContext,
difference_operator: DifferenceOperator,
witness_payload: DSWitnessPayload,
ds_digest: bytes32 (digest of the canonical encoding of the DS with ds_digest field zeroed).
Where:
ArtifactRef is:
artifact_digest: bytes32,
artifact_type: enum (ROUTE, REPRESENTATION, CLAIM, CANONICAL_FORM),
artifact_schema_digest: bytes32.
TransformContext is:
kernel_id: KernelID,
phase_id: PhaseID,
control_profile_digest: ControlProfileDigest,
determinism_profile_digest: bytes32,
interpretation_pins_digest: bytes32 (AppD),
canonicalizer_digest: bytes32 (Ch05/AppA).
BudgetContext is:
corridor_class: CorridorClass,
budgets: BudgetVector,
budget_profile_digest: bytes32 (AppG).
Well-formedness invariants.
involved_addresses are canonical-sorted and duplicate-free.
left_ref and right_ref are pin-consistent with transform_context.interpretation_pins_digest.
difference_operator normalization pins match transform_context canonicalizer pins.
ds_digest equals (\mathrm{Digest}(\mathrm{Enc}_A(\mathrm{DS}_\text{zeroed}))).
15.3.2 DS Kind System
DS must support the following defect families; each family has a canonical witness payload with additional invariants.
DSKind enum:
COMMUTATION_DEFECT
CARRY_HATCH_BOUNDARY_DEFECT
CORRIDOR_TYPING_DEFECT
MIGRATION_DEFECT
OTHER_DEFECT (reserved, requires explicit extension pin)
(i) Commutation Defect
A CommutationDefect asserts that two sequences of legal operations (words) that should commute or be equivalent are not.
Witness payload:
generators_digest: bytes32 (pinned generator set identifier),
word_left: list[GeneratorID],
word_right: list[GeneratorID],
word_ordering_pin: bytes32,
result_left_digest: bytes32,
result_right_digest: bytes32,
commutation_claim: enum (COMMUTE, ASSOCIATE, DISTRIBUTE, FUSE, OTHER),
minimality_trace_digest: bytes32 (optional but required when CE is minted).
Invariant. word_left and word_right are the canonical-minimal pair under:
shortest total length (|w_L|+|w_R|),
then shorter max length (\max(|w_L|,|w_R|)),
then lexicographic order by GeneratorID with pinned comparator,among all pairs producing the same diff class under the DifferenceOperator.
(ii) Carry/Hatch Boundary Defect
A Carry/HatchBoundaryDefect asserts that a disagreement arises at a legal recursion boundary (Ch14). These are structural boundaries, not bugs; legality is handled by boundary repair discipline.
Witness payload:
boundary_id: bytes16,
boundary_type: enum (CARRY, HATCH),
boundary_time: TimeIndex,
attempted_action: enum (RECURSE, INLINE, REWRITE_PAST, RECLASSIFY, OTHER),
boundary_clause_digest: bytes32 (digest of the boundary semantics statement),
observed_effect_digest: bytes32 (digest of minimal observed contradiction).
Invariant. attempted_action = REWRITE_PAST implies RS is empty (repair disallowed); CE obligation is immediate.
(iii) Corridor Typing Defect
A CorridorTypingDefect asserts that the same artifact is classified differently between corridors (OK/NEAR/AMBIG/FAIL), or that a classification is inconsistent with the evidence.
Witness payload:
left_type: TruthType,
right_type: TruthType,
typing_rule_digest: bytes32 (rule set in AppG),
evidence_plan_ref: EvidencePlanRef (required if either side is AMBIG due to insufficient measurement),
classification_trace_digest: bytes32.
Invariant. If DSKind = CORRIDOR_TYPING_DEFECT and identifiability cannot be met under MS bounds, left_type and right_type must both be AMBIG and an EvidencePlanRef is mandatory.
(iv) Migration Defect
A MigrationDefect asserts a schema/profile mismatch between left and right.
Witness payload:
schema_left_digest: bytes32,
schema_right_digest: bytes32,
profile_left_digest: bytes32,
profile_right_digest: bytes32,
migration_edge_kind_required: enum (MIGRATE, REF, DUAL),
mismatch_summary_digest: bytes32.
Invariant. MigrationDefect must be emitted immediately upon pin mismatch during extraction; no defect-word search is allowed prior to pin alignment.
15.4 TriggerLaw (TL)
15.4.1 Definition
A TriggerLaw is a predicate over pinned state and event stream that decides whether a DS can manifest.
TriggerLaw is a pinned serializable record:
tl_version: u32,
pins_digest: PinSetDigest,
scope: TLScope,
monotonicity: TLMonotonicity,
required_measurements: list[MeasurementKey],
predicate_ir: PredicateIR,
evidence_minimizer_ir: EvidenceMinimizerIR,
output_policy: TLOutputPolicy,
tl_digest: bytes32.
Where:
TLScope = enum {LOCAL, INTER_CORPUS}.
LOCAL: predicate may depend only on artifacts/events within one corpus closure (pinned by DS.left_ref.corpus).
INTER_CORPUS: predicate may depend on multiple corpora; must declare the corpus set in required_measurements.
TLMonotonicity =
MONOTONE with monotonicity_proof_digest, or
NON_MONOTONE with nonmonotonicity_witness_digest.
Monotonicity is defined over evidence extensions:Let (\mathcal{E} \preceq \mathcal{E}') mean (\mathcal{E}) is a prefix or a subset extension consistent with MS ordering (same record identities, additional records appended or inserted without reordering past records). A TL is monotone if:[\forall \mathcal{E}\preceq \mathcal{E}';:; \mathrm{TL}(\mathcal{E})=\text{TRIGGERED} \implies \mathrm{TL}(\mathcal{E}')=\text{TRIGGERED}.]
PredicateIR is a restricted, deterministic expression language:
total boolean evaluation,
only pinned primitives (integer arithmetic with pinned overflow rules, string/bytes comparisons with pinned collation, fixed-point if numeric),
no nondeterministic functions,
no iteration over unordered maps; all iterables must be sorted under pinned comparator before fold/reduce.
EvidenceMinimizerIR specifies the deterministic method for producing the minimal evidence slice used (see §15.8.2).
TLOutputPolicy fixes output behavior: verdict domain, obligations, and trace format.
15.4.2 TL Verdict Domain
A TL evaluation yields:
TLVerdict ∈ {NOT_TRIGGERED, TRIGGERED, AMBIG, FAIL}.
Definitions:
NOT_TRIGGERED: predicate evaluates to false with sufficient evidence.
TRIGGERED: predicate evaluates to true with sufficient evidence.
AMBIG: predicate cannot be evaluated or cannot be decided due to missing required evidence under MS bounds; generates obligations.
FAIL: evaluation violates determinism constraints, schema constraints, or trace integrity; generates fences/quarantine obligations.
15.5 MeasurementSpec (MS)
15.5.1 Definition
A MeasurementSpec defines what must be logged/emitted to:
reproduce the defect,
classify it under corridor rules,
support repair search.
MeasurementSpec is a pinned serializable record:
ms_version: u32,
pins_digest: PinSetDigest,
schema: MeasurementSchema,
ordering: MeasurementOrdering,
redaction: RedactionPolicy,
digesting: DigestPolicy,
bounds: MeasurementBounds,
ms_digest: bytes32.
Where:
MeasurementSchema is an ordered list of MeasurementField:
field_id: u32 (pinned),
name: canonical string,
type: MeasurementType (sum type),
required: bool,
semantics_digest: bytes32 (pins meaning, not prose),
emission_stage: PhaseID (P/Q/B/C),
privacy_class: enum (PUBLIC, SENSITIVE, SECRET).
MeasurementOrdering defines a total order key:
primary: (logical_time: TimeIndex, event_index: u64),
secondary: (emitter_id: bytes16, record_seq: u64),
tertiary: (field-stable tie-break: bytes32 digest of record payload).All comparisons are pinned and deterministic.
RedactionPolicy:
redaction_profile_digest: bytes32,
per-field action: KEEP | DROP | HASH | TOKENIZE,
hashing_salt_digest: bytes32 (salt is pinned; salt value is part of PinnedState; determinism requires identical salt under replay),
tokenization_dictionary_digest (optional, pinned).
Redaction must be deterministic and must preserve ordering keys (or explicitly define transformed ordering keys).
DigestPolicy:
hash_algorithm_id: bytes16,
domain_sep: bytes16,
record_digest_rule: digest of canonical encoding of the redacted record,
stream_digest_rule: Merkle fold in MS order with pinned arity and concatenation format.
MeasurementBounds:
max_records: u64,
max_bytes: u64,
max_fields_per_record: u32,
truncation_rule_id: bytes16 (pinned; truncation itself is observable and logged).
15.5.2 Bounded Measurement Plans and Identifiability Hooks
MS must support bounded identifiability. For each DSKind, MS must define a bounded plan sufficient to:
reproduce the difference operator outcome,
determine corridor typing,
decide TL under replay.
If bounded identifiability cannot be satisfied, DS must be retyped as AMBIG with an EvidencePlan obligation (AppL), and TL must yield AMBIG under missing evidence rather than hallucinating determinism.
15.6 RepairSpec (RS)
15.6.1 Definition
A RepairSpec defines the legal repair search space and legality constraints. A repair is a constrained, append-only transformation sequence.
RepairSpec is a pinned serializable record:
rs_version: u32,
pins_digest: PinSetDigest,
allowed_ops: ordered list[RepairOpSpec],
allowed_edge_kinds: set[EdgeKind],
allowed_stage_injections: set[PhaseID],
budgets_consumed: BudgetVector (upper bounds),
exit_criteria: ExitCriteria,
upgrade_requirements: UpgradeRequirements,
rs_digest: bytes32.
Where:
EdgeKind includes (minimum):
EQUIV (explicit equivalence edge),
DUAL (explicit dual interpretation edge),
MIGRATE (schema/profile migration edge),
REF (reference/deferral edge).Additional edge kinds require explicit pin extension.
RepairOpSpec:
op_id: bytes16,
stage_injection: PhaseID ∈ {P,Q,B,C},
preconditions_ir: PredicateIR (deterministic),
effects_ir: EffectIR (restricted, append-only graph operations),
budgets_delta: BudgetVector,
required_witnesses: list[WitnessSpec].
ExitCriteria maps a repaired artifact to a TruthType:
classifier_digest: bytes32 (AppG rule set),
required_measurements: list[MeasurementKey] (subset of MS),
tie_break: bytes32 (pinned).
UpgradeRequirements:
For any claim of upgrade AMBIG→NEAR or NEAR→OK, a RepairCert must include the required witness bundle types and must reference the exact MS slices used.
15.6.2 Append-Only Doctrine and Boundary Constraints
All repairs are append-only:
No deletion of prior nodes/edges.
No mutation of prior boundary semantics.
Any meaning-changing transformation must be expressed as explicit edges with witnesses.
Carry/hatch boundaries (Ch14) are not errors. Repairs may only attach new structure on the later time axis; they may not “edit past” boundary semantics.
15.7 CounterexampleArtifact (CE)
15.7.1 Definition
A CounterexampleArtifact is mandatory when TL triggers and RS cannot produce OK/NEAR under budgets, or when repair is disallowed.
CounterexampleArtifact is a pinned serializable record:
ce_version: u32,
pins_digest: PinSetDigest,
ds_digest: bytes32,
tl_digest: bytes32,
ms_digest: bytes32,
rs_digest: bytes32 (or zero if repair is disallowed),
evidence_slice: EvidenceSlice,
replay_recipe: ReplayRecipe,
fences: FenceSpec,
minimality: MinimalitySpec,
ce_digest: bytes32.
Where:
EvidenceSlice:
ordered list of redacted measurement records (as MS defines),
record_digests: ordered list[bytes32],
stream_digest: bytes32,
slice_bounds: bytes (records/bytes counters).
ReplayRecipe:
required_artifact_refs: list[ArtifactRef] (canonical forms, pins, kernels),
entrypoints: list[bytes16] (replay harness IDs),
deterministic_run_config_digest: bytes32.
FenceSpec (AppK/AppO interface):
quarantine_scope: enum (LOCAL, CORPUS, INTER_CORPUS),
quarantine_key: bytes32 (routes to quarantine ledger),
allowlist_conditions_ir: PredicateIR,
denylist_conditions_ir: PredicateIR,
notification_hooks: list[bytes16] (pinned endpoints),
containment_actions: ordered list[bytes16] (pinned actions).
MinimalitySpec:
minimality_order: pinned (addresses-first, then events, then fields),
minimization_trace_digest: bytes32,
minimality_claim: enum (CERTIFIED_MINIMAL, HEURISTIC_MINIMAL),
proof_obligations: list[bytes16] (if certified minimal).
15.7.2 Minimality Ordering
CE minimality is defined with respect to a deterministic partial order:
minimize involved_addresses cardinality,
then minimize evidence_slice record count,
then minimize evidence_slice byte size,
then minimize field set (drop optional fields while preserving reproduction),
tie-break lexicographically by canonical encodings.
A CE is certified minimal if the minimization algorithm exhausts all strictly smaller candidates under the partial order within budget and proves non-reproducibility for each.
15.8 Required Laws: Safety and Routability
The following laws are mandatory and enforce that defects are safe to route, replay, and govern.
15.8.1 Trigger Determinism Law
Under identical pins and identical inputs, TL evaluation is bitwise reproducible.
Formally, for any pinned state (S) and event stream (\mathcal{E}), define:[\mathrm{EvalTL}(S,\mathcal{E},\mathrm{TL}) \mapsto (\text{verdict}, \text{slice}, \text{trace_digest}, \text{obligations})]Then for any two executions (r_1,r_2) that both conform to pinned determinism constraints:[\mathrm{EvalTL}{r_1}(S,\mathcal{E},\mathrm{TL}) = \mathrm{EvalTL}{r_2}(S,\mathcal{E},\mathrm{TL})]byte-for-byte, including slice ordering and trace digest.
Enforcement. Any deviation is TLVerdict=FAIL and requires immediate fencing instructions in CE (or an interim fence artifact if CE is not yet formed).
15.8.2 Identifiability Law
A DS must be identifiable by a bounded measurement plan; otherwise it is retyped as AMBIG with an EvidencePlan obligation (AppL).
Let (\mathrm{Plan}(\mathrm{DS})) be the MS bounded plan associated with DSKind and pins. DS is identifiable if:
within MS bounds, the logged evidence determines the DSKind-specific witness payload and the DifferenceOperator outcome to the granularity required by corridor typing rules.
If not identifiable under bounds:
DSKind is set to CORRIDOR_TYPING_DEFECT with both sides AMBIG, or DS retains original DSKind but corridor class is forced to AMBIG_CORRIDOR and EvidencePlanRef is mandatory (pinned rule chooses which), and
TL must yield AMBIG when evaluation depends on missing evidence.
15.8.3 No Silent Repair Law
Any repair that changes meaning must be expressed as explicit edges (EQUIV/DUAL/MIGRATE/REF) with witnesses. Any attempt that cannot be witnessed must remain AMBIG or FAIL.
Let (\rho) be a repair sequence transforming artifact (A) to (A'). If the semantic interpretation class changes under pinned interpretation:[\llbracket A \rrbracket \neq \llbracket A' \rrbracket]then (\rho) must include at least one meaning-changing edge kind among {EQUIV, DUAL, MIGRATE, REF}, and the repair must emit witness bundles sufficient for verification.
If witnesses cannot be produced under RS constraints/budgets, the outcome is not upgraded; it remains AMBIG or FAIL, and CE is required when TL triggers.
15.8.4 Boundary Repair Discipline
Carry/hatch boundary events are legal structural boundaries. Repair may not edit past boundary semantics; it must attach new nodes/edges under append-only doctrine.
If a defect’s involved_addresses intersect a boundary clause region:
RS may only attach post-boundary edges/nodes,
any attempt to rewrite boundary semantics is illegal and results in RS rejection and CE obligation.
15.9 Required Constructions: Deterministic Algorithms
All constructions are deterministic algorithms with pinned tie-break rules.
15.9.1 Construction (A): Defect Extraction Pipeline
Input. Two routes or two representations (R_L, R_R) that purport to establish the same claim.
Output. Either:
an EQUIV witness (explicit equivalence edge bundle), or
a package ((\mathrm{DS}, \mathrm{TL}, \mathrm{MS}, \mathrm{RS?})) with CE obligation status.
Algorithm A.0: ExtractDefect
Pinned parameters.
Canonicalizer: (\mathrm{Canon}) (Ch05/AppA).
Interpretation pins: (\Pi) (AppD).
Kernel library and generator set: (\mathcal{K}) (AppC).
Corridor typing rules and budgets: (\mathcal{G}) (AppG).
Measurement profile: (\mathcal{I}) (AppI).
Procedure.
Normalize both sides.Compute canonical forms:[C_L := \mathrm{Canon}(R_L;\Pi), \quad C_R := \mathrm{Canon}(R_R;\Pi).]Emit normalization digests into provisional MS buffer (bounded).
Align interpretation pins.If ( \Pi_L \neq \Pi_R) (schema/profile mismatch detectable by AppD pins):
Emit MigrationDefect DS immediately:
ds_kind = MIGRATION_DEFECT,
witness_payload.schema/profile digests set accordingly,
difference_operator.output_kind = MIGRATION.
Construct TL/MS for pin mismatch triggers (see TL construction A.4).
Construct RS permitting only MIGRATE/REF/DUAL edges as pinned rules allow; if no legal path exists, mark CE obligation.
Compute difference and attempt EQUIV witness.Let ((\Delta, d_\Delta) := \mathrm{DiffOp}(C_L,C_R)) under DS.difference_operator.If (\Delta = 0) in the pinned difference algebra, emit an EQUIV witness bundle:
edge kind EQUIV,
witness references to canonical forms and comparison trace digests,
certificate hooks for Ch21 governance.
Defect-word / commutation isolation (operational defects).If the defect is operational (pinned classifier says COMMUTATION_DEFECT is admissible under observed (\Delta)):
compute candidate generator set (G) from (\mathcal{K}) and transform_context.
derive shortest defect word pair ((w_L,w_R)) using Algorithm A.1 (ShortestWordIsolator).
if found, set ds_kind = COMMUTATION_DEFECT and populate witness payload.Otherwise proceed to step 5.
For higher-order interaction/curvature defects, use the hypercube inclusion–exclusion extractor (\Delta_d) to isolate the pure (d)-way mode (Algorithm A.2).
Address minimization and skeleton formation.Produce involved_addresses as the deterministic minimal set sufficient to reproduce the diff class:
start from the union of addresses referenced by (\Delta)’s report fragments,
run deterministic minimization (Algorithm A.3) under budgets to eliminate irrelevant addresses while preserving repro.
Produce TL.Construct TL as a predicate over pinned state and the MS-defined event stream fields such that:
TL(TRIGGERED) implies DS can manifest under replay,
TL(NOT_TRIGGERED) implies DS cannot manifest under replay given evidence,
TL(AMBIG) for missing evidence within bounds,
TL(FAIL) for integrity/determinism violation.
Produce MS.Emit the MS schema sufficient to:
reproduce canonicalization and diff,
evaluate TL,
classify corridor type,
seed repair search (AppM).
Emit RS or CE obligation.If a legal repair corridor exists under corridor rules and boundary discipline:
emit RS defining legal ops, budgets, exit criteria, and upgrade requirements.Otherwise:
RS is empty or omitted (pinned rule),
CE obligation is asserted.
Deterministic tie-break rules.
Any set enumeration uses canonical ordering (addresses, generator IDs, event records).
Any choice among multiple minimal candidates uses lexicographic tie-break by canonical encoding digest.
15.9.2 Algorithm A.1: ShortestWordIsolator (Deterministic)
Goal. Find the canonical-minimal pair ((w_L,w_R)) of generator words producing a disagreement consistent with the DS difference operator.
Inputs.
generator set (G) (sorted by pinned order),
max_length (L_{\max}) from budgets,
canonical left form (C_L), right form (C_R),
difference operator (\mathrm{DiffOp}).
Output.
minimal ((w_L,w_R)) or NONE.
Procedure.
Enumerate word pairs in increasing total length (\ell = |w_L|+|w_R|) up to (2L_{\max}).
For each (\ell), enumerate pairs in pinned lexicographic order:
first by (|w_L|), then (|w_R|),
then lexicographically by word sequences (GeneratorID order).
For each candidate pair:
apply words via pinned kernel semantics:[X := w_L(C_L), \quad Y := w_R(C_R),]
compute (\mathrm{DiffOp}(X,Y)) and test whether it matches the target diff class under pinned equivalence-of-diffs.
Return first match.
This procedure is deterministic by construction.
15.9.3 Algorithm A.2: Hypercube Inclusion–Exclusion Extractor (\Delta_d)
Purpose. Isolate pure (d)-way interaction terms with an optimal term count (2^d).
Let (d\ge 1). Let (U={1,\dots,d}). Let each axis (i) correspond to a binary choice of applying an operation or enabling a feature/interaction component (\theta_i \in {0,1}). Define a function:[F : {0,1}^d \to \mathcal{V}]where (\mathcal{V}) is the pinned difference algebra (vector-like: supports addition and additive inverses under pinned rules; if not available, the embedding into such an algebra is part of pins).
Define the hypercube difference operator:[\Delta_d[F] ;=; \sum_{S\subseteq U} (-1)^{d-|S|},F(\mathbf{1}_S),]where (\mathbf{1}_S\in{0,1}^d) has ones on indices in (S) and zeros elsewhere.
Operational instantiation.
(F(\mathbf{1}_S)) is the result (or a measured scalar/feature of the result) when exactly the subset of operations/features indexed by (S) is enabled/applied under pinned control profile.
The extractor yields the pure (d)-way interaction residual.
Optimality (term count). Under the pinned model where isolating the pure (d)-way multilinear coefficient requires distinguishing all (2^d) subset combinations, any extractor that is exact for all multilinear functions requires at least (2^d) evaluations. Therefore (\Delta_d) is optimal in term count under the standard evaluation oracle model. (The formal proof is pinned as part of AppA’s extractor library and referenced by extractor_proof_digest in control pins.)
Determinism.
Subset enumeration is canonical (increasing subset cardinality, then lexicographic).
Signs are computed by pinned parity rules.
15.9.4 Algorithm A.3: Deterministic Address Minimization
Goal. Minimize involved_addresses while preserving reproducibility of the defect class under replay.
Inputs.
initial address set (A_0) (sorted),
reproduction predicate (\mathcal{R}(A)): “using only addresses (A) and the MS evidence slice bounds, DiffOp outcome remains in target diff class,”
minimization budget (B).
Procedure (addresses-first delta minimization).
Initialize (A := A_0).
For each address (a) in (A) in canonical order:
propose (A' := A \setminus {a}),
if (\mathcal{R}(A')) holds within remaining budget, set (A := A').
Repeat pass until no removals occur or budget exhausted.
Output (A) and a minimization trace digest (hash of decisions in canonical order).
This procedure is deterministic and produces a canonical fixed point under the budgeted greedy minimization rule.
15.10 Construction (B): Trigger Evaluation
A TL evaluation must output:
verdict,
minimal evidence slice used,
digest of decision trace,
required follow-up obligations if verdict is AMBIG/FAIL.
15.10.1 Algorithm B.0: EvalTL
Inputs.
pinned state (S),
event stream (\mathcal{E}) (as MS defines ordering and redaction),
TL.
Outputs.[(\text{verdict}, \text{slice}, \text{trace_digest}, \text{obligations})]
Procedure.
Validate stream integrity.
Check MS schema conformance, ordering totality, redaction determinism markers, and digest chain validity.
If any check fails: verdict = FAIL; obligations include fence trigger key + integrity repair plan id.
Extract required measurements.
Collect the subset of fields/records referenced by TL.required_measurements.
If missing under bounds: verdict = AMBIG; obligations include EvidencePlanRef and missing key list digest.
Evaluate predicate_ir deterministically.
Evaluate TL.predicate_ir under pinned semantics.
Record an ordered trace of evaluation steps (operator, operands digests, result).
Compute trace_digest as digest of canonical encoding of the trace.
Compute minimal evidence slice used.
Apply TL.evidence_minimizer_ir to derive the minimal slice sufficient to reproduce the predicate outcome under pinned replay.
Minimality is defined by a pinned partial order (records-first then fields), and computed deterministically.
Emit obligations.
If verdict = AMBIG: obligations include missing evidence keys, suggested measurement upgrades allowed by MS bounds extension policy, and any AppL EvidencePlan hooks.
If verdict = FAIL: obligations include fences/quarantine key and remediation hooks.
15.11 Required Certificates: Witness Bundles for Governance
Certificates are typed witness bundles consumable by later governance (Ch21). Each certificate is a pinned serializable type with a verification algorithm.
15.11.1 DefectCert
Purpose. Certify that DS is well-formed, pinned, and reproducible from referenced artifacts.
DefectCert fields:
cert_version: u32,
pins_digest: PinSetDigest,
ds_digest: bytes32,
ms_digest: bytes32,
reproduction_recipe_digest: bytes32,
reproduction_trace_digest: bytes32,
validity: enum (VALID, INVALID),
verifier_id: bytes16,
cert_digest: bytes32.
Verification algorithm.
Reconstruct DS from ds_digest reference.
Validate DS invariants (§15.3.1).
Execute defect reproduction using MS bounded evidence plan; confirm the DifferenceOperator yields the same diff class and the witness payload constraints hold.
Produce reproduction_trace_digest deterministically.
15.11.2 TriggerCert
Purpose. Certify TL determinism and trace digests.
TriggerCert fields:
cert_version,
