pins_digest,
tl_digest,
ms_digest,
evaluation_trace_digest,
evidence_slice_digest,
determinism_check_digest,
validity,
verifier_id,
cert_digest.
Verification algorithm.
Run EvalTL twice in pinned replay mode and confirm byte-for-byte equality of outputs (verdict, slice, trace_digest, obligations digests).
determinism_check_digest commits to both runs and their identicality.
15.11.3 CounterexampleCert
Purpose. Certify CE is minimal, replayable, and fenced correctly.
CounterexampleCert fields:
cert_version,
pins_digest,
ce_digest,
replay_trace_digest,
minimality_trace_digest,
fence_validation_digest,
validity,
verifier_id,
cert_digest.
Verification algorithm.
Replay CE using replay_recipe and evidence_slice; confirm DS difference reproduces and TL triggers (or evaluation yields the claimed FAIL with matching integrity failures).
Validate FenceSpec conformity to AppK/AppO interface pins.
Validate minimality claim:
CERTIFIED_MINIMAL requires exhaustive proof obligations within budget; otherwise INVALID or downgraded to HEURISTIC_MINIMAL under pinned governance rule.
15.11.4 RepairCert
Purpose. Certify that a repair sequence is legal under corridor budgets and produces the stated truth type.
RepairCert fields:
cert_version,
pins_digest,
rs_digest,
repair_sequence_digest,
budgets_consumed: BudgetVector,
pre_state_digest,
post_state_digest,
exit_type: TruthType,
required_witness_bundle_digests: list[bytes32],
verification_trace_digest,
validity,
verifier_id,
cert_digest.
Verification algorithm.
Check each RepairOpSpec legality (preconditions/effects under pinned IR; append-only).
Check budgets consumed do not exceed RS limits and corridor budgets.
Recompute exit criteria classifier under MS evidence; confirm claimed TruthType and any upgrade requirements are met.
If an upgrade is claimed, validate required witness bundles and explicit meaning-changing edges.
15.12 Routing Discipline: From Defect to Governance
A defect artifact package is routable when the following are satisfied:
DS, TL, MS are pinned and have canonical digests.
EvalTL is deterministic (Trigger Determinism Law).
DS is identifiable under MS bounds, or explicitly AMBIG with EvidencePlan obligations.
No repair is silently applied; all meaning changes are explicit edges with witnesses.
Boundary repair discipline is enforced; illegal repair attempts immediately yield CE/fences.
If TL triggers and no OK/NEAR can be produced under RS budgets, CE is mandatory and must include fences/quarantine instructions.
The routing key for governance is the tuple of digests:[(\mathrm{ds_digest}, \mathrm{tl_digest}, \mathrm{ms_digest}, \mathrm{rs_digest?}, \mathrm{ce_digest?})]which uniquely identifies the mechanized failure instance under pins.
Ch15⟨0032⟩ — Defect Skeletons and Trigger Laws
Ch16⟨0033⟩ — Unified State Vector and the (T_U) Step
[○Arc 5 | ○Rot 2 | △Lane Sa | ω=15]Workflow role: single coherent update of ○□△; invertibility where declared; checkpoints.Primary hubs: → AppA → AppN → AppO → AppI → AppM.
16.0 Purpose
Ch16 defines the single authoritative operational semantics for the machine-step of HD‑SCT:
One coherent step updates Square (□), Circle (○), and Triangle (△) under pinned profiles.
The step produces a replayable state trajectory with checkpoint digests.
This chapter is the bridge from “framework as geometry” to “framework as executable machine”.
Everything below is normative unless marked “NOTE”.
16.1 Required objects
16.1.1 Pin context (\Pi)
A pin is a reference to an artifact/spec whose digest uniquely determines interpretation.
Minimum pin set
The unified state must carry all pin digests required to interpret all subsequent operations, including:
(\pi_{\text{corridor}}) — corridor policy pin (Option A/B + any HD generalization parameters)
(\pi_{\text{router}}) — router table / routing semantics pin
(\pi_{\text{grammar}}) — grammar / admissible program surface pin
(\pi_{\text{enc}}) — canonical encoding pin (serialization + domain separators)
(\pi_{\text{env}}) — environment pin (runtime / platform / numeric model constraints)
(\pi_{\square}) — SquareStep profile pin
(\pi_{\circ}) — CircleStep profile pin
(\pi_{\triangle}) — TriangleStep profile pin
(\pi_{H}) — hash/digest algorithm pin (or hash suite pin)
(\pi_{\text{order}}) — step order pin (see §16.3)
(\pi_{\text{ckpt}}) — checkpoint policy pin
(\pi_{\text{rng}}) — RNG/seed derivation pin (if any stochasticity exists)
Rule: If any pin above is referenced by a replay capsule, it MUST be import‑verifiable (ImportCert, §16.8).
16.1.2 UnifiedState (S_{\text{total}})
A typed record combining □, ○, △ plus the pin context and step bookkeeping.
Canonical record shape (minimum)
[S_{\text{total}} ;=; \langleS_{\square},;S_{\circ},;S_{\triangle},;\Pi,;k,;R\rangle]
Where:
(S_{\square}) : Square carrier
(S_{\circ}) : Circle carrier
(S_{\triangle}) : Triangle carrier (default (\mathbb{Z}_3^3), or pinned HD generalization)
(\Pi) : pin context (digests, not just names)
(k \in \mathbb{N}) : current step index / tick
(R) : replay determinism state (e.g., RNG state or master seed material)
Hard requirement: The encoding of (S_{\text{total}}) used for digesting MUST be the pinned canonical encoding from (\pi_{\text{enc}}).
16.1.3 SquareStep operator (T_{\square})
A pinned operator on the square carrier.
Inputs: (S_{\square}), pinned square profile (\pi_{\square}), read‑views of other carriers as permitted, boundary bus (below), step seed material as permitted.
Output: updated (S_{\square}') and emitted boundary events.
Bijection declaration
SquareStep must declare exactly one of:
BIJECTIVE: a pinned inverse exists (T_{\square}^{-1}) under (\pi_{\square}), and is supplied (or reference-supplied) as a pinned artifact; or
NON‑BIJECTIVE: explicitly declared, including the precise information loss mechanism.
16.1.4 CircleStep operator (T_{\circ})
A pinned tick/carry operator on the circle carrier.
Inputs: (S_{\circ}), (\pi_{\circ}), boundary bus, permitted read‑views, step seed.
Output: (S_{\circ}') and carry events.
Replay obligation: carries MUST reproduce identically under replay given pins + seed + inputs.
If an inverse is declared, it must be pinned and replayable.
16.1.5 TriangleStep operator (T_{\triangle})
A pinned control update on Triangle carrier:
Default carrier: (\mathbb{Z}_3^3)
HD generalization: pinned by (\pi_{\triangle})
TriangleStep includes:
corridor policy (Option A/B as pinned in (\pi_{\text{corridor}}))
hatch/carry boundary interactions (how boundary events are absorbed/produced)
emissions that may constrain □ or interpret ○ carries
16.2 Boundary bus and interfaces
16.2.1 BoundaryBus (B)
To make “explicit interfaces” concrete, all cross‑carrier interactions pass through a typed boundary bus rather than hidden side effects.
Minimum bus fields:
(B.\text{carry}): ordered list of carry events (from ○, possibly transformed by △ policy)
(B.\text{hatch}): hatch/open/close boundary events (from △)
(B.\text{corridor}): effective corridor state / policy snapshot for this step (from △)
(B.\text{notes}): deterministic annotations (strictly pinned schema; used for transcript)
Ordering rule: event ordering inside each list is canonical and pinned (either via (\pi_{\text{enc}}) or a bus schema pin).
16.2.2 Read‑views (anti‑footgun rule)
Each substep receives:
its own carrier (mutable in the abstract)
read‑views of other carriers (immutable snapshots) as explicitly declared by profile pins
the bus (B) (read/write within declared subfields)
No substep may mutate another carrier directly.
This enforces “single coherent update” while still allowing pinned order semantics.
16.3 Unified step (T_U)
16.3.1 Order is pinned
Let (\mathcal{O}) be the ordered list of substeps (a permutation of ({\square,\circ,\triangle})).
Law (Order is pinned):
(\mathcal{O}) is contained in (\pi_{\text{order}}).
If (\mathcal{O}) changes, that is a MIGRATE event.
Normative default for Ch16⟨0033⟩
Unless overridden by (\pi_{\text{order}}) (i.e., you are explicitly migrating), the canonical order is:
[\mathcal{O}_{0033} = [;\circ \rightarrow \triangle \rightarrow \square;]]
Rationale (normative): ○ produces carries, △ consumes/mediates boundary interactions and corridor state, □ applies corridor‑constrained transformation.
(If your system already standardized a different order earlier, keep that—just pin it here. The key is: declare it and digest it.)
16.3.2 Definition of one unified step
Given pinned profiles and order, one step is:
[T_U(S_{\text{total}}, x_k) ;=; S_{\text{total}}']
Where (x_k) is the step input packet (possibly empty, but if present it is part of determinism).
Operational semantics (AppA→AppM)
AppA — Acquire & Assert
Verify all required pins exist in (\Pi).
Import/resolve pinned profiles (or ensure they are already resolved).
Verify pin digests match (ImportCert surface).
AppN — Normalize4. Canonicalize any inputs (x_k) under (\pi_{\text{enc}}).5. Derive step seed material:[\text{seed}k = \text{Derive}(\pi{\text{rng}}, R, k, \Pi)]Derive MUST be pinned and deterministic.
AppO — Operate (ordered substeps)6. Initialize bus (B \leftarrow B_0(\Pi)) (empty, with pinned schema/version).7. For each (u \in \mathcal{O}):
if (u=\circ): ((S_{\circ}, B, \ell_{\circ}) \leftarrow T_{\circ}(S_{\circ}, \pi_{\circ}, \text{seed}_k, x_k, \text{views}, B))
if (u=\triangle): ((S_{\triangle}, B, \ell_{\triangle}) \leftarrow T_{\triangle}(S_{\triangle}, \pi_{\triangle}, \text{seed}_k, x_k, \text{views}, B))
if (u=\square): ((S_{\square}, B, \ell_{\square}) \leftarrow T_{\square}(S_{\square}, \pi_{\square}, \text{seed}_k, x_k, \text{views}, B))
AppI — Integrate8. Apply any pinned end‑of‑step bus reconciliation:
corridor snapshot sealing
hatch/carry finalization rules
prohibition checks (e.g., “unconsumed carry” if policy demands)This reconciliation function is pinned (either part of (\pi_{\triangle}) or a dedicated pin).
AppM — Manifest9. Increment step index (k \leftarrow k+1).10. Emit deterministic transcript entry (\ell_k) (see §16.6).11. Possibly emit checkpoint digest(s) based on (\pi_{\text{ckpt}}) (see §16.5).
Return (S_{\text{total}}') where only carriers + bookkeeping changed, and (\Pi) remains pinned-identical (unless MIGRATE).
16.4 Required laws
16.4.1 Determinism under pinned environment
Law: Same pins + same seed material + same inputs ⇒ identical trajectory digests.
Formally, for any two runs (r_1,r_2):[(\Pi, S_{\text{total}}^{(0)}, {x_k}){r_1} = (\Pi, S{\text{total}}^{(0)}, {x_k})_{r_2}\Rightarrow\forall k,; D_k^{(r_1)} = D_k^{(r_2)}]
Where (D_k) are checkpoint digests defined in §16.5.
Environment pin (\pi_{\text{env}}) must cover all sources of nondeterminism that could affect results (numeric mode, concurrency model, etc.). If something cannot be pinned, it MUST be logged as a deterministic input (or forbidden).
16.4.2 Invertibility where declared
Let SquareStep declare BIJECTIVE with pinned inverse (T_{\square}^{-1}), and CircleStep declare an inverse (T_{\circ}^{-1}).
Then the unified step MUST provide either:
Inverse capsule for (T_U^{-1}), or
An explicit statement of why invertibility fails (e.g., △ corridor clipping / lossy policy), with truth typing impact.
Truth typing impact (minimum)
Each substep has a truth type:
(\mathsf{Bijective})
(\mathsf{LeftInvertible})
(\mathsf{RightInvertible})
(\mathsf{Lossy}(\text{reason}))
Unified truth type:
(\mathsf{Bijective}) iff all substeps are bijective and bus reconciliation is bijective.
Otherwise, the unified type is the meet/worst of the chain, and the reason must be attributable to a pinned policy.
16.4.3 Checkpoint integrity
Checkpoint digests are part of the witness surface.
If expected digest ≠ computed digest during replay: FAIL/CONFLICT.
The harness MUST report:
first mismatching step index,
expected vs actual digest,
pin digest summary,
transcript hash prefix (if enabled).
16.5 Checkpointing and digests
16.5.1 Digest function
All digests are computed using the pinned hash suite (\pi_H) and pinned encoding (\pi_{\text{enc}}).
Define:[\text{Enc}(S_{\text{total}};\pi_{\text{enc}}) \in {0,1}^*]
Checkpoint digest at step (k):[D_k = H_{\pi_H}(\text{"HD-SCT/Ch16/Checkpoint"} ;|;k ;|;\text{PinsDigest}(\Pi) ;|;\text{Enc}(S_{\text{total}}^{(k)};\pi_{\text{enc}}))]
Final digest (D_{\text{final}}) is either:
(D_{K}) (if final step is checkpointed), or
a separately domain-separated hash with “Final”.
PinsDigest((\Pi)) is itself a canonical, pinned encoding of the pin digest set.
16.5.2 Checkpoint policy (pinned)
(\pi_{\text{ckpt}}) defines:
checkpoint indices (explicit list) OR frequency (e.g., every (m) steps)
whether step‑0 (initial) is checkpointed
whether transcripts are also hashed into digests (optional but recommended)
16.6 Transcript and deterministic logs
16.6.1 Deterministic transcript entry
For each step (k), produce a transcript entry (\ell_k) with pinned schema:
Minimum fields:
(k)
(\mathcal{O}) (or hash pointer to (\pi_{\text{order}}))
(\text{seed}_k) commitment (not necessarily raw seed; can be a hash if secrecy matters)
boundary event summaries (counts + canonical hashes of event lists)
substep logs (\ell_{\circ}, \ell_{\triangle}, \ell_{\square}) in the exact execution order
checkpoint digest if produced at this step
Rule: transcript ordering is part of semantics. Reordering log fields is a MIGRATE unless schema pin keeps old order.
16.7 Required constructions (algorithms)
(A) Unified-step executor (reference algorithm)
Input: (S_{\text{total}}^{(0)}), step count (K), pinned profiles (resolved by pins), input stream ({x_k}).Output: (S_{\text{total}}^{(K)}), checkpoint digests, transcript.
Pseudo-code (normative structure):
ExecUnified(S_total, K, Profiles, Inputs):
AssertPinsPresentAndValid(S_total.Pi, Profiles)
transcript = []
checkpoints = []
for k in 0..K-1:
x = Inputs[k] // may be empty but must be deterministic
// AppN: normalize + seed
xN = Canonicalize(x, Pi.pi_enc)
seed = DeriveSeed(Pi.pi_rng, S_total.R, S_total.k, S_total.Pi)
// AppO: ordered substeps
B = EmptyBus(Pi) // pinned schema/version
for u in OrderFromPin(Pi.pi_order):
if u == "CIRCLE":
(S_total.C, B, logC) = CircleStep(S_total.C, Profiles.Circle, seed, xN, Views(S_total), B)
if u == "TRIANGLE":
(S_total.T, B, logT) = TriangleStep(S_total.T, Profiles.Triangle, seed, xN, Views(S_total), B)
if u == "SQUARE":
(S_total.Q, B, logQ) = SquareStep(S_total.Q, Profiles.Square, seed, xN, Views(S_total), B)
// AppI: reconcile bus
(S_total, B, logI) = ReconcileEndOfStep(S_total, B, Profiles)
// AppM: advance + log + checkpoint
S_total.k += 1
entry = MakeTranscriptEntry(S_total.k, Pi, seed, B, logC, logT, logQ, logI)
transcript.append(entry)
if ShouldCheckpoint(S_total.k, Pi.pi_ckpt):
D = CheckpointDigest(S_total, Pi.pi_enc, Pi.pi_H)
checkpoints.append((S_total.k, D))
finalD = FinalDigest(S_total, Pi.pi_enc, Pi.pi_H)
return (S_total, checkpoints, finalD, transcript)
(B) Replay capsule format (minimum)
Ch16 defines the minimal ReplayCapsule for unified steps.
Minimum ReplayCapsule fields
initial state: either embedded or hash pointer
pins (or pin digest set)
step count (K)
expected checkpoint digests ({(k_i, D_{k_i})})
expected final digest (D_{\text{final}})
deterministic logs (ordered) OR transcript hash commitment (depending on size)
A compact JSON-like schema:
{
"capsule_version": "Ch16⟨0033⟩",
"initial_state_ref": { "type": "embedded|hashptr", "value": "..." },
"pins_digest": "H(Pi)",
"pins": { "pi_corridor": "...", "pi_router": "...", "...": "..." },
"order_pin": "pi_order_digest",
"step_count": 1000,
"checkpoint_policy_pin": "pi_ckpt_digest",
"expected_checkpoints": [
{"k": 100, "digest": "D_100"},
{"k": 200, "digest": "D_200"}
],
"expected_final_digest": "D_final",
"transcript_mode": "full|commitment",
"expected_transcript_commitment": "H(transcript)" // if commitment mode
}
Replay harness requirements (normative)
A replay harness MUST:
Import/validate all pins referenced (ImportCert).
Reconstruct initial state.
Run ExecUnified for (K) steps.
Compare:
each expected checkpoint digest
final digest
transcript (full equality or commitment equality)
Output ReplayCert on success; FAIL/CONFLICT report on mismatch.
16.8 Required certificates
16.8.1 ReplayCert
Asserts that replay reproduces identical trajectory and digests.
Minimum contents:
capsule digest
pin digest summary
runner identity (and its env pin digest)
PASS/FAIL, and if FAIL: first mismatching step + expected/actual
16.8.2 RegressionCert
Covers boundary cases and edge conditions, at minimum:
carry cascades (○ multi-carry propagation)
hatch events (△ open/close transitions)
corridor clipping (△ lossy boundary if Option A/B dictates)
inverse edges (verify declared inverses; verify unified inverse capsule if applicable)
“empty input” vs “non-empty input” determinism
step-order invariance tests that MUST FAIL unless MIGRATE is invoked (guards against accidental reorder)
16.8.3 ImportCert
Importer/verifier validates:
every referenced pin exists
artifact digest matches
pin dependency closure is satisfied (e.g., square profile references encoding spec; must match (\pi_{\text{enc}}))
16.8.4 AuditCert
Deterministic audit reports suitable for deployment conformance:
deterministic transcript commitment
checkpoint digest list
pin digest list
MIGRATE boundary detection (order/schema/version mismatches)
16.9 Inverse capsule (when supported)
16.9.1 When (T_U^{-1}) exists
If all of the following hold:
(T_{\square}) is BIJECTIVE with pinned inverse
(T_{\circ}) has pinned inverse
(T_{\triangle}) is invertible under pinned corridor policy (no clipping / no lossy reconcile)
end‑of‑step reconciliation is invertible
Then define inverse order:[\mathcal{O}^{-1} = \text{reverse}(\mathcal{O})]and:[T_U^{-1} = T_{o_1}^{-1} \circ T_{o_2}^{-1} \circ T_{o_3}^{-1}](with the inverses aligned to the same pinned bus semantics).
16.9.2 If invertibility fails
The chapter MUST:
identify the exact pinned policy causing failure (e.g., “corridor clipping under (\pi_{\text{corridor}})”)
surface the truth type downgrade: (\mathsf{Lossy}(\cdot))
specify what witness is still guaranteed (e.g., forward replay determinism still holds)
16.10 Conformance checklist (for implementers)
This chapter is satisfied iff:
UnifiedState includes □, ○, △, step index, replay state, and full pin digest set.
Pinned order is declared and digest-bound; order change triggers MIGRATE.
Determinism: same pins+seed+inputs ⇒ identical trajectory digests.
Checkpointing: digest function + checkpoint policy are pinned; mismatch is FAIL/CONFLICT.
ReplayCapsule minimal fields are defined; replay harness is normative.
Invertibility: declared bijections provide inverses or explicitly downgrade truth typing.
Certificates: ReplayCert, RegressionCert, ImportCert, AuditCert are defined and emitted by the toolchain.
Ch17⟨0100⟩ — Transform Spine: (P→Q→B→C) as Universal Action Grammar
[○Arc 5 | ○Rot 2 | △Lane Su | ω=16]Primary hubs: → AppA → AppN → AppC → AppI → AppM
17.0 Normative Scope: Universal Action Grammar
This chapter defines the universal action grammar of HD‑SCT: every framework-permitted transformation SHALL be represented as a typed four-stage pipeline[\mathsf{P}\ \to\ \mathsf{Q}\ \to\ \mathsf{B}\ \to\ \mathsf{C},]with explicit pins, explicit stage state, and addressable artifacts at each stage. No transformation is well-formed unless it is fully placed into this spine with complete contracts and replay witnesses.
The spine is a compiler-grade contract system: it eliminates hidden degrees of freedom by requiring that all choice, phase, kernel selection, and corridor control enter only via declared injection points, represented as typed pins, and that all outputs are explicit addressable artifacts. Any transformation that cannot be uniquely assigned to one stage under the pinned interpretation rules SHALL be classified AMBIG and rejected from the deterministic lane unless explicitly routed through the ambiguity protocol in AppA/AppD.
17.1 Required Objects and Core Types
17.1.1 Canonical Serialization, Digests, and Addressing
Let (\mathsf{Ser}(\cdot)) be a canonical, deterministic, versioned serialization function (AppN) and (\mathsf{H}(\cdot)) be a cryptographic digest function.
Digest[\mathsf{Digest}(x) := \mathsf{H}(\mathsf{Ser}(x)).]
Addressable artifact reference[\mathsf{ARef} := \langle \textsf{kind},\ \textsf{schema_id},\ \textsf{digest},\ \textsf{size},\ \textsf{media},\ \textsf{loc}\rangle]where (\textsf{digest}=\mathsf{Digest}(\textsf{payload})), and (\textsf{loc}) is a retrieval locator (content-addressed store, bundle offset, or import container pointer).
Every artifact emitted by any stage MUST be represented by an (\mathsf{ARef}). The payload MAY be embedded or external, but the digest MUST correspond to the canonical serialized payload.
17.1.2 Pins, PinSets, and Pin Schemas
A pin is the unique injection mechanism for all choice and control.
Pin[\mathsf{Pin} := \langle \textsf{pin_id},\ \textsf{type_id},\ \textsf{value},\ \textsf{value_digest}\rangle]with (\textsf{value_digest}=\mathsf{Digest}(\textsf{value})).
PinSet[\mathsf{PinSet} := \text{finite map }(\textsf{pin_id} \mapsto \mathsf{Pin})]with uniqueness of (\textsf{pin_id}).
Pin schema[\mathsf{PinSchema} := \langle \textsf{type_id},\ \textsf{constraints},\ \textsf{canonicalization}\rangle]governing validation and canonical form (AppN).
All nondeterminism MUST be eliminated by requiring that every potential tie, kernel choice, phase ordering decision, corridor routing, and any data-dependent branch that could vary across implementations be determined by pins. Any stage executor that reads ambient environment (time, host entropy, unspecified iteration order) without pin mediation violates determinism and SHALL fail certification.
17.1.3 Stage State and Stage Artifacts
A stage produces:
stage output value (typed data flowing to the next stage),
stage state (structured, explicit; never implicit prose),
stage artifacts (addressable, replay-critical).
Stage state MUST be serializable under (\mathsf{Ser}) and MUST have a digest. Stage state MAY be emitted as an artifact (recommended), but at minimum MUST appear as a structured object inside the stage transcript.
Define a uniform stage transcript record:
StageTranscript[\mathsf{StageTranscript} :=\langle\textsf{stage},\ \textsf{stage_spec_digest},\ \textsf{input_digests},\ \textsf{pins_used},\ \textsf{state_digest},\ \textsf{artifacts},\ \textsf{output_digest},\ \textsf{invariants_claimed}\rangle.]
Each transcript MUST list exactly which pins were consumed and MUST include digests for inputs, state, and outputs.
17.1.4 PipelineSpec ((\Pi)) as Typed Composition
A PipelineSpec is the minimal typed object defining a spine instance:
[\Pi := \mathsf{C}\circ \mathsf{B}\circ \mathsf{Q}\circ \mathsf{P}.]
Formally, a PipelineSpec is a 4‑tuple of stage specifications with explicit types:
StageSpec[\mathsf{StageSpec} :=\langle\textsf{stage},\ \textsf{version},\ \textsf{executor_id},\ \textsf{type_in},\ \textsf{type_out},\ \textsf{pin_requirements},\ \textsf{artifact_kinds},\ \textsf{invariants}\rangle.]
PipelineSpec[\mathsf{PipelineSpec} :=\langle\mathsf{P_spec},\ \mathsf{Q_spec},\ \mathsf{B_spec},\ \mathsf{C_spec},\ \textsf{compatibility_proof}\rangle]where (\textsf{compatibility_proof}) attests that (\textsf{type_out}) matches (\textsf{type_in}) along the chain and that all required invariants are composable (ContractCert; AppC).
Stages MAY be identity stages, but identity MUST be explicit with a StageSpec and transcript; “skipping” a stage is represented as an identity stage with explicit invariants and empty artifact list.
17.2 Stage Interfaces and Required Artifacts
17.2.1 Common Interface Template
Each stage (\mathsf{S}\in{\mathsf{P},\mathsf{Q},\mathsf{B},\mathsf{C}}) MUST implement a deterministic partial function:[\mathsf{S} : (\textsf{Input},\ \mathsf{PinSet},\ \mathsf{ArtifactStore}) \to (\textsf{Output},\ \textsf{State},\ \textsf{Artifacts},\ \mathsf{StageTranscript})]subject to the determinism and contract laws (17.3–17.5).
The ArtifactStore is content-addressed: retrieval by digest MUST be deterministic and MUST validate payload digest.
17.2.2 Partition Stage ((\mathsf{P}))
Purpose. Decompose an input into explicit parts under a declared partition policy.
Input type. (\mathcal{X}) (framework input object, including imported containers already decoded when (\mathsf{C}^{-1}) exists).
Output type.[\mathsf{POut} := \langle \textsf{parts}:\mathsf{Parts},\ \textsf{pstate}:\mathsf{PState},\ \textsf{part}:\mathsf{PArt}\rangle.]
Parts.[\mathsf{Parts} := \text{finite sequence of }\langle \textsf{part_id},\ \textsf{payload_ref},\ \textsf{span_ref?},\ \textsf{attrs}\rangle]where (\textsf{payload_ref}) is an (\mathsf{ARef}) to the part payload and (\textsf{span_ref?}) optionally anchors provenance (source ranges, graph slices, object paths).
PState (required fields).[\mathsf{PState} :=\langle\textsf{partition_policy_id},\\textsf{ordering_policy},\\textsf{normalization_rules},\\textsf{part_index},\textsf{p_pins_consumed}\rangle.]
PArt (required artifacts).
(\mathsf{PArt.Man}): PartitionManifest (addressable): list of parts with digests, stable ordering, schema IDs.
(\mathsf{PArt.Prov}): PartitionProvenance (addressable): mapping from each (\textsf{part_id}) to source anchors and normalization steps (or explicit “none”).
(\mathsf{PArt.Inv}): PartitionInvariantReport (addressable): evaluation results of claimed invariants.
All three MUST be emitted as (\mathsf{ARef}) entries.
17.2.3 Quantize Stage ((\mathsf{Q}))
Purpose. Map parts into quantized units under an explicit quantizer and kernel policy. Quantization includes discretization, coding, normalization into finite alphabets, and any representation change that reduces or constrains degrees of freedom.
Input type. (\mathsf{POut}).
Output type.[\mathsf{QOut} := \langle \textsf{qunits}:\mathsf{QUnits},\ \textsf{qstate}:\mathsf{QState},\ \textsf{qart}:\mathsf{QArt}\rangle.]
QUnits.[\mathsf{QUnits} := \text{finite sequence of }\langle \textsf{qunit_id},\ \textsf{symbol_ref},\ \textsf{source_part_id},\ \textsf{attrs}\rangle]where (\textsf{symbol_ref}) is an (\mathsf{ARef}) to the quantized symbol payload (token, bin index, lattice coordinate, codeword, etc.).
QState (required fields).[\mathsf{QState} :=\langle\textsf{quantizer_id},\textsf{kernel_choice_id},\textsf{codebook_refs},\textsf{rounding_policy},\textsf{tie_break_policy},\textsf{q_pins_consumed}\rangle.]
QArt (required artifacts).
(\mathsf{QArt.Tab}): QuantizationTable (addressable): mapping parts → quantized symbols, including any residual policy.
(\mathsf{QArt.CB}): CodebookBundle (addressable): referenced codebooks and versions; MAY be empty if quantization is purely structural but then the quantizer MUST be fully specified in QState.
(\mathsf{QArt.Err}): QuantizationErrorCertificate (addressable): either (i) proof of losslessness / bijection, or (ii) explicit error bounds, distortion metrics, and irreversibility flag.
(\mathsf{QArt.Inv}): QuantizationInvariantReport (addressable).
The QuantizationErrorCertificate is mandatory: quantization invertibility is never assumed.
17.2.4 Bridge Stage ((\mathsf{B}))
Purpose. Bind circle/square/triangle interactions under pinned bridges, enforcing corridor constraints and resolving compatibility between phase (○), kernel (□), and corridor (△) decisions.
Let:
○ Circle phase be represented by a phase plan (\Phi) (ordering / staging / temporal or logical phases),
□ Square kernel be represented by kernel identifiers (K) (algorithmic operator choice / basis),
△ Triangle corridor be represented by corridor constraints (\Gamma) (allowed lanes, routing rules, admissible interactions).
Bridge constructs an explicit interaction structure consistent with pins and corridor rules.
Input type. (\mathsf{QOut}).
Output type.[\mathsf{BOut} := \langle \textsf{bstruct}:\mathsf{BStruct},\ \textsf{bstate}:\mathsf{BState},\ \textsf{bart}:\mathsf{BArt}\rangle.]
BStruct (minimal required form).[\mathsf{BStruct} :=\langle\textsf{nodes}:\mathsf{BNodes},\textsf{edges}:\mathsf{BEdges},\textsf{bindings}:\mathsf{Bindings}\rangle]where nodes include quantized units and bridge nodes; edges encode permitted interactions; bindings attach ○/□/△ semantics explicitly.
BState (required fields).[\mathsf{BState} :=\langle\textsf{phase_plan_ref},\textsf{kernel_binding_ref},\textsf{corridor_rule_ref},\textsf{bridge_policy_id},\textsf{conflict_resolution_policy},\textsf{b_pins_consumed}\rangle.]
BArt (required artifacts).
(\mathsf{BArt.Graph}): BridgeGraph (addressable): canonical graph encoding nodes/edges/bindings with stable ordering.
(\mathsf{BArt.Pins}): BridgePinWitness (addressable): minimal pin subset sufficient to reproduce all bridge choices (projection witness).
(\mathsf{BArt.Corr}): CorridorComplianceReport (addressable): proof or check result that all interactions respect corridor constraints (△Lane Su included as corridor parameterization).
(\mathsf{BArt.Inv}): BridgeInvariantReport (addressable).
Any binding decision (including selection among multiple admissible edges) MUST be justified by pins and recorded in BridgePinWitness. If two distinct bindings satisfy constraints and no pins discriminate them, the operation is AMBIG unless the conflict resolution policy is itself fully pinned.
17.2.5 Code Stage ((\mathsf{C}))
Purpose. Encode/serialize the bridged structure into containers and exportable artifacts.
Input type. (\mathsf{BOut}).
Output type.[\mathsf{COut} := \langle \textsf{container_ref}:\mathsf{ARef},\ \textsf{cstate}:\mathsf{CState},\ \textsf{cart}:\mathsf{CArt}\rangle.]
CState (required fields).[\mathsf{CState} :=\langle\textsf{container_format_id},\textsf{schema_bundle_ref},\textsf{encoding_policy},\textsf{compression_policy},\textsf{signature_policy},\textsf{c_pins_consumed}\rangle.]
CArt (required artifacts).
(\mathsf{CArt.Cont}): ContainerPayload (addressable): the exact serialized container bytes (or chunked bundle).
(\mathsf{CArt.Man}): ExportManifest (addressable): lists all included artifacts by digest, schema IDs, sizes, and roles; includes pipeline and stage transcript digests.
(\mathsf{CArt.Sig}): SignatureBundle (addressable): signatures, public-key identifiers, and verification chain if signing is enabled; else explicit “unsigned” record.
(\mathsf{CArt.Inv}): CodeInvariantReport (addressable).
The container MUST embed or reference sufficient information to permit import verification to reconstruct pins and validate all stage artifacts (ImportCert; AppI/AppM).
17.3 Required Laws
17.3.1 Stage Contract Completeness Law
For every operation (\tau) admitted into the HD‑SCT transformation set, there MUST exist a PipelineSpec (\Pi) and a pin assignment (\mathsf{PinSet}) such that execution yields transcripts (T_P,T_Q,T_B,T_C) satisfying:
Stage assignment completeness. Every effect of (\tau) is attributed to exactly one stage (\mathsf{P}/\mathsf{Q}/\mathsf{B}/\mathsf{C}) by the stage interpretation rules (AppA/AppD).
Pin consumption completeness. Each stage transcript lists all pins consumed; no hidden dependency is permitted.
Artifact emission completeness. Each stage emits the mandatory artifacts defined in 17.2, or explicit identity-stage artifacts where required.
Invariant declaration and preservation. Each stage declares invariants and supplies an invariant report artifact evaluating them.
A stage contract is a verifiable tuple:[\mathsf{Contract}(\mathsf{S}) :=\langle \textsf{pins_required},\ \textsf{pins_optional},\ \textsf{artifacts_required},\ \textsf{output_type},\ \textsf{invariants}\rangle]and MUST be included (by digest) in StageSpec.
17.3.2 No Cross-Stage Ambiguity Law
If an effect could be explained by more than one stage assignment, the framework SHALL force a unique assignment via pinned interpretation rules, otherwise the operation SHALL be classified AMBIG.
Pinned interpretation rules. A total decision procedure (\mathsf{AssignStage}(\tau,\Pi,\mathsf{PinSet})) MUST exist (AppA/AppD). If (\mathsf{AssignStage}) returns multiple admissible stage assignments and no discriminating pin exists that is declared in the relevant StageSpec, then the operation is AMBIG.
AMBIG prohibition. A pipeline run that is AMBIG MUST NOT produce a StageDeterminismCert nor PipelineReplayCert.
Dominance principle (normative default). In the absence of explicit override pins, stage assignment SHALL be the earliest stage capable of explaining the effect under the following dominance ordering:
Partition (structure of decomposition),
Quantize (representation / discretization / codebook mapping),
Bridge (interaction binding / corridor enforcement),
Code (serialization / packaging / export).
Overrides are allowed only when a dedicated, typed override pin is declared and consumed, and the override decision is recorded in the stage transcript.
17.3.3 Composability Law
Let (\Pi) be a PipelineSpec and let (R) be a run producing outputs with transcripts ((T_P,T_Q,T_B,T_C)). Composability requires:
Type composability. The output type of each stage matches the next stage’s input type.
Artifact referential integrity. Every reference digest in later stages MUST correspond to an artifact digest produced earlier or present in the ArtifactStore with verified digest.
Invariant composability. Invariants declared by earlier stages that are required by later stages MUST be explicitly listed as preconditions in later StageSpecs. Any invariant relied upon but not declared is a contract violation.
17.3.4 Invertibility Law and Witness Requirement
Invertibility is stage-local and MUST be witnessed.
A stage (\mathsf{S}) is invertible under pins if there exists a deterministic inverse executor (\mathsf{S}^{-1}) and an explicit witness (W_S) such that for all valid inputs (x) and pins (p),[\mathsf{S}^{-1}(\mathsf{S}(x,p),\ p,\ W_S) = x]and verification of digests succeeds.
No stage inversion is assumed.
If a stage is not invertible, it MUST emit an irreversibility witness describing what information is lost and what guarantees remain (e.g., error bounds in (\mathsf{QArt.Err})).
Invertibility of the full pipeline requires invertibility of each stage or an explicit global inversion witness proving that information is recoverable from later-stage artifacts.
Stage inversion witnesses MUST be addressable artifacts or embedded structured records with digests.
17.3.5 Injection Discipline Law for ○□△
Circle phase (○), Square kernel choice (□), and Triangle corridor decisions (△) MUST enter the pipeline only through declared injection points, implemented as pins.
A stage may only depend on ○/□/△ decisions if:
the corresponding pins are declared in StageSpec.pin_requirements, and
the pins are explicitly listed in StageTranscript.pins_used, and
the resulting decisions are recorded in the stage’s required artifacts (e.g., (\mathsf{BArt.Pins}), (\mathsf{QState.kernel_choice_id}), (\mathsf{BState.corridor_rule_ref})).
Hidden side channels are forbidden: ambient iteration order, filesystem ordering, network timing, and unspecified hash map traversal are prohibited dependencies unless pinned and canonicalized.
17.4 Deterministic Executors (Algorithms) Per Stage
All executors below are normative: they define required behavior classes. Implementations MAY vary internally, but MUST produce identical transcripts and artifact digests for identical inputs and pin assignments, under the same StageSpec version and canonicalization rules.
17.4.1 Deterministic Tie-Breaking and Canonical Ordering
A deterministic executor MUST eliminate unordered structure ambiguity by canonical ordering rules:
Any set of items MUST be converted to a sequence using a total order derived from canonical keys:[\textsf{key}(u) := (\textsf{schema_id}(u),\ \mathsf{Digest}(u),\ \textsf{stable_id}(u),\ \textsf{fallback_rank})]where (\textsf{fallback_rank}) is obtained from a declared tie-break pin if needed.
If two items share identical keys and are semantically distinct, the executor MUST require an explicit tie-break pin. Absent such a pin, the run is AMBIG.
17.4.2 Stage Executor: Partition ((\mathsf{P}))
Input: (x:\mathcal{X}), (\mathsf{PinSet}_P), storeOutput: (\mathsf{POut}), transcript
Algorithm (\mathsf{ExecP}):
Validate pins. Validate (\mathsf{PinSet}_P) against (\mathsf{P_spec.pin_requirements}) and canonicalize pin values.
Normalize input. Apply normalization rules specified by (\mathsf{PState.normalization_rules}) (either fixed by StageSpec or selected via pins).
Compute partition. Apply (\textsf{partition_policy_id}) to derive candidate parts.
Canonicalize ordering. Order parts using (\textsf{ordering_policy}); if ordering is underdetermined, consume a tie-break pin.
Emit part payload artifacts. For each part, serialize payload, store as (\mathsf{ARef}) with digest.
Build PartitionManifest and Provenance. Emit (\mathsf{PArt.Man}) and (\mathsf{PArt.Prov}) as addressable artifacts.
Evaluate invariants. Produce (\mathsf{PArt.Inv}) (e.g., coverage, non-overlap, provenance completeness).
Assemble transcript. Record input digest(s), pins used, state digest, artifact digests, output digest.
Determinism requirement: for fixed (x) and pins, the manifest and all part digests MUST be identical across runs.
17.4.3 Stage Executor: Quantize ((\mathsf{Q}))
Input: (\mathsf{POut}), (\mathsf{PinSet}_Q), storeOutput: (\mathsf{QOut}), transcript
Algorithm (\mathsf{ExecQ}):
Validate/canonicalize pins; ensure kernel choice pin presence if StageSpec declares alternative kernels.
Load referenced codebooks (if any) by digest; verify digests.
For each part in PartitionManifest order:
compute quantized symbol(s) using quantizer and kernel choice,
apply rounding policy,
if a tie arises (equal-distance codewords, ambiguous bin edges), consume tie-break pin and record the selected branch.
Emit QuantizationTable artifact mapping parts → symbols with digests.
Emit CodebookBundle artifact or explicit “none” record with full quantizer specification in QState.
Emit QuantizationErrorCertificate:
If lossless: provide bijection proof object and inverse lookup witness.
If lossy: provide explicit distortion metrics, error bounds, and irreversibility flag.
Evaluate invariants; emit QuantizationInvariantReport.
Assemble transcript.
Determinism requirement: all quantized symbols and QArt artifacts MUST be uniquely determined by pins; any unresolved tie yields AMBIG.
17.4.4 Stage Executor: Bridge ((\mathsf{B}))
Input: (\mathsf{QOut}), (\mathsf{PinSet}_B), storeOutput: (\mathsf{BOut}), transcript
Algorithm (\mathsf{ExecB}):
Validate/canonicalize pins; require explicit corridor rule pin if corridor is selectable.
Load phase plan (\Phi), kernel binding descriptors, and corridor rules (\Gamma) via digests or pin-selected canonical IDs; verify.
Construct candidate interaction graph:
nodes: all QUnits plus required bridge nodes (phase nodes, kernel nodes, corridor gate nodes),
edges: admissible interactions under (\Gamma) and (\Phi).
Resolve binding choices:
If multiple admissible edges/bindings exist, select using explicit pins (Bridge selection pins).
If selection remains underdetermined, classify AMBIG.
Canonicalize graph encoding (stable node IDs, stable edge ordering).
Emit BridgeGraph artifact and BridgePinWitness (minimal pin projection):
BridgePinWitness MUST contain exactly the pins necessary to reproduce every binding decision.
Emit CorridorComplianceReport:
either a proof object (if corridor rules are formalized) or a deterministic check log showing each constraint verified.
Evaluate invariants; emit BridgeInvariantReport.
Assemble transcript.
Determinism requirement: the exact graph encoding digest MUST be reproduced on replay given the same pins and same upstream digests.
17.4.5 Stage Executor: Code ((\mathsf{C}))
Input: (\mathsf{BOut}), (\mathsf{PinSet}_C), storeOutput: (\mathsf{COut}), transcript
Algorithm (\mathsf{ExecC}):
Validate/canonicalize pins; select container format and encoding policy.
Produce ExportManifest listing:
pipeline spec digest(s),
all stage transcript digests,
all artifacts (PArt/QArt/BArt plus any embedded state artifacts),
schema bundle digest(s).
Serialize container deterministically:
deterministic field ordering,
deterministic compression settings (if used, they MUST be fully pinned),
deterministic chunking (chunk size pinned if applicable).
Emit ContainerPayload artifact (bytes) and its digest.
Emit SignatureBundle:
If signing enabled: deterministic signature scheme with pinned key ID and canonical signing input.
Else: explicit unsigned record artifact.
Evaluate invariants; emit CodeInvariantReport.
Assemble transcript.
Determinism requirement: container bytes digest MUST be identical on replay given identical inputs and pins.
17.5 Pipeline Scheduler and Capsule Builder (Algorithms)
17.5.1 Pipeline Scheduler
The scheduler computes the required stage sequence and witnesses for a target operation (\tau). The universal spine always exists; the scheduler may assign identity StageSpecs where (\tau) does not affect that stage.
Define:
(\mathsf{StageImpact}(\tau)\subseteq {\mathsf{P},\mathsf{Q},\mathsf{B},\mathsf{C}}): stages affected by (\tau).
(\mathsf{RequiredPins}(\Pi,\tau)): pins required by StageSpecs selected for (\tau).
Algorithm (\mathsf{Schedule}(\tau,\textsf{policy})):
Determine candidate stage impacts using interpretation rules (AppA/AppD).
For each stage (\mathsf{S}):
if (\mathsf{S}\in\mathsf{StageImpact}(\tau)), select a StageSpec (\mathsf{S_spec}) compatible with (\tau) and policy;
else select identity StageSpec with explicit invariants and empty artifacts.
Construct PipelineSpec (\Pi) and compute (\mathsf{RequiredPins}(\Pi,\tau)).
If stage assignment is not unique under current pins and policy, return AMBIG classification with the set of discriminating pin types required to disambiguate.
Output (\Pi) and required pin schema list.
The scheduler MUST produce a compatibility proof (ContractCert input) that the selected StageSpecs compose and that all required artifacts for import are produced.
17.5.2 Capsule Builder (Replay Capsule Construction)
A replay capsule is the minimal self-contained object sufficient to reproduce a pipeline run and verify the output digests.
Define:
ReplayCapsule[\mathsf{Capsule} :=\langle\textsf{pipeline_spec_digest},\textsf{pinset_digest},\textsf{pins},\textsf{input_refs},\textsf{artifact_closure},\textsf{expected_transcripts},\textsf{expected_output_digests},\textsf{verification_policy}\rangle.]
(\textsf{artifact_closure}) MUST include every artifact required to replay the run (or content-addressed locators whose retrieval is itself deterministic and verified by digest).
Algorithm (\mathsf{BuildCapsule}(R)) for a completed run (R):
Collect PipelineSpec digest and canonical pinset (including pin schemas).
Collect all StageTranscripts and required artifacts:
include (\mathsf{PArt.}), (\mathsf{QArt.}), (\mathsf{BArt.}), (\mathsf{CArt.}),
include any codebooks, phase plans, corridor rules, schema bundles by digest.
Compute artifact closure by transitive digest references from manifests.
Record expected transcript digests and final container digest.
Output capsule as an addressable artifact and emit its digest.
Capsules are the primary witnesses for PipelineReplayCert.
17.6 Required Certificates (Schemas and Verification)
All certificates are explicit, addressable, and verifiable objects (AppC). A certificate is valid only if its verification procedure succeeds deterministically.
17.6.1 StageDeterminismCert
A StageDeterminismCert attests that a stage executor is deterministic under declared pins and canonicalization.
StageDeterminismCert[\mathsf{StageDeterminismCert} :=\langle\textsf{stage_spec_digest},\textsf{pin_schema_digests},\textsf{canonicalization_digest},\textsf{tie_break_rules_digest},\textsf{determinism_statement},\textsf{verification_procedure_id},\textsf{proof_or_test_evidence_refs}\rangle.]
Verification (\mathsf{VerifyStageDet}(cert)) MUST check:
StageSpec and pin schemas exist and validate.
Canonicalization and tie-break rules are total (no unpinned branch remains).
Evidence is sufficient under policy: either formal proof object or deterministic conformance test suite with fixed seeds pinned and recorded.
A StageSpec lacking StageDeterminismCert SHALL be treated as non-certified and SHALL NOT be used in deterministic lanes.
17.6.2 PipelineReplayCert
A PipelineReplayCert attests that the full (\mathsf{P}\to\mathsf{Q}\to\mathsf{B}\to\mathsf{C}) chain replays identically.
PipelineReplayCert[\mathsf{PipelineReplayCert} :=\langle\textsf{capsule_ref},\textsf{pipeline_spec_digest},\textsf{stage_transcript_digests},\textsf{final_output_digest},\textsf{replay_verification_log_ref}\rangle.]
Verification (\mathsf{VerifyReplay}(cert)):
Load capsule, validate all included digests and pin schemas.
Execute stages deterministically using the StageSpecs referenced.
Recompute transcripts and output digests.
Accept iff all transcript digests and final output digest match capsule expectations.
Replay verification MUST be performed without external side effects not captured by artifacts (no network fetch unless digest-verified and declared in the capsule closure).
17.6.3 ContractCert
A ContractCert attests that stage contracts are complete and compatible with corridor rules and composability laws.
ContractCert[\mathsf{ContractCert} :=\langle\textsf{pipeline_spec_digest},\textsf{stage_contract_digests},\textsf{type_compatibility_proof_ref},\textsf{invariant_compatibility_proof_ref},\textsf{corridor_rule_digest},\textsf{verification_log_ref}\rangle.]
Verification MUST establish:
Each StageSpec declares required pins and artifacts (completeness).
The composed types match.
Any invariant required downstream is declared upstream and verified upstream.
Corridor compliance requirements appear explicitly in Bridge StageSpec and are satisfied by BArt.Corr.
17.6.4 ImportCert
An ImportCert attests that import verification reconstructs pins and validates all stage artifacts from a container.
ImportCert[\mathsf{ImportCert} :=\langle\textsf{container_digest},\textsf{export_manifest_digest},\textsf{reconstructed_pinset_digest},\textsf{artifact_verification_log_ref},\textsf{schema_verification_log_ref}\rangle.]
Verification (\mathsf{VerifyImport}(container)) (AppI/AppM):
Decode container deterministically per (\textsf{container_format_id}).
Load ExportManifest; verify its digest and that it lists all expected stage transcript digests and artifact digests.
Reconstruct pins:
pins MUST be present explicitly or reconstructible from manifest + declared pin witness artifacts (notably (\mathsf{BArt.Pins})),
reconstructed pinset digest MUST match the manifest-stated pinset digest if provided.
Verify every artifact payload digest matches its reference.
Verify schema bundle and stage specs digests; verify signatures if present.
Output ImportCert and accept only if all checks succeed.
Import MUST NOT rely on implicit defaults; any missing pin required by StageSpec is an import failure.
17.7 Universal Action Grammar: Semantic Normal Form
A transformation in HD‑SCT is in spine normal form if it is represented by:[R = \langle \Pi,\ \mathsf{PinSet},\ x,\ T_P,T_Q,T_B,T_C,\ \mathsf{Capsule}\rangle]such that:
(\Pi) is a valid PipelineSpec with ContractCert.
Every stage spec in (\Pi) has a StageDeterminismCert.
Execution produces transcripts (T_*) whose digests match the capsule.
(\mathsf{VerifyReplay}) succeeds yielding PipelineReplayCert.
(\mathsf{VerifyImport}) succeeds on the exported container yielding ImportCert.
This normal form is the universal action grammar of the framework: any admissible operation is equivalent to exactly one spine normal form instance up to identity-stage substitution and canonical pin projection.
17.8 Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
17.8.1 Mandatory Stage Outputs
For each stage (\mathsf{S}\in{\mathsf{P},\mathsf{Q},\mathsf{B},\mathsf{C}}), a valid run MUST emit:
StageTranscript with: stage, stage_spec_digest, input_digests, pins_used, state_digest, artifacts[], output_digest, invariants_claimed.
Stage state as a structured serializable record with digest.
Required artifacts:
Partition ((\mathsf{P})): PartitionManifest, PartitionProvenance, PartitionInvariantReport.Quantize ((\mathsf{Q})): QuantizationTable, CodebookBundle (or explicit none with full quantizer spec), QuantizationErrorCertificate, QuantizationInvariantReport.Bridge ((\mathsf{B})): BridgeGraph, BridgePinWitness, CorridorComplianceReport, BridgeInvariantReport.Code ((\mathsf{C})): ContainerPayload, ExportManifest, SignatureBundle (or explicit unsigned record), CodeInvariantReport.
All artifacts MUST be addressable by digest ((\mathsf{ARef})).
17.8.2 Mandatory Laws
Contract completeness: stage assignment, pins consumed, artifacts emitted, invariants preserved are explicit.
No cross-stage ambiguity: unique stage assignment enforced by pinned interpretation rules; else AMBIG.
Composability: types, artifact references, and invariants compose along (\mathsf{P}\to\mathsf{Q}\to\mathsf{B}\to\mathsf{C}).
Invertibility is witnessed: never assumed; losslessness/irreversibility is certified.
Injection discipline: ○ phase, □ kernel, △ corridor decisions only via declared pins; no side channels.
17.8.3 Mandatory Algorithms
(\mathsf{ExecP},\mathsf{ExecQ},\mathsf{ExecB},\mathsf{ExecC}): deterministic, canonical ordering, pinned tie-breaks, emit required artifacts and transcripts.
(\mathsf{Schedule}(\tau,\textsf{policy})): select StageSpecs (including identity) and required pin schemas; return AMBIG if not uniquely stage-assignable under pins.
(\mathsf{BuildCapsule}(R)): compute artifact closure and expected transcript/output digests; emit replay capsule.
17.8.4 Mandatory Certificates
StageDeterminismCert per stage spec: verifies determinism under pins.
ContractCert per pipeline spec: verifies completeness + compatibility + corridor alignment.
PipelineReplayCert: verifies replay identical to capsule.
ImportCert: verifies import reconstructs pins and validates all artifacts.
All certificates are addressable artifacts with deterministic verification procedures.
Ch17⟨0100⟩ — Transform Spine: (P→Q→B→C) as Universal Action Grammar
Ch18⟨0101⟩ — Integration: Buckets, Codes, Containers, and Replay
[○Arc 5 | ○Rot 2 | △Lane Me | ω=17]Workflow role: bucket invertibility; coder determinism; container self-description; salvage/seek.Primary hubs: → AppA → AppN → AppF → AppI → AppM.
Chapter intent
Ch18 turns the pipeline into a distributable artifact system: stable containers that can be exported, imported, and verified without “implicit context.” A container must carry everything needed to prove:
Deterministic encoding (given pins)
Deterministic decoding (given pins)
Explicit pinned dependencies (bucket rules, codebooks/coders, schema/toolchain)
Salvage doctrine for corruption (typed + truth-scoped outcomes)
Replay harness expectations (what it means to “replay” and what must match)
Compatibility + migration with explicit edges (no silent upgrades)
Certificates are not “reports”; they are first-class objects that participate in verification.
18.1 Core objects (minimum required set)
18.1.1 Bucket
A Bucket is an explicitly declared partition structure over some domain of items (records, tokens, nodes, segments, events, etc.). It exists to:
Assign each item to a bucket (partition)
Enable invertibility when declared: reconstruct membership deterministically
Required fields
BucketID: stable name
Domain: what items it partitions
Partition rule: canonical function (or rule set)
Invertibility declaration:
invertible: true|false
If true: required inverse rule / reconstruction recipe
If false: explicit failure modes + expected loss semantics
Bucket law: invertibility where declared
If invertible: true, then for all items in scope, the bucket must support:
bucket_of(x) is deterministic under pins
items_in(bucket) (or reconstruction mechanism) is deterministic under pins
The composition must be identity on declared scope:
x ∈ items_in(bucket_of(x))
If a bucket is not invertible, the container MUST declare:
what information is discarded,
whether loss is bounded,
which verification claims are weakened.
18.1.2 Codebook / Coder tables
A Codebook is a pinned mapping that makes encoding/decoding deterministic. A Coder is the executable implementation constrained by the pinned codebook.
Required properties
Deterministic: same inputs + same pins ⇒ same outputs
Pinned: codebook and coder are referenced by digest and versioned identity
Totality and failure modes are explicit:
Unknown symbol handling
Out-of-range values
Overflow/underflow semantics
“Reserved” codes policy
Coder determinism law
Given:
payload P
pins Π including bucket rules + codebooks + coder identities + canonicalization rules
Then:
encode(P, Π) MUST be bitwise deterministic
decode(encode(P, Π), Π) MUST be deterministic
Any nondeterminism (threading, ordering, locale, float mode, random seeds) MUST be pinned or forbidden.
18.1.3 Container
A Container is a self-describing bundle:
manifest + payload + pins + witnesses + certificates
It is not “a file.” It is an artifact with explicit identity and verifiability.
Container invariants
A container MUST:
Describe itself (schema version, layout, canonicalization rules)
Carry an explicit pin manifest
Carry digests for integrity
Provide verification hooks (witnesses + replay harness expectations)
Reject ambiguous interpretation
18.1.4 Replay harness specification
A Replay Harness defines the import-verifiable procedure for decoding and checking claims.
It specifies:
Required pins and acceptable pin ranges (or exact digests)
Deterministic runtime assumptions (or recorded execution traces)
What constitutes “match” (exact bytes, structural equality, tolerances)
What digests must match (manifest, payload chunks, decoded structure, derived outputs)
Import verification MUST validate pins and replays before acceptance.
18.1.5 Compatibility matrix + migration tools
A container ecosystem MUST include:
A compatibility matrix: which decoder/harness versions can accept which container schema versions
Explicit MIGRATE edges:
MIGRATE(vA → vB) is a named, versioned tool
No silent upgrades during import
If migration is needed, import must fail with an actionable migration path
18.2 Required laws
18.2.1 Deterministic encoding/decoding under pins
For any container C with pins Π:
Encode(Decoded(C), Π) must reproduce the same canonical payload bytes (or produce a canonical-equivalent payload under the container’s canonicalization law).
Decode(Payload(C), Π) must reproduce the same decoded structure and derived outputs as claimed by witnesses/certs.
If this cannot be achieved, the container type is invalid for distributable artifacts.
18.2.2 Bucket invertibility and declared failure modes
Buckets must obey their invertibility declarations, and any non-invertibility must:
be declared in manifest
have typed failure modes
propagate into certificate truth scopes (see Salvage + Truth below)
18.2.3 Salvage outcomes are typed and truth-scoped
Corruption handling must not be hand-wavy. Every salvage attempt yields a typed result:
OK: fully verified, no salvage needed
NEAR: partially recovered, with bounded uncertainty
FAIL: not recoverable to any meaningful verified claim
“Truth-scoped” means: each claim in the container becomes one of:
Proven true (verified by digest/replay)
Unknown (missing/uncertain but not contradicted)
Proven false (digest mismatch / replay mismatch)
A salvage pipeline MUST produce a structured report that separates these scopes.
18.2.4 Import verification validates pins + replay before acceptance
An importer MUST:
Parse manifest (schema validation)
Validate pin manifest (all required pins present; digests match)
Validate payload integrity (chunk digests, Merkle root, etc.)
Validate certificates/witnesses per policy
Execute replay harness (or verify recorded replay proof) per policy
Only then: mark container as accepted/imported
If any step fails, import fails with a typed error (no partial silent acceptance).
18.3 Required constructions
18.3.1 Encoder
Encoder takes canonical source structure S plus pins Π and produces:
Payload: encoded bytes (chunked)
Manifest: self-description + layout + digests
Pins: explicit pin manifest
Witnesses: replay inputs/outputs as required
Initial certificates (at least ExportCert; optionally ReplayCert)
Encoder must enforce:
canonical ordering rules,
canonical serialization rules,
deterministic bucket assignment,
deterministic codebook usage.
18.3.2 Decoder
Decoder takes (Manifest, Payload, Pins) and produces decoded structure S'.
Decoder must:
refuse to run without required pins
refuse ambiguous versions
surface typed errors (pin missing, digest mismatch, schema mismatch, unsupported version, replay mismatch)
18.3.3 Verifier
Verifier is a policy-driven checker. Minimal verifier behavior:
Verify pins by digest
Verify payload chunk digests (and root digest if present)
Verify manifest digest (if the manifest is itself signed/digested)
Verify certificate chains
Verify replay claims using harness rules
A verifier produces a VerificationReport with:
pass/fail
which claims are verified
which are unknown
which are disproven
18.3.4 Salvage pipeline
The salvage pipeline runs when integrity checks fail.
Salvage phases (required)
TriageIdentify corrupted regions: which chunks/digests mismatch, which pins missing, which certificate proofs broken.
Seek (salvage/seek doctrine)Attempt recovery using redundancy:
mirrored chunks
erasure coding (if used)
witness bundles (e.g., decoded summaries)
replay traces (if they include sufficient reconstruction material)
Rebuild candidate containerProduce a new container candidate C* with:
replaced/recovered chunks marked
explicit salvage annotations
updated digests
salvage certificate (or salvage section inside ReplayCert/ExportCert)
Truth-scope classificationMark each claim as true/unknown/false with reasons.
Salvage output type (required)
SalvageResult = { status: OK|NEAR|FAIL, report: SalvageReport, candidate_container?: C* }
18.3.5 Migration tools
Migration is explicit. A migration tool:
takes container schema version v_old
outputs container schema version v_new
preserves claims only where provable
emits a migration witness bundle and a compatibility certificate update
No silent upgrades: a decoder may suggest migration but must not silently do it.
18.4 Container format (normative expectations)
18.4.1 Self-description: Manifest
The manifest is the “constitution” of the container. It MUST include at least:
container_schema_version
payload_layout (chunking rules, ordering, compression/encryption declarations)
canonicalization_rules (ordering, numeric/text normalization rules, endianness, float mode if relevant)
bucket_spec references (by digest + semantic ID)
codebook/coder references (by digest + semantic ID)
pin_manifest_digest
payload_digest_root (or list of chunk digests)
witness_index (what witnesses exist and where)
certificate_index
Manifest must be canonicalizable
Manifest serialization must be deterministic. Whatever format you use, the spec must define:
canonical key ordering
canonical number formatting
canonical string normalization (if any)
canonical whitespace/encoding rules
If manifest canonicalization is not defined, deterministic encoding cannot be proven.
18.4.2 Pins
Pins are the explicit dependency lock. A pin manifest includes:
Bucket specs (rules, versions, digests)
Codebooks (tables, versions, digests)
Coder implementations (artifact digests)
Harness spec (digest)
Any runtime constraints that affect determinism (e.g., float mode, locale, seed, algorithm flags)
Pins are not optional metadata; they are part of the artifact’s identity.
18.4.3 Witness bundles
Witnesses are the minimal additional data needed to prove claims without relying on external context.
Examples:
expected decoded digest(s)
sample replay traces
derived output digests
minimal test vectors for coder tables
bucket reconstruction checks
Witnesses must be explicitly scoped:
what they prove
what they do not prove
18.5 Replay harness expectations
18.5.1 Harness contract
The replay harness defines:
Inputs:
container (manifest + payload + pins)
policy (strictness level)
Procedure:
verify pins
verify integrity
decode deterministically
run specified checks (bucket inversion checks, codebook test vectors, derived output reproduction)
Outputs:
ReplayReport
ReplayCert (if issued)
18.5.2 Replay matching modes (recommended)
Define at least two modes:
Strict mode: bitwise-equal payload and bitwise-equal derived outputs.
Structural mode: semantic equivalence of decoded structure + digest equality of canonicalized decoded form.
If “tolerances” exist (floats), they must be pinned and explicitly declared. Otherwise, they are a determinism violation.
18.6 Compatibility + migration
18.6.1 Compatibility matrix (required)
Provide a matrix mapping:
container schema versions ↔ decoder versions
harness versions ↔ certificate versions
bucket/codebook schema ↔ coder versions
The matrix must explicitly say:
supported
unsupported
supported with migration (and which MIGRATE edge applies)
18.6.2 Migration edges (required)
A MIGRATE edge is an object with:
from_version
to_version
tool_id
tool_digest
preservation_claims (what is guaranteed preserved)
known_losses (what may be dropped or reinterpreted)
witness_requirements (what must be provided for migration)
post_migration_verification (what must be rechecked)
Importers must never apply migration implicitly.
18.7 Certificates (first-class objects)
All certificates share a common skeleton:
cert_type
cert_version
subject_container_digest
pins_digest
harness_digest (if applicable)
claims (typed)
witness_bundle (or pointer to witnesses)
issued_at
issuer_id (tool identity; pinned)
signature (optional but recommended if you support trust domains)
18.7.1 ExportCert (required)
Purpose: attests the container is a valid export artifact.
Minimum claims:
Manifest canonicalization succeeded
Pins are complete and pinned
Payload digests match manifest declarations
Required objects exist (bucket, codebook/coder, container layout, harness spec)
Witness bundle expectations:
manifest digest
pins digest
payload root digest
codebook test vectors (minimal)
18.7.2 ReplayCert (required)
Purpose: attests a replay was performed (or cryptographically proven) and matched expectations.
Minimum claims:
Verified pins (digests match)
Decoded deterministically under harness
Produced expected decoded digest(s)
Bucket inversion checks passed where declared invertible
Codebook/coder test vectors passed
Witness bundle expectations:
harness ID + digest
decoded canonical digest(s)
replay trace summary (or full trace if policy requires)
environment pins relevant to determinism
18.7.3 RegressionCert (required)
Purpose: attests this container matches a baseline (or set of baselines) under specified regression rules.
Minimum claims:
Baseline identifiers and digests
Comparison method (strict/structural/metric-based) pinned
Result: pass/fail with deltas
Witness bundle expectations:
baseline digests
diff artifacts (or digested diff summaries)
metric outputs if relevant
18.7.4 CompatCert (required)
Purpose: attests compatibility assertions between container versions and decoder/harness versions.
Minimum claims:
Supported decoder/harness versions
Required MIGRATE edges for unsupported pairs
No silent upgrade rule enforced
Witness bundle expectations:
compatibility matrix snapshot digest
migration tool digests where applicable
18.8 Import acceptance procedure (normative)
An importer must implement:
Parse + validate manifest schema
Verify manifest canonical digest (if declared)
Verify pin manifest
all required pins present
digests match
no unpinned required dependency
Verify payload integrity
chunk digests match
root digest matches
Verify ExportCert (required)
Verify ReplayCert (required for acceptance)
either run harness locally, or verify a replay proof accepted by policy
Verify compatibility
if unsupported: fail with explicit MIGRATE edge suggestion
Accept container and record VerificationReport
Any failure must produce a typed error:
PIN_MISSING
PIN_DIGEST_MISMATCH
PAYLOAD_DIGEST_MISMATCH
UNSUPPORTED_SCHEMA_VERSION
MIGRATION_REQUIRED
REPLAY_MISMATCH
BUCKET_INVERSION_FAILED
CODEBOOK_VECTOR_FAILED
CERT_INVALID / CERT_MISSING
18.9 Relationship to pipeline hubs (AppA→AppN→AppF→AppI→AppM)
Ch18 is where the multi-app pipeline becomes artifact-stable:
AppA/AppN: produce or transform structures that must be bucketed deterministically
AppF/AppI: finalize encoding rules and enforce pin completeness
AppM: import/verify/replay authority (or the canonical importer)
The “integration” contract is: no stage may emit an artifact that cannot be replay-verified downstream.
18.10 What this chapter “makes true”
After Ch18, the framework can ship containers as stable artifacts where:
Every container is self-describing
Every decode is replay-verifiable
Every dependency is pinned
Every corruption path yields a typed salvage outcome with truth scopes
Every version evolution is explicit via MIGRATE edges
Certificates are first-class verifiable objects, not prose
Ch19⟨0102⟩ — Mycelium Metro: Cross-Corpus Navigation as a Graph
[○Arc 6 | ○Rot 0 | △Lane Su | ω=18]Workflow role: graph execution of “reading”; overlays; hub cap; cross-scope pins.Primary hubs: → AppA → AppP → AppC → AppI → AppM
19.0 Chapter purpose in the HD‑SCT tome
This chapter formalizes navigation as executable routing, not prose scanning.
A “reading” is defined as:
compiling an intent into one or more RoutePlans,
deterministically constructing / re-constructing metro overlays (orbit / rail / triad),
executing plans over a typed graph of globally addressable atoms, and
producing only those claims whose evidence is backed by explicit routes + certificates.
The system MUST specify:
metro overlay edges (ORBIT_NEXT, RAIL_NEXT, ARC_TRIAD) as REF payloads,
RoutePlan as the executable unit,
HubCap discipline (≤ 6 hubs) with a mandatory signature,
cross-manuscript pinning and INTER contract rules,
a compilation model that turns “reading intent” into executable routes,
certificates: OverlayCert, RouterDeterminismCert, HubCapCert, NarrativeCompileCert.
19.1 Graph model
19.1.1 Global atoms and addresses
Atom: the smallest globally addressable unit of content (sentence, proposition, code cell, figure-caption, theorem, etc.).Each Atom has a globally unique Address.
Address (normative minimal fields):
manuscript_id (globally unique)
station_id (within manuscript)
atom_id (within station)
version_id (content hash or immutable revision)
profile_id (interpretation profile; see §19.6)
A route is only executable over addresses that are pinned to manuscript + profile + version (or are proven internal to the current pinned scope).
19.1.2 Stations and StationHeader
Station: a container of atoms with a header that allows deterministic adjacency derivation.
StationHeader (minimal normative fields sufficient for overlays):
manuscript_id
chapter_id
station_id
omega (ω): stable ordinal within manuscript traversal order
lane_id (e.g., Su)
arc_id (e.g., 6)
rot_id (e.g., 0)
triad_role ∈ {ENTRY, CORE, EXIT} (if the station participates in an arc triad; else NONE)
scope_tags (for lane/arc eligibility)
version_id
StationHeader mapping rules are the only allowed source for overlay construction. Overlays are not curated facts; they are recomputations.
19.1.3 Typed edges
We assume a base typed graph:
Node types: Station, Atom, Hub
Edge types (minimum needed in this chapter):
REF — intra-corpus navigation reference with structured payload
INTER — cross-manuscript link (requires pins; §19.5)
All metro overlays in this chapter are represented as REF edges with deterministic payloads.
19.2 MetroOverlay edges as REF payloads
19.2.1 MetroOverlay edge schema
A MetroOverlay edge is a REF edge whose payload includes:
overlay_type ∈ {ORBIT_NEXT, RAIL_NEXT, ARC_TRIAD}
from_station (addressable)
to_station (addressable)
derivation_key (the exact key computed from StationHeader mapping)
overlay_version (hash of overlay construction rules + input headers)
constraints (optional, but deterministic when present)
Normative payload skeleton:
REF.payload := {
overlay_type: OverlayType,
from: StationAddress,
to: StationAddress,
derivation_key: bytes,
overlay_version: hash,
constraints: { ... } // MUST be derivable, not editorial
}
19.2.2 ORBIT_NEXT (chapter orbit)
Purpose: define the default “forward motion” through stations, across chapters, without prose scanning.
Construction (deterministic):
Let S be the list of all stations in a manuscript, sorted by (omega) ascending (or by a stable composite key if ω is not global).For each station S[i], define:
next = S[i+1] if i+1 < |S|
else next = ⊥ (explicit terminal) unless the manuscript declares cyclic traversal
Then emit:
REF( S[i] → next, overlay_type=ORBIT_NEXT ) for all valid next
Derivation key MUST be a stable encoding of:
(manuscript_id, omega, omega+1, version_id(s), overlay_rules_hash)
Non-negotiable law: ORBIT_NEXT is never asserted manually. It is always recomputed. (§19.6.1)
19.2.3 RAIL_NEXT (lane rail)
Purpose: provide deterministic travel along a “lane” (theme/process lane), e.g. Lane Su.
Construction (deterministic):
For each lane_id = L, collect all stations whose StationHeader.lane_id = L.Sort them by (omega) ascending.Emit REF edges linking consecutive stations in this ordered list:
RAIL_NEXT: lane=L
Derivation key MUST encode:
(manuscript_id, lane_id, omega_i, omega_{i+1}, versions, rules_hash)
Lane eligibility MUST come only from headers and scope tags; no editorial insertion.
19.2.4 ARC_TRIAD (arc triads)
Purpose: create short-hop “triad jumps” inside a narrative/logic arc (Entry → Core → Exit), enabling structured revisit and cross-check.
Construction (deterministic):
For each (manuscript_id, arc_id = A):
Collect all stations with StationHeader.arc_id = A and triad_role ≠ NONE.
Partition by triad_group_id if the manuscript defines multiple triads per arc; otherwise the triad is the unique set of roles per arc.
For each triad group, ensure exactly one of each role:
ENTRY, CORE, EXIT
Emit REF edges connecting each role to the others with payload identifying:
arc_id, triad_group_id, from_role, to_role
Minimal emission set:
ENTRY → CORE, CORE → EXIT, EXIT → ENTRY (directed cycle)and optionally the full clique (ENTRY↔EXIT etc.) if declared by rules.
Derivation key MUST encode:
(manuscript_id, arc_id, triad_group_id, from_role, to_role, versions, rules_hash)
19.3 RoutePlan: the executable unit of reading
19.3.1 Definition
A RoutePlan is an executable object that completely specifies a navigational read.
A RoutePlan MUST contain:
target (address / query / station-set selector)
hub_sequence (ordered hubs, capped; §19.4)
truth_intent (typed; §19.6.4)
obligations (what must be produced during execution)
drop_log (deterministic; §19.4.4)
pins (cross-scope pins; §19.5)
scope (which manuscripts + versions + profiles are valid)
route_constraints (deterministic constraints: max hops, required overlays, disallowed edges, etc.)
Normative skeleton:
RoutePlan := {
plan_id: hash,
target: TargetSpec,
hub_sequence: [Hub] // length ≤ HubCap
truth_intent: TruthType,
obligations: [Obligation],
scope: ScopeSpec,
pins: [Pin],
route_constraints: RouteConstraints,
drop_log: DropLog
}
Executable means: given (Graph, RoutePlan), execution is deterministic and yields a reproducible transcript (routes traversed, atoms visited, certificates produced).
19.3.2 TargetSpec
Target MUST be one of:
a global address (Atom or Station),
a station selector (lane=Su, arc=6, rot=0, omega∈[a,b]),
a claim-needed selector (atoms that can satisfy a truth obligation),
a pinned INTER destination (explicit manuscript + profile pins required).
19.3.3 Obligations (minimum set)
Every RoutePlan MUST declare its obligations. At minimum:
EVIDENCE: list visited atom addresses used as support
ROUTES: the exact edge-walks used (with overlay types)
CERTS: required certificates (see §19.8)
DROPS: explicit drops due to HubCap or missing pins
AMBIG_MARKS: places where intent could not be satisfied
19.4 Hub discipline and HubCap policy (≤ 6)
19.4.1 Hubs are not metaphors
A Hub is a typed execution phase in routing. Hubs are not UI screens; they are required steps in a deterministic router.
Primary hubs (declared):
AppA — Addressing / resolving targets into addresses and admissible scopes
AppP — Planning / producing candidate routes under constraints
AppC — Checking / enforcing contracts, pins, and cap; producing cert fragments
AppI — Truth typing / interpretation profile application; obligation alignment
AppM — Memo / replay / caching of route transcripts and evidence bundles
(If your tome defines different semantics for these names, the structure here remains: addressing → planning → checking → truth → memo.)
19.4.2 HubCap rule
HubCap = 6 (max hubs in hub_sequence).
HubCap policy:
|hub_sequence| ≤ 6 MUST be enforced by the router.
A mandatory signature MUST appear in every RoutePlan’s hub sequence:
[\Sigma = {\mathrm{AppA, AppI, AppM}}]
Meaning: every RoutePlan MUST include at least one occurrence of each of AppA, AppI, AppM (order may be constrained by compiler policy, but presence is mandatory).
Truth overlay insertion rule: AppI MUST appear before any claim-bearing obligation is discharged (before emitting “supported claim” output).
19.4.3 Cap enforcement is semantic, not cosmetic
If an intent would require more than 6 hubs to satisfy obligations, the system MUST NOT silently exceed the cap. It must:
split intent into multiple RoutePlans (compiler-level decomposition), or
return AMBIG with an evidence plan, or
drop non-essential subgoals with deterministic logging.
19.4.4 DropLog (deterministic)
DropLog is a required field of RoutePlan output and must be deterministic.
DropLog entries MUST include:
drop_reason ∈ {HUBCAP_EXCEEDED, PIN_MISSING, SCOPE_VIOLATION, EDGE_DISALLOWED, NO_ROUTE}
drop_point (hub + step)
what_was_dropped (subgoal / candidate route / edge type)
required_fix (e.g., “add pins for manuscript X with profile Y”)
replay_token (so the same drop can be reproduced)
A DropLog is not “debug text”; it is a formal artifact that blocks false certainty.
19.5 Cross-manuscript link contract (INTER)
19.5.1 INTER edges are only routable when pinned
Any cross-manuscript traversal uses an INTER edge.
Contract: Any INTER edge traversal MUST include pins for:
source manuscript ID + version + profile
destination manuscript ID + version + profile
Unpinned links are not OK-routable.
19.5.2 Pin structure
A Pin minimally contains:
manuscript_id
version_id (or immutable content hash)
profile_id (interpretation profile)
optional scope_label (human-friendly name; not used for determinism)
19.5.3 Interpretation profiles are part of the address
A route crossing manuscripts without explicit profile_id is undefined behavior.“Convenient default interpretation” is not allowed for executable reading.
19.6 Required laws
19.6.1 Overlay determinism law
Law (Overlay Determinism): Metro overlays MUST be recomputable from StationHeader mapping rules and pinned corpus versions. They MUST NOT be asserted as freehand edges.
Operational consequence:
Overlays have a generator hash.
Overlay edges must be derivable from headers and generator version.
“I linked these because it felt right” is invalid in MetroOverlay space.
19.6.2 Router determinism + HubCap enforcement law
Law (Router Determinism): Given identical:
pinned graph (content + headers),
overlay rules hash,
target + constraints,
scope + pins,
the router MUST output the same RoutePlan(s), the same route order, and the same DropLogs.
Law (Cap Enforcement): Any route output violating HubCap is invalid and MUST be rejected at AppC.
19.6.3 Cross-scope pin completeness law
Law (Pin Completeness): Any executable plan that can traverse an INTER edge MUST carry complete pins for all manuscripts reachable under that plan.
No “partial pins” and no “we’ll pin later” execution.
19.6.4 Truth typing cannot be bypassed
Law (Truth Typing Non-Bypass): Truth intent is a typed object in RoutePlan and MUST be inserted via AppI. No route may discharge claim-bearing obligations without passing through AppI.
Minimal TruthType lattice (example; adjust to your tome):
T0: QUOTE (verbatim / direct evidence)
T1: PARAPHRASE (faithful restatement; requires alignment obligations)
T2: DERIVE (logical derivation; requires rule references)
T3: INFER (probabilistic inference; requires uncertainty bounds)
T4: SPECULATE (explicitly marked; cannot be upgraded without new evidence)
Routes that look “shorter” but skip truth typing are convenience routes and must be rejected.
19.7 Required constructions
19.7.1 Overlay construction procedure
Input: pinned manuscripts, their StationHeaders, overlay generator version.Output: a set of REF edges with payloads (ORBIT_NEXT, RAIL_NEXT, ARC_TRIAD) + OverlayCert (§19.8.1).
Construction steps:
Normalize headersValidate required StationHeader fields exist and are pinned to versions.
Build ORBIT_NEXTSort by ω (or declared traversal key); link consecutive stations.
Build RAIL_NEXTFor each lane, filter stations by lane_id, sort by ω, link consecutive.
Build ARC_TRIADFor each arc, assemble triads by roles; emit deterministic triad edges.
Emit OverlayCertHash:
input headers (ordered)
overlay generator version
output edge list (ordered)producing overlay_version.
19.7.2 Narrative compiler
A Narrative is not a freeform story; it is a compiled artifact whose claims must be backed by executable routes.
Narrative compilation:
Input: IntentSpec (what you want to know / prove / summarize)
Output:
ordered list of RoutePlans,
a claim set with evidence bindings,
NarrativeCompileCert,
possibly an AMBIG status with evidence plans.
Validity rule:
A narrative is VALID iff every claim used is supported by:
explicit route transcript(s) produced by executing RoutePlans, and
required certificates.
Otherwise the narrative MUST remain AMBIG, and the compiler MUST output an evidence plan (RoutePlans that would resolve ambiguity if executed).
19.8 Required certificates
Certificates are the non-negotiable proof objects that prevent “hand-wavy reading.”
19.8.1 OverlayCert
Attests that overlays were generated deterministically.
Must include:
overlay_generator_id (hash/version)
input_headers_hash
output_edges_hash
overlay_version
scope_pins_used
19.8.2 RouterDeterminismCert
Attests deterministic planning and ordering.
Must include:
router_id (hash/version)
inputs_hash (target, constraints, pins, overlay_version)
routeplan_hashes (ordered)
ordering_rule_id (stable sort description / tie-breaker hash)
19.8.3 HubCapCert
Attests HubCap compliance and signature inclusion.
Must include:
hubcap_value (≤ 6)
hub_sequence
proof of Σ={AppA,AppI,AppM} inclusion
any DropLog entries caused by cap enforcement
19.8.4 NarrativeCompileCert
Attests the narrative-to-routes compilation.
Must include:
intent_hash
routeplan_list_hash (ordered)
claims_hash
for each claim: list of supporting routeplan transcripts + evidence atom addresses
status ∈ {VALID, AMBIG}
if AMBIG: evidence plan RoutePlans
19.9 Worked example (schematic)
Intent: “Establish what Ch19 asserts about cross-corpus navigation, and which rules block unpinned links.”
Compiler output (example RoutePlan set):
RoutePlan #1
target: StationSelector(chapter=Ch19, omega≈18)
hub_sequence: [AppA, AppP, AppC, AppI, AppM]
truth_intent: T0: QUOTE
obligations: EVIDENCE, ROUTES, CERTS
scope: {manuscript=HD‑SCT‑tome@vX, profile=default_strict}
pins: (single-manuscript pins)
result: produces evidence atoms stating “navigation is deterministic route planning + replay,” plus OverlayCert + HubCapCert.
RoutePlan #2
target: INTER contract rules (edge-type rule index)
hub_sequence: [AppA, AppP, AppC, AppI, AppM]
truth_intent: T2: DERIVE
obligations include contract derivation + pin completeness check
result: emits the “unpinned links are not OK-routable” rule with evidence atoms + RouterDeterminismCert.
