[\mathsf{EvidenceRow} :=\langle\mathsf{EID},;\mathsf{ClaimAddr},;\mathsf{WitnessType},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{WitnessPtr},;\mathsf{InputDigests},;\mathsf{OutputDigests},;\mathsf{Metrics},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{ExpiryPulse?},;\mathsf{Supersedes?},;\mathsf{SchemaVer}\rangle]
Required fields:
EID: EvidenceID (defined in B.S2.a).
ClaimAddr: canonical GlobalAddr of the subject claim (node/edge/route/certificate).
WitnessType: pinned enum describing what the row proves, at minimum:
ReplayWitness (replay capsule proves claim),
EquivWitness (EQUIV proof object),
DualWitness (DUAL proof object),
MigrationWitness (MIGRATE proof object),
ResidualLedger (NEAR bounds),
EvidencePlan (AMBIG plan),
ConflictPacket (quarantine/fence evidence),
AuditWitness (audit proof object).
Scope: pinned enum {LOCAL, INTER} plus optional scope bindings:
LOCAL: manuscript_id required.
INTER: ordered pair (src_manuscript_id, dst_manuscript_id) required.
TruthType: pinned enum {OK, NEAR, AMBIG, FAIL, CONFLICT}.
PinsDigest: digest of the complete pin-closure required to interpret this row (AppA/AppD/AppI).
ReplayPtr: pointer to replay capsule (or deterministic replay recipe) sufficient to reproduce the verdict. Required for OK and NEAR; optional for AMBIG when an EvidencePlan is the only object; required for FAIL/CONFLICT when reproducible.
WitnessPtr: pointer to the primary witness artifact for the WitnessType.
InputDigests: canonical ordered list of digests of inputs required by replay (containers, profiles, policies, codebooks).
OutputDigests: canonical ordered list of digests of outputs claimed by the witness.
Metrics: optional pinned metric outputs (residual bounds, commutation residuals) with metric digests and units. Mandatory for NEAR.
IssuedPulse: PulseID at which this row is issued (Ch20).
ExpiryPulse?: PulseID at which this row ceases to qualify for OK routing under the stability contract (mandatory for NEAR, optional otherwise).
Supersedes?: optional EvidenceID of a prior row that this row supersedes (append-only supersession).
SchemaVer: evidence schema version (pinned, immutable).
B.S1.b — EvidenceTableAn EvidenceTable is an append-only multiset of EvidenceRows with canonical ordering and index structures.
[\mathsf{EvidenceTable} :=\langle\mathsf{TableID},;\mathsf{PolicyDigest},;\mathsf{CanonBytesDigest},;\mathsf{RowsDigest},;\mathsf{RowIndexDigest},;\mathsf{PulseDigestRef},;\mathsf{SchemaVer}\rangle]
RowsDigest commits to the canonical list of rows.
RowIndexDigest commits to canonical indices (by claim addr, by EID, by truth type, by witness type, by pulse).
PulseDigestRef binds the table state to the pulse digest chain (Ch20).
B.S1.c — Index invariantsIndices are derived; the table commits to a canonical index digest. Index derivation must be deterministic and replayable:
Index key order: canonical lexicographic order over serialized keys.
Collision resolution: deterministic and logged.
B.S1.d — StabilityContract recordA StabilityContract is a pinned rule set specifying when an EvidenceRow may be treated as stable for routing under given corridor requirements.
[\mathsf{StabilityContract} :=\langle\mathsf{ContractID},;\mathsf{Pins},;\mathsf{RulesOK},;\mathsf{RulesNEAR},;\mathsf{RulesAMBIG},;\mathsf{RulesFAIL},;\mathsf{RulesCONFLICT},;\mathsf{ExpiryPolicy},;\mathsf{RenewalPolicy},;\mathsf{MigrationPolicy},;\mathsf{SchemaVer}\rangle]
B.S2 — Operators
B.S2.a — EvidenceID derivation (pinned)EvidenceID MUST be content-derived and collision-resistant under pinned canonicalization.
Define:
(R := \mathsf{ser}(\mathsf{EvidenceRowZeroed})) where EID and any signature fields are zeroed and Supersedes? is preserved.
(k :=) a pinned domain-separation tag "AppB/EvidenceRow".
Then:[\boxed{\mathsf{EID} = \mathsf{H}\big(k ,|, \mathsf{H}(R) ,|, \mathsf{PinsDigest}\big)}]where (\mathsf{PinsDigest}) is the digest of the pin-closure referenced by the row.
Collision handling.If an implementation detects (\mathsf{EID}) collision with a distinct row (distinct canonical bytes), it MUST:
Treat as integrity failure (typed CONFLICT),
Emit a ConflictPacket witness row (WitnessType=ConflictPacket) describing:
both row digests,
collision digest,
reproduction procedure,
Quarantine both rows for OK routing until resolved by schema/policy migration.
No silent disambiguation suffixes are permitted; any disambiguation must be explicit via migration and pinned rule changes.
B.S2.b — Row insertion and append-only disciplineEvidenceTable update is a DeltaPack operation. Insertion is append-only:
Rows are appended, never rewritten.
Supersession is represented only by a new row referencing Supersedes?.
Let (T_p) be the evidence table at pulse (p). Applying a DeltaPack at pulse (p+1) yields:[T_{p+1} = T_p \cup \Delta T_{p+1}]where (\Delta T_{p+1}) is the set of new rows.
B.S2.c — Canonical row ordering in table commitsEvidenceTable commits to a canonical ordering of rows by a pinned comparator:
Primary key:
IssuedPulse ascending
ClaimAddr canonical order
TruthType order (OK > NEAR > AMBIG > FAIL > CONFLICT) for deterministic grouping
WitnessType canonical enum order
EID lexicographic
This ordering is used to compute RowsDigest. Any change to ordering rules is a meaning-bearing policy change and requires explicit migration.
B.S2.d — Merge operator for evidence tablesEvidence tables merge only through DeltaPack application and deterministic merge rules. For merging two sources (T^A, T^B) into (T^{A\cup B}), define:
merge input: two row streams and their pulse ranges
merge output: a unified row stream with deterministic conflict detection
Merge algorithm:
Validate chain integrity and policy compatibility (AppD/Ch20).
Collect all rows, deduplicate by EID with exact equality of canonical row bytes.
If two distinct rows share an EID, emit a merge conflict and quarantine (see B.S2.a collision handling).
Recompute indices deterministically.
Emit MergeDeterminismCert.
B.S3 — Invariants
B.S3.a — EvidenceRow well-formednessAn EvidenceRow is well-formed iff:
ClaimAddr parses under AppA grammar and resolves under pinned registry.
PinsDigest resolves to a complete pin-closure required by the witness type.
ReplayPtr presence matches truth type requirements:
OK: required
NEAR: required
AMBIG: optional, but required if any deterministic selection is asserted
FAIL/CONFLICT: required if reproducible, optional only if policy explicitly permits non-reproducible fails (not permitted in publish corridors)
Metrics is present and complete if TruthType=NEAR.
IssuedPulse is valid under PulseID policy.
EID equals the pinned derivation function output.
B.S3.b — Stability contract soundnessIf a StabilityContract marks an EvidenceRow as usable for OK routing, then:
The row must be TruthType=OK
Replay must close under the pinned replay harness, and all referenced digests must validate
The row must not be expired under ExpiryPolicy
The row must not be quarantined by any applicable quarantine/ revocation policy
B.S3.c — Expiry and renewal monotonicityExpiry is monotone in time: once expired, a row cannot become unexpired. Renewal occurs only via a new EvidenceRow that supersedes prior evidence and references a later pulse and later replay.
B.S3.d — Migration compatibility invariantsIf schema/policy pins change, evidence stability must be re-evaluated under MigrationPolicy:
Rows referencing obsolete schema pins are not OK-routable unless explicitly migrated.
Migration is represented by new rows with WitnessType=MigrationWitness and TruthType per corridor evaluation.
B.S4 — Protocols
B.S4.a — Evidence issuance protocolTo issue evidence for a claim:
Determine ClaimAddr and Scope.
Select WitnessType and produce WitnessPtr and ReplayPtr.
Compute PinsDigest for the complete closure required to interpret the witness and to replay verification.
Compute input and output digests.
Determine TruthType:
OK: replay closes, digests match, invariants hold exactly
NEAR: bounded residual, metrics provided, expiry defined, obligations recorded
AMBIG: evidence plan or bounded candidate set, no unpinned tie-breaks
FAIL/CONFLICT: deterministic failure witness or conflict packet
Compute EID.
Append as DeltaPack row insertion at IssuedPulse.
B.S4.b — Evidence lookup protocolGiven a claim address and a corridor requirement, lookup proceeds:
Retrieve all rows matching ClaimAddr.
Filter by Scope compatibility.
Filter by valid pins under the current policy epoch (AppD/Ch20).
Apply StabilityContract to determine which rows are admissible under the corridor.
Choose the best admissible row by pinned preference order:
prefer OK over NEAR over AMBIG over FAIL over CONFLICT
prefer latest IssuedPulse subject to non-expiry
tie-break by EID
Emit selected evidence row plus any required disclosures (NEAR metrics) or evidence plan (AMBIG).
B.S4.c — Table merge protocol under DeltaPacksMerge is performed by applying imported DeltaPacks and reconstructing the EvidenceTable deterministically. The merge procedure must:
validate import integrity (digests, signatures),
validate pulse chain integrity,
validate row schemas and EIDs,
detect collisions and conflicts deterministically,
re-emit indices and RowsDigest,
emit MergeDeterminismCert.
B.S4.d — NEAR renewal protocolIf a row is NEAR and ExpiryPulse is reached (or imminent under policy), renewal is performed by issuing a new row with Supersedes? set to the prior EID and with one of:
OK upgrade via new replay closure, or
NEAR renewal via tightened bounds or extended evidence, with a new expiry and replay pointer.
Renewal must be deterministic and append-only.
❀ B.F — Flower: Evidence Semantics as Typed Claims over Pinned Models
B.F1 — Objects
B.F1.a — Claim models and scopeA claim is evaluated under a pinned model (M_\Pi) determined by policy pins. Evidence rows bind a claim to a witness inside (M_\Pi). The semantic statement of an evidence row is:
If TruthType=OK: claim holds in (M_\Pi) under pinned evaluation.
If TruthType=NEAR: claim holds up to bounded error in (M_\Pi) under pinned metric.
If TruthType=AMBIG: claim is underdetermined; evidence plan required.
If TruthType=FAIL/CONFLICT: claim cannot be relied on; quarantine and/or conflict resolution required.
B.F1.b — Metric binding for NEARNEAR evidence must bind a metric (d) by digest, and a bound (\epsilon), such that:[d(\text{observed}, \text{expected}) \le \epsilon.]The metric definition is pinned and import-verifiable.
B.F2 — Operators
B.F2.a — Promotion operator for truth typesEvidence stability is monotone via supersession and renewal; upgrades must be explicit rows. No implicit promotions exist.
B.F3 — Invariants
B.F3.a — No semantic inference from REFEvidence semantics cannot be inferred from reference edges. Only witnessed types in EvidenceRow can promote a claim.
☁ B.C — Cloud: Uncertainty, AMBIG Discipline, and Expiry as Safety Envelope
B.C1 — Objects
B.C1.a — EvidencePlan linkage for AMBIGIf TruthType=AMBIG, EvidenceRow must include:
WitnessType=EvidencePlan
WitnessPtr pointing to a bounded candidate set plus discriminators and routes
optional ReplayPtr if deterministic generation is asserted
B.C1.b — ExpiryPolicyExpiryPolicy is pinned and specifies:
which witness types may expire (at minimum NEAR)
default expiry windows
conditions under which expiry is accelerated (e.g., policy epoch change)
renewal obligations
B.C2 — Operators
B.C2.a — Quarantine overlayQuarantine is a masking layer over evidence: a quarantined row is not OK-routable even if TruthType=OK, until unquarantined by explicit governance procedures.
B.C3 — Invariants
B.C3.a — Evidence reliance requires stability contract satisfactionNo route may treat evidence as stable unless the StabilityContract permits it under the corridor. Routes must carry disclosures and expiry obligations.
✶ B.R — Fractal: Evidence Across Time, Migration, and Deterministic Merge
B.R1 — Objects
B.R1.a — Evidence lineageSupersession creates a lineage DAG:[\mathsf{EID}{0} \to \mathsf{EID}{1} \to \cdots]where edges are Supersedes? pointers. Lineage does not delete prior evidence; it layers it.
B.R1.b — Policy epochs and evidence revalidationWhen policy pins change (new policy epoch), evidence must be revalidated or migrated. Rows remain addressable but may become non-routable for OK corridors.
B.R2 — Operators
B.R2.a — Deterministic merge as replayable operationMerging evidence tables is defined as replaying DP application and rebuilding the table deterministically. Any mismatch in merged digests is a deterministic failure.
B.R3 — Invariants
B.R3.a — Append-only integrity under time axisEvidence tables evolve only by appended rows under DeltaPacks; table digests are pinned to pulse chain digests. Any discontinuity in the chain is a quarantine condition.
B.R4 — Required Certificates
B.R4.a — EvidenceTableCertAn EvidenceTableCert attests that:
RowsDigest matches the canonical ordering of contained rows,
index digests match deterministic index construction,
all rows validate (schema, EID derivation, pin closure rules),
pulse digest references validate.
B.R4.b — MergeDeterminismCertA MergeDeterminismCert attests that a merge:
is independent of import order (given pinned pulse ordering),
yields the same merged RowsDigest and RowIndexDigest under replay,
detects collisions deterministically and emits conflict packets when needed.
Certificates must be import-verifiable: all referenced rows, pins, and replay artifacts must be resolvable by digest.
AppB Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
EvidenceRow is the canonical record binding ClaimAddr to a WitnessType under PinsDigest, producing a TruthType with ReplayPtr/WitnessPtr and digests.
EvidenceID is derived as a pinned hash of the canonical EvidenceRow content and PinsDigest; collisions are CONFLICT and quarantined.
EvidenceTable is append-only and updated only via DeltaPacks; row ordering and index construction are deterministic and pinned.
StabilityContract specifies when evidence is OK-routable, including expiry/renewal rules for NEAR and migration rules across policy epochs.
Table merge is deterministic under pinned pulse ordering; conflicts are detected and certified; no silent resolution.
EvidenceTableCert and MergeDeterminismCert are required, import-verifiable, and bind table digests and merge outcomes.
AppB — Evidence Tables, IDs, and the Stability Contract
AppC — Square Interior (4^4 Tile), Addressing, and Local Proof Objects
Station role: □ interior mechanics; local atom semantics; core addressability.Purpose: define the local 4^4 tile semantics as the storage surface of meaning; addresses, lenses, facets, atoms; local link kinds and invariants.
□ C.S — Square: 4^4 Tile Semantics, Address Grammar, Local Links, Local Proof Objects
C.S1 — Objects
C.S1.a — The 4^4 tile and slot spaceA tile is the minimal storage surface of meaning inside the corpus graph. Each tile decomposes into slots by the product:[\mathsf{Slot} := \mathsf{Lens}\times\mathsf{Facet}\times\mathsf{Atom}]with:
(\mathsf{Lens} := {S,F,C,R}) with pinned order (S \prec F \prec C \prec R),
(\mathsf{Facet} := {1,2,3,4}) with numeric order,
(\mathsf{Atom} := {1,2,3,4}) with numeric order.
A tile slot is the triple ((L,f,a)\in\mathsf{Slot}). A tile instance binds a tile identifier (\mathsf{TileID}) to a finite set of slot payloads:[\mathsf{Tile}(\mathsf{TileID}) := {, (L,f,a) \mapsto \mathsf{PayloadRef}_{L,f,a},}.]
Each payload reference is content-addressed by digest and schema ID:[\mathsf{PayloadRef} := \langle \mathsf{SchemaID},\ \mathsf{Digest},\ \mathsf{Size},\ \mathsf{Locator}\rangle.]
C.S1.b — Addressing: GlobalAddr, SlotAddr, and LocalAddrAll semantics are addressable.
A GlobalAddr identifies a corpus object (chapter, appendix, registry object, or other globally routable node) and is parsed by AppA.
A SlotAddr refines a GlobalAddr by selecting a lens/facet/atom:[\mathsf{SlotAddr} := \langle \mathsf{GlobalAddr},\ L,\ f,\ a\rangle.]
A LocalAddr refines a SlotAddr to an internal object path inside the payload schema:[\mathsf{LocalAddr} := \langle \mathsf{SlotAddr},\ \mathsf{FieldPath}\rangle.]
LocalAddr is the atomic reference unit for local proofs, local link targets, and deterministic expansions.
C.S1.c — Formal address grammar and canonical orderingAddresses MUST be parsed by AppA and canonicalized by AppA canonical bytes rules. Slot selection is canonical and must not depend on presentation.
Normative EBNF additions for SlotAddr and LocalAddr:
SlotAddr := GlobalAddr "." Lens "." Facet "." Atom ;
LocalAddr := SlotAddr ":" FieldPath ;
FieldPath := PathSeg { "/" PathSeg } ;
PathSeg := ID | ID "[" Int "]" ;
Canonical ordering of SlotAddr is the lexicographic order on:[(\mathsf{GlobalAddrCanon},\ L,\ f,\ a)]where (L) uses the pinned lens order and (\mathsf{GlobalAddrCanon}) is the AppA canonical form.
Canonical ordering of LocalAddr is lexicographic on:[(\mathsf{SlotAddrCanon},\ \mathsf{FieldPathCanon})]with FieldPathCanon computed by pinned normalization:
normalize . and .. segments are forbidden,
bracket indices are canonical integers (no leading zeros),
path separators are / only.
C.S1.d — Local node types and proof objectsWithin a tile, every payload schema MUST implement a minimal typed node vocabulary to support proof-carrying semantics.
Minimum local node types:
ClaimNode: a statement that can be true-typed under a corridor.
DefNode: definition node (introduces names, types, or constraints).
RuleNode: inference rule / rewrite rule node (typed, pinned).
DerivationNode: derivation structure applying rules to premises.
WitnessNode: evidence object binding claim to replay or proof artifacts.
DataNode: dataset / instance / trace / log prefix digest.
CodeNode: code artifact pointer with schema and digest.
IndexNode: local index structure enabling deterministic traversal.
MetaNode: pinned metadata required to interpret the above (schema/pins).
A LocalProofObject is a structured node family that binds a ClaimNode to its verification artifact set. Minimum local proof object types:
ReplayProof: references a replay capsule and expected digests.
FormalProof: references a derivation graph with axioms/rules pinned.
TestProof: references regression fixtures and pass/fail digests.
BoundedProof: references a residual ledger for NEAR.
Every proof object MUST be content-addressed and must include the pin closure required to interpret it.
C.S2 — Operators
C.S2.a — Canonicalization operators for tile payloadsEach payload schema (\mathsf{SchemaID}) MUST define:
(\mathsf{Parse}_{\mathsf{Schema}}) : bytes → AST (total or typed error),
(\mathsf{NF}_{\mathsf{Schema}}) : AST → canonical normal form,
(\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathsf{Schema}}) : normal form → canonical bytes.
Schema-level canonicalization MUST satisfy determinism and stability:[\mathsf{NF}{\mathsf{Schema}}(\mathsf{Parse}{\mathsf{Schema}}(b))\ \text{is unique for valid }b.]
C.S2.b — Local closure operatorDefine the local closure check for a tile:[\mathsf{Close}(\mathsf{Tile}) \in {\mathsf{true},\mathsf{false}}]which returns true iff all LocalAddr references inside the tile resolve to:
existing payload refs by digest,
existing internal nodes by FieldPath,
and existing schemas by SchemaID,under the pinned registry and import policy.
Closure failures are typed and must produce a local failure witness object.
C.S2.c — Local expansion operatorA local expansion is a deterministic function that produces derived nodes/edges inside the same tile or produces new tiles via explicit expansion rules.
Define:[\mathsf{Expand} : (\mathsf{Tile},\ \mathsf{ExpandRuleID},\ \mathsf{Pins}) \to (\mathsf{Tile}',\ \mathsf{ExpansionWitness})]where:
(\mathsf{ExpandRuleID}) is pinned,
(\mathsf{Tile}') is the tile after appending derived objects (append-only locally),
(\mathsf{ExpansionWitness}) commits to:
inputs digests,
rule digest,
derived outputs digests,
deterministic ordering used.
Expansions are permitted only if explicitly declared by rule and if their outputs remain in the tile’s local closure.
C.S2.d — Local proof verification operatorDefine:[\mathsf{VerifyLocalProof} : (\mathsf{LocalProofObject},\ \mathsf{Pins},\ \mathsf{CorridorSpec}) \to \mathsf{TruthType}]which produces ({\mathsf{OK},\mathsf{NEAR},\mathsf{AMBIG},\mathsf{FAIL},\mathsf{CONFLICT}}) and must also emit:
replay transcript digest if replay is required,
residual ledger if NEAR,
evidence plan if AMBIG,
conflict packet if CONFLICT.
Verification is deterministic under pinned environment and pinned tie-break rules.
C.S3 — Local Link Typing (REF/IMPL/PROOF/…) and Permission Rules
Local links are edges whose endpoints are LocalAddr or SlotAddr. Every edge is typed by LinkKind and is permitted only when the typing judgment holds.
C.S3.a — LinkKind vocabulary (minimum)[\mathsf{LinkKind} := {\mathsf{REF},\mathsf{IMPL},\mathsf{PROOF},\mathsf{TEST},\mathsf{DATA},\mathsf{CERT},\mathsf{EQUIV},\mathsf{DUAL},\mathsf{MIGRATE},\mathsf{CONFLICT}}]A tile MAY define additional link kinds only by schema migration; additional kinds must not be inferred.
C.S3.b — LocalEdge schema[\mathsf{LocalEdge} :=\langle\mathsf{EdgeID},;\mathsf{From},;\mathsf{Kind},;\mathsf{To},;\mathsf{PayloadRef?},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse}\rangle]where:
(\mathsf{From},\mathsf{To}\in{\mathsf{LocalAddr},\mathsf{SlotAddr}}),
(\mathsf{PayloadRef?}) is required for kinds whose meaning depends on additional structure (PROOF/TEST/CERT/MIGRATE/CONFLICT),
(\mathsf{PinsDigest}) pins the interpretation closure,
(\mathsf{IssuedPulse}) binds the edge to time axis semantics (Ch20).
C.S3.c — Typing judgmentsLet (\Gamma) be the local typing environment derived from pinned schema + pinned policy:[\Gamma := \langle \mathsf{SchemaPins},\ \mathsf{CorridorPins},\ \mathsf{PolicyPins},\ \mathsf{OperatorTablePins} \rangle.]Let (\Gamma \vdash u : \tau) denote that node/address (u) has type (\tau) under (\Gamma).
Edge permission is defined by judgments of the form:[\Gamma \vdash (u \xrightarrow{K} v)\ \mathsf{perm}]
Minimum permission rules:
REF[\frac{\Gamma \vdash u:_* \quad \Gamma \vdash v:_*}{\Gamma \vdash (u \xrightarrow{\mathsf{REF}} v)\ \mathsf{perm}}]REF is allowed only as addressability; it carries no semantic commitment unless accompanied by PROOF/EQUIV/DUAL/MIGRATE.
IMPL (implementation link)[\frac{\Gamma \vdash u:\mathsf{SpecNode} \quad \Gamma \vdash v:\mathsf{CodeNode}}{\Gamma \vdash (u \xrightarrow{\mathsf{IMPL}} v)\ \mathsf{perm}}]IMPL payload MUST include:
code digest,
build pins,
interface contract digest,
and must be stable under corridor pins.
PROOF[\frac{\Gamma \vdash u:\mathsf{ClaimNode} \quad \Gamma \vdash v:\mathsf{LocalProofObject}}{\Gamma \vdash (u \xrightarrow{\mathsf{PROOF}} v)\ \mathsf{perm}}]PROOF payload MUST include:
proof object digest,
replay capsule digest (if applicable),
expected output digests,
and must pin the corridor spec used.
TEST[\frac{\Gamma \vdash u:\mathsf{ClaimNode} \quad \Gamma \vdash v:\mathsf{TestProof}}{\Gamma \vdash (u \xrightarrow{\mathsf{TEST}} v)\ \mathsf{perm}}]TEST payload MUST include:
fixture set digest,
harness digest,
pass/fail summary digest.
DATA[\frac{\Gamma \vdash u:\mathsf{ClaimNode} \quad \Gamma \vdash v:\mathsf{DataNode}}{\Gamma \vdash (u \xrightarrow{\mathsf{DATA}} v)\ \mathsf{perm}}]DATA is evidence attachment; its semantics are defined by Proof nodes that consume it.
CERT[\frac{\Gamma \vdash u:_* \quad \Gamma \vdash v:\mathsf{CertNode}}{\Gamma \vdash (u \xrightarrow{\mathsf{CERT}} v)\ \mathsf{perm}}]CERT payload MUST include certificate digest and verification policy pins.
EQUIV / DUAL / MIGRATEThese are meaning-bearing and require explicit witnesses:[\Gamma \vdash (u \xrightarrow{\mathsf{EQUIV}} v)\ \mathsf{perm}\Rightarrow\exists w:\mathsf{EquivWitness}\ \text{such that } u \xrightarrow{\mathsf{PROOF}} w \ \wedge\ v \xrightarrow{\mathsf{PROOF}} w.]Analogous requirements apply for DUAL and MIGRATE with corresponding witness types and corridor legality constraints. No EQUIV/DUAL/MIGRATE is permitted without witness payload references.
CONFLICTCONFLICT links are permitted only to conflict packets:[\frac{\Gamma \vdash u:_* \quad \Gamma \vdash v:\mathsf{ConflictPacket}}{\Gamma \vdash (u \xrightarrow{\mathsf{CONFLICT}} v)\ \mathsf{perm}}]CONFLICT payload MUST include:
minimal witness set digests,
reproduction recipe digest,
fence spec digest.
C.S3.d — Forbidden inferencesNo edge kind implies any other edge kind. In particular:
REF does not imply EQUIV.
IMPL does not imply correctness of implementation.
DATA does not imply validity.Only PROOF/TEST/CERT evidence objects can upgrade truth status under AppI/AppM.
C.S4 — Invariants: Determinism, Local Closure, and Local Soundness
C.S4.a — Determinism of local expansionsFor any fixed tile (\mathsf{Tile}), fixed rule ID (\mathsf{ExpandRuleID}), and fixed pins (\mathsf{Pins}):[\mathsf{did}(\mathsf{Expand}(\mathsf{Tile},\mathsf{ExpandRuleID},\mathsf{Pins}).\mathsf{Tile}')\ \text{is deterministic.}]If multiple expansions are possible without discriminating pins, the expansion is AMBIG and must emit an EvidencePlan (AppL) rather than selecting arbitrarily.
C.S4.b — Local closure invariantA tile is locally closed iff:
all referenced digests resolve,
all referenced LocalAddr paths resolve within payload schemas,
all edge permission judgments hold under pinned typing environment (\Gamma).
Local closure failure is non-routable for OK and must be surfaced via typed failure nodes and, if exported, via container quarantine.
C.S4.c — Local proof soundness invariantA ClaimNode may be treated as OK-routable only if:
there exists a PROOF or TEST edge to a witness object,
the witness verifies deterministically under pinned corridor spec,
and no applicable CONFLICT or revocation fences mask the claim.
C.S4.d — Canonical ordering invariantsAll sequences committed to digests inside a tile MUST use pinned canonical ordering. Any unordered collection must be converted to an ordered sequence via pinned comparator prior to serialization/digesting.
C.S5 — Protocols: Local Construction, Validation, and Regression Fixtures
C.S5.a — Tile construction protocolTo construct a tile:
Allocate (\mathsf{TileID}) and bind to a GlobalAddr context.
For each slot ((L,f,a)) to be populated:
select schema ID,
construct payload AST,
canonicalize to normal form,
encode to canonical bytes,
store payload and record digest in (\mathsf{PayloadRef}_{L,f,a}).
Construct local nodes and edges:
every edge must pass permission judgments,
every meaning-bearing edge must include witness payload references.
Compute tile digest as the digest of canonical encoding of:
tile header,
ordered slot list,
ordered edge list,
ordered local indices.
C.S5.b — Local validation protocolValidation produces a LocalValidationReport artifact:
closure checks,
schema resolution checks,
edge permission checks,
proof verification checks (for those requested by corridor),
and deterministic digests of the report.
C.S5.c — Square-local regression fixturesA square-local regression suite MUST include:
Address grammar fixtures
canonical SlotAddr/LocalAddr parsing and ordering.
Edge typing fixtures
minimal graphs that exercise each LinkKind rule, including rejection cases.
Closure fixtures
dangling digest reference detection,
dangling LocalAddr path detection,
schema mismatch detection.
Determinism fixtures
repeated local expansion yields identical digests.
Witness fixtures
PROOF and TEST objects verify deterministically or fail deterministically.
Conflict fixtures
conflict packet reproduction and fence behavior.
Export fixtures
tile containerization retains digests and validates on import.
Each fixture set must commit to expected digests and must be replayable under pinned environment. A fixture failure blocks publication for corridors that require OK proofs for local claims.
C.S5.d — Local export protocolLocal tile export must include:
slot payloads (or references),
edge set and indices,
schema pins,
proofs and required certificates,
and a manifest describing required verification steps.
❀ C.F — Flower: Local Basis Changes and Interpretation-Preserving Views
C.F1 — Objects
C.F1.a — View objectsA view is an interpretation-preserving projection of square-local payloads into alternative representations (e.g., spectral coordinates, harmonic summaries, normalized invariants). Views are auxiliary and do not replace the square payload.
A view is:[\mathsf{View} := \langle \mathsf{SourceSlotAddr},\ \mathsf{ViewType},\ \mathsf{ViewPayloadRef},\ \mathsf{PinsDigest}\rangle]and must be derived deterministically.
C.F1.b — View schemas and operator tablesEvery view must pin:
its view schema digest,
the operator table digest defining any symbols in the view,
the canonical bytes digest.
C.F2 — Operators
C.F2.a — View derivation[\mathsf{DeriveView} : (\mathsf{Tile},\ \mathsf{ViewType},\ \mathsf{Pins}) \to \mathsf{View}]Deterministic under pins. If multiple derivations are possible without discriminating pins, derivation is AMBIG.
C.F3 — Invariants
C.F3.a — View non-authoritativenessViews must not change the authoritative square payload; any discrepancy between view and payload is resolved by reverting to square-local proofs and witnesses. Views cannot upgrade truth type without explicit proof objects.
C.F4 — Protocols
C.F4.a — View regression fixturesFixtures must verify:
view derivation determinism,
stable digest commitments,
and that view computations do not introduce unpinned numerical nondeterminism.
☁ C.C — Cloud: Uncertainty, Approximate Locals, and NEAR/AMBIG Artifacts
C.C1 — Objects
C.C1.a — Residual ledger local formA local residual ledger binds:
metric digest,
bound,
scope (LocalAddr ranges),
expiry pulse,
replay pointer.
NEAR truth for local claims requires residual ledgers. AMBIG requires evidence plans.
C.C2 — Operators
C.C2.a — Local ambiguity planEvidencePlan objects are local-address scoped and must enumerate bounded candidate sets and discriminators. No implicit ambiguity resolution is permitted.
C.C3 — Invariants
C.C3.a — No silent NEARNEAR is illegal without residual ledger and expiry/renewal obligations.
C.C4 — Protocols
C.C4.a — Local uncertainty regression fixturesFixtures must ensure:
NEAR requires ledger,
AMBIG requires evidence plan,
and truth typing upgrades are impossible without explicit witnesses.
✶ C.R — Fractal: Local Recursion, Expansion Ladders, and Sealing
C.R1 — Objects
C.R1.a — Local expansion ladderLocal expansions may define a ladder of derived objects. Each rung is content-addressed, and transitions are explicit edges with witnesses. No implicit recursion is permitted.
C.R2 — Operators
C.R2.a — Seal operatorA tile (or a tile subset) can be sealed by emitting a SealCert that binds:
tile digest,
closure report digest,
regression suite digest,
and applicable corridor policy digest.
Sealing is append-only and produces a new cert node.
C.R3 — Invariants
C.R3.a — Sealed tile invariantsA sealed tile must remain verifiable under the pinned environment assumptions; if those assumptions change, the seal remains historically valid but may require migration or re-sealing under new policy.
C.R4 — Protocols
C.R4.a — Local sealing workflowSeal requires:
closure report PASS,
regression fixtures PASS,
proof witnesses resolved and verified,
absence of unresolved conflicts or revocations in scope.
AppC Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
A tile is a slot-indexed payload set over (\mathsf{Lens}\times\mathsf{Facet}\times\mathsf{Atom}).
SlotAddr and LocalAddr are canonical address forms; ordering is pinned and deterministic.
Local edges are typed by LinkKind; permission rules are stated as typing judgments under pinned environment (\Gamma).
REF provides addressability only; EQUIV/DUAL/MIGRATE require explicit witnesses.
Local closure requires digest resolvability, path resolvability, schema resolvability, and edge permission validity.
Local expansions are deterministic under pins; ambiguity requires EvidencePlan rather than arbitrary choice.
Local proofs are explicit objects; claim truth is upgraded only by verified proof/test/cert objects under pinned corridors.
Square-local regression fixtures must cover grammar, edge typing, closure, determinism, witnesses, conflicts, and export/import behavior.
AppC — Square Interior (4^4 Tile), Addressing, and Local Proof Objects
AppD — Registry (IDs, Profiles, Pinned Policies)
Station role: profile pinning + registry discipline; prevents silent forks.Purpose: define Ms⟨mmmm⟩ IDs, profile digests, pinned policies; registry as the anchor of interpretation and routing stability.
□ D.S — Square: Registry Data Model, IDs, and Mandatory Manifests
D.S1 — Objects
D.S1.a — Canonical bytes and digestsLet (\mathsf{ser}(\cdot)) be the pinned canonical serialization (AppA CanonBytesSpec). Let (\mathsf{H}(\cdot)) be the pinned digest function. For any object (X),[\mathsf{did}(X) := \mathsf{H}(\mathsf{ser}(X)).]All registry keys, values, and certificates are computed only from (\mathsf{ser}) and (\mathsf{H}) under pinned versions.
D.S1.b — ID typesIDs are stable, typed, canonical references.
MsID (manuscript identifier): textual form Ms⟨Hex⟩, value is 128-bit (or larger, pinned) derived deterministically (D.S2.a).
ProfileID: typed identifier for profile objects; derived deterministically (D.S2.b).
PolicyID: typed identifier for policy packs; derived deterministically (D.S2.c).
SchemaID: typed identifier for schema objects; derived deterministically.
RouterID / CorridorID / GrammarID / CanonBytesID / EnvPinsID: typed identifiers for mandatory interpretation components.
Each ID type is a pair (\langle \textsf{type_tag}, \textsf{value}\rangle) where (\textsf{type_tag}) is a pinned enum and (\textsf{value}) is a fixed-length byte string encoded as hex in canonical form.
D.S1.c — Manifest schema (mandatory digests)A Manifest is the minimal record required to interpret any published artifact set under deterministic routing and verification. Manifest is mandatory for: manuscripts, bundles, profiles, corridors, routers, and replay harnesses.
[\mathsf{Manifest} :=\langle\mathsf{ManifestVer},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{MsID},;\mathsf{PolicyID},;\mathsf{RouterID},;\mathsf{CorridorID},;\mathsf{GrammarID},;\mathsf{CanonBytesID},;\mathsf{EnvPinsID},;\mathsf{SchemaSetDigest},;\mathsf{RevocationSetDigest},;\mathsf{PulsePolicyDigest},;\mathsf{SignaturePolicyDigest},;\mathsf{Issuer},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Mandatory fields and constraints:
RouterID, CorridorID, GrammarID, PolicyID, CanonBytesID, EnvPinsID are mandatory and must resolve by digest in the registry.
SchemaSetDigest must resolve to the complete schema closure required to interpret all objects referenced by the manifest.
RevocationSetDigest must resolve to the revocation policy inputs used by import verification.
PulsePolicyDigest must resolve to the PulseID mapping policy (Ch20).
The manifest must be signed (or explicitly marked unsigned under a pinned signature policy that permits it).
A manifest lacking any mandatory digest is invalid for OK routing and must be treated as non-importable under strict import policies.
D.S1.d — RegistrySnapshot and RegistryLogThe registry is an append-only system with snapshot views.
RegistrySnapshot:[\mathsf{RegSnap} :=\langle\mathsf{SnapVer},;\mathsf{PulseID},;\mathsf{PrevSnapDigest},;\mathsf{EntrySetDigest},;\mathsf{IndexDigest},;\mathsf{PolicyDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]where:
PrevSnapDigest chains snapshots,
EntrySetDigest commits to the canonical set of entries,
IndexDigest commits to canonical indices,
PolicyDigest pins registry rules used to build the snapshot.
RegistryLog is the append-only sequence of registry update events expressed as DeltaPacks (Ch20). The authoritative state at pulse (p) is the deterministic replay of all registry DPs up to (p), summarized by (\mathsf{RegSnap}(p)).
D.S1.e — RegistryEntry schemaA RegistryEntry binds a typed key to a value under pinned rules.
[\mathsf{RegEntry} :=\langle\mathsf{Key},;\mathsf{Value},;\mathsf{EntryType},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Supersedes?},;\mathsf{Sig?}\rangle]
Key: typed identifier or typed composite key (e.g., (MsID, ProfileID), (SchemaID), (RouterID)).
Value: either a digest, a structured record digest, or a pointer record containing digest + retrieval info.
EntryType: enum describing semantics:
BIND (key binds to value),
ALIAS (key aliases another key),
MIGRATE (key transitions to new key/value with witness),
REVOKE (value revoked),
FENCE (quarantine/fence entry),
NOTE (non-semantic annotation; forbidden for interpretation-critical keys).
PinsDigest: pin closure required to interpret the entry (at minimum CanonBytesID + PolicyID).
IssuedPulse: Ch20 pulse binding.
Supersedes?: prior entry pointer for the same key (append-only replacement).
Sig?: signature if required by policy for the entry type.
D.S1.f — Profile object schemaA Profile is a pinned interpretation object used by routing and verification (router/corridor/grammar/policy compositions, schema sets, determinism constraints).
[\mathsf{Profile} :=\langle\mathsf{ProfileVer},;\mathsf{ProfileID},;\mathsf{ManifestDigest},;\mathsf{Components},;\mathsf{PolicyClosureDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Components must include at least: RouterID, CorridorID, GrammarID, CanonBytesID, EnvPinsID, and any lane/overlay policies required by routing (Ch19).
PolicyClosureDigest must commit to all policies the profile depends on (including Pulse policy, signature policy, import policy).
Profiles are immutable; updates are represented only as MIGRATE edges with witnesses (D.S2.d).
D.S1.g — PolicyPack schemaA PolicyPack is the pinned set of rules governing interpretation and verification.
[\mathsf{PolicyPack} :=\langle\mathsf{PolicyVer},;\mathsf{PolicyID},;\mathsf{Rules},;\mathsf{TieBreakRules},;\mathsf{ImportRules},;\mathsf{RevocationRules},;\mathsf{PulseRules},;\mathsf{SchemaRules},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
All rule sets are objects referenced by digest and must be canonically serialized.
D.S2 — Operators
D.S2.a — MsID derivation and deterministic collision resolutionLet (\mathsf{ManuscriptSeed}) be the canonical seed record for a manuscript:[\mathsf{ManuscriptSeed}:=\langle \mathsf{ManifestDigest},\ \mathsf{GenesisPulse},\ \mathsf{GenesisPolicyDigest},\ \mathsf{Issuer}\rangle]with canonical serialization.
Define the base MsID candidate:[\mathsf{MsID}0 := \mathrm{Trunc}{128}\big(\mathsf{H}(\textsf{"MsID"}\ |\ \mathsf{did}(\mathsf{ManuscriptSeed}))\big)]encoded as Ms⟨Hex⟩.
Collision resolution is deterministic:
Let (\mathsf{MsID}i := \mathrm{Trunc}{128}\big(\mathsf{H}(\textsf{"MsID/"}i\ |\ \mathsf{did}(\mathsf{ManuscriptSeed}))\big)) for (i\ge 1).If (\mathsf{MsID}_0) is already bound to a different manuscript seed digest, choose the smallest (i\ge 1) such that (\mathsf{MsID}_i) is unbound or bound to the same seed digest. Record the collision resolution as a registry event with:
EntryType=NOTE forbidden; collision resolution must be BIND plus a CollisionRecord artifact signed under policy.
Any binding of a MsID must include the manuscript seed digest in its value payload to prevent silent forks.
D.S2.b — ProfileID derivationDefine:[\mathsf{ProfileID} := \mathrm{Trunc}_{128}\big(\mathsf{H}(\textsf{"ProfileID"}\ |\ \mathsf{did}(\mathsf{Profile}))\big)]where (\mathsf{Profile}) is serialized with ProfileID field zeroed. Collision handling follows the same deterministic suffix rule as MsID and must be recorded as a signed collision record if it occurs.
D.S2.c — PolicyID derivationDefine:[\mathsf{PolicyID} := \mathrm{Trunc}_{128}\big(\mathsf{H}(\textsf{"PolicyID"}\ |\ \mathsf{did}(\mathsf{PolicyPack}))\big)]with analogous deterministic collision handling.
D.S2.d — Profile lifecycle operators (create, pin, migrate, revoke)
CreateProfile[\mathsf{CreateProfile}(\mathsf{Manifest}, \mathsf{Components}, \mathsf{PolicyClosure}) \to \mathsf{Profile}]Requirements:
all component digests resolve,
manifest mandatory digests present,
schema pin closure present,
profile signed under signature policy.
PinProfilePinning is binding a ProfileID to a stable registry entry:[\mathsf{PinProfile}(\mathsf{Profile}) \to \mathsf{RegEntry}]EntryType = BIND, Key = ProfileID, Value = (\mathsf{did}(\mathsf{Profile})).
MigrateProfileMigration is append-only evolution:[\mathsf{MigrateProfile}(\mathsf{ProfileID}{old},\mathsf{ProfileID}{new},\mathsf{MigrateWitness}) \to (\mathsf{RegEntry},\mathsf{Cert})]Requirements:
new profile object exists and is pinned,
MIGRATE witness certificate exists and verifies,
migration policy allows the transition,
migration is recorded as EntryType=MIGRATE with a payload referencing witness digest.
RevokeProfile / RevokeDigestRevocation is a signed registry entry:[\mathsf{Revoke}(d,\mathsf{Reason},\mathsf{EffectivePulse}) \to \mathsf{RegEntry}]EntryType = REVOKE, Key = digest or typed key, Value includes reason and effective pulse. Revocation must be signed by authorized revocation authority.
Revocation is never deletion; it is an overlay constraint applied by import verification and routing.
D.S2.e — Registry queries as deterministic functionsAll registry queries are pure functions of a RegistrySnapshot digest and query input.
Let (\mathsf{RegSnap}) be the pinned snapshot. Define:
ResolveKey:[\mathsf{ResolveKey}(\mathsf{RegSnap}, \mathsf{Key}) \to \mathsf{Value} \cup \bot]Returns the latest effective binding for Key, after applying:
MIGRATE chains,
revocation overlays,
fences/quarantines,under pinned resolution policy.
ResolveProfile:[\mathsf{ResolveProfile}(\mathsf{RegSnap}, \mathsf{ProfileID}) \to \mathsf{ProfileDigest} \cup \bot]Must verify profile not revoked and schema pins are compatible with the caller policy.
ResolveManifest:[\mathsf{ResolveManifest}(\mathsf{RegSnap}, \mathsf{MsID}) \to \mathsf{ManifestDigest} \cup \bot]Must resolve manuscript seed binding deterministically.
ListActive:[\mathsf{ListActive}(\mathsf{RegSnap}, \mathsf{TypeTag}) \to \text{canonical ordered list of keys}]Ordering is pinned (lexicographic by canonical key bytes).
No query may depend on external state beyond the snapshot and pinned policies. Any caching must be keyed by snapshot digest and query digest and must not affect results.
D.S3 — Invariants
D.S3.a — No silent forks invariantFor any typed key (k) and snapshot (\mathsf{RegSnap}), the resolution of (k) is unique:[\left|{\mathsf{Value} : \mathsf{ResolveKey}(\mathsf{RegSnap},k)=\mathsf{Value}}\right|\le 1.]If multiple distinct values are admissible under the same pins, the registry is in CONFLICT state and must be fenced; routing must treat affected keys as non-OK-routable until resolved by explicit governance actions.
D.S3.b — Append-only registry invariantRegistry evolves only by DeltaPacks. No entry is deleted. Supersession is explicit via Supersedes? pointers and MIGRATE edges. Snapshot chain is linear in pulse order and anchored by previous snapshot digest.
D.S3.c — Mandatory digest completeness invariantAny Manifest registered as deployable or publishable must contain the mandatory digests (router/corridor/grammar/policy/canonbytes/envpins/schema set/revocation/pulse policy). Missing mandatory digests forbids OK routing and import acceptance under strict policies.
D.S3.d — Deterministic collision handling invariantIf collisions occur, resolution is deterministic, minimal index is chosen, and a signed collision record is appended. Any non-deterministic collision resolution is forbidden.
D.S4 — Protocols
D.S4.a — Registry update protocol (DeltaPack)All registry modifications are expressed as DeltaPack ops (Ch20). The protocol for applying registry DPs is:
Validate DP signature and policy epoch compatibility.
Validate canonical serialization digests for all referenced objects.
Apply ops in deterministic order; reject any op that would overwrite an existing binding without explicit supersession linkage.
Recompute indices and snapshot digests deterministically.
Emit RegistryCert and, if applicable, ForkPreventionCert.
D.S4.b — Registry snapshot protocolAt each PulseID (p), compute (\mathsf{RegSnap}(p)) as a deterministic function of:
previous snapshot digest,
all registry DPs in pulse order,
pinned resolution policy,
pinned canonicalization.
D.S4.c — Import-side registry validation protocolImport verification must:
verify registry snapshot chain,
verify all referenced manifests and profiles by digest,
apply revocations deterministically,
reject or quarantine based on policy.
D.S4.d — Deterministic resolution protocol for “current profile”If policy defines a “current” profile per manuscript, resolution must be deterministic and pinned, e.g.:
latest-by-PulseID among non-revoked profiles,
authority-rank tie-break,
digest lexicographic final tie-break.
Any ambiguity yields AMBIG or CONFLICT depending on whether an evidence plan exists; OK routing is forbidden in ambiguity.
❀ D.F — Flower: Interpretation Stability, Policy Epochs, and Semantic Continuity
D.F1 — Objects
D.F1.a — Interpretation closureAn InterpretationClosure is the minimal set of pinned objects required to interpret a corpus element:[\mathsf{IC} := \langle \mathsf{CanonBytesID},\ \mathsf{GrammarID},\ \mathsf{PolicyID},\ \mathsf{SchemaSetDigest},\ \mathsf{EnvPinsID} \rangle.]Every routable claim must carry an IC digest in its pin closure.
D.F1.b — Policy epochA policy epoch is identified by (\mathsf{PolicyID}). Changing policy epoch is meaning-bearing unless a MigrationWitness certifies equivalence of interpretation closure. Policy epoch changes are recorded as registry entries and referenced by manifests.
D.F2 — Operators
D.F2.a — Continuity predicateDefine a continuity predicate:[\mathsf{Continuous}(\mathsf{IC}{old},\mathsf{IC}{new}) \in {\mathsf{true},\mathsf{false}}]which is true only if the pinned migration policy provides an explicit witness that interpretation semantics are preserved. Otherwise, claims must be re-validated under the new closure and cannot be treated as OK by inheritance.
D.F3 — Invariants
D.F3.a — Interpretation anchoring invariantAny route plan claiming OK must pin a single interpretation closure for each scope. Mixing closures without explicit EQUIV/MIGRATE witnesses is forbidden.
D.F3.b — Manifest coherence invariantManifest digests must resolve to policies and schemas that mutually agree on canonical encoding and grammar. Any mismatch is an import failure or quarantine condition.
D.F4 — Protocols
D.F4.a — Policy upgrade protocolPolicy changes are introduced only by:
new PolicyPack object,
registry binding,
optional migration witness that states what remains equivalent and what requires revalidation.
☁ D.C — Cloud: Ambiguity, Conflicts, Revocations, and Quarantine Semantics
D.C1 — Objects
D.C1.a — Fork recordA fork is a situation where the same typed key can resolve to multiple distinct values under identical pins. A ForkRecord is:[\mathsf{ForkRecord}:=\langle \mathsf{Key},\ \mathsf{Values},\ \mathsf{Witnesses},\ \mathsf{PulseID},\ \mathsf{ResolutionPolicyDigest}\rangle.]
D.C1.b — Quarantine recordA QuarantineRecord is a registry entry that marks a key/value as non-OK-routable:[\mathsf{QuarantineRecord}:=\langle \mathsf{Target},\ \mathsf{Reason},\ \mathsf{EffectivePulse},\ \mathsf{EvidenceRefs}\rangle.]
D.C2 — Operators
D.C2.a — Deterministic quarantine propagationQuarantine propagation computes the closure of quarantined digests through dependency closures. Propagation is deterministic and pinned by policy.
D.C3 — Invariants
D.C3.a — Revocation precedence invariantRevocation masks bindings: a revoked digest cannot be returned by ResolveKey/ResolveProfile unless policy explicitly permits quarantined resolution; such permission must be explicit and never treated as OK.
D.C3.b — Conflict classification invariantIf two admissible interpretations exist and neither is disambiguated by pinned policy, the result is CONFLICT, not OK; affected routes must be fenced.
D.C4 — Protocols
D.C4.a — Conflict response protocolOn fork detection:
Emit ForkRecord.
Emit quarantine entries for affected keys.
Require explicit governance action: either MIGRATE to unify, or explicit selection by new pinned policy with witness.
✶ D.R — Fractal: Replayable Registry Evolution, Fork Prevention, and Certificates
D.R1 — Objects
D.R1.a — RegistryCertA RegistryCert attests:
snapshot digest correctness,
entry set correctness,
index digest correctness,
mandatory manifest digests present where required,
deterministic resolution procedures.
Minimum fields:[\mathsf{RegistryCert}:=\langle \mathsf{RegSnapDigest},\ \mathsf{PulseID},\ \mathsf{PolicyDigest},\ \mathsf{VerifierDigest},\ \mathsf{Result},\ \mathsf{Sig}\rangle.]
D.R1.b — ForkPreventionCertA ForkPreventionCert attests that within a defined scope:
no typed key resolves to multiple values under identical pins,
all collisions are either absent or resolved deterministically with signed collision records,
all forks are quarantined and fenced.
Minimum fields:[\mathsf{ForkPreventionCert}:=\langle \mathsf{RegSnapDigest},\ \mathsf{Scope},\ \mathsf{ForkSetDigest},\ \mathsf{QuarantineSetDigest},\ \mathsf{VerifierDigest},\ \mathsf{Result},\ \mathsf{Sig}\rangle.]
D.R2 — Operators
D.R2.a — Snapshot replay operator[\mathsf{ReplayRegistry}(\mathsf{GenesisSnap}, {\mathsf{DP}}_{\le p}, \mathsf{PolicyEpochs}) \to \mathsf{RegSnap}(p)]Deterministic replay must reproduce snapshot digest exactly. Any mismatch yields FAIL/CONFLICT per policy and must be recorded as a conflict packet.
D.R3 — Invariants
D.R3.a — Replay closure invariantRegistry state is defined by replay; snapshots are summaries. Any consumer must be able to reconstruct snapshot digests from the DP stream and pinned policy.
D.R3.b — No hidden state invariantNo registry query or resolution may depend on hidden state. All required state is pinned and content-addressed (snapshots + DP stream + policy).
D.R4 — Protocols
D.R4.a — Certificate issuance protocolAt each pulse:
Compute snapshot deterministically.
Verify mandatory-digest completeness for newly registered manifests and profiles.
Detect collisions and forks; apply deterministic quarantine.
Emit RegistryCert and ForkPreventionCert.
Append certificates as DeltaPack additions.
AppD Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
Registry is append-only and replay-defined; snapshots are deterministic summaries pinned to PulseID.
Manifests require mandatory digests: router, corridor, grammar, policy, canonbytes, envpins, schema set, revocation set, pulse policy, signature policy.
MsID/ProfileID/PolicyID are deterministically derived from canonical serialized objects with domain separation; collisions are resolved deterministically by minimal index rehash and recorded as signed collision records.
Profiles are immutable; lifecycle is create → pin → migrate → revoke, with migration requiring explicit witnesses and revocation requiring authorized signatures.
Registry queries are pure functions of snapshot digest and query input; no hidden state; deterministic tie-breakers are pinned.
RegistryCert and ForkPreventionCert are required; forks are quarantined and fenced; OK routing is forbidden through unresolved ambiguity.
AppD — Registry (IDs, Profiles, Pinned Policies)
AppE — Circle Gear, Phase Profiles, and Tick/Carry Semantics
Station role: ○ gear mechanics; phase profiles and carry semantics.Purpose: formalize phase representations, refinement policies, and tick/carry rules; provide replayable phase evolution and alignment hooks.
□ E.S — Square: PhaseProfile Objects and Discrete Circle Carriers
E.S1 — Objects
E.S1.a — Circle carriers (coarse and refined)A phase carrier is a finite cyclic group (\Sigma_N := \mathbb{Z}_N) for a pinned integer (N\ge 2).
Two canonical ring sizes are required:
Coarse ring: (N=15), denoted (\Sigma_{15}), used as the 15-station metro carrier.
Cross-dimensional refined ring: (N=B_d), denoted (\Sigma_{B_d}), where:[B_d := 15\cdot 3^{d-1}.]The refined ring refines the 15-station carrier by a factor (3^{d-1}) internal strata per station.
E.S1.b — PhaseProfile schema (mandatory)A PhaseProfile is the pinned policy object defining the representation, refinement, and stepping semantics of circle evolution.
[\mathsf{PhaseProfile} :=\langle\mathsf{PhaseVer},;\mathsf{PhaseID},;\mathsf{Mode},;\mathsf{Dim},;\mathsf{RingSize},;\mathsf{RefineRule},;\mathsf{DigitDecomp},;\mathsf{AlignSchedule},;\mathsf{BoundaryPolicy},;\mathsf{TickPolicy},;\mathsf{InverseTickPolicy},;\mathsf{CarryPolicy},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Required fields:
PhaseID: content-addressed identifier (\mathsf{did}(\mathsf{PhaseProfile})) with PhaseID field zeroed.
Mode: enum {COARSE_15, REFINED_Bd, CUSTOM}.
Dim: dimension (d\in\mathbb{N}_{\ge 1}) if Mode=REFINED_Bd; otherwise Dim=⊥ must be explicit.
RingSize: integer (N) with:
Mode=COARSE_15 ⇒ (N=15),
Mode=REFINED_Bd ⇒ (N=B_d),
Mode=CUSTOM ⇒ (N) pinned and justified by explicit corridor policy.
RefineRule: pinned rule describing refinement between ring sizes (see E.S2.c).
DigitDecomp: pinned digit decomposition policy (gear stack), see E.S1.c.
AlignSchedule: pinned schedule specifying how phases align to StationHeader and to higher-level lanes/arcs (see E.S1.d).
BoundaryPolicy: pinned boundary convention for quantization and wrap boundaries.
TickPolicy: pinned definition of tick step(s) (\Delta) and step selection rules.
InverseTickPolicy: pinned definition of inverse tick and its domain of validity.
CarryPolicy: pinned carry extraction, carry logging, and carry propagation semantics.
PinsDigest: digest of full pin closure required to interpret and replay phase evolution.
SchemaPins: schema closure required to interpret phase artifacts.
Sig: signature under pinned signature policy.
E.S1.c — Digit decomposition (macro station + stratum digits)For Mode=REFINED_Bd with (N=B_d), define:
macro station width (W_d := 3^{d-1})
station projection:[\pi_{\mathrm{st}}^{(d)}(u) := \left\lfloor \frac{u}{W_d}\right\rfloor \in \Sigma_{15}]
stratum coordinate:[\pi_{\mathrm{str}}^{(d)}(u) := u \bmod W_d \in \Sigma_{W_d}]
ternary gear digits:[\pi_{\mathrm{str}}^{(d)}(u) = \sum_{i=1}^{d-1} t_i \cdot 3^{d-1-i},\quad t_i\in{0,1,2}.]
DigitDecomp must pin:
digit order (most-significant-first),
encoding/decoding procedures,
and canonical ordering for digit lists.
E.S1.d — Alignment scheduleAlignSchedule is a pinned function:[\mathsf{Align} : (\mathsf{PulseID},\ \mathsf{StationHeader},\ \mathsf{PhaseProfile}) \to \mathsf{PhaseAnchor}]where (\mathsf{PhaseAnchor}) is a canonical reference point in (\Sigma_N) or in (\mathbb{T}^1) if a continuous representation is used.
AlignSchedule must specify:
whether alignment is by omega (station ordinal), by lane, by arc, by triad role, or by explicit anchor tables,
the exact mapping formula or lookup table,
and how alignment interacts with refinement (coarse→refined mapping) and with tick indexing.
E.S2 — Operators
E.S2.a — Tick operator (deterministic translation)Given ring size (N) and step size (s\in\Sigma_N), define:[\mathsf{Tick}_{N,s}(u) := u + s \pmod N.]TickPolicy must define one of:
Fixed step: (s) is a pinned constant.
Scheduled step: (s = s(k,\Pi)) is a pinned deterministic function of step index (k) and pins (\Pi).
Set step: (s\in S\subseteq\Sigma_N) chosen by pinned tie-break rules from a candidate set (no unpinned choice).
Tick operator must emit:
next state (u'),
carry log entries as required by CarryPolicy,
and a tick witness record (E.S3).
E.S2.b — Inverse tick operator (when declared)If InverseTickPolicy declares invertibility, it must supply:[\mathsf{InvTick}_{N,s}(u) := u - s \pmod N,]together with a domain declaration specifying when inverse is admissible. If the tick is scheduled and depends on (k), inverse must be defined relative to the same pinned schedule and must include the required step index or schedule witness.
If invertibility is not declared, inverse tick must not be assumed.
E.S2.c — Refinement operator between ring sizesFor refined mode:[B_{d+1}=3B_d.]Define projection:[\pi_{d+1\to d}(u) := \left\lfloor \frac{u}{3}\right\rfloor \in \Sigma_{B_d}.]Define lifts:[\lambda_{d\to d+1}^{(t)}(u) := 3u + t,\quad t\in{0,1,2}.]
RefineRule must pin:
which projections/lifts are used,
how lift digit (t) is selected (pinned by corridor/triangle policy),
boundary behavior and tie-break rules.
E.S2.d — Carry extraction and loggingCarryPolicy defines:
the carry boundary sets,
the carry extraction function,
and the log schema.
Minimum carry extraction for refined mode uses the macro/stratum decomposition.
Let (u = W_d \sigma + \gamma). For a tick by step (s\in\Sigma_{B_d}), define:[u' = (u+s)\bmod B_d,\quad u' = W_d\sigma' + \gamma'.]Define carry event when macro station index changes:[\mathsf{Carry} := \mathbf{1}{\sigma'\neq \sigma}.]Optionally, define carry magnitude as:[\mathsf{CarryMag} := (\sigma'-\sigma)\bmod 15.]CarryPolicy must pin:
whether carry is boolean or magnitude,
whether stratum boundary carries are logged,
and whether carry propagation across axes (for (\mathbb{T}^d)) is enabled.
Carry logs must be emitted in a canonical order and must include:
prior state digest,
tick step digest,
boundary condition digest,
and resulting state digest.
E.S3 — Phase Witness Formats (Ch16/Ch17 dependency)
E.S3.a — TickWitnessA TickWitness is the minimal witness artifact produced by a tick:
[\mathsf{TickWitness} :=\langle\mathsf{PhaseID},;\mathsf{PulseID},;k,;N,;u,;s,;u',;\mathsf{CarrySummary},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{TickDigest}\rangle]where:
(k) is the tick index,
(u) is previous phase state,
(s) is the step (or step selector digest),
(u') is next phase state,
CarrySummary includes carry events and boundary digests,
TickDigest is (\mathsf{did}(\mathsf{TickWitness})) with TickDigest field zeroed.
TickWitness must be sufficient to replay the tick under pinned policy.
E.S3.b — CarryLogRecordA CarryLogRecord is emitted when carry boundaries are crossed:
[\mathsf{CarryLogRecord} :=\langle\mathsf{PhaseID},;\mathsf{PulseID},;k,;N,;u,;s,;u',;\mathsf{CarryType},;\mathsf{CarryValue},;\mathsf{BoundaryDigest},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{RecordDigest}\rangle]
CarryType ∈ {MACRO_CARRY, STRATUM_CARRY, AXIS_CARRY, CUSTOM} pinned by policy. BoundaryDigest must commit to the boundary rule definition used for this record.
E.S3.c — AlignmentWitnessAn AlignmentWitness binds station header alignment to phase state:
[\mathsf{AlignmentWitness} :=\langle\mathsf{PhaseID},;\mathsf{StationAddr},;\mathsf{StationHeaderDigest},;\mathsf{AlignScheduleDigest},;\mathsf{AnchorValue},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{AlignDigest}\rangle]
AnchorValue is a canonical representative of the anchor in (\Sigma_N) (or in (\mathbb{T}^1) if continuous anchor is declared), and must be derivable deterministically.
E.S4 — Invariants
E.S4.a — Deterministic evolution invariantFor fixed PhaseProfile and fixed pinned environment:[(u,k,\Pi) \mapsto u' \text{ is deterministic.}]This implies (\mathsf{did}(\mathsf{TickWitness})) is deterministic for the same inputs.
E.S4.b — Inverse correctness invariant (when declared)If InverseTickPolicy declares invertibility, then for all admissible (u):[\mathsf{InvTick}{N,s}(\mathsf{Tick}{N,s}(u)) = u.]If the tick is scheduled by (k), then:[\mathsf{InvTick}(k+1,\Pi)(\mathsf{Tick}(k,\Pi)(u)) = u]with admissibility conditions pinned in policy.
E.S4.c — Refinement coherence invariantFor refined profiles:[\pi_{d+1\to d}(\lambda_{d\to d+1}^{(t)}(u)) = u]for all (u) and all (t). Any digit selection policy affects which refined child is chosen, but projection must always return the parent.
E.S4.d — Carry log completeness invariantIf CarryPolicy requires carry logging, then every carry event must be logged, and the carry log digest must match the deterministic recomputation from the tick transcript. Missing carry logs is a deterministic failure.
E.S5 — Protocols
E.S5.a — Phase execution protocol (used by Ch16)Given UnifiedState at step (k), PhaseProfile, and pins:
Compute step size (s) deterministically from TickPolicy.
Compute (u'=\mathsf{Tick}_{N,s}(u)).
Compute carry events and boundary digests per CarryPolicy.
Emit TickWitness and CarryLogRecord(s) as required.
Return (u') and the emitted witness artifacts.
E.S5.b — Phase refinement protocolGiven phase state (u_d \in \Sigma_{B_d}) and desired refinement (d\to d+1):
Determine lift digit (t\in{0,1,2}) using pinned lift selection rules (may depend on triangle/corridor policy).
Compute (u_{d+1}=\lambda_{d\to d+1}^{(t)}(u_d)).
Emit refinement witness including digit selection justification pins.
E.S5.c — Phase import protocol (used by AppN/AppO)On import, PhaseProfile and all pinned schedules must be validated. Any missing policy digest yields non-OK import classification. Phase state must be validated as belonging to (\Sigma_N) and must be consistent with any declared refinement commitments.
❀ E.F — Flower: Continuous Phase Representation and Quantization Hooks
E.F1 — Objects
E.F1.a — Continuous phase formA continuous phase is (\phi\in\mathbb{T}^1) (or (\Phi\in\mathbb{T}^d)). If a continuous representation is enabled, PhaseProfile must pin:
quantization operator (Q_d(\phi)=\lfloor B_d \phi \rfloor) with boundary policy,
inverse mapping to interval representatives,
and equivalence class semantics for boundary points.
E.F1.b — Phase metricA pinned circular metric:[\mathrm{dist}_{\mathbb{T}^1}(a,b)=\min{|(a-b)\bmod 1|,\ 1-| (a-b)\bmod 1|}]is required when NEAR bounds or alignment residuals are used.
E.F2 — Operators
E.F2.a — Quantize-to-ring operator[Q_N(\phi)=\left\lfloor N\phi \right\rfloor \in \Sigma_N]with pinned boundary policy.
E.F2.b — Dequantize interval representativeA pinned representative function:[\mathsf{Rep}_N(u)=\frac{u+\beta}{N},\quad \beta\in[0,1]]with (\beta) pinned (e.g., (\beta=\tfrac12) for center).
E.F3 — Invariants
E.F3.a — Boundary determinismIf (\phi) lies on a quantization boundary, boundary policy pins must force a unique representative. Otherwise the operation is AMBIG.
E.F3.b — Alignment residual invariantsAlignmentWitness may include residuals:[r = \mathrm{dist}{\mathbb{T}^1}(\phi,\phi{\mathrm{anchor}})]with pinned metric digest and bound for NEAR.
☁ E.C — Cloud: Uncertainty, NEAR, and Phase Drift Ledgers
E.C1 — Objects
E.C1.a — PhaseResidualLedgerA PhaseResidualLedger is required for NEAR phase claims:
[\mathsf{PhaseResidualLedger} :=\langle\mathsf{MetricDigest},;\mathsf{Bound},;\mathsf{Observed},;\mathsf{Expected},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{ExpiryPulse},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{LedgerDigest}\rangle]
Scope binds whether the ledger applies to:
a specific tick,
a range of ticks,
an alignment schedule,
or a refinement mapping.
E.C2 — Operators
E.C2.a — Drift monitoring functionA pinned function mapping tick witnesses and alignments to drift measures. Drift is observational and must not affect tick semantics.
E.C3 — Invariants
E.C3.a — No silent NEARAny non-zero residual in claimed deterministic equality must be represented as NEAR with a ledger, or must be FAIL if the corridor forbids approximation.
✶ E.R — Fractal: Replay Closure and PhaseReplayCert
E.R1 — Objects
E.R1.a — PhaseReplayCapsuleA PhaseReplayCapsule contains:
PhaseProfile digest,
initial phase state (u_0),
tick count (K),
pinned tick schedule inputs,
expected sequence digest commitments:
tick witness digests,
carry log digests,
final state digest.
E.R2 — Operators
E.R2.a — Phase replay executorDeterministic replay:[(u_0,\Pi,\mathsf{PhaseProfile},K)\to (u_K,\mathsf{TickWitnesses},\mathsf{CarryLogs})]and all digests must match expected commitments.
E.R3 — Invariants
E.R3.a — Replay determinism invariantFor identical inputs and pins, the replay produces identical witness digests and final state digest.
E.R3.b — Schedule determinism invariantIf the tick schedule depends on (k) or other context, schedule derivation must be pinned and must be recorded in TickWitness or in schedule witness artifacts.
E.R4 — Required Certificate
E.R4.a — PhaseReplayCertA PhaseReplayCert attests that phase evolution replays identically under pinned environment and policy.
Minimum fields:[\mathsf{PhaseReplayCert} :=\langle\mathsf{PhaseProfileDigest},;\mathsf{CapsuleDigest},;\mathsf{EnvPinsDigest},;\mathsf{ExpectedFinalDigest},;\mathsf{ObservedFinalDigest},;\mathsf{WitnessDigestSet},;\mathsf{Result},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]where Result is PASS iff all expected digests match observed digests, including carry logs.
AppE Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
PhaseProfile pins ring size (N), refinement rule, digit decomposition, alignment schedule, boundary policy, tick and inverse-tick policies, carry policy, and pin closure digest.
Tick is a deterministic translation on (\Sigma_N); step selection is pinned; inverse tick is permitted only when explicitly declared and witnessed.
Carry semantics and carry boundary logging are pinned; required carry events must be logged deterministically with boundary rule digests.
For refined profiles (N=B_d), macro station and stratum decomposition is canonical; refinement satisfies (B_{d+1}=3B_d) with pinned lift digit selection and deterministic projection.
Phase witness formats (TickWitness, CarryLogRecord, AlignmentWitness) are mandatory artifacts for Ch16/Ch17 and must be content-addressable.
PhaseReplayCert is required and must validate deterministic replay of tick evolution, carry logs, and final state digests.
AppE — Circle Gear, Phase Profiles, and Tick/Carry Semantics
AppF — Transport (Rotation as Conjugacy), DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE Discipline
Station role: lawful transport; conjugacy-based swaps; corridor budgets.Purpose: define transport legality as a contract over pinned normal forms and budgets; encode DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE semantics and commutation accounting.
□ F.S — Square: Transport Objects, Legality Contracts, and Budgeted Proof Surfaces
F.S1 — Objects
F.S1.a — Typed endpoints and endpoint closureA transport is defined between typed endpoints. An Endpoint is a fully pinned address record:
[\mathsf{Endpoint} :=\langle\mathsf{GlobalAddr},;\mathsf{Lens},;\mathsf{Dim},;\mathsf{Depth},;\mathsf{SchemaPinsDigest},;\mathsf{CanonBytesDigest},;\mathsf{NFProfileDigest},;\mathsf{MetricDigest},;\mathsf{CorridorDigest},;\mathsf{PolicyDigest},;\mathsf{EnvPinsDigest}\rangle]
Endpoint closure rules:
The endpoint is valid only if all referenced digests resolve under import policy.
A transport claim is undefined if either endpoint lacks any required digest field.
F.S1.b — Transport kindsTransport kind vocabulary is closed:
[\mathsf{Kind} := {\mathsf{DUAL},\mathsf{EQUIV},\mathsf{MIGRATE}}.]
A transport edge MUST be exactly one of these kinds. No implicit kind conversion is permitted.
F.S1.c — Budget ledgerTransport is budgeted by a pinned budget vector:
[\mathsf{Budget} := \langle \kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi\rangle]with semantics:
(\kappa): commutation residual budget (holonomy/spin residual capacity)
(\beta): representational drift budget (approximation / metric residual capacity)
(\delta): recursion depth budget (max nested verifications / hatch depth)
(\chi): compute budget (max operations / search / replay cost)
A BudgetLedger records budget usage for an execution:
[\mathsf{BudgetLedger} :=\langle\mathsf{BudgetDigest},;\mathsf{Used}_{\kappa},;\mathsf{Used}_{\beta},;\mathsf{Used}_{\delta},;\mathsf{Used}_{\chi},;\mathsf{ChargeItems}\rangle]
ChargeItems is an ordered list of ledger entries, each binding a charge to a witness digest and a scope.
F.S1.d — Transport schema (declared endpoints + witness + ledger)A TransportEdge is the canonical record:
[\mathsf{TransportEdge} :=\langle\mathsf{EdgeID},;\mathsf{Kind},;\mathsf{Src},;\mathsf{Dst},;\mathsf{MapFwdRef},;\mathsf{MapBwdRef?},;\mathsf{DomainSpec},;\mathsf{InvariantSet},;\mathsf{WitnessBundleRef},;\mathsf{BudgetLedgerRef},;\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaVer}\rangle]
Required fields:
Src/Dst: Endpoint objects.
MapFwdRef: addressable artifact reference to the forward map.
MapBwdRef?: required when invertibility is claimed by invariants or kind.
DomainSpec: declared domain/range restrictions; a transport is undefined outside DomainSpec.
InvariantSet: the set of invariants claimed preserved (NF equality, decode equivalence, commutation constraints, schedule constraints).
WitnessBundleRef: pointer to the witness bundle sufficient to validate the edge.
BudgetLedgerRef: pointer to the ledger produced by evaluation or reserved by policy.
TruthType: {OK, NEAR, AMBIG, FAIL, CONFLICT}.
IssuedPulse: time axis binding (Ch20).
PinsDigest: digest of pin closure required to interpret and replay this transport.
F.S1.e — Witness bundle schemaA witness bundle is a canonical list of addressable artifacts:
[\mathsf{WitnessBundle} :=\langle\mathsf{BundleID},;\mathsf{BundleType},;\mathsf{Artifacts},;\mathsf{ReplayCapsules},;\mathsf{ExpectedDigests},;\mathsf{SchemaPinsDigest},;\mathsf{EnvPinsDigest}\rangle]
BundleType must include at minimum:
DualWitnessBundle
EquivWitnessBundle
MigrateWitnessBundle
CommutationReceiptBundle
ConflictPacketBundle
Artifacts list ordering is canonical by digest.
F.S2 — Operators
F.S2.a — Normal form operator and equality predicateTransport legality is evaluated against pinned normal forms.
For each endpoint, NFProfileDigest pins a canonical normal form operator:[\mathsf{NF} : \mathsf{Payload} \to \mathsf{NFPayload}.]
Define NF equality under pins:[x \equiv_{\mathsf{NF}} y \iff \mathsf{did}(\mathsf{NF}(x)) = \mathsf{did}(\mathsf{NF}(y)).]
NF equality is the default criterion for OK equivalence claims unless the corridor pins an alternative equivalence metric.
F.S2.b — Conjugacy transport of operators (rotation as conjugacy)Let (u:\mathsf{Src}\to\mathsf{Dst}) be an invertible transport with inverse (u^{-1}). For any endomorphism (A) on Src, define pushforward:[u_{\ast}A := u\circ A\circ u^{-1}.]For any endomorphism (B) on Dst, define pullback:[u^{\ast}B := u^{-1}\circ B\circ u.]Conjugacy is the only permitted meaning-preserving operator transport semantics when invertibility is claimed.
F.S2.c — Transport evaluation operatorDefine:[\mathsf{EvalTransport} : (\mathsf{TransportEdge}, \mathsf{CorridorSpec}) \to (\mathsf{TruthType}, \mathsf{BudgetLedger}, \mathsf{WitnessBundle})]Deterministic under pins. It must:
validate endpoint pins,
validate map digests and schema pins,
validate domain applicability,
evaluate invariant checks,
compute commutation receipts when required,
produce budget charges and truth typing.
F.S2.d — Composition of transports (path)A transport path is a sequence of transport edges:[P = (e_1,\dots,e_n)]where (e_i:\mathsf{V}_{i-1}\to\mathsf{V}_i). The composite map exists only if domain/range specs compose. Truth typing is the meet of edge truth types under corridor ordering; budget usage aggregates under pinned ledger rules.
F.S3 — Invariants
F.S3.a — Kind-specific admissibility invariants
DUAL invariant. DUAL is permitted only for adjacent lens swaps under a pinned adjacency profile; adjacency must be validated by witness bundle. DUAL must not be used to encode non-adjacent swaps; those require explicit chains or EQUIV/MIGRATE.
EQUIV invariant. EQUIV requires:
explicit forward and backward maps over declared domain,
proof that the round trip preserves NF (or pinned equivalence metric),
replay closure producing expected digests.
MIGRATE invariant. MIGRATE is required when:
interpretation pins change,
NF profiles change,
schemas change,
semantic invariants are intentionally modified,
or prior EQUIV claims no longer hold under the new pin closure.MIGRATE must include compatibility matrices, rollback plan, and import constraints.
F.S3.b — No silent equivalenceNo transport can be treated as semantic equivalence without an explicit EQUIV witness bundle or a DUAL witness bundle validated under corridor rules. REF is not transport.
F.S3.c — Deterministic tie-breaksIf multiple candidate transport paths exist between endpoints, selection is deterministic only if tie-break rules are pinned. Otherwise the path selection must be typed AMBIG with evidence plan.
F.S3.d — Conflict invariantsIf two admissible transport paths produce different NF digests under identical pins and identical inputs, the result is CONFLICT. CONFLICT must produce a conflict packet and trigger quarantine fences.
F.S4 — Protocols
F.S4.a — DUAL protocolA DUAL edge must include:
adjacency proof under pinned adjacency profile,
MapFwd and MapBwd (or explicit non-invertibility statement if corridor allows DUAL without invertibility; default forbids),
NF-preservation check or pinned equivalence metric check,
commutation receipts if required by corridor,
budget ledger and truth typing.
F.S4.b — EQUIV protocolAn EQUIV edge must include:
MapFwd and MapBwd,
DomainSpec and RangeSpec,
proof of round-trip NF equality:[x \equiv_{\mathsf{NF}} (g\circ f)(x)\quad\forall x\in\mathrm{Dom}]and[y \equiv_{\mathsf{NF}} (f\circ g)(y)\quad\forall y\in\mathrm{Range}]
replay capsule proving the above (expected digests pinned),
truth typing and residual ledger if NEAR.
F.S4.c — Transport path agreement protocolIf routing relies on path equivalence:
build a holonomy witness loop and evaluate it under corridor rules,
require commutation receipts and/or path-difference receipts to be OK (or NEAR if allowed with disclosure),
otherwise mark AMBIG/CONFLICT.
❀ F.F — Flower: Commutation Receipts and Spin/Holonomy Witnesses
F.F1 — Objects
F.F1.a — CommutationReceiptA CommutationReceipt is a witness object certifying that two operations commute (or do not) on a declared domain under pinned metrics.
[\mathsf{CommutationReceipt} :=\langle\mathsf{ReceiptID},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{Endpoints},;\mathsf{OpARef},;\mathsf{OpBRef},;\mathsf{LoopRef},;\mathsf{DomainSpec},;\mathsf{MetricDigest},;\mathsf{Residual},;\mathsf{BudgetKappa},;\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse}\rangle]
Where:
LoopRef is the commutator loop:[\mathrm{Spin}(A,B) = A\circ B\circ A^{-1}\circ B^{-1}.]
Residual is the pinned metric distance from identity on the declared domain:[r = d(\mathrm{Spin}(A,B)(x), x).]
Truth typing:
OK if (r=0) under pinned metric and replay closes,
NEAR if (0<r\le \kappa) with residual ledger,
FAIL if (r>\kappa),
CONFLICT if replay disagreement.
F.F1.b — PathDifferenceReceiptA receipt comparing two paths (P,Q:\mathsf{Src}\to\mathsf{Dst}):[\mathsf{Loop}(P,Q)=Q^{-1}\circ P]with residual and truth typing as above.
F.F2 — Operators
F.F2.a — Receipt builderReceipt generation is deterministic: given operator references, domain spec, metric digest, and pins, the builder must produce identical receipt digest.
F.F2.b — Receipt consumption ruleA transport path may claim reorderings or equivalences only if it references receipts whose truth type meets corridor thresholds.
F.F3 — Invariants
F.F3.a — Receipt scope invarianceReceipts are valid only over declared DomainSpec and pinned Endpoint closure. Any scope widening requires a new receipt.
F.F4 — Protocols
F.F4.a — Receipt regression fixturesRegression must include:
commuting pairs that must be OK,
near-commuting pairs that must be NEAR with ledger,
non-commuting pairs that must FAIL,
conflicting replays that must CONFLICT.
☁ F.C — Cloud: Conflict Packet Format and Quarantine Interfaces
F.C1 — Objects
F.C1.a — ConflictPacket (required format)A ConflictPacket is the minimal reproducible contradiction record:
[\mathsf{ConflictPacket} :=\langle\mathsf{ConflictID},;\mathsf{Src},;\mathsf{Dst},;\mathsf{PathARefs},;\mathsf{PathBRefs},;\mathsf{WitnessSet},;\mathsf{ReproRecipe},;\mathsf{ExpectedDigests},;\mathsf{ObservedDigests},;\mathsf{FenceSpec},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Required properties:
WitnessSet is minimal under pinned minimization order (addresses-first then events then fields).
ReproRecipe is deterministic and includes:
pins digest,
replay capsule digests,
environment pins digest,
exact step ordering.
FenceSpec specifies which edges/routes are quarantined and how propagation is computed.
F.C1.b — Quarantine recordA quarantine record is an append-only certificate that masks routes/edges for OK routing until resolved.
F.C2 — Operators
F.C2.a — Conflict classifierIf two admissible transports disagree under identical pins, classify CONFLICT, emit ConflictPacket, and quarantine affected edges and dependent routes.
F.C2.b — Conflict resolutionResolution may occur only via:
new EQUIV witness that collapses the disagreement with replay closure, or
explicit MIGRATE with compat matrix and rollback plan.
F.C3 — Invariants
F.C3.a — No silent conflict resolutionNo conflict may be “resolved” by preference. Resolution must be explicit and evidenced.
F.C4 — Protocols
F.C4.a — Conflict regression fixturesFixtures must include:
deterministic reproduction,
fence propagation correctness,
resolution pathways producing new certs.
✶ F.R — Fractal: MIGRATE Protocol, Compatibility Matrices, Rollback, and Import Constraints
F.R1 — Objects
F.R1.a — CompatibilityMatrixA compatibility matrix binds old/new profiles and specifies what remains valid.
[\mathsf{CompatMatrix} :=\langle\mathsf{OldPinsDigest},;\mathsf{NewPinsDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaChanges},;\mathsf{NFChanges},;\mathsf{MetricChanges},;\mathsf{EdgeKindChanges},;\mathsf{TruthRuleChanges},;\mathsf{ImpactedScopes},;\mathsf{ImpactedClaimsDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
F.R1.b — RollbackPlanA rollback plan is a deterministic mapping from new deployment state back to a pinned prior state:
[\mathsf{RollbackPlan} :=\langle\mathsf{FromProfile},;\mathsf{ToProfile},;\mathsf{TriggerPredicates},;\mathsf{RollbackSteps},;\mathsf{ExpectedDigests},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
F.R1.c — ImportConstraintsA MIGRATE must specify import constraints:
[\mathsf{ImportConstraints} :=\langle\mathsf{MinSchemaVer},;\mathsf{RequiredCerts},;\mathsf{DisallowedOldPins},;\mathsf{MigrationToolsDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
F.R2 — MIGRATE protocol (required)
A MIGRATE edge is required when semantics or interpretation pins change. A valid MIGRATE must include:
Old profile digest and new profile digest.
CompatMatrix with explicit impacted claims and rule changes.
Regression suite proving critical invariants remain valid or are intentionally revised.
RollbackPlan that is deterministic and replay-verifiable.
ImportConstraints that reject silent acceptance of obsolete artifacts.
MigrationCert binding the above and attesting replay closure.
MIGRATE issuance is append-only and binds to PulseID.
F.R3 — Required certificates
F.R3.a — TransportCertA TransportCert certifies that a TransportEdge is valid and its truth type is correctly typed under corridor rules.
Minimum fields:
[\mathsf{TransportCert} :=\langle\mathsf{TransportEdgeDigest},;\mathsf{Kind},;\mathsf{SrcDigest},;\mathsf{DstDigest},;\mathsf{WitnessBundleDigest},;\mathsf{BudgetLedgerDigest},;\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{VerifierDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Verification requires:
endpoint pins resolve,
map digests resolve,
invariant checks and receipts validate,
budget ledger matches computed charges,
replay reproduces digests and truth typing.
F.R3.b — MigrationCertA MigrationCert certifies MIGRATE correctness.
Minimum fields:
[\mathsf{MigrationCert} :=\langle\mathsf{OldProfileDigest},;\mathsf{NewProfileDigest},;\mathsf{CompatMatrixDigest},;\mathsf{RollbackPlanDigest},;\mathsf{ImportConstraintsDigest},;\mathsf{RegressionCertDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayCertDigest},;\mathsf{VerifierDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Verification requires:
all referenced artifacts resolve,
regression suites pass under pinned environment,
replay validates migration mapping and post-migration behavior,
rollback plan is executable and matches expected digests,
import constraints enforce non-silent upgrades.
AppF Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
Transport endpoints are fully pinned Endpoint records; transports are undefined without endpoint closure.
TransportEdge schema must include kind (DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE), explicit maps, domain spec, invariants, witness bundle, budget ledger, truth type, pins digest, issued pulse.
