Rotation as conjugacy is the only meaning-preserving operator transport semantics when invertibility is claimed.
Commutation receipts are required artifacts: Spin/PathDifference loops with residuals typed against (\kappa); replay determinism is mandatory.
Conflicts produce ConflictPackets with minimal witness sets, deterministic reproduction recipes, and quarantine fences; no silent resolution.
MIGRATE protocol requires compatibility matrix, rollback plan, import constraints, regression suites, and MigrationCert; no silent upgrades.
TransportCert and MigrationCert are required, import-verifiable, and bind truth typing and replay closure.
AppF — Transport (Rotation as Conjugacy), DUAL/EQUIV/MIGRATE Discipline
AppG — Triangle Governor, Depth/Recursion Policies, Carry/Hatch Interfaces
Station role: △ control semantics; recursion legality; hatch/carry governance.Purpose: define triangle modes and corridor pinning; formalize how depth, carry, hatch events constrain legal recursion and tunneling.
□ G.S — Square: Triangle Policy Objects, Depth Ledgers, and Legal Recursion Events
G.S1 — Objects
G.S1.a — Triangle carriers and mode policyTriangle is the control plane. Its role is to pin admissible corridors, govern depth/recursion legality, and mediate carry/hatch boundaries.
Triangle phase alphabet:[\mathbb{Z}_3 := {0,1,2}.]
Two admissible mode families are supported; selection is pinned and meaning-bearing.
Global Triangle mode (B):[\mathcal{T}^{B} := \mathbb{Z}_3,\qquad \tau \in \mathcal{T}^{B}.]
Per-axis Triangle mode (A):[\mathcal{T}^{A}_d := (\mathbb{Z}_3)^d,\qquad \boldsymbol{\tau}=(\tau_1,\dots,\tau_d)\in\mathcal{T}^{A}_d.]
A TriangleModePolicy is:[\mathsf{TriMode} :=\langle\mathsf{TriVer},;\mathsf{Mode},;\mathsf{Dim},;\mathsf{QuantizerSpec},;\mathsf{MixSpec?},;\mathsf{AggSpec?},;\mathsf{CorridorPinSpec},;\mathsf{CarrySpec},;\mathsf{HatchSpec},;\mathsf{TieBreakSpec},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]where:
Mode ∈ {AXIS, GLOBAL} selects Option A or B.
Dim is required for AXIS.
QuantizerSpec pins the trit extraction rule.
MixSpec is required for GLOBAL when a scalar triangle is derived from multi-axis state.
AggSpec is optional, but if used it must be pinned.
CorridorPinSpec pins corridor selection rules.
CarrySpec and HatchSpec pin carry/hatch semantics and triggers.
TieBreakSpec pins all tie-breaking across discrete choices.
PinsDigest commits to the full closure required for deterministic governance.
G.S1.b — Corridor pinning as a triangle-governed selectionTriangle pins which corridor profile is active at a step. Corridor selection is not inferred; it is a deterministic function of:
triangle mode state,
pinned corridor policy,
pinned state summaries (phase/square/carriers),
and pinned tie-break rules.
Define:[\mathsf{SelectCorridor} :(\mathsf{TriState},\mathsf{StateSummary},\mathsf{TriMode}) \to \mathsf{CorridorID}]where (\mathsf{CorridorID}) is a digest-qualified corridor profile identifier.
Any corridor change is an explicit event logged to the carry/hatch bus and committed to transcripts. Corridor selection must be replayable from pinned inputs.
G.S1.c — Depth ledger typesTriangle governs recursion depth. A DepthLedger is a canonical record:
[\mathsf{DepthLedger} :=\langle\mathsf{LedgerVer},;\mathsf{PulseID},;\mathsf{Dim},;\mathsf{DepthIndex},;\mathsf{DepthBudget},;\mathsf{ActiveCorridorID},;\mathsf{HatchState},;\mathsf{CarryState},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{LedgerDigest}\rangle]
DepthIndex is the current recursion index (integer).
DepthBudget is the maximum allowed depth under policy.
HatchState and CarryState summarize open recursion windows and carry boundary state.
LedgerDigest is did(DepthLedger) with LedgerDigest field zeroed.
G.S1.d — Carry event schema (triangle-governed carry interface)Carry is the boundary mechanism by which incremental evolution crosses an admissibility threshold and triggers a legal update (e.g., station boundary, hub boundary, phase boundary, policy boundary).
A CarryEvent is:
[\mathsf{CarryEvent} :=\langle\mathsf{CarryVer},;\mathsf{PulseID},;k,;\mathsf{CarryType},;\mathsf{CarryKey},;\mathsf{CarryValue},;\mathsf{BoundaryRuleDigest},;\mathsf{PreStateDigests},;\mathsf{PostStateDigests},;\mathsf{CorridorIDPre},;\mathsf{CorridorIDPost},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{CarryDigest}\rangle]
Required fields:
CarryType ∈ {PHASE_CARRY, HUB_CARRY, DEPTH_CARRY, POLICY_CARRY, CUSTOM} pinned vocabulary.
CarryKey identifies the boundary locus (e.g., station index, hub coordinate, gear digit position, depth boundary).
BoundaryRuleDigest commits to the carry predicate used to decide the event.
PreStateDigests and PostStateDigests are digests of relevant state components.
CorridorIDPre/Post are corridor pins before and after the carry.
CarryDigest is did(CarryEvent) with CarryDigest field zeroed.
CarryEvent ordering is canonical and must be stable under replay.
G.S1.e — Hatch event schema (legal recursion boundary)A HatchEvent is the only legal mechanism to increase depth, spawn a new recursion frame, or introduce a higher-level observer state. Hatch is not “a rewrite”; it is an append-only boundary event.
[\mathsf{HatchEvent} :=\langle\mathsf{HatchVer},;\mathsf{PulseID},;k,;\mathsf{ParentAddr},;\mathsf{ChildAddr},;\mathsf{TriggerDigest},;\mathsf{InheritanceSpecDigest},;\mathsf{ChildInitSpecDigest},;\mathsf{CheckpointRef},;\mathsf{Obligations},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{HatchDigest}\rangle]
Required semantics:
ParentAddr and ChildAddr are explicit; no implicit child creation.
TriggerDigest commits to the hatch predicate evaluation evidence.
InheritanceSpecDigest commits to which profiles/pins are inherited unchanged and which are overridden (overrides must be explicit).
ChildInitSpecDigest commits to child initialization offsets (deterministic).
CheckpointRef is mandatory: hatch creates a checkpoint boundary.
ReplayPtr must reproduce hatch legality and child initialization.
HatchDigest is did(HatchEvent) with HatchDigest field zeroed.
G.S1.f — Triangle state (governor microstate)Triangle’s operational microstate is a fixed trit triple:[G := (t_0,t_1,t_2)\in\mathbb{Z}_3^3]with canonical encoding, used to select control modes, threshold gates, and governance phase under pinned semantics. Any expansion beyond (\mathbb{Z}_3^3) must be a schema-migrated profile, not an implicit extension.
G.S2 — Operators
G.S2.a — Triangle quantization operatorTriangle reads phase/state and produces trits deterministically.
Pinned base quantizer:[Q_3(u) := \lfloor 3u \rfloor \in \mathbb{Z}_3,\quad u\in[0,1).]
Wrapped quantizer at wrap (R):[Q_3^{(R)}(\phi) := Q_3(\mathrm{frac}(R\phi)).]
Option A (axis):[\mathsf{Tri}^{A}_R(\Phi) := (Q_3^{(R)}(\phi_1),\dots,Q_3^{(R)}(\phi_d))\in(\mathbb{Z}_3)^d.]
Option B (global):[\mathsf{Tri}^{B}R(\Phi) := Q_3^{(R)}(\phi{\mathrm{global}}(\Phi))\in\mathbb{Z}3,]where (\phi{\mathrm{global}}) is pinned by MixSpec and must be deterministic.
G.S2.b — Corridor selection operatorGiven triangle mode and state summaries, corridor selection is:[\mathsf{CorridorID} := \mathsf{SelectCorridor}(\mathsf{TriState},\mathsf{StateSummary},\mathsf{TriMode})]where:
StateSummary is a digest-qualified summary of (i) phase carrier state, (ii) square carrier stability markers, (iii) prior carry/hatch states.
SelectCorridor must be deterministic and must emit a selection witness (see G.S3).
G.S2.c — Carry trigger operatorCarry detection is a deterministic predicate family:[\mathsf{CarryTrig} : (\mathsf{PreState},\mathsf{PostState},\mathsf{TriMode},\mathsf{CarrySpec}) \to {\mathsf{true},\mathsf{false}}.]If true, a CarryEvent must be emitted with the boundary rule digest.
Carry types may include:
phase boundary crossing (E ring carry),
hub basin crossing (Ch06 hub mesh),
corridor threshold crossing (Ch08),
or policy epoch boundary crossing (Ch20).
All carry types must be enumerated and pinned; no ad-hoc carry emission is permitted.
G.S2.d — Hatch legality operatorHatch occurs only when the hatch trigger is satisfied and budget allows.
Define:[\mathsf{HatchAllowed} : (\mathsf{DepthLedger},\mathsf{TriggerEvidence},\mathsf{TriMode}) \to {\mathsf{true},\mathsf{false}}]with constraints:
DepthIndex + 1 ≤ DepthBudget
TriggerEvidence verifies under pinned witness rules
InheritanceSpec is valid and pins are complete
CheckpointRef is produced and valid
If HatchAllowed is false and hatch is attempted, the action is illegal and must be recorded as a failure witness and quarantined when applicable.
G.S2.e — TriangleStep operator (used by Ch16)TriangleStep updates:
governor trits (G),
DepthLedger,
and emits carry/hatch events as required.
TriangleStep is a deterministic function:[\mathsf{TriangleStep} : (\mathsf{TriState},\mathsf{StateSummary},\mathsf{TriMode},k,\mathsf{PulseID}) \to (\mathsf{TriState}',\mathsf{DepthLedger}',\mathsf{CarryEvents}^\star,\mathsf{HatchEvents}^\star,\mathsf{Witnesses})]with all outputs canonically ordered and digest-committed.
G.S3 — Witness formats (interfaces to Ch06–Ch10 and Ch16–Ch18)
G.S3.a — CorridorSelectionWitness[\mathsf{CorrSelWit} :=\langle\mathsf{PulseID},;k,;\mathsf{TriModeDigest},;\mathsf{TriStateDigest},;\mathsf{StateSummaryDigest},;\mathsf{SelectedCorridorID},;\mathsf{SelectionRuleDigest},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{WitDigest}\rangle]SelectionRuleDigest pins the exact decision rule; WitDigest is content-addressed.
G.S3.b — TunnelingLegalityWitnessA tunnel step is legal only if it satisfies hub-preserving constraints and corridor constraints. Tunneling legality witness is:
[\mathsf{TunnelLegWit} :=\langle\mathsf{PulseID},;k,;\mathsf{Dim},;\mathsf{PhaseProfileDigest},;\mathsf{HubPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{StepVector},;\mathsf{DomainSpecDigest},;\mathsf{CorridorID},;\mathsf{LegalityResult},;\mathsf{ResidualLedgerRef?},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{WitDigest}\rangle]
LegalityResult ∈ {OK, NEAR, AMBIG, FAIL} typed under corridor rules. NEAR requires residual ledger.
G.S3.c — HatchWitnessA HatchWitness binds the hatch trigger, legality checks, and checkpoint digests:[\mathsf{HatchWit} :=\langle\mathsf{HatchDigest},;\mathsf{TriggerEvidenceDigest},;\mathsf{DepthLedgerPreDigest},;\mathsf{DepthLedgerPostDigest},;\mathsf{CheckpointDigest},;\mathsf{InheritanceSpecDigest},;\mathsf{ChildInitSpecDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{PinsDigest}\rangle]
G.S4 — Invariants
G.S4.a — Pinned mode invariantTriangle mode (AXIS vs GLOBAL) is pinned. Any change requires explicit migration of TriMode policy and must be recorded as an append-only event.
G.S4.b — No silent recursion invariantDepth increases are legal only via HatchEvents that satisfy HatchAllowed and produce checkpoints and replay pointers. Any implicit recursion is illegal.
G.S4.c — Append-only boundary invariantCarry and hatch are boundary events. Boundary semantics cannot be rewritten; they can only be extended with new nodes/edges/certs under the time axis.
G.S4.d — Corridor determinism invariantFor identical inputs and pins, SelectCorridor must produce identical SelectedCorridorID and identical selection witness digest. Any mismatch is CONFLICT.
G.S4.e — Budget adherence invariantHatch and tunneling legality must charge budgets deterministically and must fail when budgets are exceeded. Budget overflow cannot be ignored.
❀ G.F — Flower: Tunneling Legality and Hub-Preserving Constraints (Interface to Ch06–Ch10)
G.F1 — Objects
G.F1.a — Hub mesh and corridor neighborhoodLet (\mathcal{H}^{(d)}\subset\mathbb{T}^d) be the pinned hub mesh. A hub corridor at radius (\rho) is:[\mathrm{Corr}\rho(\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) := \bigcup{\mathbf{h}\in\mathcal{H}^{(d)}} {\Phi\in\mathbb{T}^d:\mathrm{Dist}(\Phi,\mathbf{h})\le \rho}.](\rho) is pinned by corridor spec.
G.F1.b — Allowed step setLet (\Delta\mathcal{H}\subset\mathbb{T}^1) be the pinned allowed 1D step set (e.g., sextile-based family plus fine denominators). The multi-axis step set is:[\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)} := {\delta\in\mathbb{T}^d:\delta_i\in\Delta\mathcal{H}\cup{0}}.]The exact set and its ordering are pinned by HubPolicyDigest.
G.F2 — Operators
G.F2.a — Hub-preserving legality predicateA tunnel step (\delta) applied at phase (\Phi) is legal if:
(\delta\in\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)}),
(\Phi\in\mathrm{Corr}\rho(\mathcal{H}^{(d)})) and (\Phi+\delta \in\mathrm{Corr}\rho(\mathcal{H}^{(d)})),
any required commutation receipts for the step schedule are satisfied (Ch09),
any required meta-zero snap constraints are satisfied or bounded by residual ledger (Ch10),
corridor policy permits the step type under current truth threshold.
Triangle governs which (\rho), which (\Delta\mathcal{H}), and which receipts are required via pinned CorridorPinSpec and HubPolicyDigest.
G.F2.b — Hub-first routing constraintTriangle may require a hub-first plan:[\Phi \to \mathrm{Snap}{\mathcal{H}}(\Phi) \to \cdots \to \mathrm{Snap}{\mathcal{H}}(\Phi')]where Snap is pinned and must preserve coarse hub class under truncation. This requirement is part of corridor pinning and is enforced by TunnelLegalityWitness checks.
G.F3 — Invariants
G.F3.a — Coarse hub class stability under truncationThe pinned hub classifier must be stable under declared truncation operators. Any instability must be treated as AMBIG/FAIL per corridor.
G.F3.b — Visibility and resolution invariantIf the phase profile uses refined ring (B_d), Triangle must enforce that circle resolution is adequate for dimension (d) when tunneling is claimed to be visible; otherwise, the operation is AMBIG due to aliasing.
☁ G.C — Cloud: Truth Typing for Control Actions and Uncertainty Artifacts
G.C1 — Objects
G.C1.a — ControlTruth recordEvery triangle-governed decision emits a truth record:
[\mathsf{CtrlTruth} :=\langle\mathsf{DecisionID},;\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{ResidualLedgerRef?},;\mathsf{EvidencePlanRef?},;\mathsf{ConflictPacketRef?},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse}\rangle]
OK: replay closes and invariants hold exactly.
NEAR: bounded residual ledger is present.
AMBIG: bounded candidate set and evidence plan is present.
FAIL/CONFLICT: failure witness or conflict packet is present.
G.C2 — Operators
G.C2.a — Evidence plan requirementAny nondiscriminated discrete choice (corridor selection among multiple candidates, lift digit selection among multiple admissible digits, hub basin tie) must produce AMBIG with an evidence plan unless a pinned tie-break resolves it.
G.C3 — Invariants
G.C3.a — No silent NEAR and no silent AMBIGNEAR requires residual ledger; AMBIG requires evidence plan. Absence is FAIL.
✶ G.R — Fractal: Recursion Governance, Checkpoint Sealing, and Certificates
G.R1 — Objects
G.R1.a — DepthCheckpointA checkpoint is mandatory at hatch boundaries. A DepthCheckpoint binds:
parent state digests,
child state digests,
corridor ID,
TriMode policy digest,
and replay pointer.
G.R2 — Operators
G.R2.a — Hatch replay verifierReplays hatch legality from the recorded witnesses and confirms:
trigger evidence validity,
inheritance correctness,
child init correctness,
checkpoint digest match.
G.R3 — Invariants
G.R3.a — Recursion is append-onlyA hatch creates a new branch frame; it cannot overwrite a prior frame. Any attempt to “rewrite past boundary” is illegal.
G.R4 — Required certificates
G.R4.a — TriangleGovernanceCertCertifies TriMode policy determinism, corridor selection determinism, and carry/hatch witness correctness under replay.
G.R4.b — HatchCertCertifies HatchEvent legality, checkpoint match, and replay closure.
G.R4.c — TunnelLegalityCertCertifies tunnel step legality under pinned hub mesh, corridor, commutation receipts, and meta-zero requirements.
AppG Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
Triangle mode policies (GLOBAL vs AXIS) are pinned and meaning-bearing; changes require explicit migration.
Triangle selects corridors deterministically via pinned CorridorPinSpec and emits CorridorSelectionWitness; replay must reproduce selections.
Depth is governed by DepthLedger with explicit budgets; depth increase is legal only via HatchEvent producing checkpoints and replay pointers.
Carry events are boundary events emitted deterministically with boundary rule digests and pre/post state digests; carry semantics are pinned.
Tunneling legality is governed by pinned hub mesh corridors, allowed step sets, commutation receipts, and meta-zero snap constraints; legality produces TunnelLegalityWitness and is truth typed.
NEAR requires residual ledgers; AMBIG requires evidence plans; FAIL/CONFLICT require failure/conflict artifacts.
Triangle governance, hatch behavior, and tunnel legality require certificates with replay closure.
AppG — Triangle Governor, Depth/Recursion Policies, Carry/Hatch Interfaces
AppH — Coupling and Topology (Multi-axis, Multi-rail Constraints)
Station role: cross-axis coupling; topology constraints for multi-dimensional consistency.Purpose: define coupling constraints, product-structure invariants, and topology witnesses that prevent illegal cross-axis inference.
□ H.S — Square: Coupling Contracts, Product-Structure Invariants, Multi-Rail Constraints
H.S1 — Objects
H.S1.a — Axis index set and state carriersFix dimension (d\ge 1). Let ([d]:={1,\dots,d}). Axis-coupled structures are defined over:
Phase torus (\mathbb{T}^d) or its discretizations (\Sigma_{B_d}).
Square carrier (\mathcal{S}{d,k}) and its factorization into ((\mathbb{Z}{4^k})^d) or ((\mathbb{Z}_4)^{dk}) under pinned decomposition.
Triangle carrier ((\mathbb{Z}_3)^d) (Option A) or (\mathbb{Z}_3) (Option B) under pinned mode policy.
H.S1.b — Rail system and multi-rail constraintsA rail is a pinned control schedule defining an axis-wise sequencing regime. A rail system is a tuple:[\mathsf{Rails}:=\langle \mathsf{RailID},\ \mathsf{LaneSet},\ \mathsf{ScheduleSpec},\ \mathsf{PinsDigest}\rangle]where:
LaneSet is a finite set of lane identifiers (e.g., Su/Me/Sa) or extended lane alphabets pinned by policy.
ScheduleSpec is a deterministic mapping:[\mathsf{Sched} : (\mathsf{PulseID}, k, \mathsf{StateSummary}) \to \mathsf{LaneSel}]with (\mathsf{LaneSel}) a finite selection describing which lane applies on which axis and which coupling constraints activate.
A multi-rail constraint is a predicate restricting simultaneous lane assignments across axes. Multi-rail constraints are part of coupling contracts and must be pinned.
H.S1.c — CouplingContractA CouplingContract is the meaning-bearing object defining when axes may be treated as independent and when they are coupled.
[\mathsf{CouplingContract}:=\langle\mathsf{CoupleVer},;\mathsf{Dim},;\mathsf{CoupleMode},;\mathsf{AxisPartition},;\mathsf{AllowedCouplings},;\mathsf{DisallowedCouplings},;\mathsf{WitnessRequirements},;\mathsf{TieBreakSpec},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Where:
CoupleMode ∈ {PRODUCT, BLOCK, GLOBAL}.
AxisPartition partitions ([d]) into disjoint blocks (B_1,\dots,B_m), pinned.
PRODUCT: all blocks are singletons.
BLOCK: blocks can be >1.
GLOBAL: a single block ([d]).
AllowedCouplings and DisallowedCouplings are finite sets of coupling patterns expressed as typed constraints over operations (tunnel steps, lifts, projections, and scheduling).
WitnessRequirements is a pinned list of required witness families to assert coupling legality (see H.S2 and H.F).
H.S1.d — Multi-axis tunnel step objectA multi-axis tunnel step is a vector:[\delta \in \mathbb{T}^d]or a discrete ring step on (\Sigma_{B_d}) with associated lift/projection references. The canonical step object is:
[\mathsf{TunnelStep} :=\langle\mathsf{StepVer},;\mathsf{Dim},;\mathsf{StepVector},;\mathsf{AxisSupport},;\mathsf{StepSetDigest},;\mathsf{RailSelDigest},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{StepDigest}\rangle]
AxisSupport is the set of axes where (\delta_i\neq 0).
StepSetDigest pins the allowed step set (\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) (AppG/Ch06).
RailSelDigest pins the lane selection applicable at the step.
StepDigest is content-addressed.
H.S2 — Operators
H.S2.a — Coupling legality predicateCoupling legality is a deterministic predicate:[\mathsf{LegalCouple} :(\mathsf{CouplingContract},\mathsf{StateSummary},\mathsf{TunnelStep},\mathsf{CorridorID}) \to {\mathsf{true},\mathsf{false}}.]
A tunnel step is legal under coupling if and only if all the following hold:
AxisSupport respects AxisPartition: coupling constraints must allow simultaneous nonzero steps on the axis set selected.
Multi-rail constraints: lane assignments on the axis set satisfy pinned multi-rail constraints.
Allowed step membership: (\delta\in\Delta\mathcal{H}^{(d)}) (or equivalent discrete step membership) under pinned StepSetDigest.
Corridor compliance: the step stays inside the pinned corridor neighborhood on (\mathbb{T}^d) or ring representation.
Required topology receipts (spin/holonomy) are satisfied when noncommuting schedules could yield path dependence (H.F2).
If any required condition cannot be decided due to missing pins, the result is AMBIG (by emitting evidence plan under AppL) rather than assuming legality.
H.S2.b — Product-structure factorization operatorFor CoupleMode=PRODUCT, the operator family must factorize across axes:
For any axis-separated operators (A_i) acting on axis (i), the combined operator satisfies:[A = \bigotimes_{i=1}^d A_i]or, for generators in Kronecker sum form:[G = \bigoplus_{i=1}^d G_i.]
Coupling contracts must declare which factorization law applies. Any deviation from declared factorization is a coupling violation unless explicitly migrated.
H.S2.c — Block-coupling operatorFor CoupleMode=BLOCK, axes in a block (B_j) may be treated as coupled. The coupled operator is constrained to act only within the block’s subspace and must be representable as:
tensor product across blocks, and
arbitrary (but pinned) operator inside each block.
Formally:[\mathsf{Op} = \bigotimes_{j=1}^m \mathsf{Op}{B_j}]with each (\mathsf{Op}{B_j}) pinned by digest.
H.S2.d — Cross-axis inference prohibition operatorDefine the prohibition rule:[\mathsf{Infer}(i \Rightarrow j) \text{ is forbidden unless }\mathsf{CoupleMode}\neq \mathsf{PRODUCT}\text{ and explicit witness exists.}]
This is enforced by requiring that any inference edge whose source and target addresses lie on different axis blocks must reference a CouplingWitness proving that coupling is active and legal for the inference.
H.S3 — Invariants
H.S3.a — Axis partition stability invariantAxisPartition is pinned and meaning-bearing. Any change to AxisPartition requires MIGRATE and must invalidate prior coupling witnesses unless explicitly revalidated.
H.S3.b — No illegal cross-axis inferenceAny claim that transfers information from axis (i) to axis (j) across different coupling blocks without a CouplingWitness is invalid for OK routing.
H.S3.c — Multi-axis tunnel legality invariantA multi-axis tunnel step is admissible only if:
coupling contract permits the axis support,
multi-rail constraints permit the simultaneous lane selection,
topology receipts for noncommutation are satisfied where required.
H.S3.d — Deterministic tie-break invariantAny ambiguity in axis ordering, lane ordering, or step selection must be resolved by a pinned tie-break. Unpinned tie-breaks produce AMBIG.
H.S4 — Protocols
H.S4.a — Coupling witness generation protocolTo assert legality of a multi-axis step, generate:
CouplingLegalityWitness (H.F1.b) proving coupling contract compatibility.
RailWitness proving the lane selection used and satisfying multi-rail constraints.
TopologyReceiptSet proving required commutation/holonomy conditions (H.F2).
A replay capsule pointer reproducing the above checks deterministically.
H.S4.b — Multi-axis tunnel execution protocolGiven a pinned state and tunnel step:
Compute lane selection deterministically.
Validate coupling legality.
Validate topology receipts when required.
Execute step (AppG/Ch06) and emit step witness plus coupling/topology witness references.
H.S4.c — Square-local regression fixtures for couplingFixtures must include:
PRODUCT mode: verify factorization and forbid cross-axis inference without witness.
BLOCK mode: verify allowed intra-block couplings and forbidden inter-block couplings.
GLOBAL mode: verify that coupling is explicitly pinned and that topology receipts gate commutation-sensitive schedules.
Multi-rail constraints: verify that forbidden lane combinations are rejected deterministically.
Tie-break fixtures: verify deterministic resolution where multiple choices are allowed by contract.
❀ H.F — Flower: Topology Invariants, Holonomy/Spin Receipts, and Noncommutation Control
H.F1 — Objects
H.F1.a — Topology policy and required receiptsA topology policy specifies which commutation relations must be proven (or bounded) for certain composite actions.
[\mathsf{TopoPolicy}:=\langle\mathsf{TopoVer},;\mathsf{Dim},;\mathsf{ReceiptRequirements},;\mathsf{MetricDigest},;\mathsf{KappaBudget},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
ReceiptRequirements is a pinned set of required receipt templates (spin loops, path-difference loops) keyed by operator IDs.
H.F1.b — CouplingLegalityWitness[\mathsf{CoupleWit}:=\langle\mathsf{PulseID},;k,;\mathsf{CouplingContractDigest},;\mathsf{RailSelDigest},;\mathsf{TunnelStepDigest},;\mathsf{CorridorID},;\mathsf{LegalityResult},;\mathsf{DecisionTraceDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{WitDigest}\rangle]LegalityResult is truth-typed; NEAR requires residual ledger; AMBIG requires evidence plan.
H.F1.c — TopologyReceiptSetA TopologyReceiptSet is the set of receipts required by TopoPolicy for a specific action schedule:
[\mathsf{TopoReceipts}:=\langle\mathsf{PulseID},;k,;\mathsf{TopoPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ReceiptRefs},;\mathsf{AggregateResidual},;\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{PinsDigest}\rangle]
ReceiptRefs is an ordered list of receipt digests; ordering is canonical by digest.
H.F2 — Operators
H.F2.a — Spin/holonomy receipts integration pointsTopology invariants are enforced by requiring receipts at specific integration points:
Schedule commutation: when two operators are composed in different orders (lane swaps, axis ordering swaps), a SpinReceipt must be present to certify commutation or bound residual.
Multi-axis vs sequential axis stepping: any claim that a simultaneous multi-axis step is equivalent to a sequence of single-axis steps requires a path-difference receipt.
Refinement and projection coherence: when coupling claims involve refined ring transitions, receipts must show that refinement/projection commutes with tunnel steps under pinned rules or must bound residual drift.
H.F2.b — Receipt evaluationGiven a receipt with residual (r) under metric (d), and kappa budget (\kappa):
OK iff (r=0) and replay closes.
NEAR iff (0<r\le\kappa) with residual ledger and scope.
FAIL iff (r>\kappa).
CONFLICT iff replay disagreement.
Receipt scope is critical: it must bind domain/spec and pins; receipts do not generalize beyond their declared scope.
H.F3 — Invariants
H.F3.a — Topology gating invariantIf TopoPolicy requires a receipt for a schedule, the schedule is non-routable for OK without that receipt. Missing receipts produce AMBIG with evidence plan or FAIL depending on corridor policy.
H.F3.b — Holonomy as path-dependence witnessIf two paths from the same start to the same end disagree under pinned normal forms, the disagreement is a topology defect. It must be recorded as a conflict packet if reproducible; it cannot be suppressed.
H.F4 — Protocols
H.F4.a — Receipt fixture protocolRegression must include:
commuting templates (must produce OK receipts),
near-commuting templates (must produce NEAR receipts with ledgers),
noncommuting templates (must produce FAIL receipts),
conflict templates (must produce CONFLICT and fences).
☁ H.C — Cloud: Uncertainty Discipline for Coupling Claims
H.C1 — Objects
H.C1.a — CouplingResidualLedgerWhen coupling is approximate, a residual ledger must bound the deviation from claimed factorization or commutation:
[\mathsf{CoupleLedger}:=\langle\mathsf{MetricDigest},;\mathsf{Bound},;\mathsf{Observed},;\mathsf{Expected},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{ExpiryPulse},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr}\rangle]
H.C1.b — CouplingEvidencePlanIf coupling legality depends on unknown structure or missing receipts, an evidence plan must enumerate:
candidate coupling states,
required receipts,
discriminators and replay routes,
budgets and stop rules.
H.C2 — Operators
H.C2.a — Truth typing for coupling legalityCoupling legality decisions are truth-typed:
OK only if all receipts and constraints verify.
NEAR only if bounded by ledger.
AMBIG only if bounded candidates exist and evidence plan emitted.
FAIL/CONFLICT when deterministically violated or replay disagrees.
H.C3 — Invariants
H.C3.a — No silent couplingCross-axis coupling cannot be inferred from proximity or correlation; it must be pinned or witnessed.
✶ H.R — Fractal: Certificates and Deterministic Coupling Governance
H.R1 — Required certificates
H.R1.a — CouplingDeterminismCertCertifies that coupling legality checks are deterministic under pinned inputs.
[\mathsf{CouplingDeterminismCert}:=\langle\mathsf{CouplingContractDigest},;\mathsf{TopoPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{FixtureSetDigest},;\mathsf{ExpectedDecisionDigests},;\mathsf{ObservedDecisionDigests},;\mathsf{Result},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Result is PASS iff all fixture decisions and witness digests match expected.
H.R1.b — TopologyCertCertifies that topology receipts are present and valid for declared schedules and that required commutation/path-equivalence constraints are satisfied.
[\mathsf{TopologyCert}:=\langle\mathsf{TopoPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ReceiptSetDigest},;\mathsf{AggregateResidual},;\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
TopologyCert is OK only if all required receipts are OK (or NEAR if allowed) and replay closes.
H.R2 — Protocols
H.R2.a — Certificate issuance protocolFor each multi-axis operation admitted into an OK route:
compute coupling legality witness,
compute required receipts,
emit CouplingDeterminismCert and TopologyCert,
attach certificates to the operation’s evidence row (AppB) and to the route transcript (Ch11/Ch19).
AppH Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
CouplingContract pins axis partition, coupling mode, multi-rail constraints, allowed/disallowed coupling patterns, and tie-break rules.
Multi-axis tunnels are legal only if coupling contract allows axis support, rail constraints are satisfied, and required topology receipts are present.
Cross-axis inference is forbidden unless coupling is explicitly active and a coupling witness exists.
Topology invariants are enforced via spin/holonomy receipts and path-difference receipts at declared integration points; missing receipts are not OK-routable.
CouplingDeterminismCert and TopologyCert are required, import-verifiable, and bind replay closure for coupling legality and topology constraints.
AppH — Coupling and Topology (Multi-axis, Multi-rail Constraints)
AppI — Corridors, Truth Typing, and Routable Outcomes
Station role: truth typing and corridor routing discipline (OK/NEAR/AMBIG/FAIL).Purpose: formalize corridor profiles, budgets, and truth typing so routing decisions are reproducible and auditable.
□ I.S — Square: CorridorProfile, Budget Discipline, and Routability Semantics
I.S1 — Objects
I.S1.a — Truth lattice and routability thresholdTruth typing is a closed vocabulary:
[\mathsf{TruthType} := {\mathsf{OK},\mathsf{NEAR},\mathsf{AMBIG},\mathsf{FAIL},\mathsf{CONFLICT}}.]
For routability and aggregation, corridors define a strict preorder (pinned):
[\mathsf{OK} \succ \mathsf{NEAR} \succ \mathsf{AMBIG} \succ \mathsf{FAIL} \succ \mathsf{CONFLICT}.]
A corridor defines a minimum admissible truth threshold:[\mathsf{MinTruth}(\mathsf{Corridor}) \in {\mathsf{OK},\mathsf{NEAR},\mathsf{AMBIG}}.]Paths whose composite truth is below (\mathsf{MinTruth}) are not routable under that corridor.
I.S1.b — Budget vectorA corridor budget is:[\mathsf{Budget} := \langle \kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi \rangle]with semantics:
(\kappa): commutation residual budget (holonomy/spin allowance),
(\beta): drift/approximation residual budget,
(\delta): recursion depth budget,
(\chi): compute/search/replay budget.
Budgets are interpreted only under pinned budget semantics. A corridor must pin the aggregation mode for each component:
additive, max, or mixed (e.g., max for (\delta), additive for (\chi)).
I.S1.c — CorridorProfile schema (mandatory)A CorridorProfile is the meaning-bearing object that defines legality, truth typing, budgets, and escalation.
[\mathsf{CorridorProfile} :=\langle\mathsf{CorrVer},;\mathsf{CorridorID},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{BudgetCaps},;\mathsf{BudgetAggSpec},;\mathsf{AllowedEdgeKinds},;\mathsf{RequiredArtifacts},;\mathsf{TypingRules},;\mathsf{EscalationRules},;\mathsf{PromotionRules},;\mathsf{DisclosureRules},;\mathsf{QuarantineRules},;\mathsf{RoutabilityRules},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Required fields:
CorridorID: content-addressed digest of CorridorProfile with CorridorID field zeroed.
Scope: {LOCAL, INTER} plus scope bindings (manuscript IDs if INTER).
PinsDigest: pin closure required to interpret this corridor (AppA/AppD).
BudgetCaps: (\mathsf{Budget}) caps.
BudgetAggSpec: per-component aggregation mode and charging rules.
AllowedEdgeKinds: mapping from truth class to allowed edge kinds.
RequiredArtifacts: mapping from truth class to mandatory artifact families.
TypingRules: deterministic rule set mapping evidence to truth typing.
EscalationRules: deterministic mapping specifying when failures trigger fences/quarantines.
PromotionRules: deterministic obligations for NEAR→OK and AMBIG→NEAR/OK transitions.
DisclosureRules: mandatory disclosure formats and propagation rules.
QuarantineRules: deterministic quarantine triggers and propagation rules.
RoutabilityRules: path acceptance predicates, tie-breaks, and thresholds.
SchemaPins: schema closure required to interpret all corridor artifacts.
I.S1.d — Allowed edge kinds per truth classCorridorProfile must define a total function:
[\mathsf{AllowedEdgeKinds} : \mathsf{TruthType} \to \mathcal{P}(\mathsf{EdgeKind})]
Minimum requirement:
(\mathsf{AllowedEdgeKinds}(\mathsf{OK})) must exclude any edge kind that requires missing proofs or missing pins.
(\mathsf{AllowedEdgeKinds}(\mathsf{NEAR})) must require residual ledger edge kinds and disclosure edges where appropriate.
(\mathsf{AllowedEdgeKinds}(\mathsf{AMBIG})) must require EvidencePlan edges.
(\mathsf{AllowedEdgeKinds}(\mathsf{FAIL})) must require FailureWitness or ConflictPacket edges if reproducible.
(\mathsf{AllowedEdgeKinds}(\mathsf{CONFLICT})) must require fence/quarantine propagation edges.
I.S1.e — Required artifact families per truth classCorridorProfile must define:
[\mathsf{RequiredArtifacts} : \mathsf{TruthType} \to \mathcal{P}(\mathsf{ArtifactKind})]
Minimum required artifacts:
OK: ReplayCapsule, WitnessBundle, PinClosure, DigestCommitments.
NEAR: all OK artifacts plus ResidualLedger and Expiry/renewal obligations.
AMBIG: EvidencePlan, bounded candidate set, discriminators, routes to evidence.
FAIL: FailureWitness and/or ReproRecipe (unless policy forbids non-reproducible failures).
CONFLICT: ConflictPacket, FenceSpec, QuarantineRecord.
I.S2 — Operators
I.S2.a — Truth typing functionTruth typing is a deterministic function:
[\mathsf{Type} :(\mathsf{Claim},\mathsf{Evidence},\mathsf{CorridorProfile}) \to \mathsf{TypedOutcome}]
where:
[\mathsf{TypedOutcome} :=\langle\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{WitnessRefs},;\mathsf{ReplayRefs?},;\mathsf{ResidualLedgerRef?},;\mathsf{EvidencePlanRef?},;\mathsf{FailureWitnessRef?},;\mathsf{ConflictPacketRef?},;\mathsf{BudgetLedgerRef},;\mathsf{Obligations},;\mathsf{OutcomeDigest}\rangle]
TypingRules must pin:
exact equality predicates (e.g., NF equality, digest equality),
admissible metrics for residuals,
required completeness checks,
replay determinism requirements.
Truth typing must reject any claim whose required artifacts are missing; missing artifacts cannot be downgraded silently to OK.
I.S2.b — Budget charging operatorA deterministic function computes the budget usage of an evaluation:
[\mathsf{Charge} :(\mathsf{Evidence},\mathsf{TypingTrace},\mathsf{CorridorProfile}) \to \mathsf{BudgetLedger}]
Charge must:
attribute each charge to a witness digest,
use pinned aggregation modes,
be replayable (charge trace digest).
If budget caps are exceeded, TypingRules must specify the resulting truth type (default FAIL, unless explicitly downgradable to AMBIG with evidence plan).
I.S2.c — Path composition truth operatorFor a path (P=(e_1,\dots,e_n)) with typed outcomes (\tau_i), define composite truth:
[\mathsf{Truth}(P) := \min_{\succ}{\tau_1,\dots,\tau_n}]under the pinned truth preorder.
Budget aggregation uses BudgetAggSpec:[\mathsf{Budget}(P) := \mathsf{Agg}(\mathsf{Budget}(e_1),\dots,\mathsf{Budget}(e_n)).]
A path is routable iff:
(\mathsf{Truth}(P) \succeq \mathsf{MinTruth}(\mathsf{Corridor})),
(\mathsf{Budget}(P)\le \mathsf{BudgetCaps}),
required artifact families for (\mathsf{Truth}(P)) are present,
no quarantine/fence blocks any edge.
I.S2.d — Escalation operator (failure to fences)EscalationRules define a deterministic mapping:[\mathsf{Escalate} : \mathsf{TypedOutcome} \to \mathsf{EscalationActions}]where EscalationActions can include:
emit fence/quarantine record,
require conflict packet,
require migration witness,
require immediate rollback under deployment rules (Ch21).
Escalation must be deterministic; any nondeterministic escalation is illegal.
I.S3 — Truth typing rules (minimum required)
TypingRules must define necessary and sufficient conditions for each truth class.
I.S3.a — OK conditionsA claim is typed OK iff all of the following hold:
PinsDigest closure resolves and matches corridor requirements.
Required artifacts for OK are present and verify (witness bundle, replay capsule, expected digests).
Replay determinism holds: replay produces exactly the committed digests.
All invariants in the claim’s InvariantSet evaluate true under pinned schemas.
Budget caps are respected.
No revocation or quarantine applies.
I.S3.b — NEAR conditionsA claim is typed NEAR iff:
All pin closure and replay requirements hold,
The claim fails at least one OK equality check but satisfies bounded residual constraints under a pinned metric,
A ResidualLedger is present with:
metric digest,
bound,
measured residual value,
scope,
expiry pulse,
promotion obligations,
replay pointer reproducing the measurement,
Budget caps are respected,
Disclosure rules are satisfied.
NEAR must never be emitted without a residual ledger.
I.S3.c — AMBIG conditionsA claim is typed AMBIG iff:
The corridor cannot decide OK or NEAR due to underdetermination,
A bounded candidate set exists within compute budget,
An EvidencePlan is emitted specifying:
candidate set,
discriminators,
routes to obtain missing evidence,
promotion rules,
stop rules and budgets,
The ambiguity is explicitly represented in the outcome artifacts.
AMBIG must never be emitted without an evidence plan.
I.S3.d — FAIL conditionsA claim is typed FAIL iff any of the following holds:
required pins missing,
required artifacts missing for the attempted truth class,
replay mismatch occurs where replay is required,
budget caps exceeded and not downgradable,
invariants violated beyond admissible bounds,
domain violations (maps applied outside declared domain),
illegal edge kinds under corridor.
FAIL must include a FailureWitness if reproducible under pinned environment; otherwise it must be explicitly labeled non-reproducible only if corridor policy permits (not permitted for publish corridors).
I.S3.e — CONFLICT conditionsCONFLICT is typed when reproducible verifier disagreement exists under identical pins, or when two admissible paths yield incompatible digests and no pinned tie-break can select one.
CONFLICT must produce a ConflictPacket and fence/quarantine actions per QuarantineRules.
I.S4 — Promotion/demotion and disclosure obligations
I.S4.a — Promotion rulesPromotionRules define deterministic obligations for:
NEAR→OK: specify required refinements, new witnesses, tightened bounds, or additional replays.
AMBIG→NEAR/OK: specify discriminators and evidence acquisition routes.
Promotions are append-only (Ch20): an OK outcome supersedes a NEAR/AMBIG outcome via explicit EvidenceRow supersession, not by overwriting.
I.S4.b — Demotion rulesDemotions are not performed by retyping old evidence. Instead, demotion occurs by quarantine/revocation overlays:
if a previously OK witness is revoked or invalidated, it remains historically present but becomes non-routable by fence/quarantine.
demotion is therefore represented by new quarantine records and by updated routing outcomes at later pulses.
I.S4.c — Disclosure obligationsDisclosureRules define mandatory propagation of:
residual ledgers (NEAR),
evidence plans (AMBIG),
quarantine/fence references (FAIL/CONFLICT),
expiry and renewal constraints.
Any route transcript that cites NEAR evidence must include disclosure pointers; omission is a violation and must be typed FAIL at routing time.
❀ I.F — Flower: Corridor Geometry and Metric Binding
I.F1 — Objects
I.F1.a — Metric bindingA corridor pins metric digests for residual measurement. Metrics must be deterministic functions over canonically serialized objects or normal forms.
Metric classes include:
discrete equality metric (0 if digest equal, else 1),
norm metrics over numeric vectors with pinned numeric policy,
edit-distance-like metrics over canonical ASTs with pinned cost tables.
I.F1.b — Corridor neighborhoodsCorridor may define admissible neighborhoods for NEAR:[\mathsf{NearOK}(x) \iff d(x,\mathsf{Target}) \le \beta]with (\beta) pinned and scope defined.
I.F2 — Operators
I.F2.a — Residual computationResiduals must be computed deterministically from pinned metric and pinned canonical forms:[r := d(\mathsf{NF}(x), \mathsf{NF}(y)).]
I.F3 — Invariants
I.F3.a — Metric determinismMetric outputs must be stable across replays under pinned environment constraints.
☁ I.C — Cloud: Routable Outcomes and Planning Discipline
I.C1 — Objects
I.C1.a — Routability summaryA routability summary for a route plan includes:
minimum truth threshold,
composite truth result,
budget usage and caps,
disclosure pointers,
fence/quarantine pointers.
I.C2 — Operators
I.C2.a — Route admissibilityA route plan is admissible iff composite truth ≥ threshold and all required disclosures exist.
I.C3 — Invariants
I.C3.a — No bypassNo routing decision may bypass corridor truth typing. Any “shortcut” route not passing through typing evaluation is invalid.
✶ I.R — Fractal: CorridorReplayCert and Deterministic Verification
I.R1 — CorridorReplayCapsule
A CorridorReplayCapsule must include:
CorridorProfile digest,
set of claims evaluated (addresses and digests),
all evidence artifacts and their digests,
expected typed outcomes (digests),
expected budget ledger digests,
environment pins digest.
I.R2 — CorridorReplayCert (required)
A CorridorReplayCert certifies that corridor truth typing is reproducible under replay.
[\mathsf{CorridorReplayCert} :=\langle\mathsf{CorridorProfileDigest},;\mathsf{CapsuleDigest},;\mathsf{EnvPinsDigest},;\mathsf{ExpectedOutcomeDigest},;\mathsf{ObservedOutcomeDigest},;\mathsf{Result},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Result is PASS iff:
corridor profile resolves and verifies,
replay reproduces identical typed outcomes, ledger digests, and disclosures,
any escalation actions are identical under pinned rules.
Failure yields FAIL/CONFLICT per policy and must be recorded with reproduction pointers.
AppI Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
CorridorProfile pins budgets, aggregation rules, allowed edge kinds per truth class, required artifact families, typing rules, escalation rules, promotion rules, disclosure rules, quarantine rules, and routability thresholds.
Truth typing is deterministic: OK requires replay closure and invariant satisfaction; NEAR requires residual ledger; AMBIG requires evidence plan; FAIL requires failure witness; CONFLICT requires conflict packet and fences.
Routes are admissible only if composite truth meets corridor threshold, budgets are within caps, and disclosures are present; no bypass permitted.
Promotions are append-only via new evidence; demotions occur only via quarantine/revocation overlays.
CorridorReplayCert is required and must replay corridor typing identically under pinned environment constraints.
AppI — Corridors, Truth Typing, and Routable Outcomes
AppJ — NEAR Disclosure Ledger (Residuals, Bounds, Expiry)
Station role: NEAR is explicit and quantitative; disclosure ledger is mandatory for production reliance.Purpose: define residual ledgers, calibration, expiry, and promotion checklists for NEAR claims.
□ J.S — Square: ResidualLedger as a First-Class Evidence Object
J.S1 — Objects
J.S1.a — ResidualLedger (normative schema)A ResidualLedger is the mandatory disclosure object for any claim typed NEAR. It binds a bounded deviation to a pinned metric and calibration context, with explicit scope and expiry.
[\mathsf{ResidualLedger}:=\langle\mathsf{RLVer},;\mathsf{RLID},;\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{SubjectRefs},;\mathsf{MetricDigest},;\mathsf{MetricSpecRef},;\mathsf{Bound},;\mathsf{Observed},;\mathsf{Expected},;\mathsf{ResidualValue},;\mathsf{ResidualVector?},;\mathsf{AggregationRule},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{Calibration},;\mathsf{Expiry},;\mathsf{PromotionObligations},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Constraints:
TruthType MUST equal NEAR.
SubjectRefs is a non-empty ordered list of references to the exact objects the ledger qualifies, each reference content-addressed by digest:[\mathsf{SubjectRef}:=\langle \mathsf{Addr},\ \mathsf{Digest},\ \mathsf{SchemaID}\rangle.]
MetricDigest pins the metric function used to compute residuals; MetricSpecRef points to the metric definition artifact.
Bound is the admissibility limit; its units and interpretation are part of MetricSpecRef.
Observed and Expected are canonical references or canonical values (depending on metric family), sufficient to replay the computation.
ResidualValue is the scalar residual used for truth typing; ResidualVector is optional and must be present when the metric is vector-valued or when the aggregation rule requires it.
AggregationRule is a pinned enum {MAX, SUM, L2, L1, CUSTOM} with CUSTOM requiring a rule digest.
Scope binds applicability and non-applicability (J.S1.c).
Calibration binds how Bound and residuals are interpreted (J.S1.d).
Expiry binds when reliance expires and how renewal is required (J.S1.e).
PromotionObligations binds the upgrade pathway (J.S1.f).
ReplayPtr must reproduce the residual computation and ledger digest deterministically.
PinsDigest is the digest of the full pin-closure required to interpret and replay the ledger.
J.S1.b — ResidualLedger ID (RLID)ResidualLedger is content-addressable. Define:[\mathsf{RLID}:=\mathsf{H}(\textsf{"AppJ/ResidualLedger"} ,|, \mathsf{H}(\mathsf{ser}(\mathsf{ResidualLedgerZeroed})) ,|, \mathsf{PinsDigest})]where ResidualLedgerZeroed is the ledger with RLID and signatures zeroed but all meaning-bearing fields preserved. Collisions are treated as CONFLICT and must emit a conflict packet plus quarantine.
J.S1.c — Scope schemaScope is mandatory and must be explicit.
[\mathsf{Scope}:=\langle\mathsf{ScopeVer},;\mathsf{ScopeKind},;\mathsf{AddrSetDigest},;\mathsf{DomainSpecDigest},;\mathsf{ExclusionsDigest},;\mathsf{ValidityWindow}\rangle]
ScopeKind ∈ {LOCALADDR_RANGE, CLAIMSET, ROUTESEGMENT, PROFILESET, CUSTOM} with CUSTOM requiring schema migration.
AddrSetDigest commits to the ordered set of addresses in scope.
DomainSpecDigest commits to domain constraints (e.g., ranges of parameters, allowed input classes).
ExclusionsDigest commits to explicitly excluded addresses or parameter regions.
ValidityWindow binds time applicability:[\mathsf{ValidityWindow}:=\langle \mathsf{IssuedPulse},\ \mathsf{NotBeforePulse?},\ \mathsf{NotAfterPulse}\rangle]where NotAfterPulse is mandatory.
J.S1.d — Calibration schemaCalibration binds residual meaning to the operational environment and measurement protocols.
[\mathsf{Calibration}:=\langle\mathsf{CalVer},;\mathsf{CalID},;\mathsf{CalibrationType},;\mathsf{BaselineRef},;\mathsf{SamplingPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{EstimatorSpecDigest},;\mathsf{ConfidenceSpec?},;\mathsf{UnitSpecDigest},;\mathsf{AssumptionsDigest}\rangle]
CalibrationType ∈ {ABSOLUTE, RELATIVE_TO_BASELINE, STATISTICAL, ADVERSARIAL}.
BaselineRef is required for relative calibration and binds the baseline digests used.
SamplingPolicyDigest pins how any sampling is done (if any sampling exists).
EstimatorSpecDigest pins estimator definition for computing residuals.
ConfidenceSpec is required for statistical calibration and pins confidence intervals or tail bounds.
UnitSpecDigest pins units and scaling conventions.
AssumptionsDigest pins explicit assumptions about environment and data.
Calibration is mandatory for production reliance. Absence forces FAIL for corridors that require calibrated NEAR.
J.S1.e — Expiry schemaExpiry binds renewal requirements and safety constraints.
[\mathsf{Expiry}:=\langle\mathsf{ExpiryVer},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{ExpiryPulse},;\mathsf{RenewalMode},;\mathsf{RenewalTriggers},;\mathsf{AutoInvalidateOnPolicyChange}\rangle]
ExpiryPulse is mandatory.
RenewalMode ∈ {RENEW_TO_NEAR, PROMOTE_TO_OK, FORBID_AFTER_EXPIRY}.
RenewalTriggers is a pinned set including at minimum:
policy epoch change,
schema change,
metric change,
baseline shift beyond pinned thresholds,
drift monitor thresholds.
AutoInvalidateOnPolicyChange is pinned boolean; if true, policy digest mismatch invalidates the ledger.
J.S1.f — Promotion obligations schema (NEARPromotionChecklist binding)Promotion obligations are explicit tasks required to upgrade the claim to OK or to renew NEAR.
[\mathsf{PromotionObligations}:=\langle\mathsf{OblVer},;\mathsf{TargetTruth},;\mathsf{Tasks},;\mathsf{CompletionPredicateDigest},;\mathsf{TieBreakDigest}\rangle]
TargetTruth ∈ {OK, NEAR}.
Tasks is an ordered list of task descriptors:[\mathsf{Task}:=\langle \mathsf{TaskID},\ \mathsf{TaskType},\ \mathsf{InputsDigest},\ \mathsf{OutputsDigest},\ \mathsf{DuePulse?}\rangle]
CompletionPredicateDigest pins how tasks are checked as complete.
TieBreakDigest pins ordering and prioritization when multiple tasks exist.
J.S2 — Operators
J.S2.a — Residual computation operatorGiven metric (d) pinned by MetricDigest, define:[r := d(\mathsf{Observed}, \mathsf{Expected})]computed deterministically under pinned numeric and ordering policies.
If metric produces a vector (v), compute scalar residual via AggregationRule:
MAX: (r = \max_i |v_i|)
SUM: (r = \sum_i |v_i|)
L2: (r=\sqrt{\sum_i v_i^2})
L1: (r=\sum_i |v_i|)
CUSTOM: (r = \mathsf{Agg}(v)) where (\mathsf{Agg}) is pinned.
J.S2.b — Admissibility predicateA NEAR ledger is admissible iff:[r \le \mathsf{Bound}]and calibration requirements hold under corridor rules.
J.S2.c — Ledger verification operator[\mathsf{VerifyRL} : (\mathsf{ResidualLedger},\mathsf{CorridorProfile}) \to {\mathsf{PASS},\mathsf{FAIL}}]Verification must check:
PinsDigest closure resolves and matches corridor requirements.
MetricSpecRef resolves and matches MetricDigest.
ReplayPtr reproduces Observed/Expected extraction and residual computation.
ResidualValue matches recomputation and satisfies bound.
Scope and expiry are valid and non-contradictory.
Calibration requirements are satisfied under corridor policy.
J.S2.d — Renewal operatorRenewal is append-only: a new ResidualLedger supersedes the old via evidence-table supersession (AppB). Renewal must satisfy RenewalMode and triggers. Renewal produces a new RLID and must not mutate old ledgers.
J.S3 — Invariants
J.S3.a — Mandatory NEAR disclosure invariantNo claim may be typed NEAR without an attached ResidualLedger satisfying schema completeness, replay closure, and admissibility predicate under the corridor.
J.S3.b — Scope soundness invariantThe ledger must not be applied outside its scope. Any route that uses a NEAR claim must include the scope digest in its disclosure bundle and must validate applicability.
J.S3.c — Expiry enforcement invariantIf current pulse exceeds ExpiryPulse, the ledger is expired and cannot be used for OK-adjacent routing. Expired ledgers may remain addressable for historical audit but are non-routable for production reliance unless renewed.
J.S3.d — Calibration completeness invariantIf corridor requires calibrated NEAR, then Calibration must include required baseline and estimator specifications. Missing calibration forces FAIL.
J.S4 — Protocols
J.S4.a — Ledger issuance protocolTo issue a NEAR ledger:
Identify subject claims/edges/routes by digest and address; commit to SubjectRefs list.
Select metric by digest and resolve MetricSpecRef.
Extract Observed and Expected deterministically; commit to their digests.
Compute ResidualValue and ResidualVector if required.
Bind Scope and DomainSpec; compute scope digests.
Bind Calibration record; compute calibration digests.
Bind Expiry record; compute expiry pulse under policy.
Construct PromotionObligations (NEARPromotionChecklist).
Produce ReplayPtr sufficient to re-run 2–4 and verify 5–8.
Compute RLID and sign per signature policy.
Append ledger to EvidenceTable as a witness row (AppB) and link it to the NEAR-typed claim.
J.S4.b — Disclosure formatting rules (canonical, import-verifiable)Disclosure is a canonical bundle format:
[\mathsf{NearDisclosureBundle}:=\langle\mathsf{BundleVer},;\mathsf{SubjectRef},;\mathsf{RLDigest},;\mathsf{ScopeDigest},;\mathsf{CalibrationDigest},;\mathsf{ExpiryDigest},;\mathsf{PromotionObligationsDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Rules:
Disclosure bundles must be content-addressed and included in exported containers (Ch18/AppO) when NEAR evidence is cited.
The bundle must contain only digests and minimal canonical fields; it must not require external context.
Import verification must fail or quarantine any NEAR claim that lacks an import-verifiable disclosure bundle when the corridor threshold is NEAR or higher.
J.S4.c — Expiry enforcement protocolDuring route planning and during deployment acceptance (Ch21), apply:
If ExpiryPulse < current_pulse: treat NEAR claim as non-admissible.
If ExpiryPulse is within pinned warning window: permit but emit renewal obligation in route transcript.
If policy epoch changes and AutoInvalidateOnPolicyChange is true: invalidate.
All decisions are deterministic and replayable.
❀ J.F — Flower: Residual Geometry, Metrics, and Calibration Semantics
J.F1 — Objects
J.F1.a — Metric specificationMetricSpecRef must resolve to a metric definition object:
[\mathsf{MetricSpec}:=\langle\mathsf{MetricVer},;\mathsf{MetricID},;\mathsf{DomainType},;\mathsf{CodomainType},;\mathsf{ComputationRuleDigest},;\mathsf{NormalizationDigest},;\mathsf{UnitsDigest},;\mathsf{TieBreakDigest}\rangle]
MetricSpec must define:
domain (what is compared),
normalization (canonicalization before measurement),
computation rule,
units and scaling,
and any tie-break rules for ambiguous representations.
J.F1.b — Calibration geometryCalibrationType determines meaning of Bound:
ABSOLUTE: bound is absolute distance in pinned units.
RELATIVE_TO_BASELINE: bound is relative to baseline reference (e.g., percent change).
STATISTICAL: bound is tail probability or confidence interval width.
ADVERSARIAL: bound is maximum deviation under pinned perturbation set.
J.F2 — Operators
J.F2.a — Calibration checkA deterministic predicate verifies calibration is valid for a ledger under corridor rules, including baseline digest availability and estimator definition.
J.F3 — Invariants
J.F3.a — Metric stabilityMetric outputs must be stable under pinned environment. Any numerical nondeterminism not pinned is a violation.
☁ J.C — Cloud: Uncertainty Discipline and NEAR as a Contract, Not a Vibe
J.C1 — Objects
J.C1.a — ConfidenceSpec for statistical NEARIf CalibrationType=STATISTICAL, ConfidenceSpec is mandatory and pins:
confidence level,
estimator method,
sample selection method,
RNG seed policy if sampling is used,
and reproducible summary statistics.
J.C2 — Operators
J.C2.a — Uncertainty propagation ruleAny route that uses NEAR evidence must propagate the NEARDisclosureBundle and must preserve scope and expiry semantics. Failure to propagate is a corridor violation.
J.C3 — Invariants
J.C3.a — No silent downgrades/overclaimsNEAR cannot be treated as OK. Any overclaim is a deterministic failure and must be quarantined under AppK/AppO policies.
✶ J.R — Fractal: NEARPromotionChecklist, Replay Closure, and Certificates
J.R1 — NEARPromotionChecklist (required)
A NEARPromotionChecklist is a canonical checklist object referenced by PromotionObligations.
[\mathsf{NEARPromotionChecklist}:=\langle\mathsf{CheckVer},;\mathsf{ChecklistID},;\mathsf{TargetTruth},;\mathsf{RequiredArtifacts},;\mathsf{RequiredReplays},;\mathsf{RequiredRegressions},;\mathsf{RequiredCalibrations},;\mathsf{RequiredApprovals?},;\mathsf{CompletionPredicateDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Minimum required checklist entries for promotion NEAR→OK:
Replay re-run passes with zero residual under pinned metric, or corridor permits exact equality under canonical NF digest equality.
All inputs digests are current and not revoked; policy epoch compatibility holds.
Regression suite specified by corridor passes for the affected scope.
Calibration is refreshed if expired or if baseline shift trigger fired.
A superseding EvidenceRow is emitted with TruthType=OK and explicit supersedes pointer (AppB).
For renewal NEAR→NEAR:
Residual recomputation under same metric passes bound.
ExpiryPulse updated and recorded.
Promotion obligations updated if necessary.
J.R2 — Required certificate
J.R2.a — ResidualLedgerCertA ResidualLedgerCert attests that:
the ledger is well-formed,
replay reproduces the residual,
bound check passes,
scope and expiry are valid,
calibration requirements are satisfied.
[\mathsf{ResidualLedgerCert}:=\langle\mathsf{RLDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{ObservedResidual},;\mathsf{Bound},;\mathsf{Result},;\mathsf{VerifierDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Result is PASS iff all checks succeed deterministically.
AppJ Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
NEAR claims are valid only with a ResidualLedger that pins metric, bound, scope, calibration, expiry, promotion obligations, replay pointer, and full pin closure digest.
ResidualLedger is content-addressed; replay must reproduce residual and admissibility predicate (r\le\text{Bound}).
Disclosure formatting is canonical and import-verifiable; any NEAR usage in a route must carry a NearDisclosureBundle.
Expiry is mandatory for NEAR; expired ledgers are non-routable for production reliance unless renewed by a superseding ledger.
NEARPromotionChecklist defines the deterministic tasks required for NEAR→OK or renewal; promotions are append-only via superseding evidence rows.
ResidualLedgerCert is required for deployment-grade NEAR reliance.
AppJ — NEAR Disclosure Ledger (Residuals, Bounds, Expiry)
AppK — FAIL/CONFLICT, Quarantine, Revocation Receipts
Station role: conflict discipline; quarantine boundaries; revocation propagation.Purpose: define minimal reproducible contradiction packets, fences, revocation receipts, and propagation rules compatible with Ch20/Ch21 governance.
□ K.S — Square: ConflictPacket, Fence Rules, Revocation Receipts
K.S1 — Objects
K.S1.a — Truth overlay and masking semanticsFAIL and CONFLICT are not annotations; they are routability blockers. Quarantine and revocation are masking overlays:
A quarantined artifact remains addressable but is non-routable for OK paths.
A revoked artifact remains addressable but is forbidden to be trusted, imported, or executed under strict policies.
All overlays are append-only and bind to PulseID (Ch20).
K.S1.b — ConflictPacket schema (minimal witness set + reproduction recipe)A ConflictPacket is the minimal reproducible contradiction object. It must be self-contained relative to content-addressed references and pinned replay closure.
[\mathsf{ConflictPacket}:=\langle\mathsf{CPVer},;\mathsf{CPID},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{Subject},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{EnvPinsDigest},;\mathsf{CompetingClaims},;\mathsf{Paths},;\mathsf{MinimalWitnessSet},;\mathsf{ReproRecipe},;\mathsf{ExpectedDigests},;\mathsf{ObservedDigests},;\mathsf{Classification},;\mathsf{FenceSpec},;\mathsf{RevocationHints?},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Required fields:
CPID: content-addressed identifier derived deterministically (K.S2.a).
IssuedPulse: PulseID at which CP is issued.
Scope: {LOCAL, INTER} with manuscript bindings for INTER.
Subject: canonical references to the disputed objects:[\mathsf{Subject}:=\langle \mathsf{SrcEndpointRef},\ \mathsf{DstEndpointRef},\ \mathsf{ClaimAddrSetDigest}\rangle]
PinsDigest: full pin closure required to reproduce the contradiction (AppA/AppD/AppI).
EnvPinsDigest: environment pins required for deterministic replay (Ch16/Ch18/Ch21).
CompetingClaims: ordered list of claim references:[\mathsf{ClaimRef}:=\langle \mathsf{ClaimAddr},\ \mathsf{ClaimDigest},\ \mathsf{TruthType}\rangle]
Paths: canonical representation of at least two admissible routes/derivations that disagree:[\mathsf{PathRef}:=\langle \mathsf{PathID},\ \mathsf{EdgeDigestList},\ \mathsf{ReplayPtr},\ \mathsf{OutcomeDigest}\rangle]
MinimalWitnessSet: minimal list of witness objects sufficient to reproduce the disagreement (K.S1.c).
ReproRecipe: deterministic replay procedure binding exact inputs and ordering (K.S1.d).
ExpectedDigests / ObservedDigests: canonical digest maps binding mismatch.
Classification: enum {CONFLICT, FAIL_REPRODUCIBLE, FAIL_NONREPRODUCIBLE}.
FenceSpec: deterministic exclusion boundary object (K.S1.e).
RevocationHints?: optional list of suspected compromised artifacts; hints are non-authoritative.
K.S1.c — MinimalWitnessSet schema[\mathsf{MinimalWitnessSet}:=\langle\mathsf{OrderRuleDigest},;\mathsf{WitnessRefs}\rangle]where WitnessRefs is an ordered list of:[\mathsf{WitRef}:=\langle \mathsf{Kind},\ \mathsf{Digest},\ \mathsf{Addr?},\ \mathsf{Role}\rangle]with Kind ∈ {ReplayCapsule, Transcript, ProofObject, ResidualLedger, EvidencePlan, TransportCert, PhaseWitness, RegressionResult, LogPrefix}.
Minimality ordering is pinned; default minimization order:
minimize number of distinct addresses in scope,
minimize number of witness refs,
minimize total byte size of referenced payloads,
tie-break lexicographically by digest.
Any claim of certified minimality must include minimization trace digest.
K.S1.d — ReproRecipe schemaA ReproRecipe is the complete deterministic replay plan:
[\mathsf{ReproRecipe}:=\langle\mathsf{RecipeVer},;\mathsf{EntryCapsuleDigest},;\mathsf{InputsClosureDigest},;\mathsf{ExecutionPlan},;\mathsf{DeterminismChecklistDigest},;\mathsf{StopConditions},;\mathsf{OutputSelectionRuleDigest}\rangle]
EntryCapsuleDigest points to a replay capsule that must run.
InputsClosureDigest commits to the closure of inputs required by replay (containers, policies, schemas).
ExecutionPlan is an ordered list of step invocations (by tool digest and step parameters).
DeterminismChecklistDigest pins what must be pinned for determinism.
StopConditions specify when to stop (step limits, resource limits, mismatch detected).
OutputSelectionRuleDigest pins which outputs are compared and how.
K.S1.e — FenceSpec schema (exclude disputed routes deterministically)A FenceSpec defines deterministic exclusions.
[\mathsf{FenceSpec}:=\langle\mathsf{FenceVer},;\mathsf{FenceID},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{FenceTargets},;\mathsf{PropagationRuleDigest},;\mathsf{AllowlistRuleDigest},;\mathsf{DenylistRuleDigest},;\mathsf{ExpiryPulse?},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
FenceTargets is a canonical set of excluded items:[\mathsf{FenceTargets}:=\langle \mathsf{EdgeDigestSet},\ \mathsf{RouteDigestSet},\ \mathsf{ArtifactDigestSet},\ \mathsf{AddrSetDigest} \rangle]
PropagationRuleDigest pins how exclusions propagate to dependent routes and derived claims.
Allowlist/Denylist rules are deterministic predicates over digests and scope.
ExpiryPulse may be absent for permanent fences; presence means fence must be re-evaluated for continued enforcement.
FenceID is content-addressed; fence application is deterministic.
K.S1.f — RevocationReceipt schemaA RevocationReceipt records an authoritative revocation decision.
[\mathsf{RevocationReceipt}:=\langle\mathsf{RevVer},;\mathsf{RevID},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{AuthorityID},;\mathsf{AuthorityKeyDigest},;\mathsf{TargetKind},;\mathsf{TargetDigest},;\mathsf{ReasonCode},;\mathsf{EvidenceRefs},;\mathsf{EffectivePulse},;\mathsf{PropagationRuleDigest},;\mathsf{ImportPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
TargetKind ∈ {Artifact, Profile, Certificate, Policy, Schema, Key} (pinned enum).
TargetDigest is the digest of the revoked object.
ReasonCode is a pinned codebook entry.
EvidenceRefs is an ordered list of supporting evidence digests.
EffectivePulse is the first pulse where revocation applies for enforcement.
PropagationRuleDigest pins deterministic propagation semantics.
ImportPolicyDigest pins how import must treat the revocation.
RevID is content-addressed and derived deterministically from the receipt with RevID and Sig zeroed.
K.S2 — Operators
K.S2.a — Content-addressed IDsConflictPacket ID:[\mathsf{CPID} := \mathsf{H}(\textsf{"AppK/ConflictPacket"} ,|, \mathsf{H}(\mathsf{ser}(\mathsf{ConflictPacketZeroed})) ,|, \mathsf{PinsDigest})]FenceID and RevID are derived analogously with domain separation tags "AppK/Fence" and "AppK/Revocation".
Any ID collision between distinct canonical bytes is CONFLICT and must emit a higher-level conflict packet plus quarantine of both IDs.
K.S2.b — Conflict classification operatorGiven two admissible derivations that produce incompatible digests under identical pins, classify as CONFLICT and generate a ConflictPacket.
Deterministic classifier:[\mathsf{ClassifyConflict} : (\mathsf{EvidenceA},\mathsf{EvidenceB},\mathsf{Pins}) \to \mathsf{Classification}]Where:
CONFLICT if both sides replay deterministically and disagree on committed digests,
FAIL_REPRODUCIBLE if replay deterministically fails under pinned conditions,
FAIL_NONREPRODUCIBLE only if policy permits and determinism cannot be established.
K.S2.c — Fence application operatorFence application is a deterministic function:[\mathsf{ApplyFence} : (\mathsf{FenceSpec}, \mathsf{GraphState}) \to \mathsf{MaskedGraphState}]Masking removes routability of:
excluded edges,
excluded routes,
excluded artifacts,
and any dependent routes by propagation rule.
Masking is overlay-only; the underlying objects remain present.
K.S2.d — Revocation propagation algorithmRevocation propagation is deterministic and depends only on:
revocation receipts valid through pulse (p),
pinned propagation rules,
and dependency closure computation rules.
Let (\mathsf{DepClosure}(x)) compute the dependency closure of digest (x) under pinned rules.
For each effective revocation receipt (r) with target digest (d), define the revoked set:[\mathsf{RevSet}p := \bigcup{r:\ \mathsf{EffectivePulse}(r)\le p} \left({d}\cup \mathsf{Propagate}(d,r)\right)]where (\mathsf{Propagate}(d,r)) is defined by PropagationRuleDigest and may include:
forward closure: revoke all objects that depend on (d),
backward closure: revoke all objects (d) depends on (optional),
key-based closure: revoke all artifacts signed by compromised key digest (if TargetKind=Key),
profile closure: revoke profiles referencing revoked schemas/policies.
Propagation must be explicit and pinned. Unpinned propagation is illegal.
K.S3 — Invariants
K.S3.a — Minimal reproducibility invariantA ConflictPacket must include sufficient information to reproduce the contradiction under pinned environment and pins. Absence of required reproduction inputs is a schema failure.
K.S3.b — Deterministic fence invariantGiven the same FenceSpec and same graph state digest, ApplyFence must produce identical masked-state digest. Any nondeterminism is CONFLICT.
K.S3.c — Revocation precedence invariantRevocation overrides prior OK evidence for routing and import. If an artifact digest is in (\mathsf{RevSet}_p), then:
it is not admissible for OK routing,
it is not admissible for import acceptance under strict import policies,
any dependent claims must be downgraded via quarantine overlays.
K.S3.d — Append-only governance invariantConflicts, fences, quarantines, and revocations are appended as new objects and referenced via DeltaPacks (Ch20). No deletion or rewriting occurs.
K.S4 — Protocols
K.S4.a — ConflictPacket emission protocolOn detection of disagreement:
Confirm identical PinsDigest and EnvPinsDigest for the competing runs; if they differ, the disagreement is first typed as MIGRATE/PolicyMismatch, not CONFLICT.
Collect candidate witness objects and compute MinimalWitnessSet using pinned minimization order, within compute budget (\chi).
Construct ReproRecipe that:
references entry replay capsule(s),
binds closure digests for all required inputs,
defines deterministic step ordering.
Construct ExpectedDigests and ObservedDigests maps.
Construct FenceSpec:
include minimal exclusion targets necessary to prevent disputed routes from being used for OK.
Emit ConflictPacket with signatures.
Append ConflictPacket and FenceSpec via DeltaPack.
Update evidence tables (AppB) marking affected claims/routes as quarantined.
K.S4.b — Fence propagation protocolFor each FenceSpec:
Apply PropagationRuleDigest to compute the closure of excluded items:
edges directly excluded,
routes containing excluded edges,
claims whose only support is via excluded routes,
certificates that depend on excluded artifacts.
Emit a deterministic FenceExpansionReport artifact containing:
original targets digests,
expanded targets digests,
a proof trace digest for propagation.
Update the masked graph overlay state.
K.S4.c — Revocation issuance and import enforcement protocolRevocation issuance:
Authority signs RevocationReceipt.
Receipt is appended via DeltaPack at IssuedPulse; EffectivePulse is enforced by policy.
Import enforcement:
Importer computes (\mathsf{RevSet}_p) for the pulse window it accepts (or for the current pulse under online acceptance).
If imported bundle contains any digest in (\mathsf{RevSet}_p), importer must:
reject, or
quarantine (only if policy allows), with explicit QuarantineRecord.
Importer must record the revocation receipts used (by digest) in the import transcript.
Revocation may require fallback deployment under Ch21 rules; fallback selection must be deterministic.
❀ K.F — Flower: Path-Dependence, Holonomy Localization, and Conflict Localization
K.F1 — Objects
K.F1.a — HolonomyWitness bindingConflict packets may include holonomy/spin receipts as localization evidence. A holonomy witness is admissible only if:
operator IDs are pinned,
domain spec is pinned,
residual is computed under pinned metric,
replay closes.
Holonomy evidence is supportive; revocation and fencing decisions remain governed by pinned policies.
K.F2 — Operators
K.F2.a — PathDifference localizationGiven two paths (P,Q) between the same endpoints, conflict localization is computed by the loop:[L = Q^{-1}\circ P]and its residual. If the residual is non-zero under pinned metric, the disagreement is path-dependent and must be represented in the ConflictPacket.
☁ K.C — Cloud: Quarantine Boundaries and Non-Trust States
K.C1 — Objects
K.C1.a — QuarantineRecordA quarantine record is an overlay object that masks routability and/or import acceptance.
[\mathsf{QuarantineRecord}:=\langle\mathsf{QuarVer},;\mathsf{QuarID},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{TargetsDigest},;\mathsf{ReasonCode},;\mathsf{EvidenceRefs},;\mathsf{FenceRef?},;\mathsf{ExpiryPulse?},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Quarantine is not revocation. Quarantine marks uncertainty or conflict; revocation marks invalidity or compromised trust.
K.C2 — Operators
K.C2.a — Quarantine propagationQuarantine propagation is deterministic and may be narrower than revocation propagation. It is pinned by QuarantineRules in the active corridor or deployment profile.
✶ K.R — Fractal: Governance Closure Across Time and Deployment
K.R1 — Integration points with Ch20/Ch21
ConflictPacket, FenceSpec, and RevocationReceipt are time-indexed objects appended via DeltaPacks (Ch20).
Deployment acceptance (Ch21) must enforce:
all required fences/quarantines,
all effective revocations,
and must reject or quarantine deployments whose closures intersect revoked sets.
K.R2 — Required certificates
K.R2.a — ConflictReplayCertCertifies that ConflictPacket reproduces deterministically and that ExpectedDigests/ObservedDigests mismatch is stable under pinned replay.
K.R2.b — FenceDeterminismCertCertifies that fence propagation and masking are deterministic and produce expected masked graph digests.
K.R2.c — RevocationPropagationCertCertifies that revocation set computation and propagation produce the expected revoked closure under pinned rules and that import enforcement applies it correctly.
AppK Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
ConflictPacket is the minimal reproducible contradiction object: it must include minimal witness set, deterministic reproduction recipe, expected vs observed digest commitments, and a FenceSpec.
FenceSpec defines deterministic exclusion boundaries; fences mask routability without deleting artifacts; fence propagation is deterministic and replayable.
RevocationReceipt is an authoritative signed object binding target digest, reason, effective pulse, and pinned propagation rules; revocation overrides OK routing and import acceptance under strict policies.
Conflicts, fences, quarantines, and revocations are append-only and time-indexed via DeltaPacks; no silent resolution exists.
Deterministic certificates are required for conflict replay, fence determinism, and revocation propagation.
AppK — FAIL/CONFLICT, Quarantine, Revocation Receipts
AppL — AMBIG Evidence Plans (Bounded Search, Discriminators, Stop Rules)
Station role: AMBIG is a plan, not a shrug; bounded evidence generation and discriminators.Purpose: define EvidencePlan objects, bounded candidate generation, and deterministic stop rules to turn ambiguity into a managed workflow.
□ L.S — Square: EvidencePlan as a Deterministic, Bounded Workflow Object
L.S1 — Objects
L.S1.a — AMBIG semanticsAMBIG is a truth class indicating underdetermination under pinned rules. AMBIG is admissible only when ambiguity is bounded, and when an explicit EvidencePlan exists that specifies how to collapse ambiguity via deterministic discriminators and routable tasks.
L.S1.b — EvidencePlan schema (mandatory)An EvidencePlan is a content-addressed object:
[\mathsf{EvidencePlan}:=\langle\mathsf{EPVer},;\mathsf{EPID},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{Subject},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{EnvPinsDigest},;\mathsf{Candidates},;\mathsf{Discriminators},;\mathsf{Routes},;\mathsf{Budgets},;\mathsf{StopRules},;\mathsf{PromotionHooks},;\mathsf{ExpectedOutcomes},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Required fields:
EPID: content-addressed ID derived deterministically (L.S2.a).
IssuedPulse: time binding (Ch20).
Scope: {LOCAL, INTER} with manuscript bindings for INTER.
Subject: canonical reference to the claim(s) or route(s) that are ambiguous:[\mathsf{Subject}:=\langle \mathsf{ClaimAddrSetDigest},\ \mathsf{EndpointRefs?},\ \mathsf{CorridorID}\rangle]
PinsDigest: full pin closure required to interpret candidates, run discriminators, and evaluate stop rules.
EnvPinsDigest: pinned environment assumptions for deterministic replay.
Candidates: bounded candidate set with canonical ordering (L.S1.c).
Discriminators: bounded set of tests/proofs/log extractions with deterministic evaluation semantics (L.S1.d).
Routes: routable plans to acquire discriminator evidence (L.S1.e).
Budgets: bounded compute/search/replay budgets for executing the plan (L.S1.f).
StopRules: deterministic stop conditions (L.S1.g).
PromotionHooks: integration into Ch20 scheduler (L.S1.h).
ExpectedOutcomes: mapping from discriminator outcomes to candidate elimination/promotion states (L.S1.i).
ReplayPtr: replay capsule pointer reproducing plan construction and plan execution logic.
Sig: signature under pinned policy.
L.S1.c — Candidate schema (bounded)A candidate is an explicit, pinned hypothesis element. Candidate kinds are closed and must be pinned by schema.
[\mathsf{Candidate}:=\langle\mathsf{CandID},;\mathsf{CandKind},;\mathsf{TargetRef},;\mathsf{AssumptionsDigest},;\mathsf{PriorityKey},;\mathsf{CandDigest}\rangle]
CandKind ∈ {PATH, PINSET, PROFILE, MAP, DOMAIN, MODEL, OTHER} with OTHER requiring schema migration.
TargetRef is a digest-qualified reference (e.g., a transport path, a profile digest, a pinset completion).
AssumptionsDigest commits to extra assumptions required by that candidate (must be explicit).
PriorityKey is used for deterministic ordering and tie-break.
CandDigest is content-addressed.
Candidate set requirements:
Candidates must be finite and bounded in size by Budgets.
Candidates must be canonical ordered by:
CandKind (pinned enum order),
PriorityKey,
CandDigest lexicographic.
Any missing candidate required to represent ambiguity is a schema failure; EvidencePlan must not omit plausible candidates unless disallowed by pinned policy.
L.S1.d — Discriminator schemaA discriminator is a deterministic test that, when executed, partitions or eliminates candidates.
[\mathsf{Discriminator}:=\langle\mathsf{DiscID},;\mathsf{DiscKind},;\mathsf{InputsSpecDigest},;\mathsf{ProcedureRef},;\mathsf{OutcomeSpaceDigest},;\mathsf{CostSpec},;\mathsf{DeterminismSpecDigest},;\mathsf{DiscDigest}\rangle]
DiscKind ∈ {REPLAY_CHECK, PIN_COMPLETENESS, COMMUTATION_RECEIPT, METRIC_MEASURE, DOMAIN_TEST, REGRESSION_TEST, IMPORT_VERIFY, CUSTOM} with CUSTOM requiring schema migration.
ProcedureRef points to a deterministic procedure or harness by digest.
OutcomeSpaceDigest commits to the outcome labels and their canonical ordering.
CostSpec gives deterministic cost estimation used by budget scheduling.
DeterminismSpecDigest pins environment and tie-break requirements.
Discriminators must be finite and must have bounded cost under Budgets.
L.S1.e — Route schema (routable evidence acquisition)Routes are executable plans for producing required evidence. Each route is a RoutePlan-like object (Ch11/Ch19) restricted to evidence acquisition.
[\mathsf{EvidenceRoute}:=\langle\mathsf{RouteID},;\mathsf{Target},;\mathsf{HubSeq},;\mathsf{TruthIntent},;\mathsf{Obligations},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{BudgetClass},;\mathsf{RouteDigest}\rangle]
HubSeq must respect HubCap constraints; routes must be deterministic under pins. TruthIntent is typically {AMBIG_EVIDENCE} and cannot be treated as a semantic claim without later promotion.
L.S1.f — Budgets schemaEvidencePlan budgets are explicit:
[\mathsf{EPBudget}:=\langle\kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi,;\mathsf{MaxCandidates},;\mathsf{MaxDiscriminators},;\mathsf{MaxRoutes},;\mathsf{MaxBytes},;\mathsf{MaxSteps}\rangle]
(\chi) bounds compute/search cost; other components can be used to bound commutation tests or residual evaluations when relevant.
L.S1.g — StopRules schema (deterministic)Stop rules define when the evidence plan halts:
[\mathsf{StopRules}:=\langle\mathsf{StopVer},;\mathsf{StopOnUnique},;\mathsf{StopOnBudgetExhaust},;\mathsf{StopOnDeadlinePulse?},;\mathsf{StopOnConflict},;\mathsf{StopTieBreakDigest}\rangle]
StopOnUnique: stop when a unique remaining candidate exists.
StopOnBudgetExhaust: stop when budget is exhausted.
StopOnDeadlinePulse: optional; if present, must be pinned and enforced.
StopOnConflict: stop if discriminator outcomes are inconsistent under replay, requiring conflict handling.
StopTieBreakDigest pins tie-break rules for choosing which discriminators to run next.
L.S1.h — PromotionHooks schema (integration with Ch20 scheduler)PromotionHooks bind the evidence plan to the time-axis promotion scheduler.
