[\mathsf{PromotionHooks}:=\langle\mathsf{HookVer},;\mathsf{EligibleAfterPulse},;\mathsf{PriorityClass},;\mathsf{ScheduleKeyDigest},;\mathsf{OnResolution},;\mathsf{OnBudgetExhaust},;\mathsf{OnDeadline}\rangle]
EligibleAfterPulse: earliest PulseID the plan may be executed.
PriorityClass: deterministic priority category used by scheduling.
ScheduleKeyDigest: digest of the deterministic key used for tie-break among multiple evidence plans.
OnResolution: specifies what artifacts must be emitted when a candidate becomes unique (promotion to NEAR or OK, or issuance of a new EvidenceRow).
OnBudgetExhaust: specifies what must be emitted when budget stops without resolution (remain AMBIG with updated plan or quarantine).
OnDeadline: specifies action if deadline reached without resolution (policy-defined; may force FAIL/quarantine).
L.S1.i — ExpectedOutcomes schemaExpectedOutcomes is a deterministic mapping from discriminator outcomes to candidate elimination or promotion transitions:
[\mathsf{ExpectedOutcomes}:=\langle\mathsf{OutcomeMapDigest},;\mathsf{Rules}\rangle]where Rules is a canonical list of rules:[\mathsf{Rule}:=\langle \mathsf{DiscID},\ \mathsf{OutcomeLabel},\ \mathsf{EliminateSetDigest},\ \mathsf{PromoteActionDigest?}\rangle]EliminateSetDigest references a canonical subset of CandID values to remove; PromoteActionDigest optionally references a promotion emission action (e.g., emit NEAR ledger, emit EQUIV witness, emit MIGRATE proposal).
L.S2 — Operators
L.S2.a — EvidencePlan ID derivation[\mathsf{EPID} := \mathsf{H}(\textsf{"AppL/EvidencePlan"} ,|, \mathsf{H}(\mathsf{ser}(\mathsf{EvidencePlanZeroed})) ,|, \mathsf{PinsDigest})]where EvidencePlanZeroed is the plan with EPID and signatures zeroed. Collisions between distinct canonical bytes are CONFLICT and must produce a conflict packet plus quarantine.
L.S2.b — Candidate generation operator (bounded)Candidate generation is deterministic:
[\mathsf{GenCandidates} : (\mathsf{Subject},\mathsf{Pins},\mathsf{Policy}) \to \mathsf{Candidates}]
Constraints:
must enumerate candidates in canonical order,
must stop at MaxCandidates,
must record truncation as an explicit “candidate truncation witness” artifact when MaxCandidates is reached,
must not omit candidates based on heuristics unless explicitly disallowed by pinned policy.
If bounded enumeration cannot be achieved under budget, the result is FAIL (or AMBIG with explicit truncation witness if corridor allows).
L.S2.c — Discriminator selection operator (deterministic scheduling within plan)EvidencePlan contains multiple discriminators; execution order must be deterministic:
[\mathsf{PickNextDisc} : (\mathsf{RemainingCandidates},\mathsf{DiscSet},\mathsf{State},\mathsf{StopRules}) \to \mathsf{DiscID}]Selection must be pinned; default ordering key:
lowest estimated cost,
highest expected elimination power (pinned heuristic table),
lexicographic DiscID.
Any heuristic must be pinned by digest; otherwise discriminator selection is illegal.
L.S2.d — EvidencePlan execution operator[\mathsf{RunPlan} : (\mathsf{EvidencePlan},\mathsf{CorpusStateAtPulse}) \to \mathsf{PlanResult}]
PlanResult includes:
executed discriminators and their outcomes,
updated candidate set,
emitted evidence artifacts,
decision log digest,
stop condition triggered.
Plan execution is deterministic under pins and environment pins.
L.S2.e — Resolution operatorIf candidates become unique:[|\mathsf{Candidates}| = 1 \Rightarrow \mathsf{Resolve}(\mathsf{EvidencePlan}) \to \mathsf{ResolutionArtifactSet}]ResolutionArtifactSet must include:
updated EvidenceRow superseding AMBIG,
any required witness bundle or residual ledger,
PromotionRecord for Ch20 scheduler.
L.S3 — Invariants
L.S3.a — Boundedness invariantEvidencePlan is valid only if:
candidates set is finite and ≤ MaxCandidates,
discriminators set is finite and ≤ MaxDiscriminators,
routes set is finite and ≤ MaxRoutes,
execution budget caps are finite and pinned.
Any unbounded search is forbidden.
L.S3.b — Determinism invariantFor identical corpus state digest, pins digest, environment pins digest, and plan digest, execution produces identical PlanResult digest.
L.S3.c — Stop rule determinism invariantStop condition must be uniquely determined for any execution state under pinned StopRules. If multiple stop conditions fire simultaneously, StopTieBreakDigest pins which one is recorded as primary.
L.S3.d — No silent promotion invariantAMBIG cannot be promoted to NEAR/OK without emitting explicit promotion artifacts and evidence rows (AppB/Ch20). EvidencePlan must specify PromotionHooks; promotions must be append-only.
L.S4 — Protocols
L.S4.a — EvidencePlan issuance protocolTo issue an EvidencePlan:
Bind Subject and CorridorID; compute Subject digest commitments.
Bind PinsDigest and EnvPinsDigest closures.
Generate bounded candidate set deterministically; emit truncation witness if truncated.
Define discriminators; bind ProcedureRefs and outcome spaces by digest.
Define evidence routes required to acquire discriminator inputs; ensure HubCap compliance.
Bind budgets and stop rules; pin tie-break policies.
Bind promotion hooks for Ch20 integration.
Construct ExpectedOutcomes rules.
Produce ReplayPtr sufficient to replay candidate generation and plan execution.
Compute EPID and sign.
Append EvidencePlan as a witness row (AppB) and attach to the AMBIG-typed claim under corridor rules (AppI).
L.S4.b — EvidencePlan execution protocol (time axis)At pulse (p), the Ch20 scheduler may select EvidencePlans whose EligibleAfterPulse ≤ p. Execution must:
Validate pins and import closure.
Run deterministically with budget enforcement.
Emit PlanResult and DecisionLog artifacts.
If resolved, emit promotion artifacts (NEAR/OK) and supersede prior AMBIG evidence row.
If not resolved, emit an updated EvidencePlan (superseding) with remaining candidates and updated obligations.
If budget exhausted or deadline hit, apply OnBudgetExhaust/OnDeadline actions deterministically (may include quarantine or conversion to FAIL under policy).
❀ L.F — Flower: Discriminators as Typed Separators and Certificate-Gated Proof Paths
L.F1 — Objects
L.F1.a — Separator semanticsA discriminator partitions candidate space. For candidate set (C) and discriminator outcome (o), define:[C_o := {c\in C : \mathsf{Consistent}(c,o)}]where Consistent is pinned per discriminator.
Discriminators must be sufficient to eliminate at least one candidate on some outcome branch; discriminators that never change the candidate set are permitted only if required by policy (e.g., import verification prerequisite) and must be flagged as prerequisite discriminators.
L.F2 — Operators
L.F2.a — Certificate-gated discriminator executionSome discriminators require certificates (ReplayCert, ImportCert, TransportCert). EvidencePlan must specify required certificates and reject outcomes that cannot be certified under pinned policies.
L.F3 — Invariants
L.F3.a — Outcome space completenessFor each discriminator, the outcome space is closed and pinned; unknown outcomes are FAIL.
☁ L.C — Cloud: Ambiguity Management, Quarantine, and Non-resolution Handling
L.C1 — Objects
L.C1.a — Non-resolution reportIf a plan terminates without resolution, it must emit:
remaining candidates digest,
executed discriminators and their outcomes digests,
budget exhaustion witness or deadline witness,
next-step obligations or quarantine decision.
L.C2 — Operators
L.C2.a — Quarantine on inconsistencyIf discriminator outcomes are inconsistent under replay (same input yields different outcome), classify CONFLICT and emit conflict packet plus fences (AppK). EvidencePlan execution must stop under StopOnConflict.
✶ L.R — Fractal: EvidencePlanReplayCert and Deterministic Replay Closure
L.R1 — EvidencePlanReplayCapsule
An EvidencePlanReplayCapsule must include:
EvidencePlan digest,
corpus state digest at execution pulse,
all inputs required (routes executed, fetched artifacts, log prefixes),
expected PlanResult digest,
expected decision log digest,
environment pins digest.
L.R2 — EvidencePlanReplayCert (required)
An EvidencePlanReplayCert certifies that EvidencePlan construction and execution are deterministic and replayable.
[\mathsf{EvidencePlanReplayCert}:=\langle\mathsf{EvidencePlanDigest},;\mathsf{CapsuleDigest},;\mathsf{EnvPinsDigest},;\mathsf{ExpectedPlanResultDigest},;\mathsf{ObservedPlanResultDigest},;\mathsf{ExpectedDecisionLogDigest},;\mathsf{ObservedDecisionLogDigest},;\mathsf{Result},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Result is PASS iff:
replay reproduces the same candidate set (including ordering),
reproduces the same discriminator selection order,
reproduces the same discriminator outcomes,
reproduces the same stop condition,
and reproduces the same promotion artifacts when resolution occurs.
Failures are FAIL or CONFLICT per pinned policy and must trigger quarantine when reproducible disagreement exists.
AppL Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
EvidencePlan is mandatory for AMBIG and must include bounded candidates, discriminators, routes, budgets, stop rules, promotion hooks, expected outcome mapping, replay pointer, and pin closure digests.
Candidate generation is deterministic and bounded; truncation must be explicit with witnesses.
Discriminator selection and execution order are deterministic and pinned; unpinned heuristics are forbidden.
Stop rules are deterministic and pinned; conflict outcomes must stop and emit conflict packets/fences.
Promotion hooks integrate EvidencePlan execution into Ch20 scheduler; resolution emits append-only promotion artifacts and superseding evidence rows.
EvidencePlanReplayCert is required and must verify replay closure of plan construction and execution.
AppL — AMBIG Evidence Plans (Bounded Search, Discriminators, Stop Rules)
AppM — Fractal/Recursion, Snap/Meta-zero, Scaling and Renormalization Interfaces
Station role: recursion/multiscale carrier; snap/canonical representative + residual ledger interfaces.Purpose: define the fractal lens machinery: recursion policies, snap operators, and renormalization-compatible invariants.
□ M.S — Square: Snap as Canonical Representative + Residual Ledger Emission
M.S1 — Objects
M.S1.a — Fractal state carrierA Fractal carrier is a multiscale control/state object providing:
recursion frames (depth indexed),
checkpointing,
Snap computation state,
and renormalization interfaces.
[\mathsf{FrState}:=\langle\mathsf{FrVer},;\mathsf{SeedID},;\mathsf{PulseID},;\mathsf{DepthIndex},;\mathsf{DepthBudget},;\mathsf{ScaleIndex},;\mathsf{ScaleLadderDigest},;\mathsf{SnapPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{GateSeqDigest},;\mathsf{FrameStackDigest},;\mathsf{CheckpointChainDigest},;\mathsf{ReceiptsDigest},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
SeedID binds the aether seed identity (Ch14).
DepthIndex and DepthBudget bind recursion legality (AppG).
ScaleIndex binds multi-resolution level (scale ladder).
SnapPolicyDigest pins Snap behavior (M.S1.c).
GateSeqDigest pins the ordered corridor gate list.
FrameStackDigest commits to the recursion frame stack (M.S3).
CheckpointChainDigest commits to checkpoints (M.S4).
ReceiptsDigest binds required holonomy/commutation receipts used in Snap gating (Ch09).
M.S1.b — Meta-zero set and fixed corridorLet (\mathsf{X}) be the joint state space on which Snap acts (typically a product of □○△ carriers and pinned derived observables). Let ({P_i}_{i=1}^m) be a pinned gate family, each enforcing one corridor constraint.
Define fixed sets:[Z_i := \mathrm{Fix}(P_i) = {x\in\mathsf{X}: P_i(x)=x}.]Define the meta-zero corridor:[\mathcal{Z}\star := \bigcap{i=1}^m Z_i.]Snap is the canonical procedure to compute a representative near (\mathcal{Z}_\star) together with a residual ledger describing distances to each (Z_i) and any noncommutation effects between gates.
M.S1.c — SnapPolicy schema (normative)A SnapPolicy pins the exact Snap algorithm, including gate ordering, relaxation, stopping rules, and residual ledger semantics.
[\mathsf{SnapPolicy}:=\langle\mathsf{SnapVer},;\mathsf{PolicyID},;\mathsf{GateSeq},;\mathsf{RelaxSpec},;\mathsf{StopSpec},;\mathsf{ResidualSpec},;\mathsf{ReceiptSpec},;\mathsf{BudgetCaps},;\mathsf{TieBreakSpec},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaPins},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Required fields:
GateSeq: ordered list of gate references (\langle P_1,\dots,P_m\rangle) by digest.
RelaxSpec: relaxation parameter specification (\lambda) and update form (M.S2.c).
StopSpec: deterministic stopping rule (M.S2.d).
ResidualSpec: which residual channels are computed, with pinned metrics and aggregation rules (M.S2.e).
ReceiptSpec: which holonomy/spin receipts are required during Snap (M.F2).
BudgetCaps: (\langle \kappa,\beta,\delta,\chi\rangle) interpreted for Snap iterations and receipt checks.
TieBreakSpec: deterministic tie-break rules used for any ambiguous choices (candidate selection, multilevel scheduling).
M.S1.d — Canonical representative and SnapResult schemaA Snap computation returns a canonical representative and required evidence artifacts.
[\mathsf{SnapResult}:=\langle\mathsf{SnapResultVer},;\mathsf{InputStateDigest},;\mathsf{OutputStateDigest},;\mathsf{GateSeqDigest},;\mathsf{IterCount},;\mathsf{ResidualLedgerBundleRef},;\mathsf{ReceiptBundleRef?},;\mathsf{CheckpointRef},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{TruthType},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
TruthType is typed under the corridor profile:
OK: all residuals are zero (or satisfy exact criteria) and required receipts are OK; replay closes.
NEAR: residuals are bounded and disclosed; required receipts are OK/NEAR per policy; replay closes.
AMBIG: candidate ambiguity exists (e.g., multiple fixed points admissible) and an evidence plan is attached.
FAIL/CONFLICT: Snap cannot meet corridor/budget requirements or determinism fails; conflict packet and fences may be required.
ResidualLedgerBundleRef is mandatory for NEAR. ReceiptBundleRef is mandatory when receipt checking is required by policy.
M.S2 — Operators
M.S2.a — Gate operator interfaceEach gate (P_i) is a deterministic map:[P_i : \mathsf{X} \to \mathsf{X}]with:
gate digest,
metric digest for its residual,
domain spec digest (where the gate is defined),
and a canonical failure mode schema.
Each gate must provide a residual channel:[r_i(x) := d_i(x, P_i(x))]where (d_i) is pinned in ResidualSpec.
M.S2.b — Snap composite mapGiven GateSeq ((P_1,\dots,P_m)), define:[T := P_m\circ \cdots \circ P_1.]
M.S2.c — Snap iteration (with pinned relaxation)Snap iteration is defined as a deterministic recurrence.
Strict iteration:[x^{(n+1)} := T(x^{(n)}).]
Relaxed iteration (when RelaxSpec specifies (\lambda\in(0,1])):[x^{(n+1)} := (1-\lambda)x^{(n)} + \lambda,T(x^{(n)}),]where the linear combination is interpreted in the pinned carrier (\mathsf{X}) (if (\mathsf{X}) is non-linear, RelaxSpec must pin the interpolation operator; no implicit interpolation is permitted).
RelaxSpec must pin:
exact numeric representation policy,
rounding policy,
and whether (\lambda) is constant or schedule-dependent.
M.S2.d — StopSpec (deterministic stopping rules)StopSpec defines a deterministic stop predicate:[\mathsf{Stop}(x^{(n)},x^{(n+1)},\mathbf{r}^{(n)},n,\mathsf{Budget})\in{\mathsf{true},\mathsf{false}}]where (\mathbf{r}^{(n)}=(r_1(x^{(n)}),\dots,r_m(x^{(n)}))). Required stop components:
MaxIter (bounded by (\chi)),
ConvergenceThreshold (pinned metric over state difference),
ResidualThresholds (pinned per-gate thresholds),
CycleDetect (deterministic detection of periodicity under pinned hash history window),
ReceiptGate (stop and fail/quarantine if required receipts fail).
Stopping must not depend on wall clock; it depends only on pinned values and iteration index.
M.S2.e — Residual ledger bundle emissionResidualSpec pins the set of residual channels:
Minimum required channels:
Gate residuals (r_i(x)) for each gate.
Commutation residual(s) when gates are declared to commute or approximately commute:
for gate pairs ((P_i,P_j)) required by policy, compute:[c_{ij}(x) := d_{ij}(P_i(P_j(x)), P_j(P_i(x)))]with pinned metric (d_{ij}) and budget (\kappa).
Optional drift residuals measuring deviation from seed invariants or canonical normal forms (pins required).
Residuals must be emitted as a ResidualLedgerBundle:[\mathsf{RLB}:=\langle\mathsf{BundleVer},;\mathsf{SubjectDigest},;\mathsf{LedgerRefs},;\mathsf{AggregateResidual},;\mathsf{BudgetLedgerRef},;\mathsf{PinsDigest}\rangle]where LedgerRefs is an ordered list of ResidualLedgers (AppJ schema) keyed by channel.
M.S2.f — Snap functionThe Snap operator is:
[\mathsf{Snap} : (\mathsf{X},\mathsf{SnapPolicy},\mathsf{CorridorProfile}) \to \mathsf{SnapResult}]
Algorithmically:
Initialize (x^{(0)}:=x).
For (n=0,1,\dots):
compute (x^{(n+1)}) by iteration rule,
compute residual channels,
verify receipts as required,
update budget ledger,
evaluate stop predicate.
On stop:
compute OutputStateDigest for (x^{(n_\star)}),
emit ResidualLedgerBundleRef,
emit required receipts bundle,
emit checkpoint,
emit replay capsule pointer,
type truth under corridor rules.
M.S3 — Recursion state schemas
M.S3.a — Frame and FrameStackRecursion proceeds by explicit frames and checkpoints.
A Frame is:
[\mathsf{Frame}:=\langle\mathsf{FrameVer},;\mathsf{FrameID},;\mathsf{ParentFrameID?},;\mathsf{DepthIndex},;\mathsf{ScaleIndex},;\mathsf{StateDigest},;\mathsf{CorridorID},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse}\rangle]
A FrameStack is a canonical ordered list of frames, top at the end, with digest commitments. FrameStackDigest commits to canonical serialization.
M.S3.b — Recursion legalityDepth transitions are permitted only via HatchEvents (AppG) and must update:
DepthIndex,
FrameStack,
CheckpointChain.
Any implicit increase in DepthIndex is illegal.
M.S3.c — Scale ladder and renormalization interfaceScaleLadderDigest commits to the sequence of scale levels and the allowed transitions:[\mathsf{ScaleLadder} := \langle s_0,\dots,s_L\rangle]with deterministic transition rules:
refine (increase resolution),
coarsen (decrease resolution),
renormalize (apply pinned renormalization operator).
All scale transitions are logged and require witness references when they impact semantics.
M.S4 — Checkpointing
M.S4.a — Checkpoint schemaA checkpoint binds:
pre-state digest,
post-state digest,
SnapPolicyDigest,
GateSeqDigest,
residual bundle digest,
receipts digest (if applicable),
replay capsule digest.
[\mathsf{Checkpoint}:=\langle\mathsf{CkVer},;\mathsf{CkID},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;k,;\mathsf{PreStateDigest},;\mathsf{PostStateDigest},;\mathsf{SnapPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ResidualBundleDigest},;\mathsf{ReceiptBundleDigest?},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Checkpoint chain is a hashed chain:[\mathsf{CkChain}(t) = \mathsf{H}(\mathsf{ser}(\mathsf{CkChain}(t-1), \mathsf{did}(\mathsf{Checkpoint}_t))).]This chain is committed inside FrState.
M.S4.b — Checkpoint integrity invariantMismatch between replayed checkpoint digest and recorded checkpoint digest is FAIL/CONFLICT under corridor policy. A checkpoint cannot be “fixed”; it can only be superseded by append-only new checkpoints and new policies.
❀ M.F — Flower: Renormalization-Compatible Invariants and Topology Receipts
M.F1 — Objects
M.F1.a — Renormalization operator interfaceA renormalization operator (R_s) maps state at scale (s) to a canonical comparable state at another scale (s'):
[R_{s\to s'} : \mathsf{X}s \to \mathsf{X}{s'}]pinned by digest and schema. Renormalization-compatible invariants are those preserved under (R_{s\to s'}) for declared transitions.
M.F1.b — InvariantSpecAn InvariantSpec is:
[\mathsf{InvSpec}:=\langle\mathsf{InvVer},;\mathsf{InvID},;\mathsf{ScopeDigest},;\mathsf{PredicateRef},;\mathsf{MetricDigest?},;\mathsf{Tolerance?},;\mathsf{PinsDigest}\rangle]where PredicateRef is a digest-qualified procedure for checking the invariant.
M.F2 — Operators
M.F2.a — Receipt gatingSnapPolicy may require topology receipts (spin/holonomy) as gates. ReceiptSpec pins which receipts are required for which gate pairs or schedule reorderings. Missing or failing receipts force AMBIG/FAIL per corridor.
M.F3 — Invariants
M.F3.a — Renormalization invarianceIf an invariant is declared renormalization-compatible, its check must commute with renormalization up to declared tolerance:[\mathsf{Inv}(R(x)) \approx \mathsf{Inv}(x)]with approximation semantics pinned by InvSpec.
☁ M.C — Cloud: Truth Typing for Snap and Residual/AMBIG Discipline
M.C1 — Objects
M.C1.a — Snap truth typingSnap outcomes are typed by corridor rules:
OK: all residual channels are zero (or satisfy exact criteria), required receipts OK, replay closes.
NEAR: residual channels bounded by (\beta) and commutation bounded by (\kappa); residual ledgers required; replay closes.
AMBIG: multiple admissible fixed points or multiple admissible gate schedules without pinned discrimination; requires EvidencePlan (AppL).
FAIL/CONFLICT: determinism violation, budget overflow without allowed downgrade, or replay disagreement.
M.C2 — Operators
M.C2.a — Multi-solution ambiguity detectionIf SnapPolicy permits multiple initializations or multilevel schedules, ambiguity must be bounded and represented explicitly; otherwise failure is required.
M.C3 — Invariants
M.C3.a — No silent NEAR/AMBIGNEAR requires ResidualLedgerBundle; AMBIG requires EvidencePlan; absence is FAIL.
✶ M.R — Fractal: Replay Closure and FractalReplayCert
M.R1 — FractalReplayCapsule
A FractalReplayCapsule must include:
SnapPolicy digest,
GateSeq digests and gate artifacts,
initial state digest and retrieval closure,
environment pins digest,
expected SnapResult digest,
expected residual bundle digest,
expected checkpoint digest,
required receipt digests (if any),
budget caps and expected budget ledger digest.
M.R2 — FractalReplayCert (required)
A FractalReplayCert certifies that Snap and recursion/checkpoint behavior are reproducible under pinned environment and policies.
[\mathsf{FractalReplayCert}:=\langle\mathsf{FrStateDigest},;\mathsf{SnapPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{CapsuleDigest},;\mathsf{EnvPinsDigest},;\mathsf{ExpectedSnapResultDigest},;\mathsf{ObservedSnapResultDigest},;\mathsf{ExpectedResidualBundleDigest},;\mathsf{ObservedResidualBundleDigest},;\mathsf{ExpectedCheckpointDigest},;\mathsf{ObservedCheckpointDigest},;\mathsf{Result},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Result is PASS iff all expected digests match observed digests and all required receipts verify under pinned rules.
Mismatch yields FAIL/CONFLICT per corridor policy and triggers quarantine when required.
AppM Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
SnapPolicy pins ordered corridor gates, relaxation, stopping rules, residual channels, receipt requirements, budgets, and tie-break rules.
Snap returns a canonical representative plus ResidualLedgerBundle and checkpoint; truth typing is determined by corridor rules and must be replayable.
Recursion is represented by explicit frames, depth ledgers, and hatch/ checkpoint boundaries; no implicit recursion is permitted.
Scale transitions and renormalization operators are pinned and must preserve declared renormalization-compatible invariants within pinned tolerances.
Residual and commutation channels are mandatory outputs; NEAR requires residual ledgers; AMBIG requires evidence plans; FAIL/CONFLICT require failure/conflict artifacts.
FractalReplayCert is required and must validate deterministic replay of Snap results, residual bundles, receipt checks, and checkpoint digests.
AppM — Fractal/Recursion, Snap/Meta-zero, Scaling and Renormalization Interfaces
AppN — Containers, Buckets, Mount/Salvage Doctrine, Replay Harnesses
Station role: container system backbone; mount/salvage rules; replay harness structure.Purpose: define container formats, mount rules, salvage outcomes, and replay harness expectations used by Ch18 and enforced in Ch21.
□ N.S — Square: Container Schemas, Deterministic Manifests, and Content-Addressed Layout
N.S1 — Objects
N.S1.a — Container as a typed, self-describing bundleA Container is a self-describing, content-addressed package:
[\mathsf{Container}:=\langle\mathsf{ContVer},;\mathsf{ContID},;\mathsf{ManifestRef},;\mathsf{PayloadLayoutRef},;\mathsf{ChunkIndexRef},;\mathsf{PinManifestRef},;\mathsf{WitnessIndexRef},;\mathsf{ReplayIndexRef},;\mathsf{DisclosureIndexRef},;\mathsf{FenceIndexRef},;\mathsf{RevocationIndexRef},;\mathsf{SignatureBundleRef?},;\mathsf{ContDigest}\rangle]
ContID and ContDigest are content-addressed digests of the container bytes under canonical encoding.
All *Ref fields are addressable references (digest + schema ID + locator).
Missing required references invalidates import acceptance for deploy corridors.
N.S1.b — Deterministic manifest schema (mandatory)A ContainerManifest is the authoritative self-description.
[\mathsf{Manifest}:=\langle\mathsf{ManVer},;\mathsf{SchemaSetDigest},;\mathsf{CanonBytesDigest},;\mathsf{HashAlgDigest},;\mathsf{ContainerFormatID},;\mathsf{LayoutPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ChunkPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{CompressionPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{EncryptionPolicyDigest?},;\mathsf{PinPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ImportPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{RevocationPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{DisclosurePolicyDigest},;\mathsf{FencePolicyDigest},;\mathsf{Scope},;\mathsf{PulseRange?},;\mathsf{ProducedBy},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Deterministic requirements:
Manifest must be canonically serializable under CanonBytesDigest.
Every referenced policy digest must resolve and be included in the pin closure.
ContainerFormatID selects a concrete byte layout; format changes require migration.
If encryption is enabled, EncryptionPolicyDigest must pin algorithm, mode, key identifier policy, and deterministic IV derivation rules (or explicitly permit nondeterministic IVs and mark output non-replayable for strict corridors; default forbids nondeterministic encryption for replayable containers).
N.S1.c — Payload layout and chunk indexPayload is represented as a set of chunks. A ChunkIndex is:
[\mathsf{ChunkIndex}:=\langle\mathsf{ChunkVer},;\mathsf{ChunkPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{Chunks},;\mathsf{RootDigest},;\mathsf{IndexDigest}\rangle]
Chunks is an ordered list:[\mathsf{Chunk}:=\langle \mathsf{ChunkID},\ \mathsf{Offset},\ \mathsf{Length},\ \mathsf{ChunkDigest},\ \mathsf{Role}\rangle]
Ordering of chunks is pinned (by role then offset then digest).
RootDigest is a Merkle root or canonical fold digest over ordered chunk digests (pinned by ChunkPolicyDigest).
IndexDigest is content address for ChunkIndex with IndexDigest field zeroed.
N.S1.d — PinManifest (mandatory)A PinManifest is the explicit pin closure required to interpret and replay the container.
[\mathsf{PinManifest}:=\langle\mathsf{PinVer},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{Pins},;\mathsf{ClosureDigest},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Pins is a canonical ordered map from pin keys to digests.
ClosureDigest commits to the transitive closure of pinned digests required for interpretation (schemas, policies, profiles, codebooks, harnesses).
PinsDigest is the digest of the canonical pins map.
N.S1.e — Witness, replay, disclosure, fence, and revocation indicesIndices are mandatory tables mapping semantic roles to artifact references.
WitnessIndex: proofs, tests, expected digests, baseline pointers.
ReplayIndex: replay capsules and harness entrypoints.
DisclosureIndex: NEAR disclosure bundles (AppJ) and AMBIG evidence plans (AppL).
FenceIndex: conflict packets and fences (AppK).
RevocationIndex: revocation receipts or revocation list digests (AppK/AppO).
Each index is a deterministic, canonically ordered table with an index digest.
N.S2 — Operators
N.S2.a — Deterministic container build operator[\mathsf{BuildContainer} : (\mathsf{PayloadArtifacts},\mathsf{PinClosure},\mathsf{Policies}) \to \mathsf{Container}]
BuildContainer must:
Canonicalize all referenced artifacts and policies.
Construct deterministic layout and chunking per ChunkPolicyDigest.
Compute chunk digests and root digest deterministically.
Emit indices (PinManifest, WitnessIndex, ReplayIndex, DisclosureIndex, FenceIndex, RevocationIndex).
Emit manifest and sign as required.
Produce container bytes deterministically; ContDigest must match computed bytes digest.
Any nondeterminism in layout, ordering, compression, or encryption must be pinned and reflected in corridor truth typing; strict replay corridors forbid unpinned nondeterminism.
N.S2.b — Deterministic container parse operator[\mathsf{ParseContainer} : (\mathsf{Bytes}) \to (\mathsf{Container},\mathsf{Manifest},\mathsf{ChunkIndex},\ldots) \cup \mathsf{ParseFail}]Parsing must validate:
schema versions,
canonical encodings,
chunk index and root digest consistency,
manifest signature validity if required.
N.S2.c — Deterministic integrity verification operator[\mathsf{VerifyIntegrity} : (\mathsf{Container}) \to {\mathsf{PASS},\mathsf{FAIL}}\times \mathsf{IntegrityReport}]IntegrityReport must include:
manifest digest check,
chunk digests check,
root digest check,
index digests check,
pin manifest check.
Failures are classified deterministically with minimal failure witnesses.
N.S3 — Invariants
N.S3.a — Deterministic manifest invariantFor fixed inputs and pinned policies:[\mathsf{did}(\mathsf{Manifest})\ \text{is deterministic.}]Any manifest drift under identical inputs is a determinism failure.
N.S3.b — Content-addressed closure invariantEvery reference digest in indices must resolve to content whose digest matches the reference; otherwise the container is invalid.
N.S3.c — Replay closure invariant for replayable containersIf the container declares replayability under ReplayPolicyDigest, then:
ReplayIndex must be complete,
replay capsules must resolve,
and replay must reproduce expected digests.
A replayable container missing required replay capsules is invalid for deploy corridors.
N.S4 — Protocols: Deterministic indices and canonical ordering
N.S4.a — Canonical ordering rulesAll maps are encoded with keys in canonical byte order. All lists with semantic set meaning are sorted by pinned comparator. Chunk ordering is by (role, offset, digest).
N.S4.b — Deterministic index constructionAll index digests must be recomputable from referenced artifacts. Index construction must not depend on file system ordering or network order.
❀ N.F — Flower: Mount Rules, Seek Semantics, and Replay Harness Structure
N.F1 — Objects
N.F1.a — MountContextMounting is interpreting a container into an executable artifact store view.
[\mathsf{MountContext}:=\langle\mathsf{MountVer},;\mathsf{ContainerDigest},;\mathsf{PolicyDigests},;\mathsf{EnvPinsDigest},;\mathsf{ResolvedPinsDigest},;\mathsf{RevocationSetDigest},;\mathsf{FenceSetDigest},;\mathsf{MountDigest}\rangle]
MountContext must be content-addressed and must commit to:
the exact pins used,
the revocation receipts applied,
the fences applied,
and the environment constraints.
N.F1.b — ReplayHarness schemaA replay harness is a deterministic executor specification:
[\mathsf{ReplayHarness}:=\langle\mathsf{HarnessVer},;\mathsf{HarnessID},;\mathsf{EntryPoints},;\mathsf{InputSchemas},;\mathsf{OutputSchemas},;\mathsf{DeterminismChecklistDigest},;\mathsf{BudgetCaps},;\mathsf{ExpectedDigestRules},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
EntryPoints define callable replay programs by name and digest.
DeterminismChecklistDigest pins forbidden unpinned dependencies (time, RNG, network).
ExpectedDigestRules pins what digests are compared (bytes, NF digests, transcript digests).
N.F2 — Operators
N.F2.a — Mount operator[\mathsf{Mount} : (\mathsf{Container}, \mathsf{MountPolicy}) \to \mathsf{MountedView} \cup \mathsf{MountFail}]MountPolicy is pinned and must specify:
Required integrity checks before mount.
Pin resolution behavior: strict or permissive (deploy corridors require strict).
Revocation enforcement: must apply all effective revocations.
Fence enforcement: must apply all fences/quarantines.
Allowed materialization: what indices are materialized into local caches (must not change semantics).
MountedView is a content-addressed mapping from logical artifact roles to resolved artifact bytes and schema interpreters.
N.F2.b — Seek operator (chunk retrieval)Seek retrieves chunk bytes by chunk ID.
[\mathsf{Seek} : (\mathsf{MountedView}, \mathsf{ChunkID}) \to \mathsf{Bytes} \cup \mathsf{SeekFail}]SeekFail must be typed:
missing chunk,
digest mismatch,
revocation blocked,
fence blocked.
Seek must validate chunk digest upon retrieval.
N.F2.c — Replay operator[\mathsf{Replay} : (\mathsf{MountedView}, \mathsf{ReplayCapsule}, \mathsf{ReplayHarness}) \to \mathsf{ReplayReport}]Replay must:
verify pin closure and schemas,
execute deterministically under EnvPinsDigest,
compute outputs and transcript digests,
compare against expected digests.
N.F3 — Invariants
N.F3.a — Mount determinism invariantFor identical container digest, pinned policies, and environment pins, Mount must produce identical MountedView digests and identical resolved pin digests.
N.F3.b — Seek integrity invariantSeek must never return bytes whose digest does not match the ChunkDigest. Any mismatch yields FAIL.
N.F3.c — Replay determinism invariantReplay outcomes and transcript digests must be stable under identical pins and environment constraints.
☁ N.C — Cloud: Salvage Doctrine, Seek/Salvage Semantics, and Truth Typing
N.C1 — Objects
N.C1.a — SalvageReport schemaA salvage operation produces a structured report:
[\mathsf{SalvageReport}:=\langle\mathsf{SalvVer},;\mathsf{ContainerDigest},;\mathsf{IntegrityFailures},;\mathsf{RecoveredChunks},;\mathsf{UnrecoverableChunks},;\mathsf{RecoveredIndices},;\mathsf{TruthScope},;\mathsf{ResidualLedgerRefs?},;\mathsf{EvidencePlanRef?},;\mathsf{ReplayPtr?},;\mathsf{ResultTruthType},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse}\rangle]
TruthScope partitions claims into:
verified true under replay,
unknown (missing required bytes or pins),
disproven (digest mismatch or replay mismatch),
blocked (revocation/fence).
N.C1.b — SalvageOutcome truth typingSalvage outcomes are typed as:
OK: container mounts and verifies; no salvage required.
NEAR: partial recovery with bounded uncertainty; residual ledgers required.
FAIL: unrecoverable; must include minimal failure witnesses and may include an evidence plan if bounded recovery is possible.
CONFLICT: inconsistent recovery across replays; must emit conflict packet and fence.
Salvage truth typing must be deterministic under pinned salvage policies.
N.C2 — Operators
N.C2.a — Salvage operator[\mathsf{Salvage} : (\mathsf{Bytes}, \mathsf{SalvagePolicy}) \to (\mathsf{CandidateContainer?}, \mathsf{SalvageReport})]SalvagePolicy is pinned and must specify:
Redundancy mechanisms allowed (mirrors, erasure coding, witness reconstruction).
Maximum salvage compute budget.
Which indices may be reconstructed from witnesses.
Whether reconstructed chunks are permitted; if yes, the new container must be a new content-addressed object, never altering the original digest.
If salvage produces a candidate container, it must be explicitly marked as a new container with new digest; the original remains unchanged.
N.C2.b — Salvage truth typing rules
NEAR requires ResidualLedgerRefs bounding what is uncertain (AppJ).
AMBIG requires EvidencePlanRef for further recovery steps (AppL).
FAIL requires a reproducible failure witness set.
N.C3 — Invariants
N.C3.a — No silent salvageA salvaged container is never treated as the original; it is a new artifact. Any reliance on salvage must be disclosed via NEAR ledgers and salvage reports.
N.C3.b — Revocation precedenceSalvage cannot override revocation; if a chunk or key is revoked, salvage must treat it as blocked regardless of recoverability.
N.C4 — Protocols: Salvage regression fixtures
Salvage regression fixtures must cover:
Single-chunk corruption detection and failure witness.
Multi-chunk corruption with successful recovery via pinned redundancy.
Index corruption with reconstruction from witness bundles.
Pin manifest corruption: must fail or require evidence plan depending on policy.
Replay-index missing: must prevent deploy acceptance.
Conflict in reconstruction (two different recovered bytes): must emit conflict packet and fence.
Each fixture must bind expected salvage truth type and expected report digests.
✶ N.R — Fractal: Replay Harness Expectations and Certificates for Containers
N.R1 — ContainerReplayCapsule
A container replay capsule must include:
container digest,
required pin closure digest,
replay harness digest,
set of replay entrypoints to execute,
expected output digests,
expected transcript digest,
environment pins digest.
N.R2 — Required certificates
N.R2.a — ContainerIntegrityCertCertifies manifest, index, and chunk digests match; required for import acceptance.
N.R2.b — MountDeterminismCertCertifies that mounting produces a deterministic MountedView digest under pinned policies.
N.R2.c — SalvageDeterminismCertCertifies salvage report and candidate container digest are deterministic under pinned salvage policy.
N.R2.d — ContainerReplayCertCertifies replay harness execution over the mounted container reproduces expected digests and transcript digests under pinned environment.
AppN Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
Container schema includes deterministic manifest, chunk index with root digest, pin manifest with closure digest, and indices for witnesses, replay capsules, disclosures, fences, and revocations.
BuildContainer must be deterministic under pinned layout/chunk/compression/encryption policies; container digest is content-addressed and reproducible for identical inputs.
Mount must validate integrity, resolve pins, apply revocations and fences, and produce a deterministic MountedView; seek validates chunk digests on retrieval.
Salvage is a pinned, deterministic procedure producing a SalvageReport typed as OK/NEAR/FAIL/CONFLICT; salvaged outputs are new artifacts with new digests; no silent salvage.
Replay harnesses are pinned objects specifying deterministic execution and digest comparisons; replayable containers must include complete replay indices.
Salvage truth typing and regression fixtures are mandatory; container integrity, mount determinism, salvage determinism, and container replay certificates are required for deploy corridors.
AppN — Containers, Buckets, Mount/Salvage Doctrine, Replay Harnesses
AppO — Publication, ExportBundles, ImportVerifiers, Governance Gates
Station role: publish/import discipline; governance closure; production acceptance rules.Purpose: define mechanized publication (bundles, manifests, pins, signatures if enabled), import verification rules, and governance gates used by Ch20/Ch21.
□ O.S — Square: ExportBundle Schema, Deterministic Manifests, and Governance Gates
O.S1 — Objects
O.S1.a — ExportBundle (normative schema)An ExportBundle is a content-addressed, import-verifiable publication unit containing payloads plus all governance-relevant overlays.
[\mathsf{ExportBundle}:=\langle\mathsf{EBVer},;\mathsf{EBID},;\mathsf{BundleScope},;\mathsf{BundleManifestRef},;\mathsf{PayloadIndexRef},;\mathsf{PinManifestRef},;\mathsf{WitnessIndexRef},;\mathsf{ReplayIndexRef},;\mathsf{DisclosureIndexRef},;\mathsf{FenceIndexRef},;\mathsf{RevocationIndexRef},;\mathsf{SchemaIndexRef},;\mathsf{SignatureBundleRef?},;\mathsf{BundleDigest}\rangle]
EBID is the content-addressed identifier derived from the bundle bytes under canonical encoding and hash.
BundleDigest is the digest of the full bundle bytes (may equal EBID).
All *Ref fields are addressable references (digest + schema + locator) and are mandatory except SignatureBundleRef which may be absent only if signature policy explicitly permits unsigned bundles.
O.S1.b — BundleScopeBundleScope binds what is being published:
[\mathsf{BundleScope}:=\langle\mathsf{ScopeVer},;\mathsf{ScopeKind},;\mathsf{MsIDs},;\mathsf{PulseRange?},;\mathsf{SubjectSetDigest},;\mathsf{ImportCorridorID},;\mathsf{PolicyDigest}\rangle]
ScopeKind ∈ {LOCAL, INTER, PULSE_RANGE, PROFILE_SET, CERT_SET, CUSTOM} pinned enum.
MsIDs is required for INTER.
PulseRange is required for PULSE_RANGE (Ch20).
SubjectSetDigest commits to the ordered set of primary subjects (addresses/digests) published.
ImportCorridorID pins the corridor to be enforced on import.
PolicyDigest pins publication/import rules and governance gates.
O.S1.c — BundleManifest (deterministic and mandatory)BundleManifest is the authoritative self-description of the bundle.
[\mathsf{BundleManifest}:=\langle\mathsf{ManVer},;\mathsf{CanonBytesDigest},;\mathsf{HashAlgDigest},;\mathsf{PolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ImportCorridorID},;\mathsf{SchemaSetDigest},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{PayloadRootDigest},;\mathsf{WitnessRootDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayRootDigest},;\mathsf{DisclosureRootDigest},;\mathsf{FenceRootDigest},;\mathsf{RevocationRootDigest},;\mathsf{RegistrySnapshotDigest?},;\mathsf{ProducedBy},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Determinism requirements:
Manifest must be canonically serializable; key ordering and field omission rules are pinned by CanonBytesDigest.
All *RootDigest fields are deterministic commits to their respective indices’ chunk sets (Merkle or canonical fold pinned by policy).
RegistrySnapshotDigest is required when publishing time-axis slices (Ch20 pulse bundles) or cross-corpus bundles requiring registry anchoring.
O.S1.d — Required indicesEach index is a deterministic table mapping stable keys to artifact references.
PayloadIndex: core payload artifacts (tiles, profiles, policies, code, data, tables).
PinManifest: full pin closure (AppN) including schema and policy closure digests.
WitnessIndex: proof objects, test fixtures, expected digests, transport receipts, certificates required by corridor.
ReplayIndex: replay capsules and replay harness references required for import acceptance.
DisclosureIndex: NEAR ledgers (AppJ) and AMBIG evidence plans (AppL), plus disclosure bundles.
FenceIndex: conflict packets, fences, quarantines (AppK).
RevocationIndex: revocation receipts and revocation sets effective in the published scope (AppK).
SchemaIndex: schema closure required to interpret every object referenced in indices and to run import verifiers deterministically.
All indices must be canonically ordered and must include their own index digests.
O.S1.e — GovernanceGate objectA GovernanceGate is a pinned, decidable predicate over a bundle and its closure.
[\mathsf{GovGate}:=\langle\mathsf{GateVer},;\mathsf{GateID},;\mathsf{GateKind},;\mathsf{PredicateRef},;\mathsf{RequiredInputsDigest},;\mathsf{FailureActionSpec},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
GateKind ∈ {SIGNATURE_REQUIRED, KEY_ALLOWLIST, POLICY_EPOCH_MATCH, SCHEMA_COMPAT, REPLAY_REQUIRED, NO_REVOKED_DIGESTS, NO_FORKS, CORRIDOR_MIN_TRUTH, CUSTOM}.
PredicateRef points to a deterministic predicate procedure/harness by digest.
RequiredInputsDigest commits to the inputs required to evaluate the gate.
FailureActionSpec pins whether failure results in REJECT or QUARANTINE and which quarantine records must be emitted.
Governance gates are evaluated during import acceptance and may also be evaluated at publish time to produce PublicationCert.
O.S2 — Operators
O.S2.a — Bundle build operator[\mathsf{BuildBundle} : (\mathsf{SubjectSet},\mathsf{Policy},\mathsf{Corridor},\mathsf{RegistrySnap?}) \to \mathsf{ExportBundle}]
BuildBundle must:
Compute deterministic closure of subjects:
all referenced payload artifacts,
all pins and policy objects required,
required witnesses and replay capsules required by ImportCorridorID,
all required disclosures, fences, revocations, and schemas.
Emit indices with canonical ordering.
Compute root digests for each index.
Emit deterministic BundleManifest and sign per signature policy.
Serialize bundle deterministically and compute BundleDigest/EBID.
O.S2.b — Bundle closure computationClosure is a deterministic graph reachability computation:
[\mathsf{Closure}(\mathsf{SubjectSet}) = \mathsf{SubjectSet} \cup \mathsf{Deps}(\mathsf{SubjectSet}) \cup \mathsf{Deps}^2(\mathsf{SubjectSet}) \cup \dots]where (\mathsf{Deps}) is pinned and returns required dependencies of an object under the import corridor.
Closure must terminate under pinned budgets and must emit an explicit truncation witness if policy permits partial closure; deploy corridors should forbid truncation.
O.S2.c — Digest verification operator[\mathsf{VerifyDigests} : (\mathsf{ExportBundle}) \to {\mathsf{PASS},\mathsf{FAIL}}\times \mathsf{DigestReport}]DigestReport must include:
manifest digest validation,
index digests validation,
chunk digests validation for all artifacts referenced,
root digests validation.
O.S2.d — Gate evaluation operator[\mathsf{EvalGates} : (\mathsf{ExportBundle}, \mathsf{GovGateSet}) \to \mathsf{GateReport}]GateReport is canonically ordered and binds:
each GateID,
pass/fail,
evidence references,
required action on failure.
O.S3 — Invariants
O.S3.a — Import-verifiability invariantA bundle is import-verifiable only if:
all referenced digests resolve within the bundle or by allowed external resolution pinned in policy,
all schemas required to interpret objects are present,
all pins required for replay are present,
and required replays can be executed deterministically under EnvPins.
O.S3.b — No hidden state invariantImport acceptance depends only on:
bundle bytes,
pinned import verifier,
pinned policies and schemas included in the bundle or resolvable by digest under policy.No external hidden state is permitted.
O.S3.c — No silent fork invariantIf the bundle introduces or depends on multiple incompatible interpretations of the same typed key under identical pins, import must reject or quarantine per policy. Fork detection must be deterministic (AppD).
O.S3.d — Revocation precedence invariantAny revoked digest within the bundle’s closure must trigger failure according to revocation policy. Revocation cannot be overridden by convenience.
❀ O.F — Flower: ImportVerifier Algorithm (Deterministic Acceptance Pipeline)
O.F1 — Objects
O.F1.a — ImportVerifier schemaAn ImportVerifier is a deterministic algorithm specification pinned by digest.
[\mathsf{ImportVerifier}:=\langle\mathsf{IVerVer},;\mathsf{IVerID},;\mathsf{PolicyDigest},;\mathsf{CorridorID},;\mathsf{GateSetDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ForkPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{RevocationPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{BudgetCaps},;\mathsf{TieBreakSpec},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
TieBreakSpec pins:
ordering of evaluations,
deterministic selection among multiple replay capsules if policy permits choices,
deterministic truncation behavior if allowed (deploy corridors should forbid).
O.F1.b — ImportVerdictImport verification yields:[\mathsf{Verdict}\in{\mathsf{ACCEPT},\mathsf{REJECT},\mathsf{QUARANTINE}}]plus an import transcript and a publishable certificate (ImportAcceptanceCert).
O.F2 — ImportVerifier algorithm (mandatory steps)
Given bundle bytes (B):
Parse and canonicalizeParse bundle into ExportBundle object and BundleManifest under CanonBytesDigest. Fail if parsing or canonicalization fails.
Verify internal digestsRun VerifyDigests; fail if any manifest/index/chunk digest mismatch.
Resolve schema closureLoad SchemaIndex and verify SchemaSetDigest closure is complete for all referenced objects. Reject if schema closure incomplete for deploy corridors; quarantine only if policy explicitly allows partial interpretability.
Resolve pins and pin closureLoad PinManifest; verify PinsDigest and ClosureDigest. Reject if missing required pins for ImportCorridorID.
Evaluate revocations and fencesLoad RevocationIndex and FenceIndex. Compute effective revocation set and fence set under pinned propagation rules. If any required artifact is revoked, reject or quarantine per RevocationPolicy. Apply fences to routing/verification scope deterministically.
Fork rejection and registry anchoringIf bundle scope requires registry anchoring:
resolve RegistrySnapshotDigest,
verify RegistryCert and ForkPreventionCert in WitnessIndex,
compute fork set under ForkPolicyDigest,
reject/quarantine if forks detected per policy.
Corridor enforcement pre-checkEnforce static corridor constraints:
allowed edge kinds,
required artifacts present for MinTruth,
required disclosures present if NEAR is admissible.
Replay execution (mandatory where required)Using ReplayIndex, execute required replay capsules under ReplayPolicyDigest:
verify harness digests,
verify environment pins,
execute deterministically,
compare output and transcript digests to expected digests.If any required replay fails, reject/quarantine per policy.
Evaluate governance gatesEvaluate gate set; apply failure actions deterministically.
Compute final verdictCombine outcomes deterministically using policy precedence:
digest mismatch ⇒ REJECT
revoked critical artifact ⇒ REJECT (unless policy allows quarantine)
replay failure on required capsule ⇒ QUARANTINE or REJECT per policy
gate failure ⇒ action per FailureActionSpec
otherwise ACCEPT
Emit import transcript and ImportAcceptanceCertImport transcript is canonically serialized and content-addressed. ImportAcceptanceCert binds verdict, used policies, digests, and executed replays.
This algorithm is deterministic and must be replayable from bundle bytes and pinned verifier digest.
☁ O.C — Cloud: Corridor Enforcement, Disclosures, and Quarantine Semantics on Import
O.C1 — Objects
O.C1.a — Import transcriptAn import transcript is:
[\mathsf{ImportTx}:=\langle\mathsf{TxVer},;\mathsf{BundleDigest},;\mathsf{ImportVerifierID},;\mathsf{ManifestDigest},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaSetDigest},;\mathsf{RevocationSetDigest},;\mathsf{FenceSetDigest},;\mathsf{GateReportDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayReportDigest},;\mathsf{CorridorEvalDigest},;\mathsf{ForkEvalDigest},;\mathsf{Verdict},;\mathsf{Warnings},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Warnings is a canonical list of typed warnings; warnings must not affect verdict unless policy specifies.
O.C1.b — Corridor enforcement on importImportCorridorID pins:
MinTruth threshold,
required disclosures,
required witness classes.
If bundle does not include required disclosure bundles for NEAR items that are used by any routable claim, bundle must be quarantined or rejected under corridor rules.
✶ O.R — Fractal: PublicationCert and ImportAcceptanceCert
O.R1 — PublicationCert (required)
A PublicationCert attests that the published bundle is structurally complete, deterministically built, and governance-gate compliant under the publication corridor.
[\mathsf{PublicationCert}:=\langle\mathsf{PubVer},;\mathsf{BundleDigest},;\mathsf{BundleManifestDigest},;\mathsf{PolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ImportCorridorID},;\mathsf{GateSetDigest},;\mathsf{BuildClosureDigest},;\mathsf{DigestReportDigest},;\mathsf{GateReportDigest},;\mathsf{Result},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
BuildClosureDigest commits to the deterministic closure computation used to assemble the bundle. Result is PASS iff:
digest verification passes,
gate evaluation passes,
and mandatory indices are present and consistent.
PublicationCert does not substitute for ImportAcceptanceCert; it provides publish-time attestation.
O.R2 — ImportAcceptanceCert (required)
An ImportAcceptanceCert attests the result of running the ImportVerifier algorithm on the bundle.
[\mathsf{ImportAcceptanceCert}:=\langle\mathsf{IACVer},;\mathsf{BundleDigest},;\mathsf{ImportVerifierID},;\mathsf{PolicyDigest},;\mathsf{ImportCorridorID},;\mathsf{ImportTxDigest},;\mathsf{ExecutedReplaySetDigest},;\mathsf{GateReportDigest},;\mathsf{ForkEvalDigest},;\mathsf{RevocationEvalDigest},;\mathsf{Verdict},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Verdict is ACCEPT/REJECT/QUARANTINE. The cert is valid only if ImportTxDigest resolves and matches the transcript produced by the pinned verifier.
AppO Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
ExportBundle schema includes payloads, deterministic manifest, pin manifest, witness index, replay index, disclosure index, fence index, revocation index, schema index, and optional signature bundle under pinned policy.
ImportVerifier is a deterministic algorithm that validates digests, schema closure, pin closure, revocations, fences, forks, corridor constraints, required replays, and governance gates to produce ACCEPT/REJECT/QUARANTINE.
Import must reject or quarantine on digest mismatch, revoked closure intersections, replay failures, or fork detection per pinned policy; no hidden state is permitted.
PublicationCert attests publish-time closure and gate compliance; ImportAcceptanceCert attests import-time verification and verdict under pinned verifier.
Publication/import semantics are deployment-grade and are enforced by Ch20/Ch21; bundles must be import-verifiable and reproducible.
AppO — Publication, ExportBundles, ImportVerifiers, Governance Gates
AppP — Mycelium Interface: Cross-Corpus Linking, External Connectors, and Scope
Station role: cross-corpus interface; connectors; INTER-scope routing discipline.Purpose: define cross-manuscript linking rules, scope boundaries, connector interfaces, and cross-corpus pin requirements used by Ch19–Ch21.
□ P.S — Square: INTER Link Schema, Scope Boundaries, and Pin Requirements
P.S1 — Objects
P.S1.a — Scope boundary modelA scope is a pinned boundary that determines what artifacts, policies, and interpretations are admissible for routing and verification.
[\mathsf{Scope}:=\langle\mathsf{ScopeVer},;\mathsf{ScopeID},;\mathsf{ScopeKind},;\mathsf{MsSet},;\mathsf{ProfileSetDigest},;\mathsf{PolicyEpochSetDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaPinsDigest},;\mathsf{ConnectorSetDigest?},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
ScopeKind ∈ {LOCAL, INTER, CONNECTED, PUBLISHED} pinned enum.
MsSet is the ordered set of MsIDs in scope (required for INTER and beyond).
ProfileSetDigest commits to admissible profile digests per MsID.
PolicyEpochSetDigest commits to admissible policy epochs for interpretation (AppD).
SchemaPinsDigest commits to the schema closure required to interpret all referenced corpora.
ConnectorSetDigest commits to the connector definitions allowed (required for CONNECTED and PUBLISHED).
ScopeID is content-addressed and derived deterministically.
P.S1.b — INTER link schema (mandatory)An INTER link is a typed edge that connects objects across manuscripts. It is never a raw URL; it is a pinned, interpreted link.
[\mathsf{INTERLink}:=\langle\mathsf{InterVer},;\mathsf{InterID},;\mathsf{SrcMsID},;\mathsf{DstMsID},;\mathsf{SrcProfileDigest},;\mathsf{DstProfileDigest},;\mathsf{SrcAddr},;\mathsf{DstAddr},;\mathsf{LinkKind},;\mathsf{CompatRef?},;\mathsf{PinsDigest},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Required fields:
SrcMsID/DstMsID: manuscript IDs (Ms⟨…⟩) resolvable in the registry.
SrcProfileDigest/DstProfileDigest: explicit pinned interpretation profiles for both sides.
SrcAddr/DstAddr: addressable endpoints (GlobalAddr/SlotAddr) under the corresponding profile’s grammar and schema pins.
LinkKind: pinned enum:
REF (addressability only),
EQUIV (semantic equivalence, requires witness),
MIGRATE (meaning-bearing evolution, requires witness),
DATA (data dependency, requires import constraints),
PROOF (proof dependency, requires verification closure),
EXEC (execution dependency, requires deploy corridor and explicit governance).
CompatRef?: compatibility/migration pointer required when LinkKind ∈ {EQUIV, MIGRATE, EXEC} or whenever profiles/policies differ across endpoints.
PinsDigest: full pin closure required to interpret and validate the link, including both profiles and any compat objects.
Sig: required signature under cross-corpus governance policy.
InterID is content-addressed and derived deterministically from the link record with InterID and signatures zeroed.
P.S1.c — Compatibility edge objects (CompatRef)CompatRef points to one of:
CompatMatrix (AppF/AppD): explicit compatibility mapping between profiles/policies/schemas.
MigrateWitnessBundle: explicit MIGRATE witness with rollback/import constraints.
EquivWitnessBundle: explicit EQUIV witness with replay closure.
CompatRef is mandatory whenever a link would otherwise require implicit inference of equivalence between two different interpretation closures.
P.S1.d — Cross-corpus pin requirementsA cross-corpus link is admissible only if all of the following are pinned:
Both MsIDs and their manifest digests.
Both profile digests (Src and Dst) and their policy epochs.
CanonBytes and Grammar digests for both sides (or a single shared closure, explicitly pinned).
Corridor ID used for validation of the link kind.
Import/verifier policy digests used to accept the referenced external artifacts.
Revocation and fence sets effective in the referenced scope.
Missing any required pin makes the link non-OK-routable; it must be AMBIG with an evidence plan or FAIL depending on corridor threshold.
P.S2 — Operators
P.S2.a — Scope membership predicate[\mathsf{InScope} : (\mathsf{Scope}, \mathsf{MsID}, \mathsf{ProfileDigest}, \mathsf{PolicyEpochDigest}) \to {\mathsf{true},\mathsf{false}}]A link is valid only if both endpoints are InScope under the active scope for the route/execution.
P.S2.b — INTER link validation operator[\mathsf{ValidateINTER} : (\mathsf{INTERLink}, \mathsf{Scope}, \mathsf{CorridorProfile}) \to \mathsf{TruthType}]
Validation must:
Validate signatures and authority.
Validate pin closure resolves and matches both profile closures.
Validate both endpoints parse and resolve under pinned grammars.
Apply LinkKind rules:
REF: requires only addressability and closure validity.
EQUIV: requires EquivWitnessBundle with replay closure.
MIGRATE: requires CompatMatrix + MigrateWitnessBundle + import constraints.
DATA: requires data import rules and schema closure.
PROOF: requires proof verification closure and replay harness.
EXEC: requires deployment corridor acceptance predicates and governance gates.
Apply fences and revocations: any revoked dependency yields FAIL/QUARANTINE per policy.
P.S2.c — Cross-corpus closure computationGiven a route that traverses INTER links, compute the transitive closure of required artifacts across corpora:
[\mathsf{CrossClosure}(\mathsf{RoutePlan}) := \bigcup \mathsf{Deps}(\text{visited nodes/edges}) \cup \mathsf{Deps}(\text{profiles}) \cup \mathsf{Deps}(\text{compat objects})]
Closure computation is deterministic and bounded by budgets; truncation is permitted only if corridor allows AMBIG with evidence plan.
P.S3 — Invariants
P.S3.a — No hidden semantics invariantNo external corpus may inject hidden semantics into the system. External references are admissible only through pinned connectors and explicit interpretation profiles. Raw external identifiers (URLs, filenames, informal labels) are never interpreted as meaning-bearing without a connector object that pins the mapping.
P.S3.b — Interpretation closure separation invariantIf SrcProfileDigest and DstProfileDigest differ, equivalence cannot be assumed. EQUIV/MIGRATE links require explicit witnesses. Absent witnesses, links are not OK-routable.
P.S3.c — Fork and scope integrity invariantIf a referenced MsID has multiple incompatible profile closures under identical pins (registry fork), scope integrity fails. Routes that depend on forked corpora must be quarantined or rejected under corridor policy.
P.S3.d — Revocation precedence invariantRevoked or fenced artifacts in any included scope override route admissibility; cross-corpus routes cannot bypass revocation through aliasing.
P.S4 — Protocols
P.S4.a — INTER link issuance protocolTo issue an INTER link:
Resolve SrcMsID and DstMsID in registry snapshots and bind their manifest digests.
Select SrcProfileDigest and DstProfileDigest explicitly; bind policy epoch digests.
Validate endpoints parse under corresponding grammars and schemas.
Determine LinkKind and required witness objects:
REF: none beyond pin closure.
EQUIV: EquivWitnessBundle required.
MIGRATE: CompatMatrix + MigrateWitnessBundle + rollback/import constraints required.
EXEC: Deployment profile and conformance suite references required.
Construct PinsDigest closure including all required objects.
Sign the INTER link under cross-corpus governance policy.
Append as DeltaPack (Ch20) and include in EvidenceTable (AppB) for routable claims.
P.S4.b — Scope-bound routing protocol (Ch19–Ch21)Route planning must:
Declare an active Scope object.
Reject traversal of any INTER link whose endpoints are out of scope.
Compute CrossClosure and require import verification under AppO.
Apply corridor truth typing and disclosure propagation across corpora:
NEAR claims require disclosure bundles,
AMBIG claims require evidence plans,
FAIL/CONFLICT require conflict packets and fences.
❀ P.F — Flower: Connector Abstraction and External Corpora Without Hidden Semantics
P.F1 — Objects
P.F1.a — Connector abstractionA Connector is the only allowed mechanism to reference external corpora. A connector pins the mapping from external identifiers to internal content-addressed artifacts.
[\mathsf{Connector}:=\langle\mathsf{ConnVer},;\mathsf{ConnID},;\mathsf{ConnKind},;\mathsf{AuthorityDigest},;\mathsf{MappingSpecRef},;\mathsf{NormalizationSpecDigest},;\mathsf{FetchPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{CachePolicyDigest},;\mathsf{RedactionPolicyDigest},;\mathsf{SchemaPinsDigest},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
ConnKind ∈ {URL, FILESTORE, GIT, DATABASE, API, HUMAN_INDEXED} pinned enum.
MappingSpecRef commits to the mapping from external IDs to internal digests (and includes domain separation tags).
NormalizationSpecDigest pins canonicalization of external identifiers.
FetchPolicyDigest pins allowed retrieval behavior; deploy corridors generally forbid nondeterministic remote fetch unless the fetched bytes are content-addressed and included in the bundle.
CachePolicyDigest pins caching behavior; cache must not alter semantics and must be keyed by digest.
RedactionPolicyDigest pins privacy and sanitization rules.
P.F1.b — ExternalRefAn ExternalRef is never used directly for routing. It must be resolved through a Connector.
[\mathsf{ExternalRef}:=\langle \mathsf{ConnID},\ \mathsf{ExternalID},\ \mathsf{ExternalIDDigest}\rangle]
ExternalIDDigest is computed after normalization by the connector.
P.F2 — Operators
P.F2.a — ResolveExternalRef[\mathsf{ResolveExternalRef} : (\mathsf{ExternalRef}, \mathsf{Connector}, \mathsf{Scope}) \to \mathsf{ARef} \cup \bot]Resolution must:
normalize ExternalID deterministically,
consult MappingSpec deterministically,
return only content-addressed artifacts by digest,
reject any “live” reference that cannot be pinned and exported.
P.F2.b — Connector import disciplineIn published scopes, external references must be fully resolved and included as payload artifacts. Unresolved external references are forbidden for OK routing and must be treated as AMBIG/FAIL per corridor.
P.F3 — Invariants
P.F3.a — No hidden semantics from connectorsConnector resolution must not infer meaning. It may map identifiers to content digests and schemas only. Any semantic interpretation of external content occurs only after import verification and corridor typing under pinned profiles.
P.F3.b — Deterministic mapping invariantGiven identical connector digest and identical external identifier, ResolveExternalRef must produce identical artifact digest or (\bot).
☁ P.C — Cloud: Uncertainty Handling for Cross-Corpus Interfaces
P.C1 — Objects
P.C1.a — CrossCorpusEvidencePlanIf a required external artifact cannot be resolved or imported deterministically, a bounded evidence plan must be emitted with:
candidate external resolutions,
discriminators (e.g., fetch and hash under pinned policy),
stop rules and budgets,
promotion hooks into Ch20 scheduler.
P.C1.b — Quarantine triggersCross-corpus routes become quarantined if:
imported artifacts are revoked,
connector mapping changes without explicit migration,
forked registry states exist for required MsIDs.
✶ P.R — Fractal: CrossCorpusCert and ScopeIntegrityCert
P.R1 — Required certificates
P.R1.a — CrossCorpusCertA CrossCorpusCert attests that a set of INTER links and/or connector resolutions are valid, import-verifiable, and corridor-compliant within a declared scope.
[\mathsf{CrossCorpusCert}:=\langle\mathsf{CertVer},;\mathsf{ScopeID},;\mathsf{INTERSetDigest},;\mathsf{ConnectorSetDigest},;\mathsf{ClosureDigest},;\mathsf{ImportAcceptanceCertSetDigest},;\mathsf{ReplayCertSetDigest?},;\mathsf{Result},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Result is PASS iff:
every INTER link validates under ValidateINTER,
all required compat/witness objects verify,
closure imports are accepted under AppO,
and no revoked/fenced artifacts exist in closure.
P.R1.b — ScopeIntegrityCertA ScopeIntegrityCert attests that scope boundaries are enforced deterministically and no out-of-scope traversal occurs in the certified route set.
[\mathsf{ScopeIntegrityCert}:=\langle\mathsf{CertVer},;\mathsf{ScopeID},;\mathsf{RouteSetDigest},;\mathsf{ObservedMsSetDigest},;\mathsf{ObservedProfileSetDigest},;\mathsf{ForkCheckDigest},;\mathsf{RevocationCheckDigest},;\mathsf{FenceCheckDigest},;\mathsf{Result},;\mathsf{IssuedPulse},;\mathsf{Sig}\rangle]
Result is PASS iff:
observed manuscripts and profiles are subsets of scope sets,
no registry forks affect referenced keys,
revocation and fence policies are applied and block forbidden traversals,
route evaluation is deterministic under pinned pins and environment.
AppP Tight Spec-Only Version (Normative Extraction)
Scope is a pinned boundary object committing to allowed manuscripts, profiles, policy epochs, schemas, connectors, and pulse bindings.
INTER links require explicit Ms endpoints, explicit profile digests, explicit addresses, explicit link kind, and compat/witness references when semantics differ; unpinned links are non-OK-routable.
Connector abstraction is the only allowed mechanism to reference external corpora; it pins deterministic mapping from external IDs to internal digests and forbids importing hidden semantics.
Cross-corpus routing must compute deterministic closure, apply import verification, revocations, and fences, and enforce scope membership.
CrossCorpusCert and ScopeIntegrityCert are required, import-verifiable, and bind closure validity and scope enforcement for cross-corpus routes.
AppP — Mycelium Interface: Cross-Corpus Linking, External Connectors, and Scope
